Taharah — Purification
advanced
12 min
Acts That Do Not Permit Prayer and the Hadith of Returning Salaam
Listing non-permitting acts and addressing the hadith objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the acts for which tayammum does not permit prayer, explain the exception for recitation when junub, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the hadith of the Prophet returning salaam.

Core Idea
Tayammum for non-worship acts does not permit prayer, but the validity of tayammum and permissibility of prayer are separate rulings.

The author now lists numerous acts for which tayammum, though valid, does not permit subsequent prayer. This includes entering mosques, touching the mushaf, and more. He also addresses a potential objection from the prophetic practice. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these rulings and clarifies the fine point about recitation when one is in a state of major impurity.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited acts
Identify the acts listed: entering mosque, recitation even from mushaf, touching the mushaf, visiting graves, burying the dead, adhan, iqamah, giving or returning salaam, entering Islam.
2
Apply the condition for prayer permissions
Check if these acts are qurbah maqsudah or part of it. Most are not. For recitation, there is a nuance: if the person is junub, the act is part of worship (Quran recitation is part of prayer) and requires purification, so tayammum then permits prayer.
3
Analyze the exception for recitation
The source states that if a junub person performs tayammum for recitation, it permits prayer because recitation is part of worship and is not allowed without purification for a junub. This is the detailed view from al-Bada'i'.
4
Address the hadith objection
The objection: The Prophet performed tayammum to return salaam. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the validity of tayammum (which is valid for acts permissible without purification and missed without substitute) and the permissibility of prayer with it (which requires the intention for a qurbah maqsudah).
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that tayammum for these acts does not permit prayer. The Prophet's action does not contradict because he performed tayammum for salaam when water was absent, and the ruling on prayer is separate.

The impurity from that the intention required in tayammum is the intention of purification, and this is the correct view, so it does not negate it because it includes the intention of purification. They sufficed with the intention of purification because purification was legislated for prayer and was made a condition for permitting them, so its intention is the intention of permitting prayer, such that if he performed tayammum to teach others, prayer is not permissible with it according to the most sound view. Likewise in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. If he performed tayammum for the funeral prayer or the prostration of recitation, it is permissible for him to pray all other prayers because each of them is an intentional act of worship (qurbah maqsudah), and what is meant by intentional act of worship is that it is not obligated within something else by way of being a subsidiary. This does not contradict what is mentioned in the principles that the prostration of recitation is not an intentional act of worship, such that if he recited it in a disliked time, it is permissible to perform it in another disliked time, unlike the obligatory prayer if it becomes due in an imperfect time—it is not performed in another imperfect time, because the negation and affirmation are not from one aspect but from two aspects. What is meant here is that it was legislated as an initial act drawing near to Allah, not being subsidiary to something else, unlike entering the mosque and touching the mushaf. What is meant in the principles is that the form of prostration is not intended for its own sake at the time of recitation, but rather because it includes humility that achieves agreement with the people of Islam and opposition to the people of transgression. For this reason we said: the performance of the obligation is not restricted to this form, rather the bowing in prayer immediately substitutes for it. Likewise in Mi'raj al-Dirayah following al-Khabbaziyyah. They explicitly stated that if he performed tayammum for entering the mosque, or recitation even from the mushaf, or touching it, or visiting graves, or burying the dead, or the call to prayer, or the iqamah, or giving salaam, or returning it, or entering Islam, prayer is not permissible with that tayammum according to the majority of the mashayikh, because some of them are not intentional acts of worship, and although entering Islam is an intentional act of worship, it is valid without purification. Thus they universally prohibited in reading Quran. And in al-Muhit: he universally permitted and made equal between funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, and reading Quran. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the most correct is that it is not permissible for him to pray if he performed tayammum for recitation of Quran, and the truth requires detail: if he performed tayammum for it while he was junub, it is permissible for him to pray all other prayers with it. Likewise in al-Bada'i' and Ghayat al-Bayan. They did not distinguish in entering the mosque between being junub or having minor impurity, despite each being subsidiary to something else, namely prayer. Better to say: The condition is that the intended act be an intentional act of worship or a part of it, and it is not permissible except with purification. So recitation is a part of the intentional act of worship, but if he was junub, the last condition is met—that the act is not permissible except with purification—so the condition is complete and prayer with it is permissible. If the last condition is not met, prayer with it is not permissible. Tayammum for entering the mosque falls under this absolutely. As for minor impurity, it is obvious due to the absence of both conditions. As for major impurity, although the last condition (impermissibility without purification) is found, the first condition (being an intentional act of worship or part of it) is absent. Tayammum for touching the mushaf (or entering Islam) is excluded. He said in al-Nahr: It is not appropriate to count Islam here as occurred in Fath al-Qadir and others because it gives the impression that it is valid, but he does not pray with it like others, and the meaning is not that he lacks capacity for intention. I say: It will come that it is valid according to Abu Yusuf even if prayer with it is not valid, so its inclusion here is based on his statement. His statement: (or its remnants) He said in al-Nahr: as a person with minor ritual impurity that it is... his claim because absolutely, although it is not permissible except with it, it is not an intentional act of worship. It cannot be said that entering the mosque is worship even if not for prayer but for i'tikaf, because we say: The worship is i'tikaf, and entering the mosque is subsidiary to it, so it is a non-intentional act of worship. If he performed tayammum for the prostration of thankfulness, he does not pray the obligatory prayer with it. According to Muhammad, he prays it based on it being an act of drawing near (qurbah) according to him, whereas according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's position in this context?) it is not a qurbah. Likewise in al-Tawshih. And in Fath al-Qadir: If you say: You mentioned that the intention of tayammum for returning salaam does not render it valid according to the apparent madhhab, despite the fact that he (peace be upon him) performed tayammum for returning salaam as I mentioned earlier. The answer is that intending to return salaam with tayammum necessarily implies that he intended at the time of performing tayammum the tayammum for it, but it is possible that he intended what makes tayammum valid, then returns salaam when he has become pure! And one may object by denying the incorrectness of tayammum for salaam, as the madhhab is that tayammum for salaam is valid, but the discussion is about the permissibility of prayer with it. For this reason, Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: If he performed tayammum for salaam or returning it, he is not permitted to perform prayer with that tayammum—he did not say his tayammum is not valid. Thus it is known that the permissibility of prayer with it is a separate ruling unrelated to what he (peace be upon him) did, for he performed tayammum for salaam when water was absent, and there is no doubt about its validity. Al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Muslim: This hadith is interpreted as meaning that he was without water at the time of tayammum, because tayammum with the presence of water is not permissible for one able to use it. According to our principles, there is no need for this interpretation because according to us, for something that is missed without a substitute, tayammum is permissible even with the presence of water, like the funeral prayer. There is no doubt that returning salaam from him is based on the fact that he (peace be upon him) does not mention Allah except in a state of purity. Rather, according to us, there is a more general principle: for something for which purification is not a condition for its permissibility, it is permissible to perform tayammum for it even with the presence of water, like entering the mosque for one with minor impurity. For this reason, al-Mubtagha (?) said: It is permissible to perform tayammum for entering the mosque when water is present, and likewise for sleeping in it. End quote. End quote. With his addition in the parameter for including recitation, though it is unnecessary, because the occurrence of recitation as part of worship from one aspect does not negate its occurrence as an intended phrase from another aspect. Do you not see that they included the prostration of recitation in their statement 'intentional act of worship', though the prostration is part of the worship which is prayer. His statement: (And one may object) He said in al-Nahr: This is extremely weak, and how can one imagine what he mentioned with his statement 'you mentioned' and what he mentioned is that if he performed tayammum for salaam, prayer with it is not permissible according to the majority of mashayikh. In that case, it must be that it does not make it valid, i.e., prayer, as evidenced by his statement 'according to the apparent madhhab' because it is the subject of disagreement. I say: The remoteness of this is not hidden, and it is not appropriate for the answer he mentioned in al-Fath after the question. Reflect on his statement: (Rather, according to us, what is more general than that) i.e., more general in one respect, as mentioned by some virtuous scholars, because in the case of returning salaam, both principles come together: it is permissible without purification and it is missed without a substitute. The first principle (intentional worship) applies individually to things like funeral prayer, which is missed without a substitute and is not permissible without purification. The second principle (permissible without purification) applies individually to things like entering the mosque for one with minor impurity, which is permissible without purification from minor ritual impurity and is not described as missed without a substitute. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the intention in tayammum. The author begins by clarifying that the required intention in tayammum is the intention of purification, which is considered sufficient because purification was legislated for prayer. The core issue is whether a tayammum performed for one purpose permits performing other acts of worship, particularly prayers. The ruling: if one performs tayammum with an intention for an act that is an 'intentional act of worship' (qurbah maqsudah), such as funeral prayer or prostration of recitation, then that tayammum permits all prayers. This is because these acts are independently legislated as acts of drawing near to Allah, not as subsidiaries of something else. The passage then lists acts for which tayammum does NOT permit prayer: entering the mosque, reciting Quran (even from mushaf), touching the mushaf, visiting graves, burying the dead, adhan, iqamah, giving or returning salaam, entering Islam. The reasoning is that these are either not intentional acts of worship (like entering mosque) or are valid without purification (like entering Islam). However, there are nuances: for recitation, if the person is in a state of major impurity (junub), the tayammum does permit prayer because recitation is a part of worship and is not permissible without purification for a junub. The author then addresses a potential objection concerning the hadith of the Prophet performing tayammum to return salaam. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the validity of the tayammum itself and the permissibility of prayer with it. The Prophet's tayammum for salaam was valid because it was for an act that is permissible without purification and is missed without substitute, but that does not mean prayer with that tayammum is permissible. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tayammum for such non-worship acts does not permit prayer. This discussion demonstrates the Hanafi method of ta'lil (identifying the effective cause) and the importance of categorizing acts as 'intentional worship' or not.

Key Terms
قربة مقصودة (qurbah maqsudah): An act of worship that is intended for its own sake.
جواز الصلاة بالتيمم (jawaz al-salat bi al-tayammum): Permissibility of prayer with a particular tayammum, which depends on the intention at the time of tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person performs tayammum to recite Quran from the mushaf (while not being junub), can he then pray the obligatory prayer with that tayammum?
A) Yes, according to al-Muhit.
B) No, according to the majority of mashayikh.
C) Yes, if he intends purification.
D) No, because tayammum is only for prayer.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for non-worship acts does not permit prayer; only tayammum intended for an intentional act of worship (or part thereof, with the exception for junub recitation) permits prayer.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Tayammum for Sujud al-Shukr and the Principle of 'Ibadah Maqsudah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for sujud al-shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between intended and unintended acts of worship ('ibadah maqsudah) and apply it to the ruling on tayammum for sujud al-shukr.

Core Idea
Tayammum for a non-intended act does not permit obligatory prayer—only acts that are 'ibadah maqsudah justify tayammum.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of tayammum. The key concept is 'ibadah maqsudah—worship intended for its own sake. The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that tayammum is valid only for acts that are themselves intended acts of worship. Sujud al-shukr (prostration of thanksgiving) is debated: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it not an intended worship, while Imam Muhammad considers it a good deed (qurbah) that qualifies. This difference has practical consequences for whether one can pray fard with that tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question is: does tayammum performed specifically for sujud al-shukr suffice for performing fard prayer?
2
State the majority position and its basis
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the majority), the tayammum is not valid for fard prayer because sujud al-shukr is not an 'ibadah maqsudah—it is not an act of worship intended for its own sake.
The principle: tayammum is only for intended worship; subsidiary acts like entering the mosque do not count.
3
Identify Imam Muhammad's position and his basis
Imam Muhammad holds that sujud al-shukr is a qurbah (good deed) and thus qualifies as 'ibadah maqsudah, making the tayammum sufficient for fard prayer.
For Muhammad, the act's merit (qurbah) is enough to make it an intended worship.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority text refutes the analogy of entering the mosque: entering is a means to i'tikaf, not itself a worship. Similarly, sujud al-shukr is a spontaneous expression, not an established ritual with its own intention.
The majority's illa (effective cause) is that the act must be an independent, intended act of worship like salah or i'tikaf.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone has only this tayammum, the majority require him to repeat tayammum for fard prayer; Imam Muhammad allows him to pray fard with it.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنه وإن كان لا يحل إلا بها إلا أنه ليس بعبادة مقصودة، ولا يقال إن دخول المسجد عبادة وإن لم يكن للصلاة بل للاعتكاف لأنا نقول : العبادة الاعتكاف ودخول المسجد تبع له فكانت عبادة غير مقصودة. ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر لا يصلي به المكتوبة، وعند محمد يصليها بناء على أنها قربة عنده وعندهما ليست بقربة كذا في التوشيح.
For it, although it is not permissible except with it, except that it is not an intended act of worship, and it is not said that entering the mosque is worship even if not for prayer but for seclusion, because we say: The worship is seclusion and entering the mosque is subsidiary to it, so it is unintentional worship. And if he performs tayammum for the prostration of thanksgiving, he does not pray the obligatory prayer with it, and according to Muhammad he prays it based on the fact that it is a good deed in his view, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani?) it is not a good deed, as in al-Tawshih.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi ruling on performing tayammum for sujud al-shukr (prostration of thanksgiving). The author first establishes a general principle: tayammum is valid only for acts that are 'عبادة مقصودة' (intended worship). Acts that are not themselves intended worship but are merely means to an end do not justify tayammum. For example, entering the mosque is not itself an act of worship; rather, it is a means to i'tikaf (seclusion) which is the actual worship. Therefore, entering the mosque is not an intended worship and tayammum for it is not valid if performed solely for that purpose. Applying this principle, if one performs tayammum specifically for sujud al-shukr (a prostration of gratitude), according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (according to one view), the tayammum is not valid for performing the obligatory prayer (maktubah) because sujud al-shukr is not an intended worship. However, according to Imam Muhammad, sujud al-shukr is considered a good deed (qurbah) and thus qualifies as intended worship, so the tayammum would be valid for other prayers as well. The text notes this difference as recorded in al-Tawshih.

Key Terms
عبادة مقصودة ('ibadah maqsudah): An act of worship that is intended for its own sake, not merely as a means to another act.
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): The prostration of thanksgiving performed upon receiving a blessing or deliverance from harm.
قربة (qurbah): A deed that brings one closer to Allah; a good deed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn), if someone performs tayammum specifically for sujud al-shukr, can he then perform the obligatory prayer with that same tayammum?
A) Yes, because sujud al-shukr is a qurbah.
B) No, because sujud al-shukr is not an intended worship (عبادة مقصودة).
C) Yes, because tayammum purifies one from all hadath.
D) No, because sujud al-shukr requires wudu'.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tayammum is only valid for acts that are considered 'ibadah maqsudah (intended worship); sujud al-shukr is not, according to the majority, so tayammum for it does not permit fard prayer.

Tayammum for Returning Salam: Validity vs. Permissibility for Prayer
Inter-madhhab dispute on tayammum for salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the validity of tayammum for returning salam and its sufficiency for performing other prayers, and explain the Hanafi position with evidence.

Core Idea
Tayammum for salam is valid but does not permit salah.

This lesson addresses a subtle point: the Prophet performed tayammum to return salam, yet the Hanafi school holds that such tayammum—while valid—does not allow one to pray obligatory salah. The key is distinguishing between the validity of the act and its scope of permissibility. We will explore the objection, the Hanafi response, and the broader principle of acts lost without replacement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection is that the Prophet's tayammum for salam seems to contradict the Hanafi claim that tayammum for salam does not validate prayer.
The objection is based on apparent contradiction.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes between the validity of the tayammum and its sufficiency for prayer. The tayammum is valid, but it does not elevate one to a state of purity sufficient for acts that require purity.
Key distinction: validity vs. permissibility.
3
Examine Qadikhan's fatwa
Qadikhan explicitly states that tayammum for salam is valid but does not permit prayer. This is the relied-upon position.
Qadikhan's fatwa is a key source.
4
Understand the broader principle
Hanafis allow tayammum for acts that would be lost without replacement (ma yafutu la ila khalaf) even with water, such as funeral prayer. Returning salam is similar because it does not require purity.
This principle extends to entering mosque, etc.
5
Apply the ruling
If someone performs tayammum to return salam, he cannot subsequently pray fard. He would need a new tayammum with the intention of prayer.
Practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير : فإن قلت ذكرت أن نية التيمم لرد السلام لا تصححه على ظاهر المذهب مع أنه عليه السلام تيمم لرد السلام على ما أسلفته في الأوّل. فالجواب أن قصد رد السلام بالتيمم يستلزم أن يكون نوى عند فعل التيمم التيمم له بل يجوز كونه نوى ما يصح معه التيمم ثم يرد السلام إذا صار طاهراً ! ولقائل أن يمنع عدم صحة التيمم للسلام كما المذهب أن التيمم للسلام صحيح، وإنما الكلام في جواز الصلاة به ولهذا قال قاضيخان في فتاواه : ولو تيمم للسلام أو لرده لا يجوز له أداء الصلاة بذلك التيمم ولم يقل لا يجوز تيممه، فعلم أن جواز الصلاة به حكم آخر لا تعلق له بما فعله عليه السلام فإنه تيمم للسلام عند فقد الماء، ولا شك في صحته. قال النووي في شرح مسلم : وهذا الحديث محمول على أنه كان عادماً للماء حال التيمم فإن التيمم مع وجود الماء لا يجوز للقادر على استعماله وعلى أصولنا لا حاجة إلى هذا الحمل فإن عندنا ما يفوت لا إلى خلف يجوز التيمم له مع وجود الماء كصلاة الجنازة ولا شك أن ردّ السلام منه بناء على أنه عليه السلام لا يذكر الله تعالى إلا على طهارة، بل عندنا ما هو أعم من ذلك وهو أن ما ليست الطهارة فعله شرطاً في حله فإنه يجوز التيمم له مع وجود الماء كدخول المسجد للمحدث، ولهذا قال في المبتغى بالغين المعجمة : ويجوز التيمم لدخول مسجد عند وجود الماء وكذا للنوم فيه ا هـ .
And in Fath al-Qadir: If you say: You mentioned that the intention of tayammum for returning the greeting (salam) does not validate it according to the apparent madhhab, even though the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tayammum for returning the greeting as I mentioned earlier. The answer is that intending to return the greeting with tayammum necessitates that he intended the tayammum for it at the time of performing tayammum, but it is possible that he intended what makes tayammum valid with it, then he returns the greeting when he becomes pure. And someone may object that the tayammum for salam is not invalid, as the madhhab is that tayammum for salam is valid; rather, the discussion is about the permissibility of prayer with it. For this reason Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: If he performed tayammum for salam or for returning it, it is not permissible for him to perform the prayer with that tayammum; he did not say that his tayammum is not valid. So you know that the permissibility of prayer with it is another ruling that has no connection with what the Prophet did, for he performed tayammum for salam when water was absent, and there is no doubt about its validity. Al-Nawawi said in Sharh Muslim: This hadith is interpreted as meaning that he was without water at the time of tayammum, because tayammum in the presence of water is not permissible for one who can use it. According to our principles, there is no need for this interpretation because according to us, what is lost without replacement (ma yafutu la ila khalaf) permits tayammum for it even with water present, such as the funeral prayer. And there is no doubt that his returning the greeting was based on the fact that he does not mention Allah the Exalted except in a state of purity. Rather, according to us, there is something more general: that which purity is not a condition for its permissibility, it is permissible to perform tayammum for it even with water present, like entering the mosque for a person in a state of minor impurity. For this reason, it is said in al-Mubtagha (with the ghayn): It is permissible to perform tayammum for entering a mosque when water is present, and likewise for sleeping in it. End quote.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses an objection concerning the Prophet's tayammum for returning salam. The author of Fath al-Qadir raises a question: How can the madhhab hold that tayammum with the intention of returning salam is invalid, given that the Prophet himself performed tayammum for that purpose? The answer is twofold. First, it is possible that the Prophet intended something that makes tayammum valid (such as general purification) and then returned the salam. Second, even if he intended the salam, the question is about the permissibility of praying other prayers with that tayammum, not about the validity of the tayammum itself. Qadikhan distinguishes: the tayammum for salam is valid, but it does not permit performing the obligatory prayer. Al-Nawawi's interpretation (that the Prophet was without water) is unnecessary for the Hanafis because they allow tayammum for acts that would otherwise be lost (like funeral prayer) even in the presence of water. They also have a broader category: acts for which purity is not a condition (like entering the mosque) can be done with tayammum even if water is available. This is supported by a quote from al-Mubtagha permitting tayammum for entering a mosque and sleeping in it when water is present.

Key Terms
رد السلام (radd al-salam): Returning the greeting of salam, which is obligatory in some cases.
يفوت لا إلى خلف (ma yafutu la ila khalaf): An act that will be lost without replacement if not performed now, such as a funeral prayer that cannot be repeated.
فوت (fawt): The time after which an act can no longer be performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs tayammum with the specific intention of returning salam, what is the ruling regarding performing the obligatory prayer with that same tayammum?
A) It is permissible because the tayammum is valid.
B) It is not permissible because the tayammum was intended for a different purpose.
C) It is permissible only if water is absent.
D) It is permissible because returning salam is similar to prayer.

Key Takeaway
The validity of tayammum does not automatically permit all acts; the intention and purpose of the tayammum define its scope.

Necessity of Specific Intention (Niyyah) for Tayammum and Related Rulings
Discusses the requirement of a specific intention for tayammum, the view of Muhammad regarding a junub intending wudu', and the invalid tayammum of a kafir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of specific intention for tayammum, explain the intra-madhhab disagreement, and apply the ruling to cases such as a junub intending wudu' and the tayammum of a disbeliever.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires a specific intention; without it, the purification is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that unlike wudu', tayammum demands a specific intention to be valid. We will explore the relied-upon position, the evidence from the Qur'an, and important corollaries including the case of a junub and the invalid tayammum of a disbeliever. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The author states that a specific intention (niyyah makhsusah) is required for tayammum to be valid. This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school, contrary to a narration in al-Nawadir.
This is a condition (shart) for validity, not a pillar.
2
Understand the intra-madhhab disagreement
Al-Jassas argued that only discrimination (tamyiz) is needed, not a specific intention. The author rejects this, justifying the need for intention to make the act a purification.
The disagreement is over the level of intention required.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'so seek clean earth' (4:43) is cited. The author notes that it only indicates intention towards the earth, but the context ('and you do not find water') suggests it is for the sake of prayer, thus requiring a specific intention.
The dalala (indication) is zanni, hence the ruling is wajib not fard.
4
Apply to cases: junub and kafir
From Imam Muhammad: if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu', it suffices because the intention is for purification. For a disbeliever: his tayammum is invalid because Islam is a condition and specific intention is required, while his wudu' is valid as intention is not required.
These cases illustrate the practical implications of the intention requirement.

بالمسافر، أما إذ يتيمم لها مع وجوده لخوف الفوت فإن تيممه يبطل بفراغه منها. ومما تقدم علم أن نية التيمم لا تكفي لصحته على المذهب خلافاً لما في النوادر، ولا اعتماد عليه بل المعتمد اشتراط نية مخصوصة هي ما قدمناه لكن لا دليل عليه لأن قوله تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً إنما يدل على قصد الصعيد المترتب عليه المسح فلا يكون موجباً غير النية المعتبرة كذا في فتح القدير. ويمكن أن يقال : إن المراد قصد الصعيد لأجل الصلاة بقرينة قوله فلم تجدوا ففيه الإنباء عن المشروط كما لا يخفى. ولا تشترط نية الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء أجزأه . هكذا روي عن محمد نصاً كما نقله في التنجيس. وذكر الجصاص أنه لا حاجة إلى نية التطهير بل لا بد من التمييز لأن التيمم لهما يقع على صفة واحدة فيميز بالنية كصلوات الفرائض وليس بصحيح، الحاجة إلى النية ليقع التيمم طهارة فإذا وقع طهارة جاز له أن يؤدي ما شاء لأن الشروط يراعى وجودها لا غير، ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر يجوز أداء الظهر به بخلاف الصلوات، كذا في الخبازية وغيرها. ولا يخفى أن قول محمد لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء» معناه يريد به طهارة الوضوء لما علمت من قوله : (فلغا تيمم كافر لا وضوءه) يعني فلأجل اشتراط النية المخصوصة في التيمم بطل تيمم كافر، ولعدم اشتراط النية في الوضوء لا يبطل وضوءه، أما الأول فلأن الإسلام شرط وقوع التيمم صحيحاً عند عامة العلماء وروي عن أبي يوسف إذا تيمم ينوي الإسلام جاز حتى لو أسلم لا يجوز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم عند العامة، وعلى رواية أبي يوسف إن كان معناه للجنب كما هو الظاهر امتنع هذا التعليل .اهـ. أقول : وأنت خبير بأن قول And the permitting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) intended with it what makes tayammum valid is contrary to the apparent meaning, as is not hidden. Then it is not hidden that their statement about the permissibility of prayer with tayammum for the funeral prayer is interpreted as when he is not finding water, as qualified in al-Khulasa by 'the traveler'. But if he performs tayammum for it with the presence of water due to fear of missing it, then his tayammum becomes invalid after he finishes it. From what preceded, it is known that the intention of tayammum is not sufficient for its validity in the madhhab, contrary to what is in al-Nawadir, and no reliance is placed on it. Rather, the relied-upon is the condition of a specific intention as we have presented, but there is no proof for it because the saying of Allah Most High 'so seek clean earth' (4:43) only indicates the intention of the earth entailing wiping, so it does not necessitate other than the considered intention, as in Fath al-Qadir. And it can be said that what is intended is the intention of the earth for the sake of prayer, by the indication of His saying 'and you do not find water', for in it is the indication of the conditioned, as is not hidden. And the intention of hadath and janabah is not required, so that even if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu' by it, it suffices him. Thus it is related from Muhammad by text, as quoted in al-Tanjis. And al-Jassas mentioned that there is no need for the intention of purification, rather, discrimination is necessary because tayammum for both occurs in one manner, so it is distinguished by intention like the obligatory prayers, but it is not correct. The need for intention is so that the tayammum occurs as purification; when it occurs as purification, it is permissible for him to perform whatever he wishes, because conditions are observed in their existence only. Do you not see that if he performs tayammum for 'asr, it is permissible for him to perform zuhr with it, unlike prayers? Thus in al-Khabbaziyya and others. And it is not hidden that the statement of Muhammad: 'If a junub performs tayammum intending wudu' by it' means he intends by it the purification of wudu', since you have learned the requirement of intention for purification. And by what is established, it is known that what is in al-Qunyah from his statement 'there remained on the body of the junub a spot, then he had a minor hadath and performed tayammum for both, it is permissible, and he intends both' because if he intends one, the other remains without intention – this is based on the statement of Abu Bakr al-Jassas, as is not hidden. His statement: (So the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu') means that due to the requirement of specific intention in tayammum, the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, and due to the absence of requirement of intention in wudu', his wudu' is not invalid. As for the first, because Islam is a condition for tayammum to occur validly according to most scholars, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if he performs tayammum intending Islam, it is permissible, so that even if he becomes Muslim, he is not permitted to pray with that tayammum according to the generality. And according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, if its meaning is for the junub, as is apparent, this reasoning is prevented. End quote. I say: And you are an expert that the statement of al-Mubtagha 'with the presence of water' determines its interpretation for the one with minor impurity. Then I saw some virtuous person object to al-Nahr saying: The statement of al-Mubtagha 'with the presence of water' is either intended to mean that the water is outside the mosque or inside it. If it is the first, it is false; if it is the second, it is correct but far from his expression, by the evidence of his saying 'and likewise for sleeping in it'. End quote. And it supports what we said, and it can be said that his statement 'and likewise for sleeping in it' means if he has a wet dream in the mosque and cannot leave, he performs tayammum for sleeping in it. So the first issue is when water is inside the mosque, and the second when it is outside, and it has passed from al-Muhit in the explanation of the author's statement 'if he is junub or menstruating, etc.' And then what the author claimed about the permissibility of tayammum with the presence of water for everything that does not require purity, even if it is not something lost without substitute, is a claim.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This lengthy passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq covers several interconnected rulings about intention in tayammum. The author first addresses the objection that the Prophet's intention might have been general, but argues that this is contrary to the apparent meaning. He then clarifies that the permissibility of tayammum for funeral prayer when water is present is only for travelers; otherwise, the tayammum becomes invalid after the prayer. The core ruling is that a specific intention is necessary for tayammum, contrary to a narration in al-Nawadir. The relied-upon position is that one must intend purification for a specific purpose. The author notes that there is no explicit textual proof from the Quran for this requirement, but it can be derived from the context. Importantly, it is not necessary to intend the specific type of impurity (hadath or janabah); if a junub intends wudu', it suffices. This is from Imam Muhammad. Al-Jassas argued that only discrimination is needed, but the author rejects this, stating that intention is needed for tayammum to be a purification. Once it is a purification, any act can be performed with it. For example, if one performs tayammum for 'asr, he can also pray zuhr with it. This is distinct from prayers themselves which require separate intentions. The statement of Muhammad about a junub intending wudu' is interpreted as intending purification for wudu'. The author also discusses a case from al-Qunyah where a junub has a spot and then has minor hadath; he performs tayammum for both. The correct view is that he must intend both, otherwise one remains without intention. Finally, the passage addresses the tayammum of a disbeliever: it is invalid because Islam is a condition and specific intention is required, while his wudu' is valid because wudu' does not require intention. A narration from Abu Yusuf says if a disbeliever intends Islam with tayammum, it is permissible, but he cannot pray with it after becoming Muslim. The passage ends with a critique of an author's claim about tayammum with water present for anything not requiring purity.

Key Terms
نية مخصوصة (niyyah makhsusah): A specific intention, such as intending purification for a particular act (e.g., for prayer or for an intended worship).
تطهر (tatahhur): Purification; the state of being ritually clean.
تيمم الكافر (tayammum al-kafir): Tayammum performed by a disbeliever; it is invalid because Islam is a condition for the act to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, is a specific intention (niyyah makhsusah) required for the validity of tayammum?
A) No, because tayammum is like wudu' which does not require intention.
B) Yes, a specific intention is required for tayammum to be valid.
C) Yes, but only for tayammum from janabah.
D) No, only discrimination (tamyiz) is needed according to the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires a specific intention to be valid; this distinguishes it from wudu' and is the relied-upon Hanafi position, despite an intra-madhhab difference.

Specific Intention Required for Tayammum
Discussion on the requirement of a specific intention for tayammum validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for intention in tayammum, distinguish the mu'tamad from the views in al-Nawadir and of al-Jassas, and apply the rule to cases like a junub person.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires a specific intention for purification; a general intention is insufficient.

The Hanafi school specifies that tayammum, unlike wudu, requires a deliberate intention (niyyah) for it to be valid. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the exact nature of that intention—whether it must be for purification itself or merely for distinction between types of tayammum. The author defends the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position against opposing narrations and opinions, emphasizing that intention for purification (niyyat al-tathir) is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tamad Position
The author states that a general intention (e.g., just 'tayammum') is insufficient. The relied-upon view requires a specific intention—either for purification (tathir) or for a specific act like prayer. This contradicts a narration in al-Nawadir that allowed general intention.
The mu'tamad is based on later scholarship (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
2
Examine the Quranic Evidence
The verse 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (so head for pure earth) is cited. The author notes that this only commands seeking earth; it does not explicitly demand a specific intention. However, the context 'and you did not find water' implies the intention for prayer.
The dalil is zanni al-dalala; the ruling is inferred.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
Two opposing views are presented: (1) al-Nawadir permits a general intention; (2) Abu Bakr al-Jassas argues that only intention of distinction (tamyiz) is needed, not purification. The author refutes both, especially al-Jassas, by analogizing to prayer intentions where specific niyyah is required.
The refutation is based on the principle that tayammum must be valid as purification (taharah) to be usable for any act.
4
Apply to Practical Cases
The author gives two examples: (a) a junub who makes tayammum intending wudu (i.e., purification from minor hadath) suffices—this is from a direct narration of Imam Muhammad. (b) Tayammum made for Asr can be used for Dhuhr, unlike prayers requiring specific niyyah per salah.
This illustrates that once tayammum is valid as purification, it can serve multiple acts.
5
Resolve a Potential Contradiction
A statement in al-Qunyah suggests that if a junub has a spot and makes tayammum for both hadath and janabah, he must intend for both, otherwise one remains without intention. The author clarifies this is based on al-Jassas's view, not the mu'tamad.
The mu'tamad requires only one intention for purification; it covers all states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم وتجويز أن يكون النبي عليه السلام نوى معه ما يصح معه التيمم خلاف الظاهر كما لا يخفى، ثم لا يخفى أن قولهم بجواز الصلاة بالتيمم لصلاة الجنازة محمول على ما إذا لم يكن واجداً للماء كما قيده في الخلاصة بالمسافر، أما إذ يتيمم لها مع وجوده لخوف الفوت فإن تيممه يبطل بفراغه منها. ومما تقدم علم أن نية التيمم لا تكفي لصحته على المذهب خلافاً لما في النوادر ، ولا اعتماد عليه بل المعتمد اشتراط نية مخصوصة هي ما قدمناه لكن لا دليل عليه لأن قوله تعالى فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً إنما يدل على قصد الصعيد المترتب عليه المسح فلا يكون موجباً غير النية المعتبرة كذا في فتح القدير. ويمكن أن يقال : إن المراد قصد الصعيد لأجل الصلاة بقرينة قوله فلم تجدوا ففيه الإنباء عن المشروط كما لا يخفى. ولا تشترط نية الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء أجزأه . هكذا روي عن محمد نصاً كما نقله في التنجيس. وذكر الجصاص أنه لا حاجة إلى نية التطهير بل لا بد من التمييز لأن التيمم لهما يقع على صفة واحدة فيميز بالنية كصلوات الفرائض وليس بصحيح، الحاجة إلى النية ليقع التيمم طهارة فإذا وقع طهارة جاز له أن يؤدي ما شاء لأن الشروط يراعى وجودها لا غير، ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر يجوز أداء الظهر به بخلاف الصلوات، كذا في الخبازية وغيرها. ولا يخفى أن قول محمد لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء» معناه يريد به طهارة الوضوء لما علمت من اشتراط نية التطهير. وبما تقرر علم أن ما في القنية من قوله بقي على جسد الجنب لمعة ثم أحدث وتيمم لهما جاز وينوي لهما لأنه إذا نوى لأحدهما يبقى الآخر بلا نية مبني على قول أبي بكر الجصاص كما لا يخفى .
Book of Purity - Chapter of Tayammum. And allowing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) intended with it what makes tayammum valid is against the apparent meaning as is not hidden. Then it is not hidden that their statement about permissibility of prayer with tayammum for the funeral prayer is interpreted as when he is not finding water, as restricted in al-Khulasa to the traveler. But if he makes tayammum for it with presence of water due to fear of losing it, then his tayammum becomes invalid after finishing it. From what preceded, it is known that the intention of tayammum is not sufficient for its validity according to the school, contrary to what is in al-Nawadir, and it is not relied upon. Rather, the relied-upon is the requirement of a specific intention which we mentioned. But there is no evidence for it because His statement (the Exalted) 'so head for pure earth' only indicates the intention of the earth upon which wiping follows, so it does not necessitate other than the considered intention. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it can be said: The intended meaning is the intention of earth for the sake of prayer, by the context of His statement 'and you did not find water', for it contains indication of the condition, as is not hidden. And the intention of hadath or janabah is not required, so if a junub person makes tayammum intending by it wudu, it suffices him. Thus it is related from Muhammad explicitly, as quoted in al-Tanajjis. And al-Jassas mentioned that there is no need for intention of purification, but only distinction is necessary, because tayammum for both occurs in the same form, so it is distinguished by intention like obligatory prayers. But it is not correct; there is need for intention so that tayammum occurs as purification. So when it occurs as purification, it is permissible for him to perform whatever he wishes, because conditions are considered by their existence only. Do you not see that if he makes tayammum for Asr, it is permissible to perform Dhuhr with it, unlike prayers. Thus in al-Khabaziyyah and others. And it is not hidden that the statement of Muhammad: 'If a junub makes tayammum intending by it wudu' means he intends by it purification of wudu, as you know from the requirement of intention of purification. And by what has been established, it is known that what is in al-Qunyah from his statement: 'There remained on the body of a junub a spot, then he had an hadath and made tayammum for both, it is permissible and he intends for both, because if he intends for one, the other remains without intention' is based on the statement of Abu Bakr al-Jassas, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the required intention (niyyah) for tayammum. The author first clarifies that if one makes tayammum for a funeral prayer fearing loss of the prayer despite having water, the tayammum becomes invalid after finishing, as it was made with water present. Then he states the school's position: a general intention (e.g., just intending tayammum) is insufficient; a specific intention (e.g., for an obligatory prayer or to remove hadath) is necessary. This is the relied-upon view (mu'tamad), contrary to a narration in al-Nawadir that a general intention suffices. The author notes that there is no explicit textual proof for requiring a specific intention; the verse 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' only indicates seeking the earth, not a particular intention. However, he argues that the context 'and you did not find water' implies the intention for prayer. Next, he addresses the ruling for a junub person: if he makes tayammum intending wudu (i.e., purification from minor impurity), it suffices for both janabah and hadath, because the intention of taharah is enough. This is based on a direct narration from Imam Muhammad. The author then critiques al-Jassas's view that no intention of purification is needed—only distinction between different types of tayammum—by analogizing to prayer intentions. He explains that tayammum must be intended as taharah; once it is valid, it can be used for any act. An example: tayammum made for Asr can be used for Dhuhr, unlike obligatory prayers which require specific niyyah per prayer. The passage ends by reconciling a problematic statement from al-Qunyah regarding a junub with a spot: the requirement to intend for both hadath and janabah is based on al-Jassas's opinion, not the school's relied-upon view.

Key Terms
نية التطهير (niyyat al-tathir): Intention of purification; the specific intention to become pure from hadath (minor or major) through tayammum.
نية التمييز (niyyat al-tamyiz): Intention of distinction; al-Jassas's view that one only needs to distinguish between types of tayammum (e.g., for hadath vs. janabah), not necessarily purify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mu'tamad, which of the following intentions makes tayammum valid?
A) Simply intending to perform tayammum.
B) Intending purification from impurity (niyyat al-tathir).
C) Intending to distinguish between minor and major impurity (niyyat al-tamyiz).
D) No intention is needed.

Key Takeaway
For tayammum, the Hanafi mu'tamad requires a specific intention for purification (niyyat al-tathir) or for a specific act; a general intention does not suffice.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on a Disbeliever's Tayammum: Intention and Condition of Islam
Ruling on the validity of tayammum for a disbeliever and the condition of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum, explain why it differs from wudu, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A disbeliever's tayammum is invalid because it requires a valid intention he cannot form; his wudu is valid because it does not.

This lesson examines the first major issue in the passage: why a disbeliever's tayammum is invalid while his wudu is not. The key is the role of intention (niyyah). We will explore the majority Hanafi position, Abu Yusuf's minority view, and the reasoning behind each, culminating in the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the base text claim
The base text states: 'The tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu.' Identify the two rulings and their contrast.
2
Identify the illa (cause) for the difference
Tayammum requires a specific intention (niyyah) for its validity; wudu does not require intention. Thus, a disbeliever's lack of valid intention invalidates tayammum but not wudu.
This is the core legal reasoning (ta'lil) of the Hanafi majority.
3
Locate the dalil for the condition of Islam
The text asserts that Islam is a condition (shart) for the occurrence of valid tayammum. The disbeliever is not 'ahl' (qualified) for intention that brings reward, so his tayammum is void.
The proof is based on the nature of intention and the status of the disbeliever.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf narrates that if a disbeliever makes tayammum intending Islam (qurbah), it is valid for becoming Muslim, but not for prayer. Understand his reasoning: the intention for Islam is a valid act of worship from him at that moment.
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject this; they hold the tayammum absolutely invalid.
5
Apply the tarjih (preponderance)
The author sides with the majority and rejects Abu Yusuf's view. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that a disbeliever's tayammum is invalid for all purposes.
The tarjih authority is al-Bada'i and later Hanafi masters.

Source Text

وروي عن أبي يوسف إذا تيمم ينوي الإسلام جاز حتى لو أسلم لا يجوز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم عند العامة، وعلى رواية أبي يوسف إن كان معناه للجنب كما هو الظاهر امتنع هذا التعليل .اهـ. أقول : وأنت خبير بأن قول الأولى فيما إذا كان الماء داخل المسجد، والثانية فيما إذا كان خارجه وقد مرت عن المحيط في شرح قول المصنف ولو جنبا أو حائضاً الخ». وحينئذ فما ادعاه المؤلف من جواز التيمم مع وجود الماء في كل ما لا تشترط له الطهارة وإن لم يكن مما يفوت إلى خلف دعوى بلا دليل لأن عبارة المبتغى محتملة كما علمت وكيف وأصل مشروعية التيمم إنما هي عند فقد الماء بالنص وما يخاف فوته لا إلى بدل فيه معنى فقد الماء حكماً، أما ما سواه فلا فقد فيه أصلاً فلا يجوز فعله قال في المنية ولو تيمم لمس المصحف أو لدخول المسجد عند وجود الماء والقدرة على استعماله فذلك التيمم ليس بشيء. قال البرهان إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحها: لأن التيمم إنما يجوز ويعتبر في الشرع عند عدم الماء حقيقة أو حكماً ولم يوجد واحد منهما فلا يجوز اهـ. قوله: (وتحقيقه) أي تحقيق ما قرره في البدائع وهذا التقرير أحسن مما أجاب به بعضهم من أن الردة تحبط ثواب العمل وذلك لا يمنع زوال الحدث كمن توضأ رياء فإن الحدث يزول به وإن كان لا يثاب على وضوئه اهـ. يجوز، فالحاصل أن تيمم الكافر غير صحيح مطلقاً للصلاة والإسلام وعند أبي يوسف صحيح للإسلام لا للصلاة لأنه نوى قربة مقصودة تصح منه في الحال ولنا أن الكافر ليس بأهل للنية فما يفتقر إليها لا منه، وهذا لأن النية تصير الفعل منتهضاً مسبباً للثواب ولا فعل يقع من الكافر كذلك حال الكفر ، ولذا صححنا وضوءه لعدم افتقاره إلى النية ولم يصححه الشافعي لما افتقر إليها عنده وهي قوله : (ولا تنقضه ردة أي لا ينقض التيمم ردة لما بين أن الإسلام عندنا شرط وقوع التيمم صحيحاً بين أن الإسلام ليس شرط بقائه على الصحة حتى لو تيمم المسلم ثم ارتد عن الإسلام ـ والعياذ بالله - ثم أسلم جاز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم لأن التيمم وقع طهارة صحيحة فلا يبطل بالردة لأن أثرها في إبطال العبادات والتيمم ليس بعبادة عندنا لكنه طهور وهي لا تبطل صفة الطهورية كما لا تبطل الوضوء واحتمال الحاجة باق لأنه مجبور على الإسلام والثابت بيقين يبقى لو هم الفائدة في أصول الشرع إلا أنه لم ينعقد طهارة مع الكفر لأن جعله طهارة للحاجة والحاجة زائلة للحال بيقين وغير الثابت بيقين لا يثبت لوهم الفائدة لما أن رجاء الإسلام منه على موجب ديانته واعتقاده منقطع والجبر على الإسلام منعدم، فهو الفرق بين الابتداء والبقاء. كذا قرره في البدائع وتحقيقه أن التيمم نفسه لا ينافيه الكفر وإنما ينافي شرطه وهو النية المشروطة في الابتداء وقد تحققت وتحقق التيمم كذلك، فالصفة الباقية بعده لو اعتبرت كنفسه لا يرفعها الكفر لأن الباقي حينئذ حكماً ليس هو النية بل الطهارة . تنبيه : مقتضى ما ذكروه أن الكافر إذا توضأ أو تيمم لا يكون مسلماً به، وكذا قولهم في الإحرام إن الكافر إذا أحرم ثم أسلم فجدد الإحرام يجوز ، يقتضي أن لا يكون مسلماً بالإحرام لكن محله ما إذا لبى ولم يشهد المناسك، أما إذا لبى وشهد المناسك كلها مع المسلمين فإنه يكون مسلماً كما صرح به في المحيط. والأصل أن الكافر متى فعل عبادة فإن كانت موجودة في سائر الأديان فإنه لا يكون به مسلماً كالصلاة منفرداً والصوم والحج الذي ليس
His statement: (So the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu) means that due to the requirement of specific intention in tayammum, the tayammum of a disbeliever becomes invalid, and due to not requiring intention in wudu, his wudu is not invalidated. As for the first, because Islam is a condition for the occurrence of valid tayammum according to the general scholars, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if he makes tayammum intending Islam, it is permissible. Then even if he becomes Muslim, he cannot pray with that tayammum according to the majority. And according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, if its meaning is for a junub, as is apparent, this explanation is precluded. End. I say: And you are aware that the statement of al-Mubtagha with the existence of water determines its interpretation as for the one with minor hadath. Then I saw some virtuous objecting to al-Nahr, saying: The statement of al-Mubtagha with existence of water is either meant that the water is outside the mosque or inside. If the first, it is invalid, and if the second, it is correct but far from his wording, as evidence by his statement: 'And likewise for sleeping in it.' End. And it supports what we said. And it may be said: His statement 'And likewise for sleeping in it' means if he has a wet dream in the mosque and cannot exit, he makes tayammum for sleeping in it. So the first issue is when water is inside the mosque, and the second when it is outside. And it has passed from al-Muhit in explaining the author's statement 'And if junub or menstruating, etc.' And then what the author claimed of permissibility of tayammum with existence of water in everything that does not require purity, even if it is not something that would be missed, is a claim without evidence, because the wording of al-Mubtagha is probable as you know. And how so, the origin of legislation of tayammum is only when water is absent by text, and what is feared to be missed without substitute has the meaning of absence of water legally. As for other than that, there is no absence at all, so it is not permissible to do it. He said in al-Munyah: If one makes tayammum to touch the mushaf or to enter the mosque when water is present and he is able to use it, that tayammum is nothing. Al-Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi said in his commentary: Because tayammum is only permissible and considered in shari'ah when water is absent in reality or legally, and neither exists, so it is not permissible. End. His statement: (And its verification) i.e., verification of what was established in al-Bada'i, and this verification is better than what some responded with that apostasy invalidates the reward of the action, and that does not prevent the removal of hadath, like one who makes wudu with riya' (showing off) — the hadath is removed by it even if he is not rewarded for his wudu. End. It is permissible, so the conclusion is that the tayammum of a disbeliever is absolutely invalid for prayer and for Islam. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is valid for Islam, not for prayer, because he intended a desired act of worship that is valid from him at that time. And for us, the disbeliever is not qualified for intention, so what depends on intention is not from him. This is because intention makes the act effective as causing reward, and no act from a disbeliever occurs like that while in disbelief. Hence we accept his wudu as valid because it does not depend on intention, while al-Shafi'i does not accept it because it depends on intention according to him. And his statement: (And apostasy does not nullify it) i.e., apostasy does not nullify the tayammum, because it is established that for us Islam is a condition for the occurrence of valid tayammum, but Islam is not a condition for its continuity of validity. So if a Muslim makes tayammum, then apostatizes from Islam — may Allah protect us — then becomes Muslim again, it is permissible for him to pray with that tayammum because the tayammum occurred as a valid purification, so it is not invalidated by apostasy. Because the effect of apostasy is to invalidate acts of worship, and tayammum is not an act of worship according to us; rather it is a means of purification, and it does not nullify the quality of being a purifier, just as it does not nullify wudu. And the possibility of need remains because he is compelled to Islam, and what is established with certainty remains even if one imagines a benefit from it in the principles of sharia. However, it did not become valid as purification during disbelief because its being made purification is due to need, and the need is gone with certainty at that time, and what is not established with certainty cannot be established by imagining benefit, because hope for his Islam from him is cut off according to his religion and belief, and compulsion to Islam is nonexistent. So this is the difference between initiation and continuity. Thus it was established in al-Bada'i. And its verification: That tayammum itself is not incompatible with disbelief; rather, what is incompatible is its condition, which is the required intention in the beginning. And it has been realized, and tayammum has occurred as such. So the remaining attribute after it, if considered as itself, disbelief does not remove it, because what remains at that time legally is not the intention, but rather purification. A note: The implication of what they mentioned is that if a disbeliever performs wudu or tayammum, he does not become Muslim by it. Likewise, their statement regarding ihram: if a disbeliever assumes ihram, then becomes Muslim, then renews ihram, it is permissible. This implies that he does not become Muslim by the ihram. However, its scope is if he recites talbiyah but does not witness the rituals. But if he recites talbiyah and witnesses all the rituals with the Muslims, then he becomes Muslim, as clearly stated in al-Muhit. And the principle: that whenever a disbeliever performs an act of worship, if it is found in other religions, he does not become Muslim by it, like praying alone, fasting, and hajj that is not...
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof covering two related issues: the validity of tayammum by a disbeliever, and the effect of apostasy on a valid tayammum. First, the author explains a comment on the base text: 'The tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu.' The reason is that tayammum requires a specific intention (niyyah), and Islam is a condition for the validity of that intention; wudu does not require intention, so it remains valid. There is a narration from Abu Yusuf that if a disbeliever makes tayammum intending Islam (i.e., to become Muslim), it is valid for that purpose, but he still cannot pray with it. The author then critiques al-Mubtagha's view that tayammum is allowed even with water present for certain acts (like sleeping in the mosque) by analyzing the context. The reliable position is that tayammum is only legitimate when water is absent in reality or legally (e.g., fear of missing prayer). For acts like touching the mushaf or entering the mosque, tayammum is invalid when water is present. Second, regarding apostasy: the text establishes that if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, and later returns to Islam, the tayammum remains valid. This is because tayammum is a purification (tuhur), not an act of worship ('ibadah). Apostasy nullifies acts of worship but does not remove the state of purification. The author contrasts this with wudu, which also remains valid after apostasy. The key insight is that Islam is a condition for the initial validity of tayammum, not for its continuation. The passage concludes with a note (tanbih) that a disbeliever does not become Muslim merely by performing wudu or tayammum, nor by ihram alone unless he completes the pilgrimage rituals with the Muslims.

Key Terms
نية التمييز (niyyat al-tamyiz): Not directly used in this passage, but relevant: intention of distinction; the idea that tayammum for different reasons (e.g., hadath vs. janabah) must be distinguished by intention.
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion of Islam. In this passage, it is discussed whether it nullifies the validity of a previously performed tayammum.
طهور (tuhur): Purification; the quality of being a purifier. For tayammum and water, they are legally considered purifiers that remove hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum?
A) It is valid for prayer if he intends Islam.
B) It is invalid for all purposes.
C) It is valid for becoming Muslim but not for prayer.
D) It is valid only if water is absent and he is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's tayammum is invalid because it requires an intention he cannot form; his wudu is valid because it does not require intention.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
Effect of Apostasy on a Valid Tayammum: Continuity of Purification
Ruling on whether apostasy nullifies a validly performed tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why apostasy does not nullify a valid tayammum according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish between initial conditions (shart al-wuqu') and continuity conditions (shart al-baqa').

Core Idea
Islam is a condition for the initial validity of tayammum, not its continuity; apostasy does not break purification.

This lesson examines the second key issue in the passage: whether apostasy abrogates a previously valid tayammum. The Hanafi school holds that it does not, based on a crucial distinction between purification (tuhur) and worship (ibadah). We will trace the reasoning from al-Bada'i and understand the principle of shart al-wuqu' vs. shart al-baqa'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on apostasy
The base text states: 'And apostasy does not nullify it' (ولا تنقضه ردة). Identify that the ruling is that a valid tayammum remains valid after apostasy.
2
Understand the distinction: purification vs. worship
The text explains that tayammum is a purification (tuhur), not an act of worship ('ibadah). Apostasy nullifies acts of worship but does not remove the state of purification.
This is the core reason for the ruling.
3
Apply the principle: shart al-wuqu' vs. shart al-baqa'
Islam is a condition for the initial occurrence (shart al-wuqu') of valid tayammum, but not for its continuity (shart al-baqa'). Once tayammum is validly performed, it remains effective.
This is the formalisation from al-Bada'i.
4
Compare with wudu and the analogy of riya'
Similarly, wudu remains valid after apostasy. The text gives the example of wudu done with riya' (showing off): the hadath is removed even if there is no reward.
This reinforces that reward and purification are separate.
5
Respond to the counterargument
Some argued that apostasy invalidates the reward, thus the act is void. The Hanafi response is that even if reward is lost, the state of purification remains, just like wudu with riya'.
The passage affirms that the certainty of the purification remains.

Source Text

قوله : (فلغا تيمم كافر لا وضوءه) يعني فلأجل اشتراط النية المخصوصة في التيمم بطل تيمم كافر، ولعدم اشتراط النية في الوضوء لا يبطل وضوءه، أما الأول فلأن الإسلام شرط وقوع التيمم صحيحاً عند عامة العلماء وروي عن أبي يوسف إذا تيمم ينوي الإسلام جاز حتى لو أسلم لا يجوز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم عند العامة، وعلى رواية أبي يوسف إن كان معناه للجنب كما هو الظاهر امتنع هذا التعليل .اهـ. أقول : وأنت خبير بأن قول المبتغى مع وجود الماء يعين حمله على المحدث، ثم رأيت بعض الفضلاء اعترض على النهر فقال: إن قول المبتغى مع وجود الماء لا يخلو إما أن يكون المراد به أن الماء خارج المسجد أو داخله، فإن كان الأول فهو باطل، وإن كان الثاني فهو صحيح ولكنه بعيد من عبارته بدليل قوله وكذا للنوم فيه» اهـ. وهو يؤيد ما قلنا وقد يقال : إن قوله وكذا للنوم فيه معناه إذا احتلم في المسجد ولم يمكنه الخروج يتيمم للنوم فيه فتكون المسألة الأولى فيما إذا كان الماء داخل المسجد، والثانية فيما إذا كان خارجه وقد مرت عن المحيط في شرح قول المصنف ولو جنبا أو حائضاً الخ». وحينئذ فما ادعاه المؤلف من جواز التيمم مع وجود الماء في كل ما لا تشترط له الطهارة وإن لم يكن مما يفوت إلى خلف دعوى بلا دليل لأن عبارة المبتغى محتملة كما علمت وكيف وأصل مشروعية التيمم إنما هي عند فقد الماء بالنص وما يخاف فوته لا إلى بدل فيه معنى فقد الماء حكماً، أما ما سواه فلا فقد فيه أصلاً فلا يجوز فعله قال في المنية ولو تيمم لمس المصحف أو لدخول المسجد عند وجود الماء والقدرة على استعماله فذلك التيمم ليس بشيء. قال البرهان إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحها: لأن التيمم إنما يجوز ويعتبر في الشرع عند عدم الماء حقيقة أو حكماً ولم يوجد واحد منهما فلا يجوز اهـ. قوله: (وتحقيقه) أي تحقيق ما قرره في البدائع وهذا التقرير أحسن مما أجاب به بعضهم من أن الردة تحبط ثواب العمل وذلك لا يمنع زوال الحدث كمن توضأ رياء فإن الحدث يزول به وإن كان لا يثاب على وضوئه اهـ. يجوز، فالحاصل أن تيمم الكافر غير صحيح مطلقاً للصلاة والإسلام وعند أبي يوسف صحيح للإسلام لا للصلاة لأنه نوى قربة مقصودة تصح منه في الحال ولنا أن الكافر ليس بأهل للنية فما يفتقر إليها لا منه، وهذا لأن النية تصير الفعل منتهضاً مسبباً للثواب ولا فعل يقع من الكافر كذلك حال الكفر ، ولذا صححنا وضوءه لعدم افتقاره إلى النية ولم يصححه الشافعي لما افتقر إليها عنده وهي قوله : (ولا تنقضه ردة أي لا ينقض التيمم ردة لما بين أن الإسلام عندنا شرط وقوع التيمم صحيحاً بين أن الإسلام ليس شرط بقائه على الصحة حتى لو تيمم المسلم ثم ارتد عن الإسلام ـ والعياذ بالله - ثم أسلم جاز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم لأن التيمم وقع طهارة صحيحة فلا يبطل بالردة لأن أثرها في إبطال العبادات والتيمم ليس بعبادة عندنا لكنه طهور وهي لا تبطل صفة الطهورية كما لا تبطل الوضوء واحتمال الحاجة باق لأنه مجبور على الإسلام والثابت بيقين يبقى لو هم الفائدة في أصول الشرع إلا أنه لم ينعقد طهارة مع الكفر لأن جعله طهارة للحاجة والحاجة زائلة للحال بيقين وغير الثابت بيقين لا يثبت لوهم الفائدة لما أن رجاء الإسلام منه على موجب ديانته واعتقاده منقطع والجبر على الإسلام منعدم، فهو الفرق بين الابتداء والبقاء. كذا قرره في البدائع وتحقيقه أن التيمم نفسه لا ينافيه الكفر وإنما ينافي شرطه وهو النية المشروطة في الابتداء وقد تحققت وتحقق التيمم كذلك، فالصفة الباقية بعده لو اعتبرت كنفسه لا يرفعها الكفر لأن الباقي حينئذ حكماً ليس هو النية بل الطهارة . تنبيه : مقتضى ما ذكروه أن الكافر إذا توضأ أو تيمم لا يكون مسلماً به، وكذا قولهم في الإحرام إن الكافر إذا أحرم ثم أسلم فجدد الإحرام يجوز ، يقتضي أن لا يكون مسلماً بالإحرام لكن محله ما إذا لبى ولم يشهد المناسك، أما إذا لبى وشهد المناسك كلها مع المسلمين فإنه يكون مسلماً كما صرح به في المحيط. والأصل أن الكافر متى فعل عبادة فإن كانت موجودة في سائر الأديان فإنه لا يكون به مسلماً كالصلاة منفرداً والصوم والحج الذي ليس
His statement: (So the tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu) means that due to the requirement of specific intention in tayammum, the tayammum of a disbeliever becomes invalid, and due to not requiring intention in wudu, his wudu is not invalidated. As for the first, because Islam is a condition for the occurrence of valid tayammum according to the general scholars, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if he makes tayammum intending Islam, it is permissible. Then even if he becomes Muslim, he cannot pray with that tayammum according to the majority. And according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, if its meaning is for a junub, as is apparent, this explanation is precluded. End. I say: And you are aware that the statement of al-Mubtagha with the existence of water determines its interpretation as for the one with minor hadath. Then I saw some virtuous objecting to al-Nahr, saying: The statement of al-Mubtagha with existence of water is either meant that the water is outside the mosque or inside. If the first, it is invalid, and if the second, it is correct but far from his wording, as evidence by his statement: 'And likewise for sleeping in it.' End. And it supports what we said. And it may be said: His statement 'And likewise for sleeping in it' means if he has a wet dream in the mosque and cannot exit, he makes tayammum for sleeping in it. So the first issue is when water is inside the mosque, and the second when it is outside. And it has passed from al-Muhit in explaining the author's statement 'And if junub or menstruating, etc.' And then what the author claimed of permissibility of tayammum with existence of water in everything that does not require purity, even if it is not something that would be missed, is a claim without evidence, because the wording of al-Mubtagha is probable as you know. And how so, the origin of legislation of tayammum is only when water is absent by text, and what is feared to be missed without substitute has the meaning of absence of water legally. As for other than that, there is no absence at all, so it is not permissible to do it. He said in al-Munyah: If one makes tayammum to touch the mushaf or to enter the mosque when water is present and he is able to use it, that tayammum is nothing. Al-Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi said in his commentary: Because tayammum is only permissible and considered in shari'ah when water is absent in reality or legally, and neither exists, so it is not permissible. End. His statement: (And its verification) i.e., verification of what was established in al-Bada'i, and this verification is better than what some responded with that apostasy invalidates the reward of the action, and that does not prevent the removal of hadath, like one who makes wudu with riya' (showing off) — the hadath is removed by it even if he is not rewarded for his wudu. End. It is permissible, so the conclusion is that the tayammum of a disbeliever is absolutely invalid for prayer and for Islam. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is valid for Islam, not for prayer, because he intended a desired act of worship that is valid from him at that time. And for us, the disbeliever is not qualified for intention, so what depends on intention is not from him. This is because intention makes the act effective as causing reward, and no act from a disbeliever occurs like that while in disbelief. Hence we accept his wudu as valid because it does not depend on intention, while al-Shafi'i does not accept it because it depends on intention according to him. And his statement: (And apostasy does not nullify it) i.e., apostasy does not nullify the tayammum, because it is established that for us Islam is a condition for the occurrence of valid tayammum, but Islam is not a condition for its continuity of validity. So if a Muslim makes tayammum, then apostatizes from Islam — may Allah protect us — then becomes Muslim again, it is permissible for him to pray with that tayammum because the tayammum occurred as a valid purification, so it is not invalidated by apostasy. Because the effect of apostasy is to invalidate acts of worship, and tayammum is not an act of worship according to us; rather it is a means of purification, and it does not nullify the quality of being a purifier, just as it does not nullify wudu. And the possibility of need remains because he is compelled to Islam, and what is established with certainty remains even if one imagines a benefit from it in the principles of sharia. However, it did not become valid as purification during disbelief because its being made purification is due to need, and the need is gone with certainty at that time, and what is not established with certainty cannot be established by imagining benefit, because hope for his Islam from him is cut off according to his religion and belief, and compulsion to Islam is nonexistent. So this is the difference between initiation and continuity. Thus it was established in al-Bada'i. And its verification: That tayammum itself is not incompatible with disbelief; rather, what is incompatible is its condition, which is the required intention in the beginning. And it has been realized, and tayammum has occurred as such. So the remaining attribute after it, if considered as itself, disbelief does not remove it, because what remains at that time legally is not the intention, but rather purification. A note: The implication of what they mentioned is that if a disbeliever performs wudu or tayammum, he does not become Muslim by it. Likewise, their statement regarding ihram: if a disbeliever assumes ihram, then becomes Muslim, then renews ihram, it is permissible. This implies that he does not become Muslim by the ihram. However, its scope is if he recites talbiyah but does not witness the rituals. But if he recites talbiyah and witnesses all the rituals with the Muslims, then he becomes Muslim, as clearly stated in al-Muhit. And the principle: that whenever a disbeliever performs an act of worship, if it is found in other religions, he does not become Muslim by it, like praying alone, fasting, and hajj that is not...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof covering two related issues: the validity of tayammum by a disbeliever, and the effect of apostasy on a valid tayammum. First, the author explains a comment on the base text: 'The tayammum of a disbeliever is invalid, not his wudu.' The reason is that tayammum requires a specific intention (niyyah), and Islam is a condition for the validity of that intention; wudu does not require intention, so it remains valid. There is a narration from Abu Yusuf that if a disbeliever makes tayammum intending Islam (i.e., to become Muslim), it is valid for that purpose, but he still cannot pray with it. The author then critiques al-Mubtagha's view that tayammum is allowed even with water present for certain acts (like sleeping in the mosque) by analyzing the context. The reliable position is that tayammum is only legitimate when water is absent in reality or legally (e.g., fear of missing prayer). For acts like touching the mushaf or entering the mosque, tayammum is invalid when water is present. Second, regarding apostasy: the text establishes that if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes, and later returns to Islam, the tayammum remains valid. This is because tayammum is a purification (tuhur), not an act of worship ('ibadah). Apostasy nullifies acts of worship but does not remove the state of purification. The author contrasts this with wudu, which also remains valid after apostasy. The key insight is that Islam is a condition for the initial validity of tayammum, not for its continuation. The passage concludes with a note (tanbih) that a disbeliever does not become Muslim merely by performing wudu or tayammum, nor by ihram alone unless he completes the pilgrimage rituals with the Muslims.

Key Terms
نية التمييز (niyyat al-tamyiz): Not directly used in this passage, but relevant: intention of distinction; the idea that tayammum for different reasons (e.g., hadath vs. janabah) must be distinguished by intention.
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion of Islam. In this passage, it is discussed whether it nullifies the validity of a previously performed tayammum.
طهور (tuhur): Purification; the quality of being a purifier. For tayammum and water, they are legally considered purifiers that remove hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of apostasy on a valid tayammum?
A) It invalidates the tayammum completely.
B) It nullifies the reward but the tayammum remains valid as purification.
C) It only invalidates if the apostasy was intentional.
D) It invalidates the tayammum but wudu is unaffected.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy does not remove the state of purification; a valid tayammum remains effective after returning to Islam.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Disbeliever's Tayammum and Apostasy's Effect
Explains rulings on disbeliever's tayammum and apostasy's effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and apply the distinction between initiation and continuance of tayammum to a scenario involving apostasy.

Core Idea
A disbeliever's tayammum is invalid; but a Muslim's valid tayammum persists after apostasy.

This lesson examines two interrelated issues: the validity of a disbeliever's tayammum and whether apostasy nullifies a previously valid tayammum. We will explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and uncover the school's reasoning that distinguishes between the initiation of tayammum (which requires Islam and intention) and its continuance (which does not). By the end, you will be able to apply this distinction to real cases.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on a disbeliever's tayammum. Abu Hanifa says it is absolutely invalid; Abu Yusuf says it is valid for embracing Islam but not for prayer.
2
Analyze the proofs
Examine the dalil for each position. Abu Hanifa argues that a disbeliever lacks the capacity for intention (niyyah), which is a requirement for tayammum. Abu Yusuf argues that a disbeliever can intend an immediate act of devotion (qurbah).
Pay attention to how the source supports Abu Hanifa's view as 'our argument'.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: if a disbeliever performs tayammum and then becomes Muslim, according to Abu Yusuf he may use that tayammum for prayer, but according to Abu Hanifa he must perform a new tayammum.
This distinction matters for fatwa.
4
Apply the initiation vs. continuance principle
Understand why apostasy does not nullify tayammum: Islam is a condition for the validity of tayammum at its start (initiation), but not for its continued validity (continuance). Tayammum is a purifier, not an act of worship, so apostasy only nullifies worship, not purification.
This principle is key to the second part of the passage.
