كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
٢٦٥
يجوز، فالحاصل أن تيمم الكافر غير صحيح مطلقاً للصلاة والإسلام وعند أبي يوسف صحيح للإسلام لا للصلاة لأنه نوى قربة مقصودة تصح منه في الحال ولنا أن الكافر ليس بأهل للنية فما يفتقر إليها لا منه، وهذا لأن النية تصير الفعل منتهضاً مسبباً للثواب ولا فعل
يصح
المسألة الثانية .
يقع من الكافر كذلك حال الكفر ، ولذا صححنا وضوءه لعدم افتقاره إلى النية ولم يصححه الشافعي لما افتقر إليها عنده وهي قوله : (ولا تنقضه ردة أي لا ينقض التيمم ردة لما بين أن الإسلام عندنا شرط وقوع التيمم صحيحاً بین أن الإسلام ليس شرط بقائه على الصحة حتى لو تيمم المسلم ثم ارتد عن الإسلام ـ والعياذ بالله - ثم أسلم جاز له أن يصلي بذلك التيمم لأن التيمم وقع طهارة صحيحة فلا يبطل بالردة لأن أثرها في إبطال العبادات والتيمم ليس بعبادة عندنا لكنه طهور وهي لا تبطل صفة الطهورية كما لا تبطل الوضوء واحتمال الحاجة باق لأنه مجبور على الإسلام والثابت بيقين يبقى لو هم الفائدة في أصول الشرع إلا أنه لم ينعقد طهارة مع الكفر لأن جعله طهارة للحاجة والحاجة زائلة للحال بيقين وغير الثابت بيقين لا يثبت لوهم الفائدة لما أن رجاء الإسلام منه على موجب ديانته واعتقاده منقطع والجبر على الإسلام منعدم، فهو الفرق بين الابتداء والبقاء. كذا قرره في البدائع وتحقيقه أن التيمم نفسه لا ينافيه الكفر وإنما ينافي شرطه وهو النية المشروطة في الابتداء وقد تحققت وتحقق التيمم كذلك، فالصفة الباقية بعده لو اعتبرت كنفسه لا يرفعها الكفر لأن الباقي حينئذ حكماً ليس هو النية بل
الطهارة .
تنبيه : مقتضى ما ذكروه أن الكافر إذا توضأ أو تيمم لا يكون مسلماً به، وكذا قولهم في الإحرام إن الكافر إذا أحرم ثم أسلم فجدد الإحرام يجوز ، يقتضي أن لا يكون مسلماً بالإحرام لكن محله ما إذا لبى ولم يشهد المناسك، أما إذا لبى وشهد المناسك كلها مع المسلمين فإنه يكون مسلماً كما صرح به في المحيط. والأصل أن الكافر متى فعل عبادة فإن كانت موجودة في سائر الأديان فإنه لا يكون به مسلماً كالصلاة منفرداً والصوم والحج الذي ليس
بلا دليل لأن عبارة المبتغى محتملة كما علمت وكيف وأصل مشروعية التيمم إنما هي عند فقد الماء بالنص وما يخاف فوته لا إلى بدل فيه معنى فقد الماء حكماً، أما ما سواه فلا فقد فيه أصلاً فلا يجوز فعله قال في المنية ولو تيمم لمس المصحف أو لدخول المسجد عند وجود الماء والقدرة على استعماله فذلك التيمم ليس بشيء. قال البرهان إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحها: لأن التيمم إنما يجوز ويعتبر في الشرع عند عدم الماء حقيقة أو حكماً ولم يوجد واحد منهما فلا يجوز اهـ. قوله: (وتحقيقه) أي تحقيق ما قرره في البدائع وهذا التقرير أحسن مما أجاب به بعضهم من أن الردة تحبط ثواب العمل وذلك لا يمنع زوال الحدث كمن توضأ رياء فإن الحدث يزول به وإن كان لا يثاب على وضوئه اهـ.
Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. Page 265. [The text says:] It is permissible. So the conclusion is that the tayammum of a disbeliever is absolutely invalid for prayer and for [embracing] Islam. According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid for Islam but not for prayer, because he intended an intended act of devotion that is sound from him at that moment. Our argument: The disbeliever is not qualified for intention, so what requires it is not from him. This is because intention makes the action effective, causing reward, and no action of a disbeliever is sound in that state. Second issue: It occurs from a disbeliever in that state of disbelief, and thus we validated his ablution (wudu) because it does not require intention, but al-Shafi'i did not validate it because it requires intention in his view. His statement: 'And apostasy does not nullify it' meaning apostasy does not nullify tayammum because Islam in our view is a condition for the occurrence of tayammum validly, but not a condition for its continued validity. So if a Muslim performs tayammum, then apostatizes - God forbid - and then becomes Muslim, he may pray with that tayammum because the tayammum occurred as a valid purification. It is not invalidated by apostasy because its effect is on invalidating acts of worship, and tayammum in our view is not worship but a purifier. Apostasy does not invalidate the quality of purification, just as it does not invalidate wudu. The potential need remains because he is compelled to Islam. What is established with certainty remains even if benefit is imagined in the principles of the law, except that it did not become purification with disbelief because making it purification is due to need, and the need is certainly absent at present. What is not established with certainty does not occur due to imagined benefit, because hope of his Islam based on his religion and belief is cut off, and compulsion to Islam is absent. So this is the distinction between initiation and continuance. This is settled in Al-Bada'i'. And its verification: Tayammum itself is not incompatible with disbelief; rather, what is incompatible is its condition, which is the intention required at the beginning. That intention has occurred, and so tayammum is realized. Therefore, the remaining quality after it, if considered like itself, is not removed by disbelief because what remains at that point is not intention but purification. Note: The implication of what they mentioned is that if a disbeliever performs wudu or tayammum, he does not become Muslim by it. Similarly, their statement about ihram: If a disbeliever enters ihram, then becomes Muslim, then renews ihram, it is permissible. This would imply that he does not become Muslim by ihram. But its scope is when he recites the talbiyah but does not witness the rituals. However, if he recites the talbiyah and witnesses all the rituals with the Muslims, then he becomes Muslim, as stated in Al-Muhit. The principle: When a disbeliever performs an act of worship, if it exists in other religions, he does not become Muslim by it, such as praying alone, fasting, and hajj that is not[?] without evidence because the phrase of Al-Mughta is possible as you know. How so? The origin of legislating tayammum is only in the absence of water by text, and what is feared to be lost without a substitute has the meaning of absence of water legally. But besides that, there is no absence at all, so it is not permissible to do it. He said in Al-Munya: 'And if he performs tayammum for touching the Quran or entering the mosque while water exists and he is able to use it, that tayammum is nothing.' Al-Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi said in his commentary: 'Because tayammum is only permissible and valid in the law when water is absent in reality or legally, and neither exists, so it is not permissible.' End quote. His statement: 'And its verification' meaning the verification of what was settled in Al-Bada'i', and this exposition is better than what some answered: that apostasy cancels the reward of the deed, and that does not prevent the removal of ritual impurity, like one who performs wudu with ostentation; impurity is removed by it even if he is not rewarded for his wudu.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with two interrelated issues: the validity of a disbeliever's tayammum, and whether apostasy nullifies a valid tayammum. The author first clarifies the position of the Hanafi school. According to Abu Hanifa, a disbeliever's tayammum is absolutely invalid, whether intended for prayer or for embracing Islam. The reason given is that a disbeliever is not qualified for valid intention (niyyah), which is a required condition for tayammum. Abu Yusuf differs: he holds that a disbeliever's tayammum can be valid for embracing Islam because he can have a valid intention for a qurbah (act of devotion) that is immediately accessible, but not for prayer because prayer requires purification by a valid act. The author then supports Abu Hanifa's view. Next, the text addresses the effect of apostasy on a previously valid tayammum. The school's position is that apostasy does not nullify tayammum because tayammum is not a pure act of worship but a purifier (tuhur). Since worship (ibadah) is nullified by apostasy, but purification is not, the tayammum remains valid. The author provides a detailed reasoning, distinguishing between the initiation of tayammum (which requires Islam as a condition) and its continuance (which does not). The passage ends with a note on how a disbeliever may become Muslim by performing certain communal rituals like collective prayer or hajj, but not by tayammum alone.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
نية (niyyah): Intentional resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah; in tayammum, it is a condition for validity according to the majority.
ردة (ridda): Apostasy from Islam; it nullifies acts of worship (ibadat) but not purification (tahara).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on a disbeliever's tayammum performed before embracing Islam?
A) It is valid for prayer but not for embracing Islam
B) It is valid for embracing Islam but not for prayer
C) It is absolutely invalid
D) It is valid if he intended to become Muslim

Key Takeaway
A disbeliever's tayammum is invalid from the start due to lack of valid intention; but a Muslim's valid tayammum remains valid even after apostasy because tayammum is a purifier, not an act of worship.

Nullifiers of Tayammum and the Meaning of 'Finding Water'
Details what nullifies tayammum and interprets 'finding water' in the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nullifiers of tayammum and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'finding water' as ability to use (qudra).

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by ability to use sufficient water, not by mere sight or ownership.

Tayammum, as a substitute for wudu or ghusl, is invalidated by the same events that break wudu. Additionally, the moment a person becomes able to use enough water for purification, tayammum ceases to exist. But what exactly does 'finding water' in the Quran mean? In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the Hanafi school clarifies that it means having the physical capability to use water, not merely owning or seeing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifiers of tayammum
From the passage, list the two main causes that nullify tayammum: (1) any event that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind, urination), and (2) having the ability to use sufficient water for purification.
The first nullifier connects to the principle that the substitute follows the original in rulings.
2
Interpret the Quranic verse
Focus on the Quranic phrase 'فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً' (and you find no water) from Surah al-Ma'idah. The Hanafis interpret 'find' as 'ability to use', not mere sight or ownership.
This interpretation is based on the context of necessity: tayammum is allowed only when one is unable to use water.
3
Distinguish between wujud in tayammum and kaffarat
The author points out that 'wujud' (existence) in tayammum means ability (qudra), while in expiations (kaffarat) it means ownership (milk). Thus, if water is merely permitted to you (e.g., public water), you are considered able and cannot do tayammum.
This distinction prevents incorrect analogy between the two contexts.
4
Apply the sufficiency condition
The water must be sufficient for the obligatory parts of wudu. If the water is insufficient (e.g., only enough for one wash per limb), tayammum is not nullified according to the chosen view, provided the person uses it only once per limb.
The passage cites Al-Khulasa for the ruling that three or two washes indicate sufficient water, while one wash does not.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi debate on wording
The author critiques the expression 'nullifiers of wudu' for tayammum, arguing that the proper phrase is 'nullifiers of the original (wudu or ghusl)' because tayammum can be for janabah as well. However, he concludes both expressions are equivalent since anything that nullifies ghusl also nullifies wudu.
This is a subtle linguistic point, not affecting the ruling.

[Page 266] Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. Apostasy rather, but the nullifier of wudu and the ability to use water surplus to one's need: these prevent tayammum and raise it. And one who hopes for water... fully and charity. And whenever he does what is specific to our law, if it is from the means like tayammum, he does not become Muslim by it. If it is from the ends or the rituals like congregational prayer, hajj in complete form, the call to prayer in the mosque, and reciting the Quran, then he becomes Muslim by it, as referred to in Al-Muhit and other books of Siyar. His statement: 'Rather, the nullifier of wudu' meaning it is nullified by the actual and legal nullifiers of wudu that precede wudu, because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and without doubt the status of the substitute is below that of the original, so whatever invalidates the higher is even more likely to invalidate the lower. What is found in Sharh al-Nuqaya that it is better to say 'It is nullified by the nullifiers of the original, whether wudu or ghusl' is not accepted, because it is known that whatever nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, so the two expressions are equivalent, as is not hidden. Know that if one performs tayammum for janabah and then incurs a hadath that nullifies wudu, then his tayammum is nullified by that hadath, so the rulings of hadath apply, not those of janabah; he is in a state of minor impurity, not major. His statement: 'And the ability to use water surplus to his need' meaning that the ability to use sufficient water in excess of his need also nullifies it. We restricted it to 'sufficient' because other water is like non-existent, as we have stated. So if one performing tayammum finds water and uses it for wudu but it is insufficient for one of his feet, if he washed each limb three times or twice, his tayammum is nullified—that is the chosen view—but if only once, it is not nullified because in the former case he found water sufficient for him, since if he limited himself to one wash it would suffice. This is in Al-Khulasa. We restricted it to 'surplus' because if it is not surplus to his need, it is occupied by his need and is like non-existent, as we explained. In his statement 'ability to use water' there are two indications: first, that the 'existence' mentioned in the verse 'and you find no water' means ability, unlike the 'existence' mentioned in expiations which means ownership, so that if water is permitted to him, he may not perform tayammum due to ability; but if a destitute person who has broken an oath is offered a slave, he may expiate by other than manumission. Second, that the expression 'ability' is preferable to the expression 'seeing water' which is conditional on ability to use it. Because there was an objection: one who prays, then apostatizes, then becomes Muslim within the time must repeat the prayer even if the reward is nullified, not the act; otherwise he would not repeat the prayer since there is no difference between his prayer and his wudu. Some said: It can be answered that apostasy nullifies what is purely worship, not anything else. Prayer is pure worship, so it is nullified in reward and act, necessitating its repetition. As for wudu, it is a specific purification prescribed for permitting prayer, not pure worship, but it becomes worship through intention. Apostasy nullifies its being worship, not its being purification, so wudu and tayammum remain as purifications that permit prayer, as is clear. End quote from Fara'id. His statement: 'the two expressions are equivalent' is debatable because although everything that nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies ghusl, because wudu is nullified by hadath, which does not nullify ghusl. This is indicated by what he himself mentioned after his statement: 'Know that if he performs tayammum for janabah...' Then he says that wudu nullified what did not nullify janabah. So his statement 'it is nullified' meaning tayammum is nullified by the nullifiers of wudu entirely, and Allah knows best. Thus it becomes clear the preference for the expression 'the original' instead of 'wudu' to cover tayammum for hadath and janabah. This is in Al-Munh and similar in Al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues the commentary on the nullifiers of tayammum. The author establishes that tayammum is nullified by the same things that nullify wudu (like urine, wind, etc.), because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and the substitute's rulings follow the original. Additionally, the ability to use sufficient water (qadir 'ala al-ma') nullifies tayammum. The author clarifies that 'sufficient' water means enough for the obligatory parts of wudu, and 'surplus' means beyond what is needed for essential uses like drinking. If the water is insufficient (e.g., only enough for one wash of each limb), tayammum remains valid according to the chosen view because the available water is not considered sufficient. The passage also delves into the interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'فلم تجدوا ماء' (and you find no water) from Surah al-Ma'idah. The author argues that 'finding' here means 'ability to use' (qudra), not mere ownership or sight. This differs from expiations (kaffarat), where 'finding' means ownership. Therefore, if water is available but not owned (e.g., permitted to use without ownership), tayammum is invalid due to ability. The author also discusses the effect of apostasy on wudu and tayammum, reinforcing that apostasy nullifies the worship aspect but not the purification aspect, so wudu and tayammum remain valid as purifiers. Finally, a subtle point is made about the scope of nullifiers: tayammum for janabah is nullified by the nullifiers of wudu (not necessarily of ghusl), because the nullifier of wudu (minor hadath) does not nullify ghusl entirely but does nullify the substitute tayammum.

Key Terms
ناقض (naqid): Something that nullifies or invalidates the state of purification (taharah), nullifier.
قدرة (qudra): Ability or capability to use water, as opposed to mere ownership or sight.
وجود (wujud): Existence, but in the context of tayammum, it is interpreted as qudra (ability to use), not mere availability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It means the water is in one's possession

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is nullified by the ability to use sufficient water, and the Quranic 'finding water' must be understood as ability to use, not mere sight or ownership.

Nullifiers of Tayammum: The Substitution Principle and Ability to Use Water
Ruling with proof and elaboration on the nullifiers of tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of nullifiers of tayammum and explain the Hanafi criteria for ability to use water, including the detail about washing twice/thrice versus once.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by any nullifier of wudu and by the ability to use sufficient surplus water.

This lesson explores what nullifies tayammum. Since tayammum is a substitute for wudu, anything that nullifies wudu also nullifies tayammum. Additionally, tayammum is lifted when one gains the ability to use enough water for purification, with specific conditions about sufficiency and surplus. The passage also clarifies that 'finding water' in the Quran means having the ability to use it, not merely seeing it or owning it, and discusses the effect of apostasy on the validity of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two nullifier categories
The passage states that tayammum is nullified by (1) any nullifier of wudu (real or legal) and (2) the ability to use sufficient surplus water. Identify these from the text.
The author explains why nullifiers of wudu also apply: tayammum is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu, so what invalidates the original is more likely to invalidate the substitute.
2
Analyze the condition of ability
The nullifier of ability is specified: water must be sufficient (enough for purification) and surplus (not needed for other essential uses). The text gives an example: if one finds water, performs wudu, but it falls short for one foot, the tayammum is nullified only if he washed each limb two or three times (because one wash would have sufficed).
The chosen view (mukhtar) is that if he did two or three washes, the tayammum is nullified; if only one wash, it is not nullified.
3
Distinguish the two indications from 'ability of water'
First: 'finding water' in the tayammum verse means ability (qudrah), not ownership (milk). In expiation oaths, 'finding' means ownership. Second: the expression 'ability of water' is better than 'seeing water' because ability covers cases like illness or cold where the permitter (the excuse) ceases, even if water is not seen.
The passage uses the example of one who prays, apostatizes, then returns to Islam: his prayer is repeated because apostasy nullifies worship, but his wudu/tayammum remain valid as purification, not worship.
4
Understand the effect of apostasy
Apostasy nullifies the worship aspect (thawab and 'amal) of acts like prayer, but not the purification aspect of wudu/tayammum. So tayammum performed before apostasy remains valid for future prayers after return.
This is an important distinction: tayammum is both a purification and an act of worship, but apostasy only removes the worship element.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi debate on wording
The author critiques the view that the nullifier should be expressed as 'a nullifier of the original (wudu or ghusl)' instead of 'a nullifier of wudu'. He argues both are equivalent because everything that nullifies ghusl also nullifies wudu, but not vice versa. The preference is for 'original' to cover tayammum for both hadath and janabah.
This discussion shows the careful attention to precise legal wording in Hanafi fiqh.

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
ردة بل ناقض الوضوء وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه وراجي الماء بكامل والصدقة ومتى فعل ما هو مختص بشريعتنا فإن كان من الوسائل كالتيمم لا يكون به مسلماً، وإن كان من المقاصد أو من الشعائر كالصلاة بجماعة والحج على الهيئة الكاملة والأذان في المسجد وقراءة القرآن فإنه يكون به مسلماً إليه أشار في المحيط وغيره من كتاب السير قوله : (بل ناقض الوضوء) أي بل ينقضه ناقض الوضوء الحقيقي والحكمي المتقدمان الوضوء لأن التيمم خلف عن الوضوء، ولا شك أن حال الخلف دون حال الأصل، فما كان مبطلاً للأعلى فأولى أن يكون مبطلاً للأدنى. وما وقع في شرح النقاية من أن الأحسن أن يقال وينقضه ناقض الأصل وضوءاً كان أو غسلاً فغير مسلم، لأن من المعلوم أن كل شيء نقض الغسل نقض الوضوء، فالعبارتان على السواء كما لا يخفى واعلم أنه إذا تيمم عن جنابة وأحدث حدثاً ينقض الوضوء فإن تيممه ينتقض باعتبار الحدث فتثبت أحكام الحدث لا أحكام الجنابة فإنه محدث وليس بجنب.
قوله (وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته أي وينقضه أيضاً القدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي الفاضل عن حاجته . قيدنا بالكافي لأن غيره وجوده كعدمه وقد قدمناه. فلو وجد المتيمم ماء فتوضأ به فنقص عن إحدى رجليه إن كان غسل كل عضو ثلاثاً أو مرتين انتقض تيممه وهو المختار، أو مرة لا ينتقض لأن في الأول وجد ماء يكفيه إذ لو اقتصر على المرة كفاه . كذا في الخلاصة. وقيدنا بالفاضل لأنه لو لم يكن فاضلاً عنها فهو مشغول بها وهو كالمعدوم كما بيناه. وفي قوله وقدرة ماء» اشارتان: الأولى إفادة أن الوجود المذكور في قوله تعالى «فلم تجدوا ماء» بمعنى القدرة بخلاف الوجود المذكور في الكفارات فإنه بمعنى الملك حتى لو أبيح له الماء لا يجوز له التيمم للقدرة ولو عرض على المعسر الحانث الرقبة يجوز له التكفير بغير الإعتاق. الثانية أن التعبير بالقدرة أولى من التعبير برؤية الماء المشروطة القدرة على استعماله لأنه اعترض عليه بأن من صلى ثم ارتد ثم أسلم في الوقت يعيدها ولو حبط الثواب لا العمل لما أعاد الصلاة إذ لا فرق حينئذ بين صلاته ووضوئه. قال بعضهم : ويمكن الجواب بأن الردة تحبط ما هو عبادة لا غير والصلاة عبادة محضة فحبطت ثواباً وعملاً فيلزم إعادتها. وأما الوضوء فطهارة مخصوصة شرطت لاستباحة الصلاة وليس بعبادة محضة لكنه يصير عبادة بالنية، فالردة تحبط كون الوضوء عبادة لا كونه طهارة فيبقى الوضوء والتيمم من حيث إنهما طهارتان تصح بهما الصلاة كما لا يخفي . اهـ فرائد. قوله : فالعبارتان على السواء) فيه كلام لأنه وإن نقض الوضوء كل شيء نقض الغسل لكن لا ينقض الغسل كل ما نقض الوضوء فإن الوضوء ينقضه الحدث وهو لا ينقض الغسل، يدل عليه ما ذكره بنفسه بعدما ذكر من قوله واعلم أنه إذا تيمم عن جنابة الخ فقد نقض الوضوء ما لم ينقض الجنابة فلم يقع قوله وينقضه» أي التيمم ناقض الوضوء كلياً والله تعالى أعلم، فظهر بهذا أولوية التعبير بالأصل بدلاً . عن الوضوء لشموله التيمم عن الحدث والجنابة. كذا في المنح ونحوه في النهر .

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
كما وقع في الهداية، لأن القدرة أعم من أن تكون برؤية الماء أو بغيره، فإن المريض إذا تيمم للمرض ثم زال مرضه انتقض تيممه كما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه. ومن تيمم للبرد ثم زال البرد انتقض تيممه كما صرح به في المبتغى. فإذا تيمم للمرض أو للبرد مع وجود الماء ثم فقد الماء ثم زال المرض أو البرد ينتقض تيممه لقدرته على استعمال الماء وإن لم يكن الماء موجوداً. فالحاصل أن كل ما منع وجوده التيمم نقض وجوده التيمم، وما لا فلا. فلو قالوا وينقضه زوال ما أباح التيمم لكان أظهر في المراد، وإسناد النقض إلى زوال ما أباح التيمم إسناد مجازي لأن الناقض حقيقة إنما هو الحدث السابق بخروج النجس، وزوال المبيح شرط لعمل الحدث السابق عمله عنده واستدلوا له بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم التراب طهور المسلم ولو إلى عشر حجج ما لم يجد الماء» (۱) لأن مقتضاه خروج ذلك التراب الذي تيمم به من الطهورية إذا وجد الماء، ويستلزم انتفاء أثره وهو طهارة المتيمم لكن قال في فتح القدير: ويرد عليه أن قطع الاعتبار الشرعي طهورية التراب إنما هو عند الرؤية مقتصراً فإنما يظهر في المستقبل إذ لو استند ظهر عدم صحة الصلوات السابقة وما قيل إنه وصف يرجع إلى المحل فيستوي فيه الابتداء والبقاء لا يفيد دفعاً ولا يمسه والأوجه الاستدلال بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بقية الحديث «فإذا وجده فليمسه بشرته». وفي إطلاقه دلالة على نفي تخصيص الناقضية بالوجدان خارج الصلاة هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة .اهـ. فالحاصل أن الحديث لا يفيد إلا انتهاء الطهورية بوجود الماء، ولا يلزم من انتهاء الطهورية انتهاء الطهارة الحاصلة به كالماء تزول عنه الطهورية بالاستعمال وتبقى الطهارة الحاصلة به والجواب بالفرق بينهما وهو أن التراب طهوريته مؤقتة بشيء غير متصل به وهو وجود الماء فتثبت به الطهارة المؤقتة الحاصلة على صفة المطهر، فإذا زالت طهوريته زالت طهارته. والماء لما كان مطهراً ولا تزول طهوريته بدون شيء يتصل به ثبت به الطهارة على التأبيد لأن طهوريته إذا لم يتصل بها شيء على التأبيد إليه أشار في الخبازية. ولا يخفى أنه لا يلزم من توقيت الطهورية تأقيت الطهارة بل هو عين النزاع، فالأوجه الاستدلال ببقية الحديث كما في فتح القدير تبعاً لما في المستصفى والحديث المذكور مروي في المصابيح. والتقييد بعشر حجج لبيان طول المدة لا للتقييد به كما في قوله تعالى أن تستغفر لهم سبعين مرة [التوبة : ۸۰] فإنه لبيان الكثرة لا للتحديد كذا في المستصفى. وقال بعض الأفاضل ؛ قولهم إن الحدث السابق ناقض حقيقة لا يناسب قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأن كما
قوله: (فلو قالوا وينقضه زوال ما أباح التيمم) أي بدل قولهم وقدرة ماء لكان أظهر الخ» قوله : لكان أظهر في المراد) قال في الدرر وعليه لو تيمم لبعده ميلاً فسار فانتقص انتقض اهـ. قوله :
Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. Apostasy? But it nullifies wudu and ability of water surplus to his need, so it prevents tayammum and raises it, and one hoping for water in full, and charity, and whenever he does what is specific to our Shariah, if it is from the means like tayammum, he does not become a Muslim by it; if it is from the ends or from the rituals like congregational prayer, Hajj in complete manner, adhan in the mosque, and recitation of Quran, then he becomes a Muslim by it. Alluded to in al-Muhit and others from Kitab al-Siyar. His saying: (But it nullifies wudu) meaning it is nullified by the real and legal nullifier of wudu that preceded, because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and there is no doubt that the state of the substitute is inferior to the original, so what invalidates the higher is more likely to invalidate the lower. What is in Sharh al-Niqayah that the best is to say: 'And it is nullified by a nullifier of the original, whether wudu or ghusl' is not accepted, because it is known that everything that nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, so the two expressions are equal as is not hidden. And know that if he performed tayammum for janabah and then committed a hadath that nullifies wudu, his tayammum is nullified in consideration of the hadath, so the rulings of hadath are established, not the rulings of janabah, for he is in the state of minor impurity, not junub. His saying: (and ability of water surplus to his need) meaning it is also nullified by ability to use sufficient water, surplus to his need. We qualified with 'sufficient' because otherwise its existence is like non-existence, as we have preceded. So if the one performing tayammum finds water and performs wudu with it but it falls short for one of his feet, if he washed each limb three times or twice, his tayammum is nullified—and that is the chosen view—or if once, it is not nullified, because in the first case he found water sufficient for him, since if he had limited himself to one wash it would have sufficed him. Thus in al-Khulasa. And we qualified with 'surplus' because if it is not surplus, then it is occupied with it and is like non-existent as we explained. In his saying 'ability of water' there are two indications: first, that the existence mentioned in the verse 'you did not find water' means ability, unlike the existence mentioned in expiations where it means ownership, so that even if water is made permissible for him, tayammum is not permissible due to ability; and if a slave is presented to a destitute who has broken an oath, it is permissible for him to expiate by other than manumission. Second, that the expression 'ability' is more appropriate than the expression 'seeing water' which is conditioned on ability to use it, because an objection was raised that one who prays then apostatizes then becomes Muslim within the time repeats it, and if the reward was nullified but not the action, he would not repeat the prayer, since there would then be no difference between his prayer and his wudu. Some said: it can be answered that apostasy nullifies what is purely worship, and prayer is pure worship, so it nullifies reward and action, thus requiring repetition. As for wudu, it is a specific purification conditioned for permission of prayer and is not pure worship, but it becomes worship by intention. So apostasy nullifies the aspect of wudu as worship, not its aspect as purification, so wudu and tayammum remain as purifications by which prayer is valid, as is not hidden. End of Fara'id. His saying: 'the two expressions are equal' is debatable. Because although everything that nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies ghusl. For wudu is nullified by hadath, which does not nullify ghusl. Evidence is what he himself mentioned after, from his saying 'and know that if he performed tayammum for janabah...' for wudu was nullified while janabah was not. So his saying 'and it is nullified' i.e. tayammum, by a nullifier of wudu is not absolute, and Allah knows best. Thus the preference of the expression 'the original' instead of 'wudu' becomes apparent, for it includes tayammum for hadath and janabah. Thus in al-Munyah and similarly in al-Nahr. As occurred in al-Hidayah, because ability is more general than being by seeing water or otherwise. For if a sick person performs tayammum due to illness and then his illness ceases, his tayammum is nullified, as Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa. And one who performs tayammum for cold and then the cold ceases, his tayammum is nullified, as stated in al-Muntagha. So if he performed tayammum for illness or cold while water was present, then water was lost, then the illness or cold ceased, his tayammum is nullified due to his ability to use water even if water is not present. So the conclusion is that whatever prevented its existence nullifies tayammum by its existence, and what doesn't, doesn't. So if they said 'and it is nullified by the removal of what permitted tayammum' it would be more apparent in meaning, and attributing nullification to the removal of what permitted tayammum is metaphorical, because the real nullifier is the prior hadath by the exit of impurity, and the removal of the permitter is a condition for the action of the prior hadath in his view. And they used as evidence his statement peace be upon him: 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim, even for ten years, as long as he does not find water' because its implication is that the earth with which he performed tayammum exits from being a purifier when he finds water, and it necessitates the negation of its effect, which is the purification of the one performing tayammum. But in Fath al-Qadir: it is objected that the removal of legal validity of the purifying nature of earth is only at the time of seeing water, with restriction, and it only appears in the future; if it were retroactive, previous prayers would be invalid, and what is said that it is a description referring to the locus, so it applies to beginning and continuation, does not help nor touch. And the most correct is to use as evidence the rest of the hadith: 'And when he finds it, let him touch it to his skin.' And its generality indicates the negation of restricting nullification to finding water outside prayer; it is the saying of the three Imams. So the hadith only indicates the end of the purifying nature with finding water, and it does not necessarily follow from the end of the purifying nature the end of the purification obtained by it, like water: its purifying nature is removed by use, but the purification obtained by it remains. And the answer is the difference between them: the purifying nature of earth is temporary by something not connected to it, namely the existence of water, so the temporary purification is established in the form of purifier; so when its purifying nature ceases, its purification ceases. Water, since it is a purifier and its purifying nature does not cease without something connected to it, purification is established with it permanently, because its purifying nature is not connected to anything, as pointed out in al-Khabbaziyya. It is not hidden that it does not necessarily follow from the temporariness of the purifying nature the temporariness of purification; rather that is the very dispute. So the most correct is to use the rest of the hadith as evidence, as in Fath al-Qadir, following al-Mustasfa. And the hadith mentioned is narrated in al-Masabih. And the restriction to ten years is to indicate the length of the period, not to restrict it, as in the verse 'seek forgiveness for them seventy times' [9:80] which is to indicate abundance, not limitation. Thus in al-Mustasfa. And some virtuous scholars said: their saying that the prior hadath is the real nullifier does not conform to the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because as
His saying: (so if they said 'and it is nullified by the removal of what permitted tayammum') i.e. instead of their saying 'ability of water' it would be more apparent. His saying: 'it would be more apparent in meaning' – said in al-Durar: accordingly, if he performed tayammum due to a distance of a mile, then traveled and it decreased, it is nullified. End. His saying:

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the nullifiers of tayammum. The author first clarifies that the nullifier of wudu (real or legal) also nullifies tayammum because tayammum is a substitute for wudu; what invalidates the original more strongly invalidates the substitute. He rejects the alternative phrasing in Sharh al-Niqayah, arguing that everything that nullifies ghusl also nullifies wudu, so both expressions are equivalent. He then explains that if one performs tayammum for janabah and then has a minor hadath, only the hadath nullifies the tayammum; he becomes in a state of minor impurity, not janabah. Next, he discusses the nullifier of ability to use sufficient water that is surplus to one's water needs. He details that if one finds water, performs wudu, but it is insufficient for one foot, the tayammum is nullified if the person used two or three washes per limb (since one wash would have sufficed), but not nullified if only one wash was used. He also explains two indications from the phrase 'ability of water': first, that 'finding' in the Quran means ability, not ownership; second, that ability is a better term than 'seeing water' because it covers cases like illness or cold that may cease, making water accessible without sight. He discusses apostasy: it does not nullify the purification aspect of wudu or tayammum, only the worship aspect, so previous tayammum remains valid. The passage then debates the appropriate wording for the nullifier: some suggest 'removal of what permitted tayammum' is more accurate than 'ability of water', and the author finds this more apparent. He cites the hadith 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim...' and addresses the dispute over whether nullification is future-only or retroactive, siding with the Hanafi view that it is only future, as the purifying nature of earth ends upon finding water, but purification already obtained remains valid. He draws an analogy with water itself: used water loses its purifying property but the purification from it remains. The key point is the Hanafi position that tayammum is nullified by ability to use water (or removal of the permitter) from that point forward, not retroactively.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.
ناقض (naqid): A nullifier; something that invalidates the state of purity (wudu, ghusl, or tayammum).
قدرة (qudrah): Ability; the capacity to use water, which nullifies tayammum even if water is not physically seen but accessible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person performs tayammum for janabah and then passes wind?
A) He becomes junub again and must perform ghusl.
B) He is in a state of minor impurity only and needs wudu.
C) His tayammum remains valid because it was for janabah.
D) He must repeat both tayammum and ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is nullified by any nullifier of wudu and by the ability to use sufficient surplus water; previous prayers remain valid.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
The Preferred Wording and the Dispute on Retroactivity of Nullification
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on the elaboration of the nullifier.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers the phrase 'removal of what permitted tayammum' over 'ability of water', and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute on whether finding water nullifies tayammum retroactively.

Core Idea
The Hanafis hold that nullification of tayammum is forward-only, not retroactive, and that the proper expression is 'removal of what permitted tayammum'.

This lesson examines the precise wording of the nullifier and the key hadith evidence. The Hanafi school argues that the nullifier is more accurately described as the 'removal of what permitted tayammum' (zawaal ma abah al-tayammum) rather than 'ability of water', because the permitter (like illness, cold, or absence of water) can cease even without water being present. The lesson also addresses the major inter-madhhab dispute: does finding water retroactively invalidate prayers performed with tayammum? The Hanafi position, based on the hadith and analogical reasoning, is that nullification is only for the future.

Guided Path
1
Understand the preference for 'removal of what permitted tayammum'
The passage argues that the nullifier is better expressed as 'removal of what permitted tayammum' because ability to use water is just one case. Examples: a sick person who recovers, or one who performed tayammum for cold and then it becomes warm. In such cases, the permitter (illness/cold) is removed, so tayammum is nullified even if water is not present.
The author cites Qadikhan and al-Muntagha for the ruling that illness and cold cessation nullify tayammum.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim even for ten years as long as he does not find water' is used to argue that finding water ends the purifying nature of earth. The Hanafis respond that this only shows end of purifying nature from that point, not retroactively. The continuation 'when he finds it, let him touch it to his skin' indicates action after finding, not nullification of past acts.
The passage cites Fath al-Qadir and al-Mustasfa for the preferred interpretation.
3
Distinguish between tayammum and water analogy
The objection is: water loses its purifying quality after use but the purification remains. So why does earth not similarly retain its effect? The answer: earth's purifying nature is temporary and tied to the absence of water, while water's purifying nature is permanent until something (like use) removes it.
The analogy is used by opponents to argue for retroactivity; the Hanafis reject it based on the difference in how the purifying nature is attached.
4
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i and other schools (the 'three Imams') hold that finding water nullifies tayammum retroactively, so prayers performed with tayammum become invalid. They interpret the hadith's generality. Hanafis respond that the hadith only indicates future nullification, and that retroactivity leads to hardship and is not supported by the text.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: Hanafis do not require repeating prayers; Shafi'is do.

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
ردة بل ناقض الوضوء وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه وراجي الماء بكامل والصدقة ومتى فعل ما هو مختص بشريعتنا فإن كان من الوسائل كالتيمم لا يكون به مسلماً، وإن كان من المقاصد أو من الشعائر كالصلاة بجماعة والحج على الهيئة الكاملة والأذان في المسجد وقراءة القرآن فإنه يكون به مسلماً إليه أشار في المحيط وغيره من كتاب السير قوله : (بل ناقض الوضوء) أي بل ينقضه ناقض الوضوء الحقيقي والحكمي المتقدمان الوضوء لأن التيمم خلف عن الوضوء، ولا شك أن حال الخلف دون حال الأصل، فما كان مبطلاً للأعلى فأولى أن يكون مبطلاً للأدنى. وما وقع في شرح النقاية من أن الأحسن أن يقال وينقضه ناقض الأصل وضوءاً كان أو غسلاً فغير مسلم، لأن من المعلوم أن كل شيء نقض الغسل نقض الوضوء، فالعبارتان على السواء كما لا يخفى واعلم أنه إذا تيمم عن جنابة وأحدث حدثاً ينقض الوضوء فإن تيممه ينتقض باعتبار الحدث فتثبت أحكام الحدث لا أحكام الجنابة فإنه محدث وليس بجنب.
قوله (وقدرة ماء فضل عن حاجته أي وينقضه أيضاً القدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي الفاضل عن حاجته . قيدنا بالكافي لأن غيره وجوده كعدمه وقد قدمناه. فلو وجد المتيمم ماء فتوضأ به فنقص عن إحدى رجليه إن كان غسل كل عضو ثلاثاً أو مرتين انتقض تيممه وهو المختار، أو مرة لا ينتقض لأن في الأول وجد ماء يكفيه إذ لو اقتصر على المرة كفاه . كذا في الخلاصة. وقيدنا بالفاضل لأنه لو لم يكن فاضلاً عنها فهو مشغول بها وهو كالمعدوم كما بيناه. وفي قوله وقدرة ماء» اشارتان: الأولى إفادة أن الوجود المذكور في قوله تعالى «فلم تجدوا ماء» بمعنى القدرة بخلاف الوجود المذكور في الكفارات فإنه بمعنى الملك حتى لو أبيح له الماء لا يجوز له التيمم للقدرة ولو عرض على المعسر الحانث الرقبة يجوز له التكفير بغير الإعتاق. الثانية أن التعبير بالقدرة أولى من التعبير برؤية الماء المشروطة القدرة على استعماله لأنه اعترض عليه بأن من صلى ثم ارتد ثم أسلم في الوقت يعيدها ولو حبط الثواب لا العمل لما أعاد الصلاة إذ لا فرق حينئذ بين صلاته ووضوئه. قال بعضهم : ويمكن الجواب بأن الردة تحبط ما هو عبادة لا غير والصلاة عبادة محضة فحبطت ثواباً وعملاً فيلزم إعادتها. وأما الوضوء فطهارة مخصوصة شرطت لاستباحة الصلاة وليس بعبادة محضة لكنه يصير عبادة بالنية، فالردة تحبط كون الوضوء عبادة لا كونه طهارة فيبقى الوضوء والتيمم من حيث إنهما طهارتان تصح بهما الصلاة كما لا يخفي . اهـ فرائد. قوله : فالعبارتان على السواء) فيه كلام لأنه وإن نقض الوضوء كل شيء نقض الغسل لكن لا ينقض الغسل كل ما نقض الوضوء فإن الوضوء ينقضه الحدث وهو لا ينقض الغسل، يدل عليه ما ذكره بنفسه بعدما ذكر من قوله واعلم أنه إذا تيمم عن جنابة الخ فقد نقض الوضوء ما لم ينقض الجنابة فلم يقع قوله وينقضه» أي التيمم ناقض الوضوء كلياً والله تعالى أعلم، فظهر بهذا أولوية التعبير بالأصل بدلاً . عن الوضوء لشموله التيمم عن الحدث والجنابة. كذا في المنح ونحوه في النهر .

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
كما وقع في الهداية، لأن القدرة أعم من أن تكون برؤية الماء أو بغيره، فإن المريض إذا تيمم للمرض ثم زال مرضه انتقض تيممه كما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه. ومن تيمم للبرد ثم زال البرد انتقض تيممه كما صرح به في المبتغى. فإذا تيمم للمرض أو للبرد مع وجود الماء ثم فقد الماء ثم زال المرض أو البرد ينتقض تيممه لقدرته على استعمال الماء وإن لم يكن الماء موجوداً. فالحاصل أن كل ما منع وجوده التيمم نقض وجوده التيمم، وما لا فلا. فلو قالوا وينقضه زوال ما أباح التيمم لكان أظهر في المراد، وإسناد النقض إلى زوال ما أباح التيمم إسناد مجازي لأن الناقض حقيقة إنما هو الحدث السابق بخروج النجس، وزوال المبيح شرط لعمل الحدث السابق عمله عنده واستدلوا له بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم التراب طهور المسلم ولو إلى عشر حجج ما لم يجد الماء» (۱) لأن مقتضاه خروج ذلك التراب الذي تيمم به من الطهورية إذا وجد الماء، ويستلزم انتفاء أثره وهو طهارة المتيمم لكن قال في فتح القدير: ويرد عليه أن قطع الاعتبار الشرعي طهورية التراب إنما هو عند الرؤية مقتصراً فإنما يظهر في المستقبل إذ لو استند ظهر عدم صحة الصلوات السابقة وما قيل إنه وصف يرجع إلى المحل فيستوي فيه الابتداء والبقاء لا يفيد دفعاً ولا يمسه والأوجه الاستدلال بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بقية الحديث «فإذا وجده فليمسه بشرته». وفي إطلاقه دلالة على نفي تخصيص الناقضية بالوجدان خارج الصلاة هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة .اهـ. فالحاصل أن الحديث لا يفيد إلا انتهاء الطهورية بوجود الماء، ولا يلزم من انتهاء الطهورية انتهاء الطهارة الحاصلة به كالماء تزول عنه الطهورية بالاستعمال وتبقى الطهارة الحاصلة به والجواب بالفرق بينهما وهو أن التراب طهوريته مؤقتة بشيء غير متصل به وهو وجود الماء فتثبت به الطهارة المؤقتة الحاصلة على صفة المطهر، فإذا زالت طهوريته زالت طهارته. والماء لما كان مطهراً ولا تزول طهوريته بدون شيء يتصل به ثبت به الطهارة على التأبيد لأن طهوريته إذا لم يتصل بها شيء على التأبيد إليه أشار في الخبازية. ولا يخفى أنه لا يلزم من توقيت الطهورية تأقيت الطهارة بل هو عين النزاع، فالأوجه الاستدلال ببقية الحديث كما في فتح القدير تبعاً لما في المستصفى والحديث المذكور مروي في المصابيح. والتقييد بعشر حجج لبيان طول المدة لا للتقييد به كما في قوله تعالى أن تستغفر لهم سبعين مرة [التوبة : ۸۰] فإنه لبيان الكثرة لا للتحديد كذا في المستصفى. وقال بعض الأفاضل ؛ قولهم إن الحدث السابق ناقض حقيقة لا يناسب قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأن كما
قوله: (فلو قالوا وينقضه زوال ما أباح التيمم) أي بدل قولهم وقدرة ماء لكان أظهر الخ» قوله : لكان أظهر في المراد) قال في الدرر وعليه لو تيمم لبعده ميلاً فسار فانتقص انتقض اهـ. قوله :
Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. Apostasy? But it nullifies wudu and ability of water surplus to his need, so it prevents tayammum and raises it, and one hoping for water in full, and charity, and whenever he does what is specific to our Shariah, if it is from the means like tayammum, he does not become a Muslim by it; if it is from the ends or from the rituals like congregational prayer, Hajj in complete manner, adhan in the mosque, and recitation of Quran, then he becomes a Muslim by it. Alluded to in al-Muhit and others from Kitab al-Siyar. His saying: (But it nullifies wudu) meaning it is nullified by the real and legal nullifier of wudu that preceded, because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and there is no doubt that the state of the substitute is inferior to the original, so what invalidates the higher is more likely to invalidate the lower. What is in Sharh al-Niqayah that the best is to say: 'And it is nullified by a nullifier of the original, whether wudu or ghusl' is not accepted, because it is known that everything that nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, so the two expressions are equal as is not hidden. And know that if he performed tayammum for janabah and then committed a hadath that nullifies wudu, his tayammum is nullified in consideration of the hadath, so the rulings of hadath are established, not the rulings of janabah, for he is in the state of minor impurity, not junub. His saying: (and ability of water surplus to his need) meaning it is also nullified by ability to use sufficient water, surplus to his need. We qualified with 'sufficient' because otherwise its existence is like non-existence, as we have preceded. So if the one performing tayammum finds water and performs wudu with it but it falls short for one of his feet, if he washed each limb three times or twice, his tayammum is nullified—and that is the chosen view—or if once, it is not nullified, because in the first case he found water sufficient for him, since if he had limited himself to one wash it would have sufficed him. Thus in al-Khulasa. And we qualified with 'surplus' because if it is not surplus, then it is occupied with it and is like non-existent as we explained. In his saying 'ability of water' there are two indications: first, that the existence mentioned in the verse 'you did not find water' means ability, unlike the existence mentioned in expiations where it means ownership, so that even if water is made permissible for him, tayammum is not permissible due to ability; and if a slave is presented to a destitute who has broken an oath, it is permissible for him to expiate by other than manumission. Second, that the expression 'ability' is more appropriate than the expression 'seeing water' which is conditioned on ability to use it, because an objection was raised that one who prays then apostatizes then becomes Muslim within the time repeats it, and if the reward was nullified but not the action, he would not repeat the prayer, since there would then be no difference between his prayer and his wudu. Some said: it can be answered that apostasy nullifies what is purely worship, and prayer is pure worship, so it nullifies reward and action, thus requiring repetition. As for wudu, it is a specific purification conditioned for permission of prayer and is not pure worship, but it becomes worship by intention. So apostasy nullifies the aspect of wudu as worship, not its aspect as purification, so wudu and tayammum remain as purifications by which prayer is valid, as is not hidden. End of Fara'id. His saying: 'the two expressions are equal' is debatable. Because although everything that nullifies ghusl nullifies wudu, not everything that nullifies wudu nullifies ghusl. For wudu is nullified by hadath, which does not nullify ghusl. Evidence is what he himself mentioned after, from his saying 'and know that if he performed tayammum for janabah...' for wudu was nullified while janabah was not. So his saying 'and it is nullified' i.e. tayammum, by a nullifier of wudu is not absolute, and Allah knows best. Thus the preference of the expression 'the original' instead of 'wudu' becomes apparent, for it includes tayammum for hadath and janabah. Thus in al-Munyah and similarly in al-Nahr. As occurred in al-Hidayah, because ability is more general than being by seeing water or otherwise. For if a sick person performs tayammum due to illness and then his illness ceases, his tayammum is nullified, as Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa. And one who performs tayammum for cold and then the cold ceases, his tayammum is nullified, as stated in al-Muntagha. So if he performed tayammum for illness or cold while water was present, then water was lost, then the illness or cold ceased, his tayammum is nullified due to his ability to use water even if water is not present. So the conclusion is that whatever prevented its existence nullifies tayammum by its existence, and what doesn't, doesn't. So if they said 'and it is nullified by the removal of what permitted tayammum' it would be more apparent in meaning, and attributing nullification to the removal of what permitted tayammum is metaphorical, because the real nullifier is the prior hadath by the exit of impurity, and the removal of the permitter is a condition for the action of the prior hadath in his view. And they used as evidence his statement peace be upon him: 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim, even for ten years, as long as he does not find water' because its implication is that the earth with which he performed tayammum exits from being a purifier when he finds water, and it necessitates the negation of its effect, which is the purification of the one performing tayammum. But in Fath al-Qadir: it is objected that the removal of legal validity of the purifying nature of earth is only at the time of seeing water, with restriction, and it only appears in the future; if it were retroactive, previous prayers would be invalid, and what is said that it is a description referring to the locus, so it applies to beginning and continuation, does not help nor touch. And the most correct is to use as evidence the rest of the hadith: 'And when he finds it, let him touch it to his skin.' And its generality indicates the negation of restricting nullification to finding water outside prayer; it is the saying of the three Imams. So the hadith only indicates the end of the purifying nature with finding water, and it does not necessarily follow from the end of the purifying nature the end of the purification obtained by it, like water: its purifying nature is removed by use, but the purification obtained by it remains. And the answer is the difference between them: the purifying nature of earth is temporary by something not connected to it, namely the existence of water, so the temporary purification is established in the form of purifier; so when its purifying nature ceases, its purification ceases. Water, since it is a purifier and its purifying nature does not cease without something connected to it, purification is established with it permanently, because its purifying nature is not connected to anything, as pointed out in al-Khabbaziyya. It is not hidden that it does not necessarily follow from the temporariness of the purifying nature the temporariness of purification; rather that is the very dispute. So the most correct is to use the rest of the hadith as evidence, as in Fath al-Qadir, following al-Mustasfa. And the hadith mentioned is narrated in al-Masabih. And the restriction to ten years is to indicate the length of the period, not to restrict it, as in the verse 'seek forgiveness for them seventy times' [9:80] which is to indicate abundance, not limitation. Thus in al-Mustasfa. And some virtuous scholars said: their saying that the prior hadath is the real nullifier does not conform to the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because as
His saying: (so if they said 'and it is nullified by the removal of what permitted tayammum') i.e. instead of their saying 'ability of water' it would be more apparent. His saying: 'it would be more apparent in meaning' – said in al-Durar: accordingly, if he performed tayammum due to a distance of a mile, then traveled and it decreased, it is nullified. End. His saying:

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the nullifiers of tayammum. The author first clarifies that the nullifier of wudu (real or legal) also nullifies tayammum because tayammum is a substitute for wudu; what invalidates the original more strongly invalidates the substitute. He rejects the alternative phrasing in Sharh al-Niqayah, arguing that everything that nullifies ghusl also nullifies wudu, so both expressions are equivalent. He then explains that if one performs tayammum for janabah and then has a minor hadath, only the hadath nullifies the tayammum; he becomes in a state of minor impurity, not janabah. Next, he discusses the nullifier of ability to use sufficient water that is surplus to one's water needs. He details that if one finds water, performs wudu, but it is insufficient for one foot, the tayammum is nullified if the person used two or three washes per limb (since one wash would have sufficed), but not nullified if only one wash was used. He also explains two indications from the phrase 'ability of water': first, that 'finding' in the Quran means ability, not ownership; second, that ability is a better term than 'seeing water' because it covers cases like illness or cold that may cease, making water accessible without sight. He discusses apostasy: it does not nullify the purification aspect of wudu or tayammum, only the worship aspect, so previous tayammum remains valid. The passage then debates the appropriate wording for the nullifier: some suggest 'removal of what permitted tayammum' is more accurate than 'ability of water', and the author finds this more apparent. He cites the hadith 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim...' and addresses the dispute over whether nullification is future-only or retroactive, siding with the Hanafi view that it is only future, as the purifying nature of earth ends upon finding water, but purification already obtained remains valid. He draws an analogy with water itself: used water loses its purifying property but the purification from it remains. The key point is the Hanafi position that tayammum is nullified by ability to use water (or removal of the permitter) from that point forward, not retroactively.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.
ناقض (naqid): A nullifier; something that invalidates the state of purity (wudu, ghusl, or tayammum).
قدرة (qudrah): Ability; the capacity to use water, which nullifies tayammum even if water is not physically seen but accessible.
زوال ما أباح التيمم (zawaal ma abah al-tayammum): Removal of what permitted tayammum; the preferred expression for the nullifier, encompassing all cases where the excuse for tayammum ceases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as argued in the passage, what does the phrase 'فإذا وجده فليمسه بشرته' (when he finds it, let him touch it to his skin) indicate?
A) That finding water immediately nullifies all previous acts of worship.
B) That the nullification of tayammum is effective only from that moment forward, not retroactively.
C) That touching water to the skin is obligatory upon finding it.
D) That tayammum is invalid if water is found during prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tayammum is nullified from the moment the permitter is removed, and this nullification is forward-only; any prayers performed before are valid.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Sleep and Acts of Worship
Rulings on sleep in acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prayer and sajdah tilawah when the person is asleep, and apply the rule that sleep does not prevent certain legal effects.

Core Idea
Sleep does not void legal capacity; a sleeping person's actions can still trigger obligations.

Sleep is a state of reduced consciousness but not a full exemption from legal responsibility. In this lesson, we examine a set of rulings from Bahr al-Raiq that show how acts performed while sleeping can affect the validity of worship, the obligation of prostration, and the duty to make up prayers. These examples illustrate the Hanafi principle that sleep does not strip a person of legal personality (ahliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Read each ruling in the sub-passage and identify exactly what the sleeping person does (speaks, recites, has a wet dream, sleeps through prayer time).
Note that each scenario is from a different chapter of fiqh.
2
Determine the effect
For each act, note the legal consequence: invalidation of prayer, obligation of sajdah, requirement to restart or make up prayer.
Some consequences are immediate; others become due after waking.
3
Extract the principle
Combine the rulings to see the common thread: sleep does not cancel legal responsibility (taklif) for acts performed while asleep, and some acts become binding upon waking.
Contrast with the common misconception that sleep removes all liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نائمة ثبتت حرمة الرضاع، وفيمن تكلم في صلاته وهو نائم فسدت صلاته، وفيمن قرأ في صلاته وهو نائم حالة القيام تعتبر تلك القراءة في رواية وفيمن تلا آية سجدة وهو نائم فسمعه رجل تلزمه السجدة وفيمن قرأ عند نائم آية السجدة فلما استيقظ أخبره يجب عليه أن يسجد في قول، وفيمن قرأها وهو نائم فلما استيقظ أخبر يلزم القاريء في قول، وفيمن حلف لا يكلم فلاناً فجاء الحالف وكلمه وهو نائم ولم يستيقظ الأصح حنثه، وفيمن مس مطلقته النائمة فإنه يصير مراجعاً، وفي نائم قبلته مطلقته الرجعية بشهوة يصير مراجعاً عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وفي امرأة أدخلت ذكره في فرجها وهو نائم ثبتت حرمة المصاهرة إذا علم بفعلها، وفي امرأة قبلت النائم بشهوة ثبتت حرمة المصاهرة إذا صدقها على الشهوة، وفي الاحتلام في الصلاة يوجب الاستقبال، وفيمن نام يوماً أو أكثر تصير الصلاة ديناً في ذمته، وفي عقد النكاح بحضرة النائمين يجوز في قول والأصح اشتراط السماع.
A sleeping woman establishes the prohibition of fosterage; one who speaks in his prayer while sleeping, his prayer is invalidated; one who recites in his prayer while sleeping in the standing state, that recitation is considered in one narration; one who recites a verse of prostration while sleeping and a man hears him, the prostration is obligatory upon the hearer; one who recites in front of a sleeping person a verse of prostration, then when the sleeper wakes and is informed, he must prostrate in one opinion; one who recites it while sleeping, then when he wakes and is informed, the recitation is binding in one opinion; one who swears not to speak to so-and-so, then the swearer comes and speaks to him while he is sleeping and he does not wake, the correct view is that he breaks his oath; one who touches his divorced wife while she is sleeping becomes a revoker; if a sleeping man is kissed by his revocably divorced wife with desire, he becomes a revoker according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad; if a woman inserts his organ into her vagina while he is sleeping, the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationship is established if he knows of her act; if a woman kisses a sleeping man with desire, the prohibition of marriage is established if she confirms the desire; a wet dream during prayer necessitates restarting; one who sleeps for a day or more, prayer becomes a debt upon him; the marriage contract in the presence of sleeping people is permissible in one view, but the correct view is that hearing is required.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage type is a collection of rulings demonstrating that sleep does not render a person legally inert. The author lists thirteen distinct scenarios from various chapters of fiqh—fosterage, prayer, oaths, divorce, marriage—to show that a sleeping person can be the subject of legal consequences. For example, a sleeping woman establishes fosterage (radaa') if she nurses; speaking in prayer while sleeping invalidates the prayer; a sleeping person can be a cause for sajdah tilawah; touching a sleeping divorced wife effects revocation (raj'ah); a wet dream requires restarting prayer. The issue of kissing a sleeping man by his revocably divorced wife involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that it effects revocation, while Muhammad holds it does not. Similarly, if a woman inserts a sleeping man's organ into her vagina, the prohibition of marriage is established only if he knows afterward. The list concludes with the rule that a marriage contract in the presence of sleeping people is valid provided they hear the contract. This passage serves to support the principle that in the context of tayammum, a sleeping person may be considered capable of knowing about water.

Key Terms
نائمة (nāʾimah): A sleeping woman
مراجعاً (murājiʿan): A revoker, a husband who takes back his wife during iddah.
حرمة المصاهرة (ḥurmat al-muṣāharah): Prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a sleeping person recites a verse of sajdah and a waking person hears it, who must perform sajdah tilawah?
A) The sleeping reciter, after waking
B) The hearer
C) Both
D) No one, because the reciter was asleep

Key Takeaway
Sleep does not nullify the legal effects of recitation; a sleeping person's recitation can obligate sajdah on others and on themselves upon waking.

Sleep and Family Law
Rulings on sleep in family law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rulings on fosterage, divorce revocation (raj'ah), marriage prohibition (hurmah), and marriage contract validity involving sleeping persons.

Core Idea
A sleeping person can be the subject of family law effects: fosterage, revocation, and marriage prohibitions.

Family law often requires conscious intent, but Hanafi fiqh recognizes that some effects can arise even when one party is asleep. This lesson examines rulings on a sleeping woman establishing fosterage, a sleeping divorced wife being revoked by touch, a sleeping man being kissed by his wife, and a marriage contract witnessed by sleeping people. These illustrate that sleep does not prevent the attachment of marital legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
List the scenarios
Read the sub-passage covering: sleeping woman and radaa', touching sleeping divorced wife, kissing sleeping husband (with dispute), intercourse with sleeping man, woman kissing sleeping man, marriage contract in presence of sleepers.
Each scenario has different conditions for the effect to occur.
2
Identify the condition for each effect
Note what triggers the legal effect: for fosterage, just the act of nursing; for revocation, touching with desire; for hurmah, knowledge after the act; for marriage contract, the sleeper must hear.
Some effects require awareness afterward, others do not.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Focus on the kissing case: Abu Yusuf says revocation occurs, Muhammad says no. Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The dispute hinges on whether the sleeping husband's state affects the legal consequence of the wife's action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نائمة ثبتت حرمة الرضاع، وفيمن تكلم في صلاته وهو نائم فسدت صلاته، وفيمن قرأ في صلاته وهو نائم حالة القيام تعتبر تلك القراءة في رواية وفيمن تلا آية سجدة وهو نائم فسمعه رجل تلزمه السجدة وفيمن قرأ عند نائم آية السجدة فلما استيقظ أخبره يجب عليه أن يسجد في قول، وفيمن قرأها وهو نائم فلما استيقظ أخبر يلزم القاريء في قول، وفيمن حلف لا يكلم فلاناً فجاء الحالف وكلمه وهو نائم ولم يستيقظ الأصح حنثه، وفيمن مس مطلقته النائمة فإنه يصير مراجعاً، وفي نائم قبلته مطلقته الرجعية بشهوة يصير مراجعاً عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وفي امرأة أدخلت ذكره في فرجها وهو نائم ثبتت حرمة المصاهرة إذا علم بفعلها، وفي امرأة قبلت النائم بشهوة ثبتت حرمة المصاهرة إذا صدقها على الشهوة، وفي الاحتلام في الصلاة يوجب الاستقبال، وفيمن نام يوماً أو أكثر تصير الصلاة ديناً في ذمته، وفي عقد النكاح بحضرة النائمين يجوز في قول والأصح اشتراط السماع.
A sleeping woman establishes the prohibition of fosterage; one who speaks in his prayer while sleeping, his prayer is invalidated; one who recites in his prayer while sleeping in the standing state, that recitation is considered in one narration; one who recites a verse of prostration while sleeping and a man hears him, the prostration is obligatory upon the hearer; one who recites in front of a sleeping person a verse of prostration, then when the sleeper wakes and is informed, he must prostrate in one opinion; one who recites it while sleeping, then when he wakes and is informed, the recitation is binding in one opinion; one who swears not to speak to so-and-so, then the swearer comes and speaks to him while he is sleeping and he does not wake, the correct view is that he breaks his oath; one who touches his divorced wife while she is sleeping becomes a revoker; if a sleeping man is kissed by his revocably divorced wife with desire, he becomes a revoker according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad; if a woman inserts his organ into her vagina while he is sleeping, the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationship is established if he knows of her act; if a woman kisses a sleeping man with desire, the prohibition of marriage is established if she confirms the desire; a wet dream during prayer necessitates restarting; one who sleeps for a day or more, prayer becomes a debt upon him; the marriage contract in the presence of sleeping people is permissible in one view, but the correct view is that hearing is required.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage type is a collection of rulings demonstrating that sleep does not render a person legally inert. The author lists thirteen distinct scenarios from various chapters of fiqh—fosterage, prayer, oaths, divorce, marriage—to show that a sleeping person can be the subject of legal consequences. For example, a sleeping woman establishes fosterage (radaa') if she nurses; speaking in prayer while sleeping invalidates the prayer; a sleeping person can be a cause for sajdah tilawah; touching a sleeping divorced wife effects revocation (raj'ah); a wet dream requires restarting prayer. The issue of kissing a sleeping man by his revocably divorced wife involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that it effects revocation, while Muhammad holds it does not. Similarly, if a woman inserts a sleeping man's organ into her vagina, the prohibition of marriage is established only if he knows afterward. The list concludes with the rule that a marriage contract in the presence of sleeping people is valid provided they hear the contract. This passage serves to support the principle that in the context of tayammum, a sleeping person may be considered capable of knowing about water.

Key Terms
مراجعاً (murājiʿan): Revoker, a husband who takes back his wife during iddah.
حرمة المصاهرة (ḥurmat al-muṣāharah): Prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Automatically, regardless of desire
B) Only if she confirms the desire
C) Only if he wakes and agrees
D) Never, if he is asleep

Key Takeaway
Sleep of one party does not block family law effects like fosterage and revocation, but some effects require subsequent knowledge or confirmation.

Sleep and Oaths
Ruling on oath involving a sleeping person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that speaking to a sleeping person breaks an oath of silence.

Core Idea
An oath not to speak is broken if the swearer speaks to a sleeping person, even if the listener is unaware.

Oaths are taken seriously in Islamic law, and intentionality is key. However, the Hanafi school considers that speaking to a sleeping person counts as speaking for the oath, because the act of speaking is what matters, not the listener's awareness. This lesson examines one specific ruling from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
A person swears not to speak to a specific individual ('I will not speak to Zaid'). Later, Zaid is asleep, and the swearer speaks to him. Does the oath break?
The key is whether 'speaking to someone' requires the recipient to hear or be conscious.
2
Identify the ruling
The passage states: 'the correct view is that he breaks his oath.' So the Hanafi school holds that the oath is broken.
The phrase 'الأصح حنثه' indicates the relied-upon (sahih) view.
3
Extract the principle
The principle: an oath not to speak is about the act of address, not the addressee's reception. Speaking to someone includes any intentional verbal address.
Contrast with an oath not to let someone hear one's speech, which would require the person to hear.

Source Text
