The Principle of Permissibility Like Ownership in Breaking Tayammum
Establishes principle and applies to group water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that permissibility is like ownership in breaking tayammum and apply it to scenarios of found water.

Core Idea
Permissibility to use water breaks tayammum just like ownership.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal principle unique to the purification rules of tayammum. It explains why seeing water you are allowed to use, even if you don't own it, immediately invalidates your tayammum. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes this rule and begins to explore its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The text states: 'al-ibahatu ka al-milki fi al-naqd' – permissibility is like ownership in breaking (tayammum). This is the core ruling.
This principle is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the illah (effective cause)
The illah for breaking tayammum is the ability to use water without impediment. Both ownership and permissibility indicate this ability.
The qiyas connects the original case (ownership) to the new case (permissibility) via this illah.
3
Apply to a simple case
If a group finds enough water for one of them, all break tayammum because each is permitted to use it. This illustrates the principle in action.
The exception is when the water is legally shared (partnership or void gift).
4
Note the exception
If the water is shared among partners (e.g., a valid partnership), tayammum is not broken because no single person is independently permitted to use the full amount. Also, father-son relationship gives the father precedence.
The father can take his son's property when needed, so his tayammum breaks.
5
Cross-madhhab note
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require actual ownership or possession of water to break tayammum. The Hanafi view is more practical, as it considers the ability to use.
This difference affects travelers and those in public spaces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علم مما قدمناه أن الإباحة كالملك في النقض، فلو وجدوا مقدار ما يكفي أحدهم انتقض تيممهم بخلاف ما إذا كان مشتركاً بينهم فإنه لا ينتقض إلا أن يكون بين الأب والابن فإن الأب أولى لأن له تملك مال الابن عند الحاجة. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان ولو وهب لجماعة ماء يكفي أحدهم لا ينتقض تيممهم؛ أما عنده فلفسادها للشيوع، وأما عندهما فللاشتراك. فلو أذنوا لواحد لا يعتبر إذنهم ولا ينتقض تيممه لفسادها، وعندهما يصح إذنهم فانتقض تيمة. هذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي السراج الوهاج الصحيح الساد التيمم إجماعاً لأن هذا مقبوض بعقد فاسد فيكون مملوكاً فينفذ تصرفهم فيه .اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه وإن كان مملوكاً لا يحل التصرف وجوده كعدمه. ولو كانوا في الصلاة فجاء رجل بكوز من ماء وقال هذا لفلان فسدت صلاته خاصة، فإذا فرغوا وسألوه الماء فإن أعطاه للإمام توضأ واستقبلوا معه تمت صلاتهم وعلى من أعطاه الاستقبال ولو قال يا فلان خذ الماء فيه منهم فكان الصلاة، وإن منع : وتوضأ وحينئذ فيلزم منه صحة الصلاة بتلك الطهارة بعد وجود الماء وهو غير المطلوب تأمل. ثم اعلم أن المتيمم إذا رأى مع رجل ماء كافياً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو خارجها، وفي كل منهما إما أن يغلب على ظنه الإعطاء أو عدمه أو يشك، وفي كل منها إما أن سأله أو لا، وفي كل منها إما أن أعطاه أو لا، فهي أربعة وعشرون فإن كان في الصلاة وغلب على ظنه الإعطاء قطع وطلب الماء، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق فلو أتمها ثم سأله فإن أعطاه استأنف، وإن أبي تمت، وكذا إذا أبي ثم أعطى. وإن غلب على ظنه عدم الإعطاء أو شك لا يقطع صلاته، فإن قطع وسأل، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق. وإن أتم ثم سأل فإن أعطاه بطلت وإن أبي تمت وإن كان خارج الصلاة فإن لم يسأل وتيمم وصلى جازت الصلاة على ما في الهداية، ولا تجوز على ما في المبسوط فإن سأل بعدها فإن أعطاه أعاد وإلا فلا، سواء ظن الإعطاء أو المنع أو الشك. وإن سأل فإن أعطاه توضأ وإن منعه تيمم وصلى، فإن أعطاه بعدها لا إعادة عليه وينتقض تيممه ولا يتأتى في هذا القسم الظن أو الشك. وهذا حاصل ما في الزيادات وغيرها، وهذا الضبط من خواص هذا الكتاب و به تبين أنه إذا كان في الصلاة وغلب على طنه الإعطاء لا تبطل بل إذا أتمها وسأله ولم يعطه تمت صلاته لأنه ظهر أن ظنه كان خطأ. كذا في شرح الوقاية. فعلم منه أن ما في فتح القدير من بطلانها بمجرد غلبة ظن الإعطاء ليس بظاهر إلا أن قاضيخان في فتاواه ذكر البطلان في هذه الصورة بمجرد الظن عن محمد.
It is known from what we have presented that permissibility is like possession in breaking (tayammum). So if they found enough water for one of them, their tayammum is broken, unlike if it is shared among them, then it is not broken, except between father and son, for the father has precedence because he has the right to take his son's property when needed. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. And if a group is given water sufficient for one of them, their tayammum is not broken; according to Abu Hanifa, it is because the gift is void due to commonality (shuyu'), and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is due to partnership (ishtirak). If they authorize one person, their authorization is not considered and his tayammum is not broken due to its voidness; according to them, their authorization is valid and his tayammum is broken. This is in many books. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the correct view is that it breaks tayammum by consensus because it is held by a void contract, so it becomes owned, and their disposal is effective. But it is not hidden that even if it is owned, its disposal is not permissible; its existence is like non-existence. And if they were in prayer and a man came with a jug of water and said 'This is for so-and-so', only that person's prayer is invalidated. When they finish and ask him for water, if he gives it to the imam, he performs wudu and they repeat the prayer with him; their prayer is completed, and the one who gave it must repeat. And if he says 'O so-and-so, take the water', among them, and the prayer was... [text unclear] ... And know that if the mutayammim sees sufficient water with a man, there are cases: either he is in prayer or outside it; in each, either he has a strong presumption of being given, or not, or he doubts; and in each, either he asks or not; and in each, either he is given or not. So there are twenty-four. If he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, he cuts off and seeks water; if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, his tayammum remains. If he completes it and then asks, if given, he repeats; if refused, it is complete. And similarly if refused then given. If he has strong presumption of not being given, or doubts, he does not cut his prayer; if he cuts and asks, if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, tayammum remains. If he completes then asks, if given, it is invalidated; if refused, it is complete. If outside prayer, if he does not ask and performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is permissible according to al-Hidayah, but not according to al-Mabsut. If he asks afterward, if given, he repeats; otherwise not, regardless of presumption or doubt. If he asks, if given, he performs wudu; if refused, he performs tayammum and prays; if given afterward, no repetition, but his tayammum is broken. In this section, presumption or doubt does not apply. This is the gist of al-Ziyadat and others. This classification is unique to this book, and it shows that if he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, it is not invalidated; rather, if he completes and asks and is not given, his prayer is complete, because his presumption was false. Thus it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir about invalidation merely by strong presumption is not apparent, except that Qadikhan in his Fatawa mentions invalidation in this case by mere presumption, from Muhammad.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage type is a detailed analysis of when finding water breaks tayammum. It begins by establishing that 'permissibility is like ownership in breaking tayammum' (al-ibahah ka al-milk fi al-naqd). This means that if a mutayammim finds water he is allowed to use, it breaks his tayammum just as if he owned it. The author then applies this to cases of shared water. If a group of mutayammimin find enough water for one person, their tayammum is all broken unless the water is legally shared among them (e.g., a gift to all is void due to commonality according to Abu Hanifa, or is partnership according to the Sahibayn). The case of father and son is exceptional: the father may take his son's property if needed, so his tayammum is broken. The text also discusses a scenario where someone brings water for a specific person in a congregational prayer. Then the most extensive part: 24 scenarios for a mutayammim who sees water with another person, classified by whether he is in prayer or not, his presumption, whether he asks, and whether he is given. The ruling depends on these factors: if in prayer with strong presumption of being given, he should cut prayer and ask; otherwise he may continue. Outside prayer, he must ask (except according to al-Hidayah he may not ask and his prayer is valid). There is a dispute: some authorities (Fath al-Qadir) say strong presumption invalidates, but the author sides with the view that it does not, citing Sharh al-Wiqayah. Qadikhan reports invalidation from Muhammad. The passage also discusses a group being given water by a void gift: according to Abu Hanifa it does not break tayammum because the gift is void; according to the Sahibayn it breaks because the gift is valid as ownership is established. The text resolves by consensus that it breaks tayammum but the water is not lawful to use.

Key Terms
الإباحة كالملك في النقض (al-ibāḥatu ka al-milki fī al-naqḍ): A legal principle meaning that permissibility to use water has the same effect as ownership in breaking tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of a person having permissibility (ibahah) to use water on his tayammum?
A) It breaks his tayammum just as ownership does.
B) It does not break his tayammum unless he actually takes the water.
C) It breaks his tayammum only if he is in prayer.
D) It breaks his tayammum only if the water is owned by someone else.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that permissibility is like ownership ensures that tayammum is immediately broken when water is accessible, preventing invalid prayers.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Gift of Water to a Group
Intra-Hanafi dispute on gift to a group

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding a gift of water to a group and determine the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids a gift to a group due to commonality; the Sahibayn consider it a valid partnership.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning a gift of water to a group of people. When a group is given water sufficient for only one person, does the gift transfer ownership and thus break their tayammum? The text presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and then a later consensus view. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi rules of gift (hiba) and the concepts of shuyu' (commonality) and ishtirak (partnership).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A group of mutayammimin is given water that is enough for only one person. Does their tayammum break?
The ruling depends on whether the gift transfers ownership to the group.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa says the gift is void (fasid) due to commonality (shuyu')—the shares are unspecified, so no ownership transfers. Therefore, water is not owned and tayammum is not broken.
For Abu Hanifa, a gift without specifying shares is invalid.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the gift is valid as a partnership (ishtirak); the group owns the water collectively. Thus, tayammum is broken because each partner has ownership rights.
The Sahibayn consider the gift valid, creating shared ownership.
4
Analyze the later consensus
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj mentions a consensus that the tayammum is broken, because the water is held under a void contract but becomes owned by possession. However, the water remains unlawful to use (since the contract is void).
The text notes that even if owned, it is not permissible to use; existence like non-existence.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The author seems to lean towards the view that tayammum is not broken based on Abu Hanifa's position, but the issue remains disputed. The practical ruling is that one should avoid using such water.
Fatawa Qadikhan and other sources may provide further guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علم مما قدمناه أن الإباحة كالملك في النقض، فلو وجدوا مقدار ما يكفي أحدهم انتقض تيممهم بخلاف ما إذا كان مشتركاً بينهم فإنه لا ينتقض إلا أن يكون بين الأب والابن فإن الأب أولى لأن له تملك مال الابن عند الحاجة. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان ولو وهب لجماعة ماء يكفي أحدهم لا ينتقض تيممهم؛ أما عنده فلفسادها للشيوع، وأما عندهما فللاشتراك. فلو أذنوا لواحد لا يعتبر إذنهم ولا ينتقض تيممه لفسادها، وعندهما يصح إذنهم فانتقض تيمة. هذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي السراج الوهاج الصحيح الساد التيمم إجماعاً لأن هذا مقبوض بعقد فاسد فيكون مملوكاً فينفذ تصرفهم فيه .اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه وإن كان مملوكاً لا يحل التصرف وجوده كعدمه. ولو كانوا في الصلاة فجاء رجل بكوز من ماء وقال هذا لفلان فسدت صلاته خاصة، فإذا فرغوا وسألوه الماء فإن أعطاه للإمام توضأ واستقبلوا معه تمت صلاتهم وعلى من أعطاه الاستقبال ولو قال يا فلان خذ الماء فيه منهم فكان الصلاة، وإن منع : وتوضأ وحينئذ فيلزم منه صحة الصلاة بتلك الطهارة بعد وجود الماء وهو غير المطلوب تأمل. ثم اعلم أن المتيمم إذا رأى مع رجل ماء كافياً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو خارجها، وفي كل منهما إما أن يغلب على ظنه الإعطاء أو عدمه أو يشك، وفي كل منها إما أن سأله أو لا، وفي كل منها إما أن أعطاه أو لا، فهي أربعة وعشرون فإن كان في الصلاة وغلب على ظنه الإعطاء قطع وطلب الماء، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق فلو أتمها ثم سأله فإن أعطاه استأنف، وإن أبي تمت، وكذا إذا أبي ثم أعطى. وإن غلب على ظنه عدم الإعطاء أو شك لا يقطع صلاته، فإن قطع وسأل، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق. وإن أتم ثم سأل فإن أعطاه بطلت وإن أبي تمت وإن كان خارج الصلاة فإن لم يسأل وتيمم وصلى جازت الصلاة على ما في الهداية، ولا تجوز على ما في المبسوط فإن سأل بعدها فإن أعطاه أعاد وإلا فلا، سواء ظن الإعطاء أو المنع أو الشك. وإن سأل فإن أعطاه توضأ وإن منعه تيمم وصلى، فإن أعطاه بعدها لا إعادة عليه وينتقض تيممه ولا يتأتى في هذا القسم الظن أو الشك. وهذا حاصل ما في الزيادات وغيرها، وهذا الضبط من خواص هذا الكتاب و به تبين أنه إذا كان في الصلاة وغلب على طنه الإعطاء لا تبطل بل إذا أتمها وسأله ولم يعطه تمت صلاته لأنه ظهر أن ظنه كان خطأ. كذا في شرح الوقاية. فعلم منه أن ما في فتح القدير من بطلانها بمجرد غلبة ظن الإعطاء ليس بظاهر إلا أن قاضيخان في فتاواه ذكر البطلان في هذه الصورة بمجرد الظن عن محمد.
It is known from what we have presented that permissibility is like possession in breaking (tayammum). So if they found enough water for one of them, their tayammum is broken, unlike if it is shared among them, then it is not broken, except between father and son, for the father has precedence because he has the right to take his son's property when needed. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. And if a group is given water sufficient for one of them, their tayammum is not broken; according to Abu Hanifa, it is because the gift is void due to commonality (shuyu'), and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is due to partnership (ishtirak). If they authorize one person, their authorization is not considered and his tayammum is not broken due to its voidness; according to them, their authorization is valid and his tayammum is broken. This is in many books. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the correct view is that it breaks tayammum by consensus because it is held by a void contract, so it becomes owned, and their disposal is effective. But it is not hidden that even if it is owned, its disposal is not permissible; its existence is like non-existence. And if they were in prayer and a man came with a jug of water and said 'This is for so-and-so', only that person's prayer is invalidated. When they finish and ask him for water, if he gives it to the imam, he performs wudu and they repeat the prayer with him; their prayer is completed, and the one who gave it must repeat. And if he says 'O so-and-so, take the water', among them, and the prayer was... [text unclear] ... And know that if the mutayammim sees sufficient water with a man, there are cases: either he is in prayer or outside it; in each, either he has a strong presumption of being given, or not, or he doubts; and in each, either he asks or not; and in each, either he is given or not. So there are twenty-four. If he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, he cuts off and seeks water; if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, his tayammum remains. If he completes it and then asks, if given, he repeats; if refused, it is complete. And similarly if refused then given. If he has strong presumption of not being given, or doubts, he does not cut his prayer; if he cuts and asks, if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, tayammum remains. If he completes then asks, if given, it is invalidated; if refused, it is complete. If outside prayer, if he does not ask and performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is permissible according to al-Hidayah, but not according to al-Mabsut. If he asks afterward, if given, he repeats; otherwise not, regardless of presumption or doubt. If he asks, if given, he performs wudu; if refused, he performs tayammum and prays; if given afterward, no repetition, but his tayammum is broken. In this section, presumption or doubt does not apply. This is the gist of al-Ziyadat and others. This classification is unique to this book, and it shows that if he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, it is not invalidated; rather, if he completes and asks and is not given, his prayer is complete, because his presumption was false. Thus it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir about invalidation merely by strong presumption is not apparent, except that Qadikhan in his Fatawa mentions invalidation in this case by mere presumption, from Muhammad.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage type is a detailed analysis of when finding water breaks tayammum. It begins by establishing that 'permissibility is like ownership in breaking tayammum' (al-ibahah ka al-milk fi al-naqd). This means that if a mutayammim finds water he is allowed to use, it breaks his tayammum just as if he owned it. The author then applies this to cases of shared water. If a group of mutayammimin find enough water for one person, their tayammum is all broken unless the water is legally shared among them (e.g., a gift to all is void due to commonality according to Abu Hanifa, or is partnership according to the Sahibayn). The case of father and son is exceptional: the father may take his son's property if needed, so his tayammum is broken. The text also discusses a scenario where someone brings water for a specific person in a congregational prayer. Then the most extensive part: 24 scenarios for a mutayammim who sees water with another person, classified by whether he is in prayer or not, his presumption, whether he asks, and whether he is given. The ruling depends on these factors: if in prayer with strong presumption of being given, he should cut prayer and ask; otherwise he may continue. Outside prayer, he must ask (except according to al-Hidayah he may not ask and his prayer is valid). There is a dispute: some authorities (Fath al-Qadir) say strong presumption invalidates, but the author sides with the view that it does not, citing Sharh al-Wiqayah. Qadikhan reports invalidation from Muhammad. The passage also discusses a group being given water by a void gift: according to Abu Hanifa it does not break tayammum because the gift is void; according to the Sahibayn it breaks because the gift is valid as ownership is established. The text resolves by consensus that it breaks tayammum but the water is not lawful to use.

Key Terms
الشيوع (al-shuyūʿ): Commonality, as in a gift to multiple recipients without specifying shares, which Hanafis consider void.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirāk): Partnership, meaning shared ownership of water, which according to the Sahibayn prevents breaking tayammum because it is not exclusively one's own.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on a gift of water to a group when the shares are not specified?
A) The gift is valid and the water is owned by the group; tayammum is broken.
B) The gift is void and no ownership transfers; tayammum is not broken.
C) The gift is valid only if the recipients agree on shares.
D) The gift is void but tayammum is still broken.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a gift to a group without specifying shares is void according to Abu Hanifa, so the water is not owned and tayammum remains; the Sahibayn differ, but the operative ruling leans toward Abu Hanifa.

The 24 Scenarios of a Mutayammim Seeing Water
Taxonomy of 24 scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify and apply the 24 scenarios for a mutayammim who sees water with another person, based on being in prayer or not, presumption, asking, and being given.

Core Idea
A mutayammim's ruling depends on his situation: prayer, presumption, asking, and receiving water.

This lesson unpacks one of the most detailed taxonomies in Hanafi fiqh: the 24 scenarios (arba'un wa 'ishruna) for a person who sees water with another person while in a state of tayammum. The classification considers whether he is in prayer or not, his presumption of being given water, whether he asks, and whether he receives it. Each combination yields a specific ruling on the validity of his prayer and whether his tayammum is broken. Mastery of this taxonomy is essential for a mufti dealing with tayammum cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the variables
There are four binary variables: (1) in prayer or outside, (2) strong presumption of being given, strong presumption of not being given, or doubt, (3) asks or does not ask, (4) given or not given. This yields 2×3×2×2 = 24 scenarios.
The text explicitly states this calculation.
2
Scenario group 1: In prayer with strong presumption of being given
He should cut the prayer and seek water. If given, he performs wudu and repeats prayer. If not given, tayammum remains and prayer is valid if completed later.
This is the most active scenario.
3
Scenario group 2: In prayer with presumption of not being given or doubt
He does not cut the prayer. If he cuts and asks, and is given, he must perform wudu. If he completes then asks and is given, prayer is invalidated. If not given, prayer is valid.
He may not cut unless he has strong presumption.
4
Scenario group 3: Outside prayer
If he does not ask, performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is valid according to al-Hidayah but not according to al-Mabsut. If he asks and is given, tayammum is broken. If he asks and is refused, he performs tayammum and prays; if given afterward, no repetition but tayammum is broken.
There is a dispute between Hidayah and Mabsut regarding the permissibility of not asking.
5
Note the dispute on strong presumption
The author states that strong presumption does not invalidate prayer by itself; this is against Fath al-Qadir and Qadikhan's report from Muhammad. The author sides with Sharh al-Wiqayah.
This affects rulings where presumption is strong but no asking occurs.

A) He must repeat the prayer, and his tayammum is broken.

The Dispute on Strong Presumption Invalidating Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on strong presumption invalidating prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions within the Hanafi school on whether strong presumption of receiving water invalidates a prayer and evaluate the author's preference.

Core Idea
According to the author and Sharh al-Wiqayah, strong presumption alone does not invalidate prayer; only actual receipt of water does.

This lesson focuses on a specific legal point of dispute within the Hanafi school: does a mutayammim's strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that he will be given water invalidate his prayer if he does not ask? The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explicitly addresses this, citing Sharh al-Wiqayah in favor of no invalidation, while noting that Fath al-Qadir and Qadikhan's report from Muhammad hold the opposite. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the boundaries of legal presumption (zann) in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested scenario
A mutayammim is in prayer. He sees water with a man. He has strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the man will give him water if asked. He does not cut his prayer and completes it. Is his prayer valid?
The key: he has strong presumption but does not ask.
2
State the author's position
The author says the prayer is not invalidated. He cites Sharh al-Wiqayah: 'if he completes then asks and is not given, his prayer is complete because his presumption was false.'
Strong presumption is not certainty; it can be wrong.
3
Present the opposing view
Fath al-Qadir states that prayer is invalidated merely by strong presumption. Qadikhan in his Fatawa also mentions from Muhammad that invalidation occurs.
They consider strong presumption as equivalent to certainty in this context.
4
Analyze the proof for each
The author's proof: if presumption were to invalidate, then a person who errs in presumption would have to repeat prayers unnecessarily. The opposing view: strong presumption creates an obligation to seek water; ignoring it is like ignoring a clear sign.
The author's view aligns with the principle that actual events, not presumptions, determine rulings.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author prefers the view that prayer is not invalidated, as it is more practical and avoids hardship. This is consistent with the majority of the school.
The mufta bihi is that strong presumption alone does not invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علم مما قدمناه أن الإباحة كالملك في النقض، فلو وجدوا مقدار ما يكفي أحدهم انتقض تيممهم بخلاف ما إذا كان مشتركاً بينهم فإنه لا ينتقض إلا أن يكون بين الأب والابن فإن الأب أولى لأن له تملك مال الابن عند الحاجة. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان ولو وهب لجماعة ماء يكفي أحدهم لا ينتقض تيممهم؛ أما عنده فلفسادها للشيوع، وأما عندهما فللاشتراك. فلو أذنوا لواحد لا يعتبر إذنهم ولا ينتقض تيممه لفسادها، وعندهما يصح إذنهم فانتقض تيمة. هذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي السراج الوهاج الصحيح الساد التيمم إجماعاً لأن هذا مقبوض بعقد فاسد فيكون مملوكاً فينفذ تصرفهم فيه .اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه وإن كان مملوكاً لا يحل التصرف وجوده كعدمه. ولو كانوا في الصلاة فجاء رجل بكوز من ماء وقال هذا لفلان فسدت صلاته خاصة، فإذا فرغوا وسألوه الماء فإن أعطاه للإمام توضأ واستقبلوا معه تمت صلاتهم وعلى من أعطاه الاستقبال ولو قال يا فلان خذ الماء فيه منهم فكان الصلاة، وإن منع : وتوضأ وحينئذ فيلزم منه صحة الصلاة بتلك الطهارة بعد وجود الماء وهو غير المطلوب تأمل. ثم اعلم أن المتيمم إذا رأى مع رجل ماء كافياً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو خارجها، وفي كل منهما إما أن يغلب على ظنه الإعطاء أو عدمه أو يشك، وفي كل منها إما أن سأله أو لا، وفي كل منها إما أن أعطاه أو لا، فهي أربعة وعشرون فإن كان في الصلاة وغلب على ظنه الإعطاء قطع وطلب الماء، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق فلو أتمها ثم سأله فإن أعطاه استأنف، وإن أبي تمت، وكذا إذا أبي ثم أعطى. وإن غلب على ظنه عدم الإعطاء أو شك لا يقطع صلاته، فإن قطع وسأل، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق. وإن أتم ثم سأل فإن أعطاه بطلت وإن أبي تمت وإن كان خارج الصلاة فإن لم يسأل وتيمم وصلى جازت الصلاة على ما في الهداية، ولا تجوز على ما في المبسوط فإن سأل بعدها فإن أعطاه أعاد وإلا فلا، سواء ظن الإعطاء أو المنع أو الشك. وإن سأل فإن أعطاه توضأ وإن منعه تيمم وصلى، فإن أعطاه بعدها لا إعادة عليه وينتقض تيممه ولا يتأتى في هذا القسم الظن أو الشك. وهذا حاصل ما في الزيادات وغيرها، وهذا الضبط من خواص هذا الكتاب و به تبين أنه إذا كان في الصلاة وغلب على طنه الإعطاء لا تبطل بل إذا أتمها وسأله ولم يعطه تمت صلاته لأنه ظهر أن ظنه كان خطأ. كذا في شرح الوقاية. فعلم منه أن ما في فتح القدير من بطلانها بمجرد غلبة ظن الإعطاء ليس بظاهر إلا أن قاضيخان في فتاواه ذكر البطلان في هذه الصورة بمجرد الظن عن محمد.
It is known from what we have presented that permissibility is like possession in breaking (tayammum). So if they found enough water for one of them, their tayammum is broken, unlike if it is shared among them, then it is not broken, except between father and son, for the father has precedence because he has the right to take his son's property when needed. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. And if a group is given water sufficient for one of them, their tayammum is not broken; according to Abu Hanifa, it is because the gift is void due to commonality (shuyu'), and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is due to partnership (ishtirak). If they authorize one person, their authorization is not considered and his tayammum is not broken due to its voidness; according to them, their authorization is valid and his tayammum is broken. This is in many books. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the correct view is that it breaks tayammum by consensus because it is held by a void contract, so it becomes owned, and their disposal is effective. But it is not hidden that even if it is owned, its disposal is not permissible; its existence is like non-existence. And if they were in prayer and a man came with a jug of water and said 'This is for so-and-so', only that person's prayer is invalidated. When they finish and ask him for water, if he gives it to the imam, he performs wudu and they repeat the prayer with him; their prayer is completed, and the one who gave it must repeat. And if he says 'O so-and-so, take the water', among them, and the prayer was... [text unclear] ... And know that if the mutayammim sees sufficient water with a man, there are cases: either he is in prayer or outside it; in each, either he has a strong presumption of being given, or not, or he doubts; and in each, either he asks or not; and in each, either he is given or not. So there are twenty-four. If he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, he cuts off and seeks water; if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, his tayammum remains. If he completes it and then asks, if given, he repeats; if refused, it is complete. And similarly if refused then given. If he has strong presumption of not being given, or doubts, he does not cut his prayer; if he cuts and asks, if given, he performs wudu; otherwise, tayammum remains. If he completes then asks, if given, it is invalidated; if refused, it is complete. If outside prayer, if he does not ask and performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is permissible according to al-Hidayah, but not according to al-Mabsut. If he asks afterward, if given, he repeats; otherwise not, regardless of presumption or doubt. If he asks, if given, he performs wudu; if refused, he performs tayammum and prays; if given afterward, no repetition, but his tayammum is broken. In this section, presumption or doubt does not apply. This is the gist of al-Ziyadat and others. This classification is unique to this book, and it shows that if he is in prayer and has a strong presumption of being given, it is not invalidated; rather, if he completes and asks and is not given, his prayer is complete, because his presumption was false. Thus it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir about invalidation merely by strong presumption is not apparent, except that Qadikhan in his Fatawa mentions invalidation in this case by mere presumption, from Muhammad.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage type is a detailed analysis of when finding water breaks tayammum. It begins by establishing that 'permissibility is like ownership in breaking tayammum' (al-ibahah ka al-milk fi al-naqd). This means that if a mutayammim finds water he is allowed to use, it breaks his tayammum just as if he owned it. The author then applies this to cases of shared water. If a group of mutayammimin find enough water for one person, their tayammum is all broken unless the water is legally shared among them (e.g., a gift to all is void due to commonality according to Abu Hanifa, or is partnership according to the Sahibayn). The case of father and son is exceptional: the father may take his son's property if needed, so his tayammum is broken. The text also discusses a scenario where someone brings water for a specific person in a congregational prayer. Then the most extensive part: 24 scenarios for a mutayammim who sees water with another person, classified by whether he is in prayer or not, his presumption, whether he asks, and whether he is given. The ruling depends on these factors: if in prayer with strong presumption of being given, he should cut prayer and ask; otherwise he may continue. Outside prayer, he must ask (except according to al-Hidayah he may not ask and his prayer is valid). There is a dispute: some authorities (Fath al-Qadir) say strong presumption invalidates, but the author sides with the view that it does not, citing Sharh al-Wiqayah. Qadikhan reports invalidation from Muhammad. The passage also discusses a group being given water by a void gift: according to Abu Hanifa it does not break tayammum because the gift is void; according to the Sahibayn it breaks because the gift is valid as ownership is established. The text resolves by consensus that it breaks tayammum but the water is not lawful to use.

Key Terms
الإباحة كالملك في النقض (al-ibāḥatu ka al-milki fī al-naqḍ): A legal principle meaning that permissibility to use water has the same effect as ownership in breaking tayammum.
الشيوع (al-shuyūʿ): Commonality, as in a gift to multiple recipients without specifying shares, which Hanafis consider void.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirāk): Partnership, meaning shared ownership of water, which according to the Sahibayn prevents breaking tayammum because it is not exclusively one's own.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, does strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) of being given water invalidate a mutayammim's prayer if he does not ask and completes it?
A) Yes, it invalidates.
B) No, it does not invalidate.
C) It invalidates only if the presumption is correct.
D) It invalidates only if he asks afterward.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the dominant view is that a mutayammim's strong presumption of receiving water does not invalidate his prayer; only actual receipt after asking does.

Hope for Water and the Ruling on Delaying Prayer
Critical commentary on two matn statements: defense against redundancy and ruling on delaying prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delaying prayer when hoping to find water and identify the conditions for its recommendation.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer in hope of water is a recommendation, not an obligation, and only when water is a mile away and strongly presumed to appear later.

In this lesson, we examine two key statements from the matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq. The first is a claim of redundancy in the phrase 'it prevents and lifts tayammum' — the commentator defends it as a comprehensive rule. The second is the ruling that one who hopes to find water should delay the prayer, which is recommended, not obligatory. Understanding these points clarifies the Hanafi approach to tayammum and prayer timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two matn phrases under discussion
Locate the phrases 'فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه' and 'وراجى الماء يؤخر الصلاة' in the source. Understand the initial objection and the defense.
The first phrase is defended as non-redundant because it builds a general rule covering unlisted excuses.
2
Derive the ruling for delaying prayer
The text states that 'وراجى الماء يؤخر الصلاة' is by way of recommendation (nadb). Define 'rajāʾ' as strong presumption (ghalabat al-ẓann). Note the distance condition: a mile or more.
If distance is less, water is considered present and tayammum is invalid.
3
Apply the condition of hope
If there is no hope of finding water, do not delay the prayer initially. The benefit of waiting is to perform with complete ablution; without hope, there is no benefit.
This applies when one fears missing the prayer time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه أي القدرة على الماء تمنع جواز التيمم ابتداء وترفعه بقاء، وهذا تكرار محض لأنه لما عدّ الأعذار علم أنه لا يجوز مع القدرة ولما قال «وقدرة ماء» علم أنه ترفعه القدرة ولا يبقى إلا في موضع يجوز ابتداء فلا فائدة بذكره ثانياً، ولا يليق بمثل هذا المختصر . كذا في التبيين. وقد يقال : إنه ليس بتكرار محض لأنه إنما عد بعض الأعذار ولم يستوفها كما علم مما بيناه أولاً فربما يتوهم حصر الأعذار في المعدود وقد ذكر ضابطاً لها لتتم الأعذار فكان فيه فائدة كما لا يخفى قوله (وراجى الماء يؤخر الصلاة) يعني على سبيل الندب كما صرح به في أصله الوافي والمراد بالرجاء غلبة الظن أي يغلب على ظنه أنه يجد الماء في آخر الوقت. وهذا إذا كان بينه وبين موضع يرجوه ميل أو أكثر، فإن كان أقل منه لا يجزئه التيمم. وإن خاف فوت وقت الصلاة، فإن كان لا يرجوه لا يؤخر الصلاة أول عن الوقت لأن فائدة الانتظار احتمال وجدان الماء فيؤديها بأكمل الطهارتين، وإذا لم يكن له رجاء
His statement: 'It prevents tayammum and lifts it' meaning: ability over water prevents the permissibility of tayammum initially and lifts it after it exists. This is pure repetition because when he enumerated the excuses, it is known that it is not permissible with ability, and when he said 'and ability over water', it is known that ability lifts it, and it remains only in a place where it is initially permissible, so there is no benefit in mentioning it a second time, and it is not fitting for such a concise text. Thus in al-Tabyin. And it may be said: It is not pure repetition because he only enumerated some excuses and did not cover them all, as known from what we explained earlier. So perhaps one might suppose a restriction of excuses to those enumerated, and he mentioned a rule for them to complete the excuses, so there is benefit in it, as is not hidden. His statement: 'One who hopes for water delays the prayer' means by way of recommendation, as stated in its source al-Wafi. And the meaning of hope is strong presumption, i.e., he strongly presumes that he will find water at the end of the time. This is if between him and the place he hopes for there is a distance of a mile or more; if it is less, tayammum is not sufficient for him. And if he fears missing the time of prayer, if he does not hope for water, he does not delay the prayer initially from its time because the benefit of waiting is the possibility of finding water and performing it with the more complete of the two purifications, and if he has no hope...
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage type is a critical refinement of two statements from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first statement in the matn is 'فهي تمنع التيمم وترفعه' (it prevents tayammum and lifts it). The commentator al-Zayla'i in al-Tabyin considers this redundant, since the matn already mentioned excuses and the condition of ability. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq defends it: it is not redundant because the list of excuses is not exhaustive; this phrase serves as a comprehensive principle covering all unlisted excuses. The second statement is 'وراجى الماء يؤخر الصلاة' (one who hopes for water delays the prayer). The commentator explains that this delay is recommended (nadb), not obligatory, as clarified in the source al-Wafi. 'Hope' here means a strong presumption that water will be found at the end of the prayer time. This applies when the distance to the hoped-for water is a mile or more; if less, tayammum is not permissible because the water is considered present. If the person fears missing the prayer time and has no hope of finding water, he should not delay the prayer. The underlying principle is that waiting is beneficial only if there is a real chance of finding water, allowing performance with the more complete taharah (wudu). The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of defending the matn against claims of redundancy and clarifying the precise legal conditions for delaying prayer for water.

Key Terms
قدرة على الماء (qudrah ʿalā al-māʾ): Ability to obtain water, which prevents the validity of tayammum.
رجاء الماء (rajāʾ al-māʾ): Hoping for water, meaning a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water will be found later in the time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water later in the time?
A) Obligatory
B) Recommended
C) Permissible without preference
D) Prohibited

Key Takeaway
Hope for water justifies delaying prayer as a recommendation, provided the distance is at least a mile and the hope is a strong presumption.

Twenty-Four Scenarios: When a Mutayammim Sees Water with Another
Detailed branches of rulings for a mutayammim seeing water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a mutayammim who sees water with another person by systematically considering his state (in prayer or outside), his presumption of receiving water, whether he asks, and whether he receives it.

Core Idea
A mutayammim's prayer is not invalidated by mere sight of water; the ruling depends on his presumption of actually receiving it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a meticulous enumeration of rulings for a person performing tayammum who sees sufficient water with another person. The passage type is a ruling with multiple conditional branches. The author systematically lays out 24 scenarios based on three factors: whether he is in prayer or outside, his degree of certainty about being given water, whether he asks, and whether he is given. This showcases the Hanafi school's attention to detail and its method of deriving rulings for every possible situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main contexts
First, determine whether the mutayammim is currently in prayer or outside prayer. This is the primary division that shapes the ruling.
2
Assess the presumption of receiving water
For each context, consider the person's state of mind: does he have an overwhelming likelihood (ghalabat al-zann) that he will be given the water, does he think it unlikely, or does he have no opinion (doubt)?
In Hanafi fiqh, zann (strong presumption) can trigger an obligation to act, such as breaking prayer.
3
Consider whether he asks and whether he receives
For each combination of context and presumption, the person may ask for water or not, and if he asks, he may receive it or be refused. These two binary factors generate the remaining scenarios.
The passage handles all four combinations: ask/given, ask/not given, not ask/given (after prayer), not ask/not given.
4
Derive the ruling for each scenario
Using the principles from the passage, determine for each scenario whether the prayer is valid, whether it must be broken, and whether repetition is required. Note the key distinctions: if in prayer and strongly thinks he will be given, he must break; otherwise he may continue.
The passage gives explicit rulings for all cases, e.g., if he completes and later receives it, he must repeat.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify the disagreement between al-Hidaya and al-Mabsut regarding the case where he is outside prayer and does not ask. Also note the view of Qadikhan that mere presumption invalidates the prayer. Understand which position is mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi follows al-Hidaya: prayer is valid if he does not ask and performs tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فظن كل واحد أنه يدعوه فسدت صلاة الكل. كذا في المحيط . ثم اعلم أن المتيمم إذا رأى مع رجل ماء كافياً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون في الصلاة أو خارجها، وفي كل منهما إما أن يغلب على ظنه الإعطاء أو عدمه أو يشك، وفي كل منها إما أن سأله أو لا، وفي كل منها إما أن أعطاه أو لا، فهي أربعة وعشرون فإن كان في الصلاة وغلب على ظنه الإعطاء قطع وطلب الماء، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق فلو أتمها ثم سأله فإن أعطاه استأنف، وإن أبي تمت، وكذا إذا أبي ثم أعطى. وإن غلب على ظنه عدم الإعطاء أو شك لا يقطع صلاته، فإن قطع وسأل، فإن أعطاه توضأ وإلا فتيممه باق. وإن أتم ثم سأل فإن أعطاه بطلت وإن أبي تمت وإن كان خارج الصلاة فإن لم يسأل وتيمم وصلى جازت الصلاة على ما في الهداية، ولا تجوز على ما في المبسوط فإن سأل بعدها فإن أعطاه أعاد وإلا فلا، سواء ظن الإعطاء أو المنع أو الشك. وإن سأل فإن أعطاه توضأ وإن منعه تيمم وصلى، فإن أعطاه بعدها لا إعادة عليه وينتقض تيممه ولا يتأتى في هذا القسم الظن أو الشك. وهذا حاصل ما في الزيادات وغيرها، وهذا الضبط من خواص هذا الكتاب و به تبين أنه إذا كان في الصلاة وغلب على طنه الإعطاء لا تبطل بل إذا أتمها وسأله ولم يعطه تمت صلاته لأنه ظهر أن ظنه كان خطأ. كذا في شرح الوقاية. فعلم منه أن ما في فتح القدير من بطلانها بمجرد غلبة ظن الإعطاء ليس بظاهر إلا أن قاضيخان في فتاواه ذكر البطلان في هذه الصورة بمجرد الظن عن محمد .
He thought that each one of them was calling him, so the prayer of all was invalid. Thus in al-Muhit. Then know that if a mutayammim sees sufficient water with a man, then it is either while he is in prayer or outside it. In each case, either he thinks it likely to be given, or unlikely, or he doubts. In each case, either he asks or not, and in each case, either he is given it or not. So there are twenty-four [scenarios]. If he is in prayer and thinks it likely to be given, he should break [the prayer] and seek water. If he is given it, he performs wudu; otherwise, his tayammum remains. If he completes [the prayer] and then asks, and is given it, he must recommence; if refused, it is valid. Similarly, if he is refused then given. If he thinks it unlikely to be given or doubts, he does not break his prayer. If he breaks and asks, and is given it, he performs wudu; otherwise his tayammum remains. If he completes then asks, and is given it, his prayer is invalid; if refused, it is valid. If he is outside prayer, and he does not ask and performs tayammum and prays, the prayer is permissible according to al-Hidaya, but not permissible according to al-Mabsut. If he asks after [prayer] and is given it, he repeats; otherwise not, whether he thought likely to be given or prevented or doubted. If he asks [before prayer], then if he is given it, he performs wudu; if prevented, he performs tayammum and prays. If he is given after that, there is no repetition upon him, but his tayammum is invalidated. In this section, likelihood or doubt is not considered. This is what is obtained from al-Ziyadat and others. This classification is unique to this book. From it, it is clear that if he is in prayer and thinks it likely to be given, it is not invalid; rather, if he completes [the prayer] and asks and is not given, his prayer is valid because his thought proved wrong. Thus in Sharh al-Wiqaya. From this it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir about invalidation just by thinking it likely to be given is not apparent, except that Qadikhan in his Fatawa mentioned invalidation in this case just by the thought from Muhammad.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed enumeration of rulings for a person performing tayammum who sees sufficient water with another person. The passage type is a ruling with multiple conditional branches. The author begins by stating a general principle: if each of several people in prayer thinks that the imam is calling him, the prayer of all is invalid. Then he proceeds to the main subject: the mutayammim who sees water with a man. He systematically lays out 24 scenarios based on three factors: whether he is in prayer or outside, his degree of certainty about being given water (overwhelming likelihood of giving, overwhelming likelihood of not giving, or doubt), whether he asks for water or not, and whether he is given water or not. For each scenario, the ruling is given. For example, if he is in prayer and strongly thinks he will be given water, he must break the prayer and seek water. If he is given it, he makes wudu; if not, his tayammum remains valid. But if he completes the prayer and then asks and is refused, his prayer is valid. This shows that the mere likelihood of receiving water does not invalidate the prayer. There is a disagreement between al-Hidaya and al-Mabsut regarding the case where he is outside prayer and does not ask: al-Hidaya permits the prayer, al-Mabsut does not. The author notes that this classification is unique to this book and concludes that what is stated in Fath al-Qadir about invalidation by mere likelihood is not apparent, except that Qadikhan in his Fatawa attributed invalidation to Imam Muhammad. This passage is a prime example of Hanafi fiqh's meticulous branching (tafri') and shows the school's attention to all possible scenarios.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
ظن (zann): Overwhelming likelihood or strong presumption, as opposed to certainty (yaqin) or doubt (shakk).
رجاء (raja'): Hope or expectation of finding water, typically based on strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mutayammim is in prayer and sees water with someone, and he strongly thinks he will be given it, what should he do?
A) Continue his prayer without interruption.
B) Break his prayer and seek water.
C) Wait until the end of the prayer time.
D) Ask for water without breaking prayer.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a mutayammim's prayer upon seeing water depends on his presumption of receiving it and whether he is in prayer; the Hanafi school's detailed branches provide clear guidance for each scenario.

Is Delaying Prayer for Hope of Water Recommended Generally?
Internal Hanafi dispute on scope of recommending delay for one who hopes for water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water and evaluate the internal Hanafi dispute over the scope of the recommendation.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer for hope of water is recommended only if there is a benefit; otherwise, early prayer is better.

The ability to delay a prayer in hope of performing it with a more complete purification (wudu) seems straightforward. However, the Hanafi school contains a nuanced internal dispute: is the recommendation limited to those who genuinely expect to find water, or can it extend to any case where delay yields a spiritual or practical benefit, such as a larger congregation? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates the different positions and proofs to clarify the school's operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? (Delaying the prayer) and what is its legal classification? (Recommendable, nadb/sunnah). Note that it is not obligatory.
The passage opens by confirming the recommendable nature of this delay.
2
Understand the condition of hope (raja')
What does 'hope' mean here? It is a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) of finding water later. Also note the geographical condition: distance to water must be a mile or more for tayammum to be invalid.
Hope is not mere wishful thinking but a reasonable expectation.
3
Locate the dispute within the Hanafi school
Some Hanafi commentators restrict the recommendation to those who hope for water; others argue that delay is recommended whenever there is a benefit, even without hope. Identify the two positions and the key texts they rely on.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
4
Analyze the proofs and reconciliation
Examine the proofs: Imam Muhammad's general statement in al-Asl (delay is beloved) vs. the explicit examples in al-Hidayah (delay for congregation). How does the commentator reconcile them? He treats the examples as tamthīl (illustration) not hassar (exhaustive).
The underlying principle is benefit (maslahah), not merely hope of water.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
What is the operative ruling for fatwa? The majority view (and the author's choice) is that delay is recommended whenever there is any benefit. For a traveler alone, early prayer is better; for a person in a city, delay for congregation may be recommended even without water hope.
The author sides with Ghayat al-Bayan and validates the broader view.

قوله (وراجى الماء يؤخر الصلاة) يعني على سبيل الندب كما صرح به في أصله الوافي والمراد بالرجاء غلبة الظن أي يغلب على ظنه أنه يجد الماء في آخر الوقت. وهذا إذا كان بينه وبين موضع يرجوه ميل أو أكثر، فإن كان أقل منه لا يجزئه التيمم. وإن خاف فوت وقت الصلاة، فإن كان لا يرجوه لا يؤخر الصلاة أول عن الوقت لأن فائدة الانتظار احتمال وجدان الماء فيؤديها بأكمل الطهارتين، وإذا لم يكن له رجاء (ولا يخفى أنه وإن يتأتى هذا في حق من في المفازة فكان التعجيل أولى، ولهذا كان أولى للنساء أن يصلين في أول الوقت لأنهن لا يخرجن إلى الجماعة. كذا في مبسوطي شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام، كذا في معراج الدراية، وكذا في كثير من شروح الهداية. وتعقبهم في غاية البيان بأن هذا سهو وقع من الشارحين وليس مذهب أصحابنا أئمتنا صريح في استحباب تأخير بعض الصلوات من غير اشتراط جماعة، كذلك فإن كلام وما ذكروه في التيمم مفهوم والصريح مقدم على المفهوم. وأجاب عنه في السراج الوهاج بأن الصريح محمول على ما إذا تضمن ذلك فضيلة كتكثير الجماعة لأنه إذا لم يتضمن ذلك لم يكن للتأخير فائدة، وما لا فائدة فيه لم يكن مستحباً. وهل يؤخر عند الرجاء إلى وقت الاستحباب أو إلى وقت الجواز؟ أقوال ثالثها إن كان على ثقة فإلى آخر وقت الجواز، وإن كان على طمع فإلى آخر وقت الاستحباب، وأصحها الأول. كذا في السراج الوهاج. والحق ما في غاية البيان فإن محمداً ذكر في الأصل أن تأخير الصلاة أحب إلي ولم يفصل بين الرجاء وغيره. والذي في مبسوط شمس الأئمة إنما هو إذا كان لا . فلا يؤخر الصلاة عن وقتها المعهود يرجو تمنع التيمم وكأن التكرار مسلم عنده في قوله وترفعه». قوله : العصر لما فيه من توسعة الوقت لصلاة النوافل، ومنها تأخير العشاء إلى ما قبل ثلث الليل لما فيه من قطع السمر المنهي عنه بعدها، وقيل في الصيف يعجل كيلا تتقلل الجماعة فهذه العلل كلها مصرح بها في الهداية وغيرها وهي مفقودة في المسافر فإن الغالب عليه صلاته منفرداً وعدم التنفل بعد العصر ويباح له السمر بعد العشاء فلم يكن في تأخيره فضيلة فكان الأفضل له المسارعة إلى الصلاة. وقول الشراح كتكثير الجماعة ليس فيه حصر الفضيلة فيها بل هو تمثيل لها وذكر لبعض أفرادها فليس ذلك مخالفاً لما ذكروه من استحباب تأخير بعض الصلوات هذا ما ظهر لي والله تعالى أعلم. قوله: (والحق ما في غاية البيان الخ) حاصله تحقيق أن غير راجي الماء يؤخر أيضاً ولكن إلى أول النصف الثاني من الوقت خلاف ما يفهم من كلامهم من عدم تأخيره أصلاً لتصريحهم باستحباب تأخير بعض الصلوات (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب المواقيت ۹ ۱۰ . أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ٤. الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ٥. النسائي في كتاب المواقيت باب ٥. ابن ماجه في كتاب الصلاة باب ٤. الموطأ في كتاب الوقوت حديث ۲۷ ۲۹ . أحمد في مسنده (۲۲۹/۲، ۲۳۸) (۹/۳، ٥۲).
His statement: 'One who hopes for water delays prayer' means in a recommendable manner, as made explicit in his original al-Wafi. The meaning of 'hope' is overwhelming likelihood, i.e., he strongly thinks he will find water at the end of the time. This is when between him and the place he hopes for there is a mile or more; if less, tayammum is not sufficient for him. And if he fears missing the prayer time, then if he does not hope, he does not delay prayer from the first part of the time because the benefit of waiting is the possibility of finding water and performing it with the more complete of the two purifications. And if he has no hope... It is also said that the statements in the books about delaying apply only when there is a benefit like increasing the congregation. The author then discusses various opinions and concludes that even one who does not hope may delay to the first half of the second part of the time, contrary to what some understood. He cites the hadith: 'Delay the Zuhr prayer until it cools down, for intense heat is from the exhalation of Hell.'
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on delaying prayer for someone who hopes to find water (raji al-ma'). The commentator from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that this delay is recommendable (nadb), not obligatory. The hope is based on a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water will be found later in the time. If the distance to the water source is more than a mile, tayammum is not valid; one must use water. If one does not hope, delay is not recommended. However, there is a dispute: some scholars hold that delay is recommendable only if it yields a benefit like increasing the congregation. Others argue that the Hanafi imams explicitly recommend delaying certain prayers (e.g., Fajr till isfar, Zuhr in summer, Asr, Isha) even without an immediate hope of water. The commentator reconciles by noting that in all those cases, there is a benefit (e.g., more congregation, avoiding heat, time for nafl). For a traveler (musafir) who typically prays alone, these benefits are absent, so praying early is better. The passage also discusses whether one should delay to the preferred time (waqt al-istihbab) or to the last permissible time. The strongest view is to delay to the last permissible time if one is confident, but to the preferred time if merely hopeful. The author sides with Ghayat al-Bayan that one who does not hope may also delay, but only to the first half of the second part of the time. The hadith about cooling Zuhr is cited as evidence that delaying can be recommended even for those not specifically hoping for water.

Key Terms
رجاء (raja'): Hope or expectation of finding water, based on strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann).
الندب (al-nadb): Recommendable, commendable act (sunnah) that is not obligatory.
الوقت المعهود (al-waqt al-ma'hud): The usual or prescribed time for prayer, i.e., the optimal early portion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following best describes the operative (mufta bihi) ruling on delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water?
A) It is obligatory to delay if hope is strong.
B) It is recommended to delay only if hope exists and no other benefit is present.
C) It is recommended to delay when there is any benefit, including hope of water or larger congregation.
D) It is only recommended if the delay leads to praying in a congregation of at least 40 people.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water only if it yields a benefit; without benefit, early prayer is better, and the school's final position allows delay even without hope when a benefit exists.

Timing of Prayer for the Mutayammim: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delaying prayer for the mutayammim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on delaying prayer for the mutayammim who hopes for water and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The mutayammim who hopes for water may delay prayer further; the one who does not hope delays only to the beginning of the second half.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: when a person has performed tayammum, is it recommended to delay prayer in hopes of finding water? The answer depends on whether delay brings a virtue, and whether the person actually expects to find water. The author navigates between the views of earlier Hanafi commentators and the explicit statements of the founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The central issue is whether it is recommended (mustahabb) for a person who has performed tayammum to delay prayer, and if so, how much delay is recommended. The ruling varies based on whether the person hopes (rajā’) to find water before the end of the prayer time.
The default principle is that performing prayer at the beginning of its time is better (afḍal), unless delay brings a virtue that cannot be attained otherwise.
2
State the default Hanafi principle
The Hanafi school holds that delaying prayer is generally not recommended unless it serves a greater good, such as increasing the congregation (takthīr al-jamā‘ah) or avoiding harm. This principle is derived from the ḥadīth on delaying Ẓuhr in extreme heat and similar examples.
Women and travelers in the desert are exceptions because they do not attend congregation.
3
Locate the intra-madhhab disagreement
Some Hanafi commentators (e.g., in al-Mabsūṭ and various sharḥs of al-Hidāyah) claimed that delaying prayer for the mutayammim is unconditionally recommended. However, the author of Ghāyat al-Bayān criticized this as an oversight, arguing that the explicit texts (nuṣūṣ) of the school condition recommendation on the presence of a virtue.
The disagreement is about whether the non-hoping person should delay at all.
4
Analyze the proofs
Imam Muḥammad in al-Aṣl states: 'Delaying prayer is more beloved to me' without distinguishing between hoping and not hoping. This supports delaying for all. On the other hand, the ḥadīth 'أبردوا بالظهر' uses an imperative that indicates recommendation, but the reason given (harm from heat) is context-specific. The author argues that the non-hoping person also delays to the beginning of the second half, as that time itself is recommended (mustahabb) even without a further virtue.
The anecdote of Abū Ḥanīfa and Ḥammād shows that Abū Ḥanīfa delayed and found water, validating the practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of Al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq sides with Ghāyat al-Bayān: both the one who hopes and the one who does not hope delay, but to different extents. The hoping person may delay to the end of the recommended time (or even to the permissible time if confident), while the non-hoping person delays only to the beginning of the second half of the prayer time.
This is the operative fatwa position (muftā bihī) according to the author.

Source Text

كان أولى للنساء أن يصلين في أول الوقت لأنهن لا يخرجن إلى الجماعة. كذا في مبسوطي شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام، كذا في معراج الدراية، وكذا في كثير من شروح الهداية. وتعقبهم في غاية البيان بأن هذا سهو وقع من إن أخر الصلاة إلى آخر الوقت بقرب من الماء بمسافة أقل من ميل لكن لا يتمكن من الصلاة بالوضوء في الوقت، الأولى أن يصلي في أول الوقت مراعاة لحق الوقت وتجنباً عن الخلاف .اهـ. وذكر في المناقب أن هذه المسألة أول واقعة خالف أبو حنيفة أستاذه حماداً فصلى حماد بالتيمم في أول الوقت، ووجد أبو حنيفة الماء في آخر الوقت وصلاها وكان ذلك غرة اجتهاده فقبلها الله تعالى منه وصوبه فيه، وكانت هذه الصلاة صلاة المغرب وكان خروجهما لأجل تشييع الأعمش .
Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. And he hopes, so there is no benefit in waiting, and performing prayer at the beginning of the time is better unless delay includes a virtue that is not attained without it, like increasing the congregation. And this does not apply to the one in the desert, so hurrying is better. For this reason, it is better for women to pray at the beginning of the time because they do not go out to the congregation. Thus in Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam, thus in Miraj al-Diraya, and thus in many commentaries of al-Hidaya. And they are criticized in Ghayat al-Bayan that this is an oversight by the commentators and it is not the explicit madhhab of our imams that delaying some prayers is recommended without requiring a congregation. Likewise, their statement in the chapter of tayammum is understood, and the explicit takes precedence over the understood. And he answered in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that the explicit is carried upon when it includes a virtue like increasing the congregation, because if it does not include that, there is no benefit in delay, and that which has no benefit is not recommended. And is he to delay when hoping to the time of recommendation or to the time of permissibility? There are opinions, a third of which: if he is confident, then to the end of the time of permissibility, and if he is hopeful, then to the end of the time of recommendation, and the most correct is the first. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the truth is what is in Ghayat al-Bayan, for Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that delaying prayer is more beloved to me, and he did not distinguish between hoping and other. And what is in Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma is only if he does not ... So he does not delay prayer from its accustomed time, he hopes. The tayammum prevents, and as if the repetition is conceded by him in his statement 'and he raises it'. His statement: (And he answered in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj etc.) I say: it is supported that the places where our imams explicitly stated the recommendation of delay all include a virtue: from them is delaying Fajr to Isfar because of increasing the congregation and widening the opportunity for the sleeper and weak to attain the virtue of congregation; from them is cooling in summer Zuhr because hurrying reduces the congregation and harms people, for heat harms them, and for this the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Delay the Zuhr because severe heat is from the breath of Hell.' (1) And from them is delaying Asr because of widening the time for supererogatory prayers; and from them is delaying Isha to before the third of the night because of cutting off the prohibited night talk after it, and it is said in summer he hurries so that the congregation does not decrease. These reasons are all explicitly stated in al-Hidaya and others, and they are absent in the traveler, for he usually prays alone and does not pray supererogatory after Asr, and night talk is permissible for him after Isha, so there is no virtue in his delay, so the best for him is to hasten to prayer. And the statement of the commentators 'like increasing the congregation' does not limit virtue to that, but it is an example and mention of some of its instances, so that is not contrary to what they mentioned of recommending delay of some prayers. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best. His statement: (And the truth is what is in Ghayat al-Bayan etc.) Its summary is the verification that the one who does not hope for water also delays, but to the beginning of the second half of the time, contrary to what is understood from their speech that he does not delay at all, due to their explicit stating of recommending delay of some prayers. (1) Narrated by Bukhari in Kitab al-Mawaqit 9/10, Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah Bab 4, Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah Bab 5, Nasa'i in Kitab al-Mawaqit Bab 5, Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Salah Bab 4, Muwatta in Kitab al-Waqut Hadith 27/29, Ahmad in his Musnad (2/229, 238) (3/9, 52). That is, from the time of recommendation, which is the beginning of the last half of the time in the prayer that is recommended to delay. As for if he hopes, the recommended is to delay it beyond this recommended time. And this is the intended meaning of the one who said that delay is not recommended if he does not hope. And the intended meaning of hurrying is not the performance at the beginning of the time of permissibility, so that it would be necessarily better. And supports what we have said what al-Ispijabi mentioned in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: 'And if he is not hopeful of finding water, he performs tayammum and prays at a recommended time,' and he did not say 'prays at the beginning of the time.' And al-Kardari said in al-Manqiba: 'And the most appropriate is to carry the recommendation of delay with hope to the end of the second half, and the non-recommendation of that when there is no hope. Rather, the better when there is no hope is to perform at the beginning of the second half, as indicated by their statement: It is recommended to make Fajr bright (isfar) by reciting the sunnah recitation; then if a doubt occurs to him in the first prayer, he performs the second with purification and the sunnah recitation also, and that is only possible at the beginning of the second half.' End. And in others: 'The traveler, if he is certain of finding water or his dominant assumption is that at the end of the time, he performs tayammum at the beginning of the time and prays; if there is a mile distance between him and the water, it is permissible; and if it is less but he fears missing [the prayer], he does not perform tayammum.' End. Its summary is that distance permits tayammum absolutely. And in Miraj al-Diraya, attributed to al-Mujtaba: 'There vacillates in my heart regarding the case where he knows that if he delays prayer to the end of the time, he will be near water at less than a mile, but he will not be able to pray with ablution within the time; it is better to pray at the beginning of the time out of consideration for the right of the time and to avoid disagreement.' End. And it is mentioned in al-Manqib that this issue is the first occasion where Abu Hanifa opposed his teacher Hammad: Hammad prayed with tayammum at the beginning of the time, and Abu Hanifa found water at the end of the time and prayed with it, and that was the beginning of his ijtihad, and Allah accepted it from him and confirmed him in it. And this prayer was Maghrib, and their going out was to accompany al-A'mash.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recommended timing of prayer for a person who performs tayammum and either hopes or does not hope to find water within the prayer time. The core issue is whether delaying prayer is always better or only when it brings a specific virtue. The commentary begins by stating that performing prayer at the beginning of the time is generally better unless delay includes a virtue like increasing the congregation. For a traveler in the desert, hurrying is better since the virtue of congregation is absent, and similarly for women. The author then critiques some commentators who claimed the Hanafi imams unconditionally recommended delay for certain prayers, clarifying that the explicit texts (like those in al-Hidaya) show delay is only recommended when it brings a virtue. The example of delaying Zuhr in summer due to heat (backed by a hadith) is given, along with other cases. The discussion then moves to whether a person hoping for water (rajai) should delay to the recommended time or to the permissible time, with three opinions; the most correct is that if confident, delay to the end of permissible time, and if hopeful, to the end of recommended time. Then, the author asserts the truth is in Ghayat al-Bayan, that the one not hoping also delays to the beginning of the second half of the time, citing Muhammad's statement in al-Asl that delay is beloved without distinguishing. The passage includes supporting arguments from other Hanafi scholars (al-Ispijabi, al-Kardari) and concludes with the historical anecdote of Abu Hanifa's first ijtihad opposing his teacher Hammad, which validates delaying for hope. The overall ruling is that early prayer is afdal unless delay brings a virtue, and for the one hoping for water, delay is recommended, but for the one not hoping, delay is still recommended but only to the beginning of the second half of the time (i.e., not to the very end).

Key Terms
رجاء (rajā’): Hope or expectation of finding water before the end of the prayer time
استحباب (istihbāb): Recommendation; a ruling that is not obligatory but meritorious
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preferred view (mufta bihi), what is the ruling for a mutayammim who does not hope for water?
A) He should pray at the beginning of the time without delay.
B) He should delay to the beginning of the second half of the time.
C) He should delay to the end of the permissible time.
D) He should delay only if he hopes for water, otherwise pray immediately.

Key Takeaway
The mutayammim's recommended prayer timing depends on hope for water and the presence of virtue; the mufta bihi distinguishes between raji and non-raji in the extent of delay.

Validity of Tayammum Before Time and for Two Fard Prayers
Ruling statement with inter-madhhab dispute introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum before prayer time and for multiple fard prayers, and explain the difference between the Hanafi view of tayammum as an absolute substitute versus the Shafi'i view as a restricted substitute.

Core Idea
Tayammum is an absolute substitute, valid before time and for two fard prayers, not a mere necessity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key ruling: tayammum is valid before the prayer time begins and can be used for more than one obligatory prayer. This is based on the Hanafi understanding that tayammum is an absolute substitute (badal mutlaq) for wudu or ghusl, not a temporary concession tied to necessity. The text then introduces the inter-madhhab dispute on the nature of this substitution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The ruling: tayammum is valid before the prayer time and for two fard prayers. 'Valid' means it fulfills the condition of purification for salah.
The matn says 'wa saha qabla al-waqt wa li-fardayn' – the commentator Ibn Nujaym explains that this means tayammum is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers.
2
Understand the concept of badal
The passage states that tayammum is a substitute (badal) by consensus. However, the nature of that substitution is disputed.
Consensus (ittifaq) exists on the basic status of tayammum as a substitute; ikhtilaf arises on its modality.
3
Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i views
Hanafis: tayammum is an absolute substitute (badal mutlaq) – it is not a necessity (laysa bi-daruri). Shafi'is (opposing school) hold it is a restricted substitute tied to necessity. The passage gives only the Hanafi view due to truncation.
The text cuts off after saying 'wa yarfa'' – presumably completing the Hanafi position. The full dispute is not present.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical implication: Hanafis allow one tayammum for multiple fard prayers and before the prayer time; Shafi'is require a new tayammum for each fard and after the time enters.
This difference directly affects the daily practice of a person without water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وصح قبل الوقت ولفرضين) أي صح التيمم قبل الوقت ولفرضين. اعلم أن التيمم بدل بلا شك اتفاقاً لكن اختلفوا في كيفية البدل في موضعين: أحدهما الخلاف فيه لأصحابنا مع الشافعي، فقال أصحابنا : هو بدل مطلق عند عدم الماء وليس بضروري ويرتفع
His statement (and it is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers): i.e., tayammum is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers. Know that tayammum is a substitute without doubt by agreement, but they differed in the manner of substitution in two places: one of them is the dispute of our companions with al-Shafi'i: so our companions said: it is an absolute substitute in the absence of water, not a necessity, and it is raised [by finding water?] ...
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the validity of tayammum. The commentator Ibn Nujaym explains the concise text: 'Wa saha qabla al-waqt wa li-fardayn' meaning that tayammum is valid before the time of the obligatory prayer (i.e., you can perform tayammum before the prayer time begins, unlike wudu which is typically done after time enters) and it is valid for performing two fard prayers with one tayammum (as long as the tayammum is not broken). The passage then notes a fundamental point: tayammum is a substitute (badal) for wudu or ghusl, and there is consensus on that. However, there is a dispute on the nature of this substitution in two aspects, the first being between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that tayammum is an absolute substitute (badal mutlaq) meaning it is not a mere necessity that is nullified by the entry of time; rather, it is a full purification that raises the state of ritual purity (raf' al-hadath) just like wudu. It is not considered a 'necessity' (daruri) that disappears as soon as the necessity passes; rather, it remains valid until water is found or until it is broken by any of its nullifiers. The text cuts off before stating the Shafi'i view, which is that tayammum is only a substitute in times of necessity and becomes void as soon as one finds water or the time for the prayer ends. This distinction has practical implications for the permissibility of praying multiple fard prayers with one tayammum and of performing tayammum before the prayer time.

Key Terms
بدل مطلق (badal muṭlaq): An absolute substitute: tayammum is a full replacement for wudu/ghusl that removes ritual impurity (raf' al-hadath) and remains valid until nullified by water or other nullifiers.
ضروري (ḍarūrī): A necessity; the Hanafis negate that tayammum is merely a necessity (ليس بضروري), meaning it is a proper purification in its own right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the nature of tayammum?
A) It is a necessity substitute that becomes void when the time enters.
B) It is an absolute substitute that removes ritual impurity and remains valid until water is found.
C) It is only valid for one fard prayer and must be renewed for the next.
D) It is not a substitute for wudu but only for ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum in the Hanafi school is an absolute substitute (badal mutlaq) that remains valid for multiple fard prayers and before the prayer time, as long as water is not found and it is not nullified.
