Timing of Prayer with Tayammum when Hoping for Water
Expansion on the ruling of delaying tayammum prayer based on hope of water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on delaying prayer with tayammum when hoping for water, and apply the conditions of hope and distance to determine the mustahabb timing.

Core Idea
If you hope for water, delay prayer to the end of the second half; if not, pray at its beginning.

This lesson examines the precise timing for performing prayer with tayammum when water is expected later. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a person who hopes to find water and one who does not. We will unpack the definition of 'desirable time,' the role of distance to water, and a historical ijtihad of Imam Abu Hanifa that shaped this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage states that a person hoping for water should delay the prayer. Understand that this applies to tayammum and that the delay is mustahabb (desirable), not obligatory.
2
Define the desirable time (waqt al-istihbab)
According to the text, the desirable time is the first part of the last half of the prayer time range. Know that this is the baseline for recommendation.
The desirable time is not the very beginning, nor the very end.
3
Analyze the hope condition
When hoping for water, the recommended timing shifts: it becomes mustahabb to delay beyond the first part of the second half, up to the end of the second half.
If no hope, perform at the beginning of the second half.
4
Apply the distance condition
The passage adds a condition for a traveler certain or strongly presuming water at the end: if the distance is a mile or more, tayammum at the beginning is permissible; if less and he fears missing the time, tayammum is not allowed.
This condition refines when tayammum at the beginning is permissible, not the desirability of delay.
5
Examine the historical precedent
The story of Abu Hanifa and his teacher Hammad illustrates the ijtihad: Hammad prayed early, but Abu Hanifa delayed and found water, establishing the preferred practice.
This shows the development of the ruling within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤخر الصلاة وصح قبل الوقت ولفرضين وحوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد ولو بناء وقت يؤدي الخلاصة أي عن وقت الاستحباب وهو أول النصف الأخير من الوقت في الصلاة التي يستحب تأخيرها، أما إذا كان يرجو فالمستحب تأخيرها عن هذا الوقت المستحب، وهذا هو مراد من قال بعدم استحباب التأخير إذا كان لا يرجو، وليس المراد بالتعجيل الفعل في أول وقت الجواز حتى يلزم أن يكون أفضل، ويدل على ما قلناه ما ذكره الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي بقوله : وإن لم يكن على طمع من وجود الماء فإنه يتيمم ويصلي في وقت مستحب ولم يقل يصلي في أول الوقت. وقال الكردري في مناقبة والأوجه أن يحمل استحباب التأخير مع الرجاء إلى آخر النصف الثاني وعدم استحبابه إلى هذا عند عدم الرجاء بل الأفضل عند عدم الرجاء الأداء في أول النصف الثاني بدليل قولهم المستحب أن يسفر بالفجر في الصلاة بالقراءة المسنونة، ثم لو بدا له في الصلاة الأولى ريب يؤدي الثانية بالطهارة والتلاوة المسنونة أيضاً، وذلك لا يتأتى إلا في أول النصف الثاني اهـ. وفي غيرها : المسافر إذا كان على تيقن من وجود الماء أو غالب ظنه على ذلك في آخر الوقت فتيمم في أول الوقت وصلى؛ إن كان بينه وبين الماء مقدار ميل جاز، وإن كان أقل ولكن يخاف الفوت لا يتيمم .اهـ. فحاصله أن البعد مجوز للتيمم مطلقاً. وفي معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المجتبى : ويتخالج في قلبي فيما إذا كان يعلم أنه إن أخر الصلاة إلى آخر الوقت بقرب من الماء بمسافة أقل من ميل لكن لا يتمكن من الصلاة بالوضوء في الوقت، الأولى أن يصلي في أول الوقت مراعاة لحق الوقت وتجنباً عن الخلاف .اهـ. وذكر في المناقب أن هذه المسألة أول واقعة خالف أبو حنيفة أستاذه حماداً فصلى حماد بالتيمم في أول الوقت، ووجد أبو حنيفة الماء في آخر الوقت وصلاها وكان ذلك غرة اجتهاده فقبلها الله تعالى منه وصوبه فيه، وكانت هذه الصلاة صلاة المغرب وكان خروجهما لأجل تشييع الأعمش .
He delays the prayer, and it is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers, and fear of missing a funeral or Eid prayer, even if based on time... The summary: i.e., from the time of desirability, which is the first of the last half of the time in the prayer that is desirable to delay. As for if he hopes [for water], then it is desirable to delay it beyond this desirable time, and this is the meaning of the one who said there is no desirability of delay if he does not hope. And the meaning of hastening is not the act at the beginning of the permissible time such that it would be better. And what indicates what we said is what al-Isbijabi mentioned in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: 'And if he has no hope of finding water, he performs tayammum and prays at a desirable time, and he did not say pray at the beginning of the time.' And al-Kardari said in al-Manaqib: 'The more appropriate view is that the desirability of delay when hoping is to the end of the second half, and its absence when not hoping is to the end of that [i.e., the second half as well], rather the best when not hoping is to perform at the beginning of the second half, based on their saying: it is desirable to perform Fajr with the reading of the sunnah prayer, then if doubt occurs to him in the first prayer, he performs the second prayer with purification and the sunnah recitation as well, and that is only possible at the beginning of the second half.' And in other works: 'The traveler, if he is certain of finding water or has strong presumption at the end of the time, then he performs tayammum at the beginning of the time and prays; if between him and the water is a distance of a mile, it is permissible, and if less but he fears missing [the time], he does not perform tayammum.' So the conclusion is that distance makes tayammum permissible absolutely. And in Miraj al-Diraya, citing al-Mujtaba: 'It occurs to me that if he knows that if he delays the prayer to the end of the time he will be near water at a distance less than a mile but cannot pray with wudu within the time, the better is to pray at the beginning of the time, out of regard for the right of the time and to avoid disagreement.' And it is mentioned in al-Manaqib that this issue was the first incident in which Abu Hanifa differed from his teacher Hammad. Hammad prayed with tayammum at the beginning of the time, and Abu Hanifa found water at the end of the time and prayed, and that was the beginning of his ijtihad, and Allah accepted it from him and approved him in it. This prayer was Maghrib, and their outing was to bid farewell to al-A'mash.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling that one who hopes to find water should delay the prayer to the end of the time. The commentary explains that the 'desirable time' for prayer is the first part of the second half of the time range. If one hopes to find water, it is desirable to delay beyond that to the end of the second half. If one does not hope, then it is better to pray at the beginning of the second half. The author supports this with quotes from al-Isbijabi and al-Kardari, and then discusses the case of a traveler who is certain or has strong presumption of water at the end of the time: if the distance is a mile or more, tayammum at the beginning is allowed; if less, it is not allowed unless he fears missing the time. The passage ends with the story of Abu Hanifa differing from his teacher Hammad, showing the practical ijtihad.

Key Terms
وقت الاستحباب (waqt al-istihbab): The time when it is desirable (mustahabb) to perform prayer; here defined as the first part of the last half of the time range.
رجاء الماء (rajā' al-mā'): Hope of finding water before the end of the prayer time, which triggers the desirability of delaying the prayer.
ميل (mīl): A mile, a unit of distance used in Hanafi fiqh to determine conditions for tayammum. One mile is approximately 1.6 km.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler hopes to find water later, when is it desirable to pray with tayammum?
A) At the beginning of the time
B) In the first half of the time
C) At the end of the second half of the time
D) At the middle of the time

Key Takeaway
When hoping for water, delaying prayer to the end of the second half is mustahabb; otherwise, pray at the beginning of the second half.

Tayammum Before Time and for Multiple Prayers: The Hanafi Position and Disputes
Expansion on ruling of tayammum before time and for multiple prayers with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tayammum is valid before the prayer time and for multiple obligatory prayers, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument along with the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Tayammum is an absolute substitute that removes hadath, so it is valid before time and for multiple prayers.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rule that tayammum is valid before the prayer time and for multiple fard prayers. It addresses two key disputes: one with Imam al-Shafi'i on the nature of tayammum, and another among the Hanafi imams themselves on the basis of substitution. Understanding these disputes clarifies why the Hanafi school allows tayammum before the time and for more than one obligatory prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that tayammum is an absolute substitute that removes hadath until water is found, so it is valid before prayer time and for multiple obligatory prayers.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that tayammum is a necessary substitute that permits prayer while impurity remains, so it cannot be done before time and only for one fard.
This is based on his view that tayammum does not remove hadath.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i uses qiyas to istihada purification (which is not allowed before time) and weak athar from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ali that restrict tayammum to one prayer.
The Hanafis refute the qiyas by noting istihada has a contradiction (blood flow) while tayammum has none, and the athar are weak in chain.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter that the hadith 'turab tahur al-muslim' proves earth is a purifier, and thus tayammum removes hadath. The Shafi'i qiyas is invalid due to a clear difference in the underlying cause.
The Hanafi response relies on the explicit text and the principle of istihsan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafis can perform tayammum before time and pray multiple fard with one tayammum; Shafi'is must wait for the time and cannot combine more than one obligatory prayer.
This difference has significant implications for travelers and those in water-scarce areas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وصح قبل الوقت ولفرضين) أي صح التيمم قبل الوقت ولفرضين. اعلم أن التيمم بدل بلا شك اتفاقاً لكن اختلفوا في كيفية البدل في موضعين: أحدهما الخلاف فيه لأصحابنا مع الشافعي، فقال أصحابنا : هو بدل مطلق عند عدم الماء وليس بضروري ويرتفع به الحدث إلى وقت وجود الماء لا أنه للصلاة مبيح مع قيام الحدث. وقال الشافعي : هو بدل ضروري مبيح مع قيام الحدث حقيقة فلا يجوز قبل الوقت ولا يصلي به أكثر من فريضة عنده، وعندنا يجوز. وفي أنائين طاهر ونجس يجوز التيمم عندنا خلافاً له، ولهذا يبني الخلاف تارة على أنه رافع للحدث عندنا عنده لا رافع، وتارة على أنه طهارة ضرورية مبيح عنده مطلقة عندنا، واقتصر على الثاني صاحب الهداية. ويدفع مبنى الشافعي الأول بأن اعتبار الحدث مانعيه عن الصلاة شرعية لا يشكل معه أن التيمم رافع لارتفاع ذلك المنع به وهو الحق إن لم يقم على أكثر من ذلك دليل، وتغير الماء برفع الحدث إنما يستلزم اعتباره نازلاً عن وصفه الأول بواسطة إسقاط الفرض لا بواسطة إزالة وصف حقيقي مدنس، ويدفع الثاني بأنه طهور حال عدم الماء بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم التراب طهور «المسلم وقال في حديث الخصائص في الصحيحين وجعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً يريد به مطهراً وإلا لما تحققت الخصوصية لأن طهارة الأرض بالنسبة إلى سائر الأنبياء .ثابتة. وإذا كان مطهراً فتبقى طهارته إلى وجود غايتها من وجود الماء أو ناقض آخر . والثاني الخلاف فيه بين أصحابنا، فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف البدلية بين الماء والتراب وعند محمد بين الفعلين وهما التيمم والوضوء، ويتفرع عليه جواز اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم فأجازاه ومنعه وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. وقاس الشافعي كما ذكره النووي عدم جوازه قبل الوقت على عدم جواز طهارة المستحاضة قبل الوقت. وقال النووي: إنهم وافقونا عليه ومنع أئمتنا الحكم في المقيس عليه لأن المذهب عندنا جواز وضوئها قبل الوقت ولا ينتقض بالدخول ولئن سلم على قول من يقول بنقضها بالدخول فالفرق بينهما أن طهارة المستحاضة قد وجد ما ينافيها وهو سيلان الدم، والتيمم لم يوجد له رافع بعده وهو الحدث، أو وجود الماء فيبقى على ما كان كالمسح على الخفين بل أقوى لأن المسح مؤقت بمدة قليلة والشارع جوز التيمم ولو إلى عشر حجج ما وقولهم لا ضرورة قبله ممنوع لأن المندوب التطهر قبل الوقت ليشتغل أول الوقت بالأداء، وما استدلوا به من أثر ابن عباس قال : من السنة أن لا يصلي بالتيمم أكثر من صلاة واحدة. رواه الدارقطني. ومن أثر ابن عمر قال : يتيمم لكل صلاة وإن لم يحدث. رواه البيهقي. ومن أثر علي قال : يتيمم لكل صلاة فالكل ضعيف لأن في سند الأول الحسن بن عمارة تكلموا فيه. قال بعضهم : متروك. ذكره مسلم في مقدمة كتابه في جملة من تكلم فيه. رواه عنه أبو يحيى الجماني وهو متروك. وفي سند الثاني عامر ضعفه ابن عيينة وأحمد بن حنبل لم يجد الماء . المستحب إلا إذا تضمن التأخير فضيلة، ولذا قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أن ما في الاسبيجابي مشترك الإلزام اهـ أي أنه محتمل فللخصم أن يقول إنه دليل لي أيضاً قوله (لأن المندوب التطهر قبل الوقت) قال الرملي : : هذا صريح في أن التيمم قبل الوقت مندوب وقل من صرح به. البحر الرائق ج ١ م ١٨
His statement (and it is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers): i.e., tayammum is valid before the time and for two obligatory prayers. Know that tayammum is a substitute without doubt by consensus, but they differed regarding the manner of substitution in two places: One of them is the dispute of our companions with al-Shafi'i. Our companions said: It is an absolute substitute in the absence of water, not a necessary one, and it removes the state of ritual impurity (hadath) until the time of finding water, not that it merely permits prayer while impurity remains. Al-Shafi'i said: It is a necessary substitute that permits [prayer] while impurity remains in reality, so it is not allowed before the time, nor can one pray more than one obligatory prayer with it according to him, whereas with us it is allowed. And in the case of two vessels, one pure and one impure, tayammum is allowed with us contrary to him. Hence the dispute is built sometimes on that it removes hadath with us, not with him, and sometimes on that it is a necessary purification that permits with him, and absolute with us. The author of al-Hidayah confined to the second. And he refutes the first basis of al-Shafi'i by saying that the consideration of hadath as a legal impediment to prayer does not conflict with tayammum removing that impediment, and that is the truth if no proof to the contrary exists. And the alteration of water by removing hadath only necessitates considering it descending from its first description by means of waiving the obligation, not by removing a real contaminating description. And he refutes the second by saying that it is a purifier (tahur) in the absence of water by his statement (peace be upon him): 'Turab tahur al-muslim' (The soil is a purifier for the Muslim). And in the hadith of special characteristics in the two Sahihs: 'And the earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier (tahur),' meaning a purifier (mutahhir), otherwise the characteristic would not be realized because the purity of earth for other prophets is established. And if it is a purifier, then its purification remains until its end is reached, which is the existence of water or another nullifier. The second dispute is among our companions: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the substitution is between water and soil; according to Muhammad, between the two actions, namely tayammum and wudu. And branching from this is the permissibility of a person with wudu following a person with tayammum in prayer; the two allowed it and he (Muhammad) prevented it, and it will come later if Allah wills. And al-Shafi'i analogized, as mentioned by al-Nawawi, the impermissibility before the time to the impermissibility of a mustahada (woman with chronic bleeding) performing purification before the time. Al-Nawawi said: They agreed with us on that, and our imams prevented the ruling in the analogized case because the madhhab with us is that her wudu is permissible before the time and is not nullified by entering [the time]. And even if it is conceded according to the one who says it is nullified by entering, then the difference between them is that the purification of the mustahada has something that contradicts it, namely the flowing blood, whereas tayammum has no after that which lifts it, namely hadath or the existence of water, so it remains as it is, like wiping over khuffs, rather stronger, because wiping is limited to a short period, and the Lawgiver allowed tayammum even for ten years and more. And their saying: 'There is no necessity before the time' is rejected because it is recommended to purify before the time to occupy oneself with performance at the beginning of the time. And what they adduced from the athar of Ibn Abbas: 'It is from the sunna not to pray with tayammum more than one prayer,' narrated by al-Daraqutni, and from the athar of Ibn Umar: 'He performs tayammum for every prayer even if he does not have hadath,' narrated by al-Bayhaqi, and from the athar of Ali: 'He performs tayammum for every prayer' – all are weak because in the chain of the first is al-Hasan ibn Umara whom they criticized; some said he is abandoned. Muslim mentioned him in the introduction to his book among those criticized. It was narrated from him by Abu Yahya al-Jumani who is also abandoned. In the chain of the second is 'Amir, whom Ibn Uyayna and Ahmad ibn Hanbal declared weak. He did not find water. The desirable [time] is only if the delay includes a virtue. Hence, it is said in al-Nahr: 'It is not hidden that what is in al-Isbijabi is binding on both sides,' i.e., it is ambiguous, so the opponent can say it is also evidence for me. His statement (because it is recommended to purify before the time): al-Ramli said: This is explicit that tayammum before the time is recommended (mandub), and few have stated it explicitly. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 1, part 18.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rule that tayammum is valid before the prayer time and for more than one obligatory prayer. The commentary first explains that tayammum is a substitute by consensus, but there are two areas of disagreement: first between Hanafis and Shafi'is, and second among the Hanafi imams themselves. Against al-Shafi'i, the Hanafis argue that tayammum is an absolute substitute that actually removes hadath until water is found, not merely a license for prayer while impurity remains. This is supported by hadiths calling earth a 'tahur' (purifier). The Hanafi position allows tayammum before the time and for multiple prayers, while al-Shafi'i restricts it. The second dispute is among Hanafis: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf view the substitution as between water and soil, while Muhammad views it as between the acts of wudu and tayammum. This affects the ruling on whether a person with wudu can follow a mutayammim in prayer. The author then refutes the Shafi'i analogy to istihada and weakens the athar (reports) from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ali. Finally, it notes that some earlier sources indicate that tayammum before time is recommended (mandub), a point rarely stated.

Key Terms
بدل مطلق (badal mutlaq): An absolute substitute that completely replaces the original (water) and removes the need for it until water is found.
طهور (tahur): A purifier; something that inherently purifies, like water and soil in the state of taharah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a person perform tayammum before the time of prayer and then pray multiple obligatory prayers with that tayammum?
A) No, only before time but not for multiple prayers
B) Yes, both are allowed
C) Only for one prayer, not before time
D) It is not allowed before time, but multiple prayers are allowed

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a full substitute for water, thus valid before time and for multiple obligatory prayers—a distinctive Hanafi ruling.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Nature of Tayammum: Raf' al-Hadath vs. Mubih
Dispute with Shafi'i on tayammum's nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tayammum's legal nature, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the schools.

Core Idea
Tayammum removes hadath — it is a true purification, not a mere permitter.

The nature of tayammum — dry ablution — is not merely a theoretical question; it has direct practical consequences for when and how many prayers one can perform. The Hanafi school holds that tayammum actually removes ritual impurity (hadath) until water is found, while the Shafi'i school argues it only permits prayer without removing impurity. This lesson examines the proofs and implications of this key dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly do the Hanafis hold regarding tayammum? It removes hadath, so it is a rafi' (remover).
This is the starting point – know your school's view.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tayammum does not remove hadath; it is a mubih (permitter) that allows prayer while impurity persists.
Opponent's position must be stated fairly.
3
Examine the first basis of dispute
The Shafi'i argues that hadath is a legal impediment; the Hanafi refutes that removal of the impediment is possible without removing the impurity itself.
Focus on the distinction between legal and physical impurity.
4
Examine the second basis
The Hanafis interpret 'طهور' in the hadith as 'مطهر' (purifying agent), not merely 'pure'. This supports tayammum as a true purification.
Linguistic analysis is key here.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference results? Hanafis allow tayammum before prayer time and multiple prayers with one tayammum; Shafi'is do not.
This is the real-world consequence of the dispute.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
به
الحدث إلى وقت وجود
الماء لا أنه
للصلاة
مبيح
مع قيام الحدث. وقال الشافعي : هو بدل
ضروري مبيح مع قيام الحدث حقيقة فلا يجوز قبل الوقت ولا يصلي به أكثر من فريضة عنده، وعندنا يجوز. وفي أنائين طاهر ونجس يجوز التيمم عندنا خلافاً له، ولهذا يبني الخلاف تارة على أنه رافع للحدث عندنا عنده لا رافع، وتارة على أنه طهارة ضرورية مبيح عنده مطلقة عندنا، واقتصر على الثاني صاحب الهداية. ويدفع مبنى الشافعي الأول بأن اعتبار الحدث مانعيه عن الصلاة شرعية لا يشكل معه أن التيمم رافع لارتفاع ذلك المنع به وهو الحق إن لم يقم على أكثر من ذلك دليل، وتغير الماء برفع الحدث إنما يستلزم اعتباره نازلاً عن وصفه الأول بواسطة إسقاط الفرض لا بواسطة إزالة وصف حقيقي مدنس، ويدفع الثاني بأنه طهور حال عدم الماء بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم التراب طهور «المسلم وقال في حديث الخصائص في الصحيحين وجعلت لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً يريد به مطهراً وإلا لما تحققت الخصوصية لأن طهارة الأرض بالنسبة إلى سائر الأنبياء .ثابتة. وإذا كان مطهراً فتبقى طهارته إلى وجود غايتها من وجود الماء أو ناقض آخر .
The Book of Purification - Chapter on Tayammum. He said: It removes the hadath until the time of finding water, not that it is merely a permitter of prayer while the hadath persists. Al-Shafi'i said: It is an essential substitute that permits prayer while the hadath actually persists, so it is not permissible before the time, and one cannot pray more than one obligatory prayer with it according to him, while according to us it is permissible. And in the case of two vessels, one pure and one impure, tayammum is permissible according to us, contrary to him. Therefore, the disagreement is sometimes based on the fact that it removes hadath according to us, while according to him it does not, and sometimes on the fact that it is an essential purification that permits according to him but is absolute according to us. The author of al-Hidayah restricted himself to the second. The first basis of al-Shafi'i is refuted because considering the hadath as a legal impediment to prayer does not contradict that tayammum removes that impediment, and that is the truth if no further evidence is established. The change of water by removing hadath only necessitates considering it as descending from its first description by virtue of dropping the obligation, not by virtue of removing a real corrupting description. The second is refuted by the fact that it is a purifier in the absence of water, by his saying (peace be upon him): 'The earth is a purifier for the Muslim.' And in the Hadith of Special Characteristics in the two Sahihs: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier' — meaning a purifying agent, otherwise the specificity would not be realized, because the purity of the earth is established for other prophets. And if it is a purifying agent, then its purification remains until its end is reached by the existence of water or another invalidator.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational intra-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the nature of tayammum (dry ablution). The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author first states the Hanafi position: tayammum removes the state of ritual impurity (hadath) until water is found, meaning it is not merely a permitter for prayer while impurity remains. Al-Shafi'i, however, holds that tayammum is a necessary substitute that permits prayer but does not actually remove hadath; the impurity persists. Consequently, al-Shafi'i rules that tayammum cannot be performed before the prayer time and that only one obligatory prayer may be prayed with a single tayammum. The Hanafi school allows multiple prayers. The disagreement is then analyzed on two bases: (1) whether tayammum is a remover (raf') of hadath, and (2) whether it is a restricted or absolute permitter. The author refutes the Shafi'i position on the first basis by arguing that considering hadath as a legal impediment does not negate that tayammum lifts that impediment. The second basis is refuted by the hadith 'The earth is a purifier for the Muslim' and the hadith in the Sahihayn that the earth was made a mosque and a purifier (طهور). The word طهور is interpreted as مطهر (purifying agent), implying that tayammum is a true purification that remains effective until water is found or another invalidator occurs.

Key Terms
رفع الحدث (raf' al-hadath): The removal of ritual impurity (hadath) by tayammum, making the person pure for prayer.
مبيح (mubih): That which permits an action that was previously forbidden due to impurity, without removing the impurity itself.
طهور (tahur): A purifier; something that makes others pure (مطهر). The hadith calls earth طهور for the Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal nature of tayammum?
A) It is a temporary permit that does not remove hadath.
B) It is a purifier that removes hadath until water is found.
C) It is only valid for one obligatory prayer.
D) It cannot be performed before the prayer time.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum, in the Hanafi school, is a true purification (raf' al-hadath), allowing multiple prayers and pre-time performance, based on the interpretation of 'طهور' as a purifier.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Substitution in Tayammum
Intra-Hanafi disagreement on the nature of tayammum's substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on the nature of tayammum's substitution and explain the practical consequence for following a mutayammim in prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum substitutes water according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but the act of wudu according to Muhammad.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq reveals an important intra-Hanafi difference: what exactly does tayammum substitute? The answer shapes a practical ruling on congregational prayer. Let's examine the two positions and their branch application.

Guided Path
1
State the legal issue
Identify the core question of the dispute: what does tayammum substitute for? Is it water itself or the act of wudu?
This is a dispute about badaliyyah (substitution).
2
Identify the two positions
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf view substitution between water and earth; Muhammad views it between the two actions (tayammum and wudu).
These are the two intra-Hanafi views.
3
Connect to the branch ruling
The branch ruling (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a person with wudu may pray behind a person with tayammum. The two shaykhs allow it; Muhammad prohibits it.
This shows how a conceptual difference leads to a practical difference.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allowing the follower to pray behind a mutayammim.
The author implies this will be elaborated later.
5
Note the authority weight
The view of the two shaykhs is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is preferred due to majority and practical ease.
This illustrates the hierarchy of authority within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني الخلاف فيه بين أصحابنا، فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف البدلية بين الماء والتراب وعند محمد بين الفعلين وهما التيمم والوضوء، ويتفرع عليه جواز اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم فأجازاه ومنعه وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
The second disagreement is among our scholars: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the substitution is between water and earth; according to Muhammad, it is between the two actions, i.e., tayammum and wudu. And a branch issue arises: the permissibility of a person who has performed wudu following (as a muqtadi) a person who has performed tayammum—the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permitted it, while Muhammad prohibited it, and this will come later, God willing.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (intra_hanafi_dispute) regarding the nature of substitution (بدلية) in tayammum. The text states that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, tayammum is a substitute for water itself, meaning that earth takes the place of water as a purifying medium. According to Imam Muhammad, however, the substitution is between the two actions: tayammum is a substitute for the act of wudu, not for water per se. A practical consequence (themara) of this difference is the ruling on whether a person who has performed wudu (متوضىء) may validly pray behind a person who has performed tayammum (متيمم) as an imam. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it, because the imam's tayammum is considered a valid purification equivalent to wudu, so the follower's wudu does not conflict. Imam Muhammad prohibits it, because he sees tayammum as a substitute for the action of wudu, but the follower has performed actual wudu, so there is a discrepancy. The author notes that this will be discussed in more detail later.

Key Terms
بدلية (badaliyyah): The concept of substitution; tayammum is a substitute (badal) for either water or the act of wudu.
اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم (iqtida' al-mutawaddi' bi al-mutayammim): The act of a person who has performed wudu following a person who has performed tayammum as an imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The obligation of niyyah in tayammum
D) The nullifiers of tayammum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two views on tayammum's substitution; the relied-upon view allows a person with wudu to follow a person with tayammum in prayer.

The Permissibility of Tayammum Before Prayer Time and Refutation of Shafi'i Evidence
Establishing the permissibility of tayammum before the prayer time with proof from hadith and refutation of weak aathar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum before the prayer time, explain the distinction between tayammum and istihadah’s purification, and evaluate the weakness of the athar cited by the Shafi'is.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid before time because the condition is absence of water, not entry of time; the Shafi'i analogy with istihadah fails due to continuous invalidator.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position that tayammum may be performed before the obligatory prayer time. While the Shafi'i school analogizes it to the case of a woman with istihadah (chronic bleeding), the Hanafis reject this analogy on clear grounds. We will also examine the athar (reports from Companions) used by the Shafi'is and see why the Hanafis consider them weak.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on tayammum before the time
Identify the ruling and its basis: tayammum is permissible (mustahabb) before the time, and one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers. The condition is absence of water, not entry of time.
This ruling is from the Hanafi school of thought.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its analogical basis
The Shafi'is analogize to the mustahadah's wudu before time, which they consider invalid. They argue that tayammum before time has no necessity.
Al-Nawawi is cited as mentioning this analogy.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing the two cases
The Hanafis refute by pointing out that in istihadah, blood continuously invalidates wudu immediately, whereas in tayammum there is no continuous invalidator. The only invalidators are finding water or a new hadath.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the athar evidence from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ali
The Shafi'is cite athar that claim tayammum is only for one prayer. The Hanafis show these are weak due to weak or abandoned narrators in their chains.
Details of the chains are provided in the passage.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the permissibility of tayammum before the time and for multiple prayers, as stated in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Hidayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

وقاس الشافعي كما ذكره النووي عدم جوازه قبل الوقت على عدم جواز طهارة المستحاضة قبل الوقت. وقال النووي: إنهم وافقونا عليه ومنع أئمتنا الحكم في المقيس عليه لأن المذهب عندنا جواز وضوئها قبل الوقت ولا ينتقض بالدخول ولئن سلم على قول من يقول بنقضها بالدخول فالفرق بينهما أن طهارة المستحاضة قد وجد ما ينافيها وهو سيلان الدم، والتيمم لم يوجد له رافع بعده وهو الحدث، أو وجود الماء فيبقى على ما كان كالمسح على الخفين بل أقوى لأن المسح مؤقت بمدة قليلة والشارع جوز التيمم ولو إلى عشر حجج ما وقولهم لا ضرورة قبله ممنوع لأن المندوب التطهر قبل الوقت ليشتغل أول الوقت بالأداء، وما استدلوا به من أثر ابن عباس قال : من السنة أن لا يصلي بالتيمم أكثر من صلاة واحدة. رواه الدارقطني. ومن أثر ابن عمر قال : يتيمم لكل صلاة وإن لم يحدث. رواه البيهقي. ومن أثر علي قال : يتيمم لكل صلاة فالكل ضعيف لأن في سند الأول الحسن بن عمارة تكلموا فيه. قال بعضهم : متروك. ذكره مسلم في مقدمة كتابه في جملة من تكلم فيه. رواه عنه أبو يحيى الجماني وهو متروك. وفي سند الثاني عامر ضعفه ابن عيينة وأحمد بن حنبل
لم يجد
الماء .
المستحب إلا إذا تضمن التأخير فضيلة، ولذا قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أن ما في الاسبيجابي مشترك الإلزام اهـ أي أنه محتمل فللخصم أن يقول إنه دليل لي أيضاً قوله (لأن المندوب التطهر قبل الوقت) قال الرملي : : هذا صريح في أن التيمم قبل الوقت مندوب وقل من صرح به.
Al-Shafi'i, as mentioned by al-Nawawi, analogized the impermissibility of tayammum before the time to the impermissibility of istihadah's purification before the time. Al-Nawawi said: They (Shafi'is) agreed with us on that (the analogy), but our imams prevented the ruling in the analogized case (i.e., the case of istihadah) because according to our school, her wudu before the time is permissible and is not invalidated by the entry of time. Even if we concede to those who say it is invalidated by entry of time, there is a difference: the purification of the woman with istihadah has something that contradicts it, namely the flow of blood; tayammum has no subsequent invalidator (i.e., hadath) after it except the existence of water, so it remains as it was, like wiping over khuffs—indeed stronger, because wiping is limited to a short period, while the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum even up to ten years. Their saying 'there is no necessity before the time' is rejected because performing purification before the time is recommended to occupy oneself with the prayer at the beginning of the time. What they adduced—the athar of Ibn Abbas: 'It is from the Sunnah not to pray more than one prayer with tayammum,' reported by al-Daraqutni; the athar of Ibn Umar: 'He would perform tayammum for every prayer even if he had not had an event,' reported by al-Bayhaqi; the athar of Ali: 'He would perform tayammum for every prayer'—all these are weak. The chain of the first includes al-Hasan ibn 'Umarah, about whom they spoke; some said he is abandoned (matruk). Muslim mentioned him in the introduction of his book among those about whom they spoke. Abu Yahya al-Jummani transmitted from him, and he is abandoned. The chain of the second includes 'Amir, whom Ibn 'Uyaynah and Ahmad ibn Hanbal declared weak. The third includes al-Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah and al-Harith al-A'war, both weak. Moreover, their apparent meaning is abandoned because they (the Hanafis) allow more than one prayer (including supererogatory) with tayammum provided it is performed for the obligatory one. The end of the passage mentions that the recommended (mustahabb) is purification before time, but only if delaying does not entail a superior virtue.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that tayammum is permissible before the prayer time, contrary to the analogy made by al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'is compare tayammum to the case of a woman with istihadah (chronic bleeding), where they hold that wudu before the time is invalid. The Hanafis reject this analogy on two grounds: First, in the Hanafi school, a mustahadah's wudu before the time is valid and not invalidated by the mere entry of time. Second, even if we accept the opposing view, there is a clear difference: in istihadah, blood (which invalidates wudu) is continuously present, so wudu before the time is immediately broken. In tayammum, there is no ongoing invalidator; the absence of water is the condition, and tayammum remains valid until water is found or another invalidator occurs. The author then refutes the athar (reports from Companions) cited by the Shafi'is. The athar from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ali all contain weak or abandoned narrators. For instance, al-Hasan ibn 'Umarah is matruk; 'Amir is declared weak by Ibn 'Uyaynah and Ahmad; al-Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah and al-Harith al-A'war are weak. Additionally, the apparent meaning of those athar is contradicted by established Hanafi practice allowing multiple prayers. Finally, the passage notes that performing tayammum before the time is mustahabb (recommended) according to some scholars, as it enables one to begin prayer immediately when the time enters.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman suffering from istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding); her wudu is valid before time according to Hanafis.
أثر (athar): A report from a Companion (or sometimes the Prophet) used as evidence; here the athar from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ali are examined.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended (mustahabb); an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do the Hanafis refute the analogy of tayammum to istihadah regarding pre-time purification?
A) They accept the analogy but make an exception.
B) They argue that in istihadah, blood continuously invalidates wudu, while in tayammum there is no ongoing invalidator.
C) They say the mustahadah's wudu is invalid anyway.
D) They claim the Shafi'i view is based on weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum before the prayer time is valid because the condition is absence of water, not the entry of time; the Shafi'i analogy with istihadah and the athar evidence are refuted by clear distinction and weak chains.

The Legal Definition of Shart in Tayammum: Co-Extensiveness (Musawi) as a Resolution
Usul al-fiqh analysis of shart and musawi in tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats absence of water as a condition for tayammum using the concept of musawi (co-extensiveness), and distinguish this from the general usul principle about conditions.

Core Idea
A condition that is co-extensive with its conditioned necessitates it — here absence of water and permissibility of tayammum are inseparable.

The Hanafi scholars state that earth is a purifier on condition of absence of water. At first glance, this seems to violate the usul rule that a condition does not necessitate its conditioned. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, citing al-`Inayah, resolves the tension by explaining that when a condition and its conditioned are co-extensive (musawi), the condition does necessitate the conditioned. In tayammum, the legal absence of water (which includes inability to use it) is co-extensive with the permissibility of tayammum. Let us examine this legal analysis step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The scholars say absence of water is a condition for tayammum, but usul says a condition does not necessitate.
This contradiction is only apparent.
2
Recognize the usul principle
In usul, a condition does not imply the existence or non-existence of the conditioned when the condition is present or absent.
The general principle is that a condition is not a cause.
3
Apply the musawi exception
If the condition and conditioned are co-extensive (musawi), they are equivalent, so the condition does necessitate.
This is a specific Hanafi point derived from al-`Inayah.
4
Verify co-extensiveness in tayammum
Absence of water (legally defined as inability to use water) and permissibility of tayammum are co-extensive: whenever one is true, the other is true.
This is proven by the inseparable relationship.
5
Address the objection of illness
Even if water is physically present, a sick person cannot use it, so water is legally absent; thus co-extensiveness holds.
The legal definition of 'absence' includes inability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه. ظاهر كلام المشايخ هنا أن الشرط يلزم من عدمه عدم المشروط فإنهم قالوا: إن التراب مطهر بشرط عدم الماء فإذا وجد الماء فقد الشرط ففقد المشروط وهو طهورية التراب . والمذكور في الأصول أن الشرط لا يلزم من عدمه العدم ولا من وجوده وجود ولا عدم والجواب أن الشرط إذا كان مساوياً للمشروط استلزمه وههنا كذلك، فإن كل واحد من عدم الماء وجواز التيمم مساو للآخر لا محالة فجاز أن يستلزمه كذا في العناية، فإن قلت: لا نسلم مساواتهما الجوازه مع وجوده حال مرضه قلت: ليس بموجود فيها حكماً لأن المراد به القدرة وهو ليس بقادر.
A note: The apparent meaning of the scholars here is that a condition (shart) necessitates that if it is absent, the conditioned (mashrut) is absent. They said: Earth is a purifier on condition of absence of water. So when water is present, the condition is lost, and thus the conditioned (the purifying quality of earth) is lost. But it is mentioned in usul that a condition does not necessitate absence when the condition is absent, nor does it necessitate existence or non-existence when the condition exists. The answer is that if the condition is co-extensive (musawi) with the conditioned, then it necessitates it, and here it is so. Indeed, each of absence of water and permissibility of tayammum is co-extensive with the other inevitably, so it is permissible to necessitate it. This is from al-`Inayah. If you say: We do not accept that they are co-extensive because it is permissible in the case of illness despite the presence of water. I say: It is not considered present legally because what is meant is ability, and he is not able (due to illness).
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (critical_refinement) on the nature of the condition (shart) in tayammum. The scholars have stated that the purity of earth is conditional on the absence of water (shart 'adam al-ma'). When water is present, the condition is lost, and consequently the conditioned (i.e., the purifying quality of earth) is lost. However, in usul al-fiqh, it is a principle that a condition does not necessarily entail the absence of the conditioned when the condition is absent, nor does it entail existence or non-existence when the condition exists. For example, wudu is a condition for prayer, but its absence does not necessarily mean prayer is invalid in all cases (e.g., if one cannot find water). The author resolves this apparent contradiction by stating that here the condition and the conditioned are co-extensive (musawi), meaning that they are exactly equivalent. The absence of water and the permissibility of tayammum are inseparable: whenever water is absent, tayammum is allowed; whenever water is present (and one can use it), tayammum is not allowed. This co-extensiveness allows the condition to necessitate the conditioned. A possible objection is raised: what about a person who is sick? He can perform tayammum even if water is present because he cannot use it due to illness. The answer is that 'absence of water' in this context legally means inability to use it (lack of power/قدرة), not mere existence. Since the sick person is not able to use water, water is legally absent for him, so the condition holds.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that must be fulfilled for the validity of tayammum; here specifically the absence of water or inability to use it.
مساو (musawi): Co-extensive; the condition and conditioned have the same extension, so one implies the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi school resolve the apparent contradiction between the statement that 'earth is a purifier on condition of absence of water' and the usul principle that a condition does not necessitate?
A) They reject the usul principle.
B) They argue that the condition is co-extensive (musawi) with the conditioned.
C) They say the condition is actually a cause.
D) They say it is a special case exempted by ijma.

Key Takeaway
The condition for tayammum is the legal absence of water, and this condition is co-extensive (musawi) with its permissibility, thus satisfying the usul principles.

Tayammum to Avoid Missing a Funeral Prayer
Detailed expansion on tayammum for funeral prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on tayammum when fearing missing a funeral prayer and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement concerning the wali.

Core Idea
Tayammum is allowed to avoid missing a funeral prayer, but the wali's right to repeat creates an intra-Hanafi dispute.

When a person fears missing the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) due to being in a state of impurity, tayammum may be a viable option. However, Hanafi scholars differ on whether the wali (guardian) of the deceased may resort to tayammum, since he has the right to repeat the prayer later. This lesson examines the general ruling, the conditions imposed by some authorities, and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The author states that tayammum is permissible (ja'iz) when one fears missing the funeral prayer. This is the baseline ruling.
The ruling is unconditional in the text but later restricted by al-Hidayah.
2
Examine al-Hidayah's restrictions
Al-Hidayah adds four conditions: funeral present, person healthy, in the city, and not the wali. Understand why each condition is proposed.
The author argues these conditions are unnecessary.
3
Analyze the critique of restrictions
The author rejects the first three conditions: a sick person may do tayammum absolutely; a traveler similarly; and before the funeral is present there is no fear of missing it. This leaves the wali as the main point of contention.
Focus on the wali's case.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on the wali
Al-Hidayah says the wali cannot do tayammum because he has the right to repeat (i'aadah). Zahir al-Riwayah says he can, because waiting is disliked. Other authorities grant permission if the wali is not the one with priority or if he authorizes another.
Trace the arguments from the text.
5
Determine the mufta bihi view
According to al-Sarakhsi, the view of Zahir al-Riwayah (permissibility for all) is the relied-upon position. The passage concludes with details on various scenarios.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة) أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة، أطلقه وقيده في الهداية بأربعة أشياء : حضور الجنازة وكونه صحيحاً وكونه في المصر وكونه ليس بولي، ووافقه على الأخير في الوافي ولا حاجة إلى هذه القيود أصلاً لأن المريض يرخص له التيمم مطلقاً، وكذا المسافر وقبل حضورها لا يخاف الفوت إذ الوجوب بالحضور، وكذا لا يخاف الفوت الولي مع أن في جوازه له خلافاً ففي الهداية الصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم لأن للولي حق الإعادة فلا فوات في حقه واختاره المصنف في الكافي. وصحح في التنجيس في الإمام عدم الجواز إن كانوا ينتظرونه وإلا جاز. وفي ظاهر الرواية جوازه لهما وصححه السرخسي. وقال صاحب الذخيرة لا فرق بين الإمام والمقتدى ومن له حق الصلاة لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه والمراد بالوالي من له التقدم حتى يجوز التيمم للسلطان والقاضي والوالي على ما في الهداية لأن الوالي إذا كان لا يجوز له التيمم وهو مؤخر فمن هو مقدم عليه أولى لأن المقدم على الولي له حق الإعادة لو صلى الولي، فعلى هذا يجوز التيمم للولي إذا كان من هو مقدم عليه حاضراً اتفاقاً لأنه يخاف الفوت إذ ليس له حق الإعادة لو صلى من هو مقدم عليه كما علم في الجنائز. وكذا يجوز للولي التيمم إذا أذن لغيره بالصلاة لأنه حينئذ لا حق له في الإعادة فيخاف فوتها، ولا يجوز لمن أمره الولي. كذا في الخلاصة. وهذه التفاريع التي ذكرناها إنما هي على مختار صاحب الهداية، أما على ظاهر الرواية فيجوز التيمم للكل عند خوف الفوت ولا فرق في جوازه عند الخوف بين كونه محدثاً أو جنباً أو حائضاً أو
His saying: 'And fear of missing a funeral prayer' means that tayammum is permissible due to fear of missing the funeral prayer. He made it absolute, but in al-Hidayah it was restricted by four things: presence of the funeral, being healthy, being in the city, and not being the wali (guardian). Al-Wafi agreed on the last restriction. But there is no need for these restrictions at all, because a sick person is absolutely permitted tayammum, and similarly a traveler; before the funeral is present there is no fear of missing it since obligation arises with presence; similarly the wali does not fear missing it, although there is a disagreement on its permissibility for him. In al-Hidayah, the correct view is that the wali is not permitted tayammum because he has the right to repeat the prayer (i'aadah), so there is no loss in his case, and this was chosen by the author in al-Kafi. In al-Tanjees, it was corrected that the imam is not permitted if they are waiting for him; otherwise it is permitted. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is permitted for both (imam and wali), and al-Sarakhsi corrected this. The author of al-Dhakhirah said: There is no difference between the imam, the muqtadi, and one who has the right to pray, because waiting in it (the funeral prayer) is disliked. What is meant by 'wali' (guardian) is one who has precedence (i.e., the imam). Thus tayammum is permitted for the sultan, the qadi, and the governor according to al-Hidayah, because if the wali when he is delayed is not permitted tayammum, then one who is ahead of him is more deserving. So on this basis, tayammum is permitted for the wali if someone who is ahead of him is present, unanimously, because he fears missing it since he does not have the right of i'aadah if the one ahead prays, as is known in funerals. Similarly, tayammum is permitted for the wali if he authorizes someone else to pray, because then he has no right of i'aadah, so he fears missing it. But it is not permitted for one whom the wali appointed. This is in al-Khulasah. These details are according to the choice of the author of al-Hidayah. As for Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is permitted for everyone when fearing missing it, and there is no difference in permissibility when fearing missing it whether one is in minor impurity, major impurity, or menstruating, or...
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling (ruling_with_proof) on tayammum when one fears missing a funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author first states the general rule: tayammum is permissible to avoid missing the funeral prayer. Then he notes that al-Hidayah imposes four restrictions: (1) the funeral is present, (2) the person is healthy, (3) he is in the city, and (4) he is not the wali (guardian/next of kin who has the right to lead the prayer). However, the author argues these restrictions are unnecessary: a sick person can do tayammum absolutely, a traveler can do tayammum absolutely, and before the funeral is present, there is no fear of missing it since the obligation to pray arises only when the funeral is present. As for the wali, there is disagreement. The strong view in al-Hidayah is that the wali cannot do tayammum because he has the right to repeat the prayer (if he misses it, he can pray later), so there is no real loss. This view is also chosen by the author of al-Kafi. However, al-Tanjees states that the imam (wali) is not allowed tayammum if the people are waiting for him; otherwise it is allowed. According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission), tayammum is allowed for both the wali and the imam, and al-Sarakhsi corrected this. The author of al-Dhakhirah says there is no distinction: tayammum is allowed for anyone who fears missing the funeral prayer. The passage then elaborates on the definition of 'wali' as one who has precedence (like the sultan, qadi, or governor). If such a person fears missing the prayer because someone with greater priority (like a superior) is present, then he may do tayammum because he does not have the right of repetition if the superior prays. Similarly, if the wali appoints someone else to lead, he loses his right of repetition and may do tayammum. But a person appointed by the wali cannot do tayammum according to this detailed view. The passage concludes by noting that these details are according to the chosen position of al-Hidayah; according to Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is permissible for everyone when fearing missing the funeral, regardless of whether one is in minor or major impurity or even menstruating.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian or next of kin of the deceased who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer, a fard kifayah, which has specific rulings regarding timing and repetition.
إعادة (i'aadah): The right to repeat the funeral prayer individually after the congregation has prayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, why is the wali (guardian) not permitted to perform tayammum when fearing missing a funeral prayer?
A) Because he is usually healthy and in the city.
B) Because he has the right to repeat the prayer (i'aadah), so there is no real loss.
C) Because he is not the imam.
D) Because he should always use water.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the stronger view is that tayammum is permitted for everyone who fears missing a funeral prayer, including the wali, but some authorities restrict it for the wali due to his right to repeat.

Tayammum for Fear of Missing Funeral Prayer: Hanafi Permission and Shafi'i Objection
Explaining permissibility of tayammum when fearing to miss janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits tayammum for the funeral prayer when fearing loss, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using textual proofs and the principle of necessity.

Core Idea
Tayammum for janazah is allowed when the entire prayer would be lost, because the person is functionally unable to perform wudu in time.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on performing tayammum for the funeral prayer when water is present but one fears missing the entire prayer. We will explore the key conditions, the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the wali, and the Shafi'i objection based on the condition of water absence. The analysis will involve proof texts and the principle of necessity (darurah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum for salat al-janazah. The Hanafi school rules it permissible (ja'iz) under certain conditions, not obligatory, because it is a concession.
The ruling is mubah, but with strict conditions: fear of missing all takbirs, inability to perform wudu in time, and for the wali, additional restrictions.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The primary proofs are the hadith of Ibn Abbas (even if mawquf it is strengthened by multiple chains), the practice of Ibn Umar, and the analogy (qiyas) with the Prophet's tayammum for returning the greeting without delay.
The hadith is reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Tahawi, and al-Nasa'i. The mawquf status does not harm it due to multiple supports.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that tayammum is only valid when water is absent (the condition). With water present, even if time is short, the condition is missing, so tayammum is invalid. He requires wudu or waiting for the next funeral.
This objection is based on a strict reading of the condition of tayammum in the Quran: 'if you find no water' (4:43).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi school responds that the person is considered unable (ajiz) because performing wudu would cause loss of the entire prayer, which is not replaceable. The condition of inability for tayammum is met effectively. The practical difference: Hanafis allow tayammum in this scenario; Shafi'is require wudu or delay.
The Hanafi response is strengthened by the principle of necessity and the Prophet's precedent. The dispute is legitimate and rooted in different usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
السند
وفي سماعه عن نافع نظر. وقال ابن خزيمة: الرواية فيه عن ابن عمر لا تصح. وفي الثالث الحجاج بن أرطأه والحارث الأعور وهما ضعيفان مع أن ظاهرهما متروك فإنهم يجوزون أكثر من صلاة واحدة من النوافل مع الفرض تبعاً له بشرط أن يتيمم له، فلو تيمم لصلاة النفل لا يجوز أن يؤدي الفرض به عنده وعلى عكسه يجوز .
تنبيه. ظاهر كلام المشايخ هنا أن الشرط يلزم من عدمه عدم المشروط فإنهم قالوا: إن التراب مطهر بشرط عدم الماء فإذا وجد الماء فقد الشرط ففقد المشروط وهو طهورية التراب . والمذكور في الأصول أن الشرط لا يلزم من عدمه العدم ولا من وجوده وجود ولا عدم والجواب أن الشرط إذا كان مساوياً للمشروط استلزمه وههنا كذلك، فإن كل واحد من عدم الماء وجواز التيمم مساو للآخر لا محالة فجاز أن يستلزمه كذا في العناية، فإن قلت: لا نسلم مساواتهما الجوازه مع وجوده حال مرضه قلت: ليس بموجود فيها حكماً لأن المراد به القدرة وهو ليس بقادر .
.
:
قوله (وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة) أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة، أطلقه وقيده في الهداية بأربعة أشياء : حضور الجنازة وكونه صحيحاً وكونه في المصر وكونه ليس بولي، ووافقه على الأخير في الوافي ولا حاجة إلى هذه القيود أصلاً لأن المريض يرخص له التيمم مطلقاً، وكذا المسافر وقبل حضورها لا يخاف الفوت إذ الوجوب بالحضور، وكذا لا يخاف الفوت الولي مع أن في جوازه له خلافاً ففي الهداية الصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم لأن للولي حق الإعادة فلا فوات في حقه واختاره المصنف في الكافي. وصحح في التنجيس في الإمام عدم الجواز إن كانوا ينتظرونه وإلا جاز. وفي ظاهر الرواية جوازه لهما وصححه السرخسي. وقال صاحب الذخيرة لا فرق بين الإمام والمقتدى ومن له حق الصلاة لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه والمراد بالوالي من له التقدم حتى يجوز التيمم للسلطان والقاضي والوالي على ما في الهداية لأن الوالي إذا كان لا يجوز له التيمم وهو مؤخر فمن هو مقدم عليه أولى لأن المقدم على الولي له حق الإعادة لو صلى الولي، فعلى هذا يجوز التيمم للولي إذا كان من هو مقدم عليه حاضراً اتفاقاً لأنه يخاف الفوت إذ ليس له حق الإعادة لو صلى من هو مقدم عليه كما علم في الجنائز. وكذا يجوز للولي التيمم إذا أذن لغيره بالصلاة لأنه حينئذ لا حق له في الإعادة فيخاف فوتها، ولا يجوز لمن أمره الولي. كذا في الخلاصة. وهذه التفاريع التي ذكرناها إنما هي على مختار صاحب الهداية، أما على ظاهر الرواية فيجوز التيمم للكل عند خوف الفوت ولا فرق في جوازه عند الخوف بين كونه محدثاً أو جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء كما صرح به في النهاية وغيرها ولا بد من خوف فوت التكبيرات كلها لو اشتغل بالطهارة، فإن كان أن يدرك البعض لا يتيمم لأنه لا يخاف الفوت لأنه يمكنه أداء الأول فلا يتيمم يرجو لها عند وجود الباقي وحده. كذا في البدائع والقنية وذكر ابن أمير حاج أنه لم يقف على هذا التفصيل في صلاة الجنازة فلله الحمد والمنة والأصل في هذه المسائل أن كل موضع يفوت الأداء لا إلى خلف يجوز له التيمم وفي كل موضع لا يفوت الأداء لا يجوز. ثم اعلم بأن الصلاة ثلاثة أنواع : نوع لا يخشى فواتها أصلاً لعدم توقتها كالنوافل، ونوع يخشى فواتها أصلاً كصلاة الجنازة والعيد ونوع يخشى فواتها وتقضى بعد وقتها أصلها أو بدلها كالجمعة والمكتوبات. أما الأول فلا يتيمم لها عند وجود الماء، وأما الثاني فيتيمم لها عند وجوده عندنا ومنعه الشافعي لأنه تيمم مع عدم شرطه وقلنا هو مخاطب بالصلاة عاجز عن الوضوء لها بفرض المسألة فيجوز التيمم، ويدل له تيممه عليه الصلاة والسلام لرد السلام مع وجود الماء على ما أسلفناه خشية الفوات لأنه لو رد بعد التراخي لا يكون جواباً له وفيه ما تقدم من الاحتمال. وروى ابن عدي في الكامل بسنده عن ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال إذا فجأتك الجنازة وأنت على غير وضوء فتيمم ثم قال : هذا مرفوعاً غير محفوظ بل هو موقوف على ابن عباس، ورواه ابن أبي شيبة عنه أيضاً ورواه الطحاوي في شرح الآثار وكذا رواه النسائي في كتاب الكني. وروى البيهقي من طريق بجهة الدارقطني أن ابن عمر أتى الجنازة وهو على غير وضوء فتيمم وصلى عليها والحديث إذا كثرت طرقه وتعاضدت قویت فلا يضره الوقف لأن الصحابة كانوا تارة يرفعون وتارة لا يرفعون. ولو حضرت جنازة أخرى بعد فراغه من الصلاة وخاف فوتها ففي المجمع يعيد عند محمد ولا يعيد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أن الخلاف فيما إذا لم يتمكن من التوضؤ بين الصلاتين، أما إذا تمكن ثم فات التمكن يعيد التيمم اتفاقاً. وفي الولوالجية وعليه الفتوى. وذكر الحلواني أن التيمم في بلادنا لا يجوز للجنازة لأن الماء حول مصلى الجنازة. وأما رواية القدوري فمطلقة كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي المستصفى : لا يقال إن النص ورد في الصلاة المطلقة وصلاة تؤخر بعذر إلى اليوم الثاني في الفطر وتكون قضاء، فإذا كان كذلك كانت مما يخلفها القضاء تأمل . قوله : (وفيه ما تقدّم من الاحتمال) وهو ما مر عن الكمال أنه أن يكون نوى معه ما معه من يجوز يصح التيمم .
قوله : (وفي الولوالجية وعليه الفتوى لم أجد هذا اللفظ في الولوالجية، نعم جزم في الخانية بهذا الشرط وقال (١) كما لو صلى وللمكتوبة صلى كان له أن يصلي به مكتوبة أخرى. قوله: (ولو كان (۱) قوله: (كما لو صلى الـخ كذا بخطه ولعله كما لو تيمم تأمل اهـ مصححه.
Book of Purity - Chapter of Tayammum. Chain: There is doubt in his hearing from Nafi'. Ibn Khuzaymah said: The narration from Ibn Umar is not authentic. In the third, al-Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah and al-Harith al-A'war are both weak, and their apparent meaning is forsaken. They permit more than one optional prayer along with the obligatory one as a follow-up to it, on condition that he performed tayammum for it. So if he performed tayammum for an optional prayer, he cannot perform the obligatory prayer with it according to him, and the opposite is allowed. Note: The apparent statement of the scholars here is that the condition necessarily implies the absence of the conditioned when absent. For they said: Earth is purifying on condition of absence of water. So if water exists, the condition is lost, so the conditioned is lost, which is the purifying property of earth. It is mentioned in Usul that the condition does not necessitate absence when absent, nor existence when present, nor non-existence. The answer is that if the condition is equal to the conditioned, it necessitates it, and here it is so. For each of absence of water and permissibility of tayammum is necessarily equal to the other, so it is possible that it necessitates it, as in al-Inayah. If you say: We do not accept their equality because of its permissibility with its existence during illness; I say: It is not existent in it effectively because what is meant is ability, and he is not able. His statement: (And fear of missing the funeral prayer) means tayammum is permissible for fear of missing the funeral prayer. It was stated absolutely and restricted in al-Hidayah by four things: presence of the funeral, being healthy, being in the city, and not being a guardian (wali). He agreed with the last in al-Wafi. There is no need for these restrictions at all because the sick person is excused for tayammum absolutely, and likewise the traveler. Before its presence, he does not fear missing because obligation is by presence. Likewise the wali does not fear missing, though there is a difference of opinion on its permissibility for him. In al-Hidayah the correct view is that he is not permitted to perform tayammum because the wali has the right to repeat, so there is no loss in his regard. The author chose this in al-Kafi. In al-Tanjis, it is corrected that the imam is not permitted if they are waiting for him, otherwise it is allowed. In Zahir al-Riwayah, it is permitted for both, and al-Sarakhsi corrected it. The author of al-Dhakhirah said: There is no difference between the imam, the follower, and one who has the right to pray, because waiting in it is disliked. What is meant by wali is the one who has precedence, so tayammum is permitted for the sultan, judge, and governor as in al-Hidayah, because if the wali is not permitted tayammum and he is delayed, then one who is ahead of him is more entitled. For one who is ahead of the wali has the right to repeat if the wali prayed. On this, tayammum is permitted for the wali if someone ahead of him is present, by agreement, because he fears missing since he has no right to repeat if the one ahead of him prayed, as known in funerals. Likewise, tayammum is permitted for the wali if he authorizes another to pray, because then he has no right to repeat, so he fears missing it. It is not permitted for the one whom the wali ordered. Thus in al-Khulasah. These branches we mentioned are according to the preference of the author of al-Hidayah. As for Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is permitted for all when fearing loss, and there is no difference in its permissibility when fearing loss between one who has minor impurity, major impurity, menstruating, or postpartum, as stated in al-Nihayah and others. It is necessary to fear missing all the takbirs if he occupies himself with purification. If he can catch some, he does not perform tayammum because he does not fear missing, because he can perform the first, so he does not perform tayammum hoping for the rest when found alone. Thus in al-Bada'i' and al-Qunyah. Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned that he did not come across this detail in funeral prayer. Praise be to Allah. The principle in these matters is that wherever performance is lost without substitute, tayammum is permitted, and wherever performance is not lost, it is not permitted. Then know that prayers are three types: a type that is never feared to be lost due to lack of time, like optional prayers; a type that is feared to be lost absolutely, like funeral and Eid prayers; and a type that is feared to be lost but can be made up after its time, either its original or substitute, like Friday and obligatory prayers. As for the first, he does not perform tayammum for it when water is present. As for the second, he performs tayammum for it when water is present, according to us. al-Shafi'i prohibited it because it is tayammum without its condition. We said: He is addressed with the prayer and unable to perform ablution for it in the given scenario, so tayammum is permitted. Evidence for this is the Prophet's (peace be upon him) tayammum for returning the greeting while water was present, as we previously mentioned, for fear of missing, because if he returned after delay, it would not be a response to him. There is the previous possibility. Ibn Adi narrated in al-Kamil with his chain from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'If the funeral suddenly comes upon you while you are not in ablution, perform tayammum.' Then he said: This is marfu' but not preserved; rather it is mawquf on Ibn Abbas. Ibn Abi Shaybah also narrated it from him, and al-Tahawi narrated it in Sharh al-Athar, and al-Nasa'i narrated it in Kitab al-Kuna. al-Bayhaqi narrated from the path of al-Daraqutni that Ibn Umar came to a funeral while not in ablution, so he performed tayammum and prayed over it. If a hadith is strengthened through multiple chains and mutual support, then being mawquf does not harm it, because the Companions sometimes raised it and sometimes did not. If another funeral occurs after he finishes the prayer and he fears missing it, then in al-Majma', he repeats according to Muhammad, and does not repeat according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. The author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that the difference is when he cannot perform ablution between the two prayers. If he could and then the ability passed, he repeats tayammum by agreement. In al-Walwaljiyyah, and the fatwa is upon it. al-Hulwani mentioned that tayammum in our country is not allowed for funeral because water is around the funeral prayer area. As for the narration of al-Quduri, it is absolute, as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. In al-Mustasfa: It should not be said that the text came regarding absolute prayer, and prayer delayed by excuse to the second day of Fitr becomes qada. If so, it is something that can be made up by qada, so reflect. His statement: (And in it is the previous possibility) which is what passed from al-Kamal, that he intended with it whatever is permissible for tayammum. His statement: (And in al-Walwaljiyyah, and the fatwa is upon it) I did not find this wording in al-Walwaljiyyah. However, it is certain in al-Khaniyyah with this condition, and said: (1) as if he prayed, and for the obligatory prayer, he had the right to pray another obligatory with it. His statement: (And if he was (1) his statement: (as if he prayed etc.) as in his handwriting, perhaps it is 'as if he performed tayammum' reflect, end of corrector.

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling of tayammum for fear of missing the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author first clarifies a technical point about the condition (shart) of absence of water for tayammum, explaining that according to the Hanafi school, the absence of water is a condition for the validity of tayammum, and if water is present, the condition is lost, so tayammum is invalid. This is defended by noting that the condition and conditioned are equal in entailment. The core discussion is the permissibility of tayammum when one fears missing the entire funeral prayer. The text presents the view of Imam al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) who restricts this to four conditions: the funeral is present, the person is healthy (not sick or traveling), he is in the city, and he is not the wali (guardian) of the deceased. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq argues that these restrictions are unnecessary because the sick and traveler are already excused for tayammum absolutely, and the wali also has a valid reason. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is permitted for all when fearing loss, including the wali. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that tayammum is permitted for the wali only if he fears missing the prayer, i.e., when there is someone ahead of him who has the right to lead and thus the wali loses his right to repeat. If the wali authorizes another to pray, tayammum is also permitted. The key principle is that tayammum is allowed only when the entire prayer (all takbirs) would be lost; if one can catch even a part, tayammum is not allowed. This is because the obligation is to perform the prayer in its entirety. The text then categorizes prayers into three types based on whether they can be missed absolutely or made up. Funeral and Eid prayers cannot be made up, so tayammum is permitted for them even if water is present, according to the Hanafis. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that tayammum requires the absence of water as a condition. The Hanafi response is that the person is obligated to pray but unable to perform ablution in time, so tayammum is valid. Evidence includes the Prophet's practice of tayammum to return the greeting without delay, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of Ibn Umar (though the hadith is mawquf, it is strengthened by multiple chains). The passage also discusses what happens if multiple funerals occur: according to Imam Muhammad, one must repeat tayammum for the second funeral if ablution is not possible between them; Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf say no repetition is needed if he did not have the ability to perform ablution. The fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's view. Finally, the passage notes that some later Hanafis restricted tayammum for funeral in lands where water is abundant near the prayer area, but the general ruling remains that it is permissible.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer, also called the 'wali al-mayyit'.
خوف فوت (khawf fawat): Fear of missing the entire prayer (all takbirs) if one delays to perform ablution.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-authenticated narrations from Imam Muhammad in his six books, considered the primary source of Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is tayammum permissible for a person who fears missing the funeral prayer?
A) Only if he is sick or traveling.
B) Only if he will miss the entire prayer (all takbirs).
C) Only if no water is available in the city.
D) Only if he is not the wali of the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for funeral prayer is a Hanafi concession based on the inability to perform ablution in time; the wali is generally excluded because he can repeat, but if his right to repeat is nullified, tayammum becomes permissible for him as well.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Tayammum for Funeral Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explaining the ruling on tayammum for funeral prayer with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tayammum for funeral prayer, identify the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the principle of necessity.

Core Idea
Tayammum is allowed for funeral prayer even with water present if using water would cause missing the prayer.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the ruling of tayammum for the funeral prayer, addressing a key dispute with the Shafi'i school. The central question is whether the fear of missing the entire prayer justifies tayammum when water is available. The Hanafi school affirms this based on the principle of necessity and prophetic practice, while the Shafi'i school requires actual unavailability of water. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its condition
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding tayammum for funeral prayer: it is permissible even if water is present, provided one fears missing all the takbirat if he performs wudu.
The condition is khawf fawt of the entire prayer, not just part of it.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State the Shafi'i position: tayammum is not allowed when water is present, because the condition of inability to find water is not met.
The Shafi'i school defines 'inability' as actual absence of water.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the two main pieces of evidence: (a) the Prophet's tayammum to return the salam despite water being present, and (b) the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas and practice of Ibn 'Umar.
The Hanafi proof extends the concept of 'inability' to include fear of losing the mandated act.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand the qiyas awla argument: if the stronger prayer (obligatory) is allowed with weaker purification (tayammum), then the weaker prayer (funeral) with weaker purification is even more appropriate.
This rebuts the Shafi'i objection that funeral prayer is not analogous to the salam case.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and practical difference
Recognize how the dispute affects actual practice: Hanafis allow tayammum in such situations, while Shafi'is require wudu even if it means missing the prayer.
The practical consequence is whether one can join the congregation or must pray alone later.

نفساء كما صرح به في النهاية وغيرها ولا بد من خوف فوت التكبيرات كلها لو اشتغل بالطهارة، فإن كان أن يدرك البعض لا يتيمم لأنه لا يخاف الفوت لأنه يمكنه أداء الأول فلا يتيمم ترجو لها عند وجود الباقي وحده. الصلاة وخاف فوتها ففي المجمع يعيد عند محمد ولا يعيد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أن الخلاف فيما إذا لم يتمكن من التوضؤ بين الصلاتين، أما إذا تمكن ثم فات التمكن يعيد التيمم اتفاقاً.
