المطلقة وصلاة تؤخر بعذر إلى اليوم الثاني في الفطر وتكون قضاء، فإذا كان كذلك كانت مما يخلفها القضاء تأمل . قوله : (وفيه ما تقدّم من الاحتمال) وهو ما مر عن الكمال أنه أن يكون نوى معه ما معه التيمم . يجوز من صح . قوله : (وفي الولوالجية وعليه الفتوى لم أجد هذا اللفظ في الولوالجية، نعم جزم في الخانية بهذا الشرط وقال (١) كما لو صلى وللمكتوبة صلى كان له أن يصلي به مكتوبة أخرى. قوله: (ولو كان (۱) قوله: (كما لو صلى الـخ كذا بخطه ولعله كما لو تيمم تأمل اهـ مصححه. الجنازة ليست في معناها لأنا نقول : لما جاز أداء أقوى الصلاتين بأضعف الطهارتين لأن يجوز أداء أضعف الصلاتين بأضعف الطهارتين أولى ..
(Continuation of) the postpartum woman, as stated in al-Nihayah and others. And it is necessary to fear losing all the takbirat if he occupies himself with purification. If he can still catch some, he does not perform tayammum because he does not fear loss, as he can perform the first (prayer) and then do tayammum for the remaining part alone. This is in al-Bada'i' and al-Qunyah. Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned that he did not come across this detail in the funeral prayer, so praise be to Allah. The principle in these matters is that wherever the performance is lost without alternative, tayammum is permissible; and wherever performance is not lost, it is not permissible. Then know that prayers are of three types: a type whose loss is not feared at all because it is not time-bound, like nawafil; a type whose loss is feared entirely, like the funeral and Eid prayers; and a type whose loss is feared but is made up after its time, either originally or as a substitute, like Friday and the obligatory prayers. As for the second type, we say tayammum is performed when water is present, but al-Shafi'i prohibits it because it is tayammum without its condition. We say: he is addressed with the prayer and unable to perform wudu for it by the assumption of the case, so tayammum is permissible. Evidence is the Prophet's tayammum for returning the greeting of salaam even though water was present, as we previously mentioned, due to fear of loss, because if he returned it later, it would not be a response to him. There is the earlier doubt. Ibn 'Adi narrated in al-Kamil with his chain from Ibn 'Abbas from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he said: 'If a funeral procession suddenly comes upon you and you are not in a state of wudu, then perform tayammum.' Then he said: This is marfu' but not preserved; rather it is mauquf on Ibn 'Abbas. Ibn Abi Shaybah also narrated from him. Al-Tahawi narrated it in Sharh al-Athar, and al-Nasa'i narrated it in Kitab al-Kuna. Al-Bayhaqi narrated via a chain from al-Daraqutni that Ibn 'Umar came to a funeral while not in wudu, so he performed tayammum and prayed over it. When a hadith's chains are numerous and mutually supportive, it is strengthened, and being mauquf does not harm it because the Companions sometimes would raise it and sometimes not. If another funeral occurs after he finishes the prayer and he fears missing it, then in al-Majma' he repeats (tayammum) according to Muhammad, but does not repeat according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. The author in al-Mustasfa mentioned that the disagreement is when he cannot perform wudu between the two prayers; if he could and then the opportunity was lost, he repeats tayammum by agreement. In al-Walwaljiyyah: and this is the fatwa. Al-Halwani mentioned that tayammum in our lands is not permissible for the funeral because water is around the funeral prayer area. The narration of al-Quduri is absolute, as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. In al-Mustasfa: It cannot be said that the text came for absolute prayer, and a prayer that is delayed by excuse to the second day of Fitr becomes a makeup; if so, it is something that qada' replaces. Ponder. His saying: (And there is the earlier doubt) which is what al-Kamal mentioned: that he intended with it the tayammum he has; it is permissible. His saying: (And in al-Walwaljiyyah, and this is the fatwa) I did not find this wording in al-Walwaljiyyah; yes, in al-Khaniyyah he affirmed this condition and said: just as if he prayed and for the obligatory prayer, he may pray another obligatory with it. His saying: (And if he was...) (His saying: (Just as if he prayed... etc.) in his handwriting, and perhaps it is: just as if he performed tayammum. Ponder. His correction. The funeral is not analogous to it, for we say: Since it is permissible to perform the stronger of the two prayers with the weaker of the two purifications, then to perform the weaker of the two prayers with the weaker of the two purifications is even more appropriate.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling of tayammum for funeral prayer, addressing the condition of fearing loss of the entire prayer and the inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i. The author begins by clarifying that tayammum is only allowed if one fears missing all the takbirat of the funeral prayer; if some can be caught, no tayammum. The principle is established: wherever the act of worship is lost entirely without substitute, tayammum is permitted; otherwise not. Then prayers are classified into three types: those with no time limit (nawafil), those lost entirely without substitute (funeral, Eid), and those lost but made up later. For the second type, we allow tayammum even when water is present, but al-Shafi'i disallows it. Our proof: the person is commanded to pray but unable to perform wudu due to the scenario (fear of loss). Evidence is the hadith of the Prophet performing tayammum to return the greeting of salaam despite water being present, to avoid losing the response. This hadith supports the principle. The author then addresses doubts: a marfu' hadith from Ibn 'Abbas and a mauquf report from Ibn 'Umar are cited; the chain strength is discussed. The passage also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: if another funeral occurs after the first, Imam Muhammad requires a new tayammum, while Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf do not, unless one could have performed wudu in between. Later statements from al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Halwani add practical conditions, such as prohibition in certain regions due to water availability. The passage concludes by rejecting an analogy that the funeral is not like the salam case, arguing that if stronger prayer can be performed with weaker purification, then weaker prayer with weaker purification is even more appropriate.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use would cause harm or loss of a mandated duty.
خوف فوت (khawf fawt): Fear of missing the entire act of worship (e.g., all takbirat of funeral prayer) due to time constraints.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is tayammum allowed for the funeral prayer even though water is present?
A) Because funeral prayer is not an obligation.
B) Because the person is unable to perform wudu without missing the entire prayer, and the Prophet did tayammum for a similar reason.
C) Because tayammum is always preferred over wudu.
D) Because the funeral prayer can be made up later.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for funeral prayer is permitted in the Hanafi school when using water would cause missing the entire prayer, based on the principle of necessity and prophetic practice.

Tayammum for Eid Prayer: Conditions and Ruling
Ruling on tayammum for Eid prayer with conditions for imam and follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which tayammum is permissible for the Eid prayer and explain the ruling for the imam and follower based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tayammum for Eid is allowed when missing the prayer due to sunset is feared; the imam may also perform tayammum.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position on performing tayammum for the Eid prayer. While tayammum is normally a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable, the Hanafi school extends its permissibility to special cases where missing the Eid prayer is feared. We will examine the conditions, the disagreement between narrations regarding the imam, and the specific scenario of a follower who could catch part of the prayer with wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum for the Eid prayer. The ruling is permissibility (ja'iz) with the condition of fear of missing the prayer (zawal of the sun). Without such fear, it does not suffice.
The fear is specifically of the sun passing the zenith (zawal), after which the Eid prayer is invalidated.
2
Distinguish the imam's case
There are two narrations: from al-Hasan that the imam does not perform tayammum, and the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) that it suffices if he fears missing the time. The relied-upon position is the latter.
The imam's fear is the same as any individual's – missing the prayer due to zawal.
3
Apply the follower's case
If the follower can catch part of the prayer with the imam by performing wudu (i.e., has water and time), he should not perform tayammum. If he cannot due to fear of sunset, tayammum is allowed by agreement.
This is analogous to the funeral prayer, as referenced in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو عيد ولو بناء ) أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة عيد ولو كان الخوف بناء لما بينا أنها تفوت لا إلى بدل فإن كان إماماً ففي رواية الحسن لا يتيمم، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه لأنه يخاف الفوت بزوال الشمس حتى لو لم يخف لا يجزئه، وإن كان المقتدي بحيث يدرك بعضها مع الإمام لو توضأ لا يتيمم كما قدمناه في الجنازة وصورة الخوف في البناء يشرع في صلاة العيد ثم يسبقه حدث إماماً كان أو مقتدياً فهذه على وجوه؛ فإن كان لا يخاف الزوال ويمكنه أن يدرك شيئاً منها مع الإمام لو توضأ فإنه لا يتيمم اتفاقاً لإمكان أداء الباقي بعده، وإن كان يخاف زوال الشمس لو اشتغل بالوضوء يباح له التيمم اتفاقاً لتصوّر الفوات بالإفساد بدخول الوقت المكروه. ولو شرع بالتيمم تيمم وبنى بالاتفاق لأنا لو أوجبنا الوضوء يكون واجداً للماء في خلال صلاته فتفسد كذا في الهداية والمحيط. وقيل لا يجوز البناء بالتيمم عندهما لوجود الماء، ويجوز أن يكون ابتداؤها بالتيمم والبناء بالوضوء كما قلنا في جنب معه ماء قدر ما يكفي الوضوء فإنه يتيمم ويصلي ولو سبقه حدث فيها فإنه يتوضأ ويبني. وهذا القياس الفارق فإن في المقيس عليه لا يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف إذ التيمم ههنا أقوى من الوضوء لأنه يزيل الجنابة والوضوء لا يزيلها، وفي المقيس يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف فكان الظاهر البناء اتفاقاً. وقد يقال : إنه غير لازم لأن التيمم مثل الوضوء بدليل جواز اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم يؤيده ما ذكره قاضيخان في فصل المسح على الخفين من فتاواه أن المتيمم إذا سبقه حدث في خلال صلاته فانصرف ثم وجد ماء يتوضأ ويبني. والفرق بينه وبين المتيمم الذي وجد الماء في خلال صلاته حيث يستأنف أن التيمم ينتقض بصفة الاستناد إلى وجود الحدث عند إصابة الماء لأنه يصير محدثاً بالحدث السابق لأن الإصابة ليست بحدث وفي هذه الصلاة لم ينتقض التيمم عند إصابة الماء بصفة الاستناد لانتقاضه بالحدث الطارئ على التيمم ويمكن أن يقال: إن التيمم ينتقض عند رؤية الماء بالحدث السابق وإن كان هناك حدث طارئ لما قدمناه عن محمد أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء توجب أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئ عنها وضوء واحد. وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في باب الحدث في الصلاة ما يخالف ما ذكره قاضيخان فثبت أن البناء بالتيمم متفق الخوف بناء الظاهر ما قدره في النهر بقوله ولو كان يبني بناءً فأشار إلى أنه مفعول مطلق لفعل محذوف، ويمكن أن يكون حالاً أي ولو صلى به بانياً على ما صلاه بالوضوء قبل سبق الحدث، ويمكن أن يكون مفعولاً لأجله على القول بأنه لا يشترط فيه أن يكون فعله قلبياً أي ولو كان تيممه لأجل البناء قوله : (لا إلى بدل قدّمنا أنها تقضي إذا أخرت بعذر ومفاده أن الإمام لو حضر بلا
His saying: (or Eid, and even if building) i.e., tayammum is permissible due to fear of missing the Eid prayer, even if the fear is about building (upon a previous prayer), because it has been explained that it is lost without substitute. If he is the imam, then in the narration of al-Hasan, he does not perform tayammum; in the apparent narration, it suffices him because he fears missing it due to sunset, so if he does not fear, it does not suffice. And if the follower is such that he can catch part of it with the imam if he performed wudu, he does not perform tayammum as we mentioned for the funeral. The scenario of fear in building: he begins the Eid prayer, then an event overtakes him, whether imam or follower; this has various facets: if he does not fear sunset and can catch some of it with the imam if he performed wudu, then he does not perform tayammum by agreement because he can perform the remaining part afterwards. If he fears sunset if he occupies himself with wudu, then tayammum is allowed by agreement because loss is conceivable due to invalidation by entering the disliked time. If he began with tayammum, he performs tayammum and builds (upon the previous prayer) by agreement, because if we obligated wudu, he would be finding water during his prayer and it would become invalid. This is in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit. It is said that building with tayammum is not allowed according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the presence of water, but it is permitted to begin with tayammum and then build with wudu, as we say in the case of a person in janabah with enough water for wudu only: he performs tayammum and prays, and if an event overtakes him during it, he performs wudu and builds. This is the distinguishing analogy: in the analogized, building the strong on the weak is not necessary because tayammum here is stronger than wudu since it removes janabah while wudu does not, while in the analogy, building the strong on the weak is necessary, so the apparent is building by agreement. It may be said: it is not necessary because tayammum is like wudu, evidenced by the permissibility of a mutawaddi' following a mutayammim, supported by what Qadikhan mentioned in the chapter on wiping over khuffs in his Fatawa: if a mutayammim is overtaken by an event during his prayer, he leaves, then finds water, performs wudu and builds. The difference between him and the mutayammim who finds water during his prayer (where he must start over) is that tayammum is nullified by attribution to the occurrence of the event when water is obtained, because he becomes hadath due to the previous event, since obtaining water is not an event, and in this prayer, tayammum is not nullified upon finding water by attribution because it is already nullified by the event that occurred during the tayammum. It can be said that tayammum is nullified upon seeing water due to the previous event even if a new event occurs, as we have from Muhammad that successive causes like urine, then nosebleed, then vomiting necessitate successive events, for which one wudu suffices. This will be discussed, Allah willing, in the chapter on events during prayer, which differs from what Qadikhan mentioned. Thus it is established that building with tayammum is agreed upon regarding fear of building the apparent. What he estimated in al-Nahr by his saying: 'and if he was building' indicates that it is an absolute object of a deleted verb, and it can be a hal (circumstantial), i.e., and if he prayed with it while building upon what he had prayed with wudu before the event, and it can be an object for the sake of it, based on the opinion that it is not required that it be an act of the heart, i.e., and if his tayammum was for the sake of building. His saying: (not to a substitute) we have stated that it is made up if delayed by an excuse, and its purport is that if the imam comes without...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage focuses on tayammum for the Eid prayer and the issue of building upon a previous tayammum (al-bina'). It begins by stating that tayammum is allowed for Eid due to fear of missing it, as it is a prayer lost without substitute. The text then examines the scenario when the fear is about building upon a prayer that was interrupted by an event. For the imam, there is a narration from al-Hasan that he does not perform tayammum, but the apparent narration allows it if he fears missing the prayer by sunset. For a follower, if he can catch part of the prayer with wudu, he should not do tayammum; otherwise, if fear of sunset exists, tayammum is agreed upon. The core discussion is about building: if one starts the prayer with tayammum (due to necessity) and then during the prayer a new event occurs, can he build upon the previous prayer after performing wudu? The author explains that according to the consensus, if he began with tayammum, he may build because requiring wudu would lead to finding water during prayer, invalidating it. There is a differing opinion that building with tayammum is not allowed according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad due to the presence of water, but one may start with tayammum and then build with wudu. The author provides an analogy: a person in janabah with limited water does tayammum and prays; if an event occurs, he does wudu and builds. He then refines the ruling by distinguishing cases where tayammum is nullified by finding water versus by a new event. The passage concludes with a grammatical analysis of the word 'bina'an' (building) in the matn, showing its possible readings.

Key Terms
خوف زوال (khawf zawal): Fear of the sun passing the zenith, which marks the end of the recommended time for Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration in the Hanafi school, when is an imam allowed to perform tayammum for the Eid prayer?
A) Only if no water is available at all.
B) If he fears missing the prayer time due to sunset.
C) Only for funeral prayers, not Eid.
D) An imam is never allowed to perform tayammum.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for Eid is permissible when fear of missing the prayer time exists, and this applies to both imam and follower under specific conditions.

Building Upon Tayammum (Al-Bina'): Hanafi Position and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Elaboration on building upon tayammum with intra-madhhab dispute and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the dispute within the Hanafi school regarding building upon a prayer started with tayammum and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Building (bina') upon tayammum is allowed by consensus when the prayer was started with tayammum, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on building with wudu when water appears.

This lesson delves into a nuanced issue within Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a person starts the Eid prayer with tayammum and then is overtaken by a hadath (event) during the prayer? Can he perform wudu and continue building upon his previous prayer, or must he restart? The text presents an intra-madhhab disagreement and concludes with a relied-upon position based on analogy and authoritative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Establish the agreed scenario
If a person begins the Eid prayer with tayammum (due to necessity such as fear of missing time) and then an event (hadath) occurs, there is agreement that he may build by performing another tayammum if needed, because requiring wudu would find water during the prayer and invalidate it.
The agreement is based on the condition that the prayer was validly started with tayammum.
2
Identify the ikhtilaf
It is reported that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not allow building with tayammum when water is present during the prayer, but they allow building with wudu. The main text, however, favors the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) that building with tayammum is always allowed under the agreed scenario.
The ikhtilaf concerns whether tayammum can be used for building once water is available, or only for starting the prayer.
3
Analyze the analogy
The text draws an analogy with a person in janabah who has enough water for wudu only (not ghusl). He does tayammum and prays; if an event occurs, he performs wudu and builds. This shows building with a weaker purification (wudu) on top of a stronger (tayammum) is valid, supporting the allowance of building with tayammum.
The analogy is used to rebut the objection that building with tayammum when water is present is problematic.
4
Resolve the dispute
The author (of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) cites Qadikhan's fatwa that permits building even when water is found after the event, with a subtle distinction: tayammum is nullified by the new event, not by the presence of water, so building with wudu is valid. This leads to the conclusion that building with tayammum is also valid by extension.
The difference from the case where water appears during the prayer (without a new event) is that there the tayammum is nullified by the presence of water itself.
5
Note the criterion
The key is the timing of water acquisition relative to the hadath. If water is found after a new hadath, tayammum is already nullified, so building with wudu is allowed. If water is found without a new hadath (i.e., during the prayer while still in state of tayammum), then the tayammum is nullified and the prayer must be restarted.
This nuance resolves the apparent conflict between different narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (أو عيد ولو بناء ) أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة عيد ولو كان الخوف بناء لما بينا أنها تفوت لا إلى بدل فإن كان إماماً ففي رواية الحسن لا يتيمم، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه لأنه يخاف الفوت بزوال الشمس حتى لو لم يخف لا يجزئه، وإن كان المقتدي بحيث يدرك بعضها مع الإمام لو توضأ لا يتيمم كما قدمناه في الجنازة وصورة الخوف في البناء يشرع في صلاة العيد ثم يسبقه حدث إماماً كان أو مقتدياً فهذه على وجوه؛ فإن كان لا يخاف الزوال ويمكنه أن يدرك شيئاً منها مع الإمام لو توضأ فإنه لا يتيمم اتفاقاً لإمكان أداء الباقي بعده، وإن كان يخاف زوال الشمس لو اشتغل بالوضوء يباح له التيمم اتفاقاً لتصوّر الفوات بالإفساد بدخول الوقت المكروه. ولو شرع بالتيمم تيمم وبنى بالاتفاق لأنا لو أوجبنا الوضوء يكون واجداً للماء في خلال صلاته فتفسد كذا في الهداية والمحيط. وقيل لا يجوز البناء بالتيمم عندهما لوجود الماء، ويجوز أن يكون ابتداؤها بالتيمم والبناء بالوضوء كما قلنا في جنب معه ماء قدر ما يكفي الوضوء فإنه يتيمم ويصلي ولو سبقه حدث فيها فإنه يتوضأ ويبني. وهذا القياس الفارق فإن في المقيس عليه لا يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف إذ التيمم ههنا أقوى من الوضوء لأنه يزيل الجنابة والوضوء لا يزيلها، وفي المقيس يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف فكان الظاهر البناء اتفاقاً. وقد يقال : إنه غير لازم لأن التيمم مثل الوضوء بدليل جواز اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم يؤيده ما ذكره قاضيخان في فصل المسح على الخفين من فتاواه أن المتيمم إذا سبقه حدث في خلال صلاته فانصرف ثم وجد ماء يتوضأ ويبني. والفرق بينه وبين المتيمم الذي وجد الماء في خلال صلاته حيث يستأنف أن التيمم ينتقض بصفة الاستناد إلى وجود الحدث عند إصابة الماء لأنه يصير محدثاً بالحدث السابق لأن الإصابة ليست بحدث وفي هذه الصلاة لم ينتقض التيمم عند إصابة الماء بصفة الاستناد لانتقاضه بالحدث الطارئ على التيمم ويمكن أن يقال: إن التيمم ينتقض عند رؤية الماء بالحدث السابق وإن كان هناك حدث طارئ لما قدمناه عن محمد أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء توجب أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئ عنها وضوء واحد. وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في باب الحدث في الصلاة ما يخالف ما ذكره قاضيخان فثبت أن البناء بالتيمم متفق الخوف بناء الظاهر ما قدره في النهر بقوله ولو كان يبني بناءً فأشار إلى أنه مفعول مطلق لفعل محذوف، ويمكن أن يكون حالاً أي ولو صلى به بانياً على ما صلاه بالوضوء قبل سبق الحدث، ويمكن أن يكون مفعولاً لأجله على القول بأنه لا يشترط فيه أن يكون فعله قلبياً أي ولو كان تيممه لأجل البناء قوله : (لا إلى بدل قدّمنا أنها تقضي إذا أخرت بعذر ومفاده أن الإمام لو حضر بلا
His saying: (or Eid, and even if building) i.e., tayammum is permissible due to fear of missing the Eid prayer, even if the fear is about building (upon a previous prayer), because it has been explained that it is lost without substitute. If he is the imam, then in the narration of al-Hasan, he does not perform tayammum; in the apparent narration, it suffices him because he fears missing it due to sunset, so if he does not fear, it does not suffice. And if the follower is such that he can catch part of it with the imam if he performed wudu, he does not perform tayammum as we mentioned for the funeral. The scenario of fear in building: he begins the Eid prayer, then an event overtakes him, whether imam or follower; this has various facets: if he does not fear sunset and can catch some of it with the imam if he performed wudu, then he does not perform tayammum by agreement because he can perform the remaining part afterwards. If he fears sunset if he occupies himself with wudu, then tayammum is allowed by agreement because loss is conceivable due to invalidation by entering the disliked time. If he began with tayammum, he performs tayammum and builds (upon the previous prayer) by agreement, because if we obligated wudu, he would be finding water during his prayer and it would become invalid. This is in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit. It is said that building with tayammum is not allowed according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the presence of water, but it is permitted to begin with tayammum and then build with wudu, as we say in the case of a person in janabah with enough water for wudu only: he performs tayammum and prays, and if an event overtakes him during it, he performs wudu and builds. This is the distinguishing analogy: in the analogized, building the strong on the weak is not necessary because tayammum here is stronger than wudu since it removes janabah while wudu does not, while in the analogy, building the strong on the weak is necessary, so the apparent is building by agreement. It may be said: it is not necessary because tayammum is like wudu, evidenced by the permissibility of a mutawaddi' following a mutayammim, supported by what Qadikhan mentioned in the chapter on wiping over khuffs in his Fatawa: if a mutayammim is overtaken by an event during his prayer, he leaves, then finds water, performs wudu and builds. The difference between him and the mutayammim who finds water during his prayer (where he must start over) is that tayammum is nullified by attribution to the occurrence of the event when water is obtained, because he becomes hadath due to the previous event, since obtaining water is not an event, and in this prayer, tayammum is not nullified upon finding water by attribution because it is already nullified by the event that occurred during the tayammum. It can be said that tayammum is nullified upon seeing water due to the previous event even if a new event occurs, as we have from Muhammad that successive causes like urine, then nosebleed, then vomiting necessitate successive events, for which one wudu suffices. This will be discussed, Allah willing, in the chapter on events during prayer, which differs from what Qadikhan mentioned. Thus it is established that building with tayammum is agreed upon regarding fear of building the apparent. What he estimated in al-Nahr by his saying: 'and if he was building' indicates that it is an absolute object of a deleted verb, and it can be a hal (circumstantial), i.e., and if he prayed with it while building upon what he had prayed with wudu before the event, and it can be an object for the sake of it, based on the opinion that it is not required that it be an act of the heart, i.e., and if his tayammum was for the sake of building. His saying: (not to a substitute) we have stated that it is made up if delayed by an excuse, and its purport is that if the imam comes without...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage focuses on tayammum for the Eid prayer and the issue of building upon a previous tayammum (al-bina'). It begins by stating that tayammum is allowed for Eid due to fear of missing it, as it is a prayer lost without substitute. The text then examines the scenario when the fear is about building upon a prayer that was interrupted by an event. For the imam, there is a narration from al-Hasan that he does not perform tayammum, but the apparent narration allows it if he fears missing the prayer by sunset. For a follower, if he can catch part of the prayer with wudu, he should not do tayammum; otherwise, if fear of sunset exists, tayammum is agreed upon. The core discussion is about building: if one starts the prayer with tayammum (due to necessity) and then during the prayer a new event occurs, can he build upon the previous prayer after performing wudu? The author explains that according to the consensus, if he began with tayammum, he may build because requiring wudu would lead to finding water during prayer, invalidating it. There is a differing opinion that building with tayammum is not allowed according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad due to the presence of water, but one may start with tayammum and then build with wudu. The author provides an analogy: a person in janabah with limited water does tayammum and prays; if an event occurs, he does wudu and builds. He then refines the ruling by distinguishing cases where tayammum is nullified by finding water versus by a new event. The passage concludes with a grammatical analysis of the word 'bina'an' (building) in the matn, showing its possible readings.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building upon a previous prayer: continuing a prayer that was interrupted by an event, rather than restarting it, after performing a fresh purification.
حدث (hadath): An event that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind, urination).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), if a person begins the Eid prayer with tayammum and then a hadath occurs, which of the following is allowed?
A) He must restart the prayer.
B) He may build by performing tayammum again.
C) He may build with wudu but not with tayammum.
D) He may only build if he does not have water.

Key Takeaway
Building upon a prayer started with tayammum is valid in the Hanafi school when a new hadath occurs, and the mufta bihi allows building with either tayammum or wudu.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Tayammum for Fear of Missing Eid Prayer
Explains the ruling of tayammum for Eid prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on tayammum for Eid prayer and apply the contextual ruling based on time and place.

Core Idea
Tayammum for Eid is allowed only when missing the prayer without substitute is feared.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of tayammum for the Eid prayer. The central question is whether one may substitute tayammum for ablution when there is a risk of missing the entire Eid prayer. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, offer differing views, and later scholars reconcile them based on local circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine when tayammum is considered: fear of missing the entire Eid prayer due to time (sun's zenith) or inability to catch the imam.
2
State the apparent narration
For an imam, tayammum is valid if he fears the sun's passing; otherwise not.
Zahir al-riwayah from al-Hasan
3
Outline the intra-Hanafi dispute
When one begins with wudu, then an event occurs without fear of sun's passing and no hope of catching the imam: Abu Hanifa allows tayammum and building; the Sahibayn require wudu and disallow tayammum.
Opposing schools: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa: fear of missing the prayer without substitute (no makeup). Sahibayn: water available, prayer can be made up later.
Also debate on whether Eid prayer requires makeup
5
Apply later reconciliation
Later scholars (al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi) contextualized: if water is plentiful, tayammum not allowed; if scarce, allowed. The mufta bihi is situational.
Difference of time and place

الجنازة ليست في معناها لأنا نقول : لما جاز أداء أقوى الصلاتين بأضعف الطهارتين لأن يجوز أداء أضعف الصلاتين بأضعف الطهارتين أولى .. أن قوله (أو عيد ولو بناء ) أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة عيد ولو كان الخوف بناء لما بينا أنها تفوت لا إلى بدل فإن كان إماماً ففي رواية الحسن لا يتيمم، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجزئه لأنه يخاف الفوت بزوال الشمس حتى لو لم يخف لا يجزئه، وإن كان المقتدي بحيث يدرك بعضها مع الإمام لو توضأ لا يتيمم كما قدمناه في الجنازة وصورة الخوف في البناء يشرع في صلاة العيد ثم يسبقه حدث إماماً كان أو مقتدياً فهذه على وجوه؛ فإن كان لا يخاف الزوال ويمكنه أن يدرك شيئاً منها مع الإمام لو توضأ فإنه لا يتيمم اتفاقاً لإمكان أداء الباقي بعده، وإن كان يخاف زوال الشمس لو اشتغل بالوضوء يباح له التيمم اتفاقاً لتصوّر الفوات بالإفساد بدخول الوقت المكروه. ولو شرع بالتيمم تيمم وبنى بالاتفاق لأنا لو أوجبنا الوضوء يكون واجداً للماء في خلال صلاته فتفسد كذا في الهداية والمحيط. وقيل لا يجوز البناء بالتيمم عندهما لوجود الماء، ويجوز أن يكون ابتداؤها بالتيمم والبناء بالوضوء كما قلنا في جنب معه ماء قدر ما يكفي الوضوء فإنه يتيمم ويصلي ولو سبقه حدث فيها فإنه يتوضأ ويبني. وهذا القياس الفارق فإن في المقيس عليه لا يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف إذ التيمم ههنا أقوى من الوضوء لأنه يزيل الجنابة والوضوء لا يزيلها، وفي المقيس يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف فكان الظاهر البناء اتفاقاً. وقد يقال : إنه غير لازم لأن التيمم مثل الوضوء بدليل جواز اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم يؤيده ما ذكره قاضيخان في فصل المسح على الخفين من فتاواه أن المتيمم إذا سبقه حدث في خلال صلاته فانصرف ثم وجد ماء يتوضأ ويبني. والفرق بينه وبين المتيمم الذي وجد الماء في خلال صلاته حيث يستأنف أن التيمم ينتقض بصفة الاستناد إلى وجود الحدث عند إصابة الماء لأنه يصير محدثاً بالحدث السابق لأن الإصابة ليست بحدث وفي هذه الصلاة لم ينتقض التيمم عند إصابة الماء بصفة الاستناد لانتقاضه بالحدث الطارئ على التيمم ويمكن أن يقال: إن التيمم ينتقض عند رؤية الماء بالحدث السابق وإن كان هناك حدث طارئ لما قدمناه عن محمد أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء توجب أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئ عنها وضوء واحد. وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في باب الحدث في الصلاة ما يخالف ما ذكره قاضيخان فثبت أن البناء بالتيمم متفق الخوف بناء الظاهر ما قدره في النهر بقوله ولو كان يبني بناءً فأشار إلى أنه مفعول مطلق لفعل محذوف، ويمكن أن يكون حالاً أي ولو صلى به بانياً على ما صلاه بالوضوء قبل سبق الحدث، ويمكن أن يكون مفعولاً لأجله على القول بأنه لا يشترط فيه أن يكون فعله قلبياً أي ولو كان تيممه لأجل البناء قوله : (لا إلى بدل قدّمنا أنها تقضي إذا أخرت بعذر ومفاده أن الإمام لو حضر بلا لأنه يوم زحمة عليه. ولو شرع بالوضوء ثم سبقه الحدث ولم يخف زوال الشمس ولا يرجو إدراك الإمام قبل فراغه، فعند أبي حنيفة يتيمم ويبني وقالا يتوضأ ولا يتيمم ثم اختلف المشايخ فمنهم من قال إنه اختلاف عصر وزمان فكان في زمانه جبانة الكوفة بعيدة ولو انصرف للوضوء زالت الشمس فخوف الفوت قائم وفي زمنهما جبانة بغداد قريبة فأفتيا على وفق زمنهما، ولهذا كان شمس الأئمة الحلواني والسرخسي يقولان : في ديارنا لا يجوز التيمم للعيد ابتداء ولا بناء لأن الماء محيط بمصلى العيد فيمكن التوضؤ والبناء بلا خوف الفوت حتى لو خيف الفوت يجوز التيمم، ومنهم من جعله برهانياً . ثم اختلفوا فمنهم من جعله ابتدائياً فهما نظرا إلى أن اللاحق يصلي بعد فراغ الإمام فلا فوت وأبو حنيفة نظر إلى أن الخوف باق فيعتريه عارض يفسد عليه صلاته من ردّ سلام أو تهنئة ومنهم من جعله مبنياً على مسألة أن أفسد صلاة العيد لا قضاء عليه عنده فتفوت لا إلى بدل وعندهما عليه القضاء فتفوت إلى بدل وإليه ذهب أبو بكر الإسكاف، لكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي: الأصح أنه لا يجب قضاء صلاة العيد بالإفساد عند الكل. وفي شرح منية المصلي : لقائل أن يقول بجواز التيمم في المصر لصلاة الكسوف والسنن الرواتب ما عدا سنة الفجر إذا خاف فوتها لو توضأ فإنها تفوت لا إلى بدل فإنها لا تقضى كما في العيد، ولا سيما على القول بأن صلاة العيد سنة كما اختاره السرخسي وغيره. وأما سنة الفجر فإن خاف فوتها مع الفريضة لا يتيمم، وإن خاف فوتها وحدها فعلى قياس قول محمد لا وعلى قياس قولهما يتيمم فإن عند محمد إذا فاتته باشتغاله بالفريضة مع الجماعة عند خوف فوت الجماعة يقضيها بعد ارتفاع الشمس وعندهما لا يقضيها أصلاً.
The funeral prayer is not in its meaning, for we say: Since performing the stronger of the two prayers with the weaker of the two purifications is permitted, it is even more appropriate that performing the weaker of the two prayers with the weaker of the two purifications be permitted. His saying: 'or Eid, even if building' means: tayammum is permitted for fear of missing the Eid prayer, even if the fear is building, because we explained that it is missed without substitute. If he is an imam, in the narration of al-Hasan he does not perform tayammum, and in the apparent narration it suffices him because he fears missing by the sun's passing the zenith, so if he does not fear, it does not suffice him. And if the follower can reach part of it with the imam if he performs ablution, he does not perform tayammum, as we mentioned in the funeral prayer. The case of fear in building: he begins the Eid prayer then an event precedes him, whether imam or follower, so these are aspects: if he does not fear the zenith and can reach something of it with the imam if he performs ablution, then he does not perform tayammum by agreement because it is possible to perform the remainder after him. And if he fears the sun's passing the zenith if he busies himself with ablution, tayammum is permissible by agreement because of the conception of loss by invalidation upon entering the disliked time. If he begins with tayammum, he performs tayammum and builds by agreement, because if we required ablution, he would be a finder of water during his prayer, so it would be invalidated. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit. It is said: building with tayammum is not permitted according to them due to the presence of water, and it is permissible that its beginning be with tayammum and building with ablution, as we said regarding a junub who has water sufficient for ablution: he performs tayammum and prays, and if an event precedes him in it, then he performs ablution and builds. This is distinguishing qiyas because in the analogized-upon, building the strong upon the weak is not necessary, for tayammum here is stronger than ablution because it removes janabah and ablution does not remove it, while in the analogized-from, building the strong upon the weak is necessary, so the evident is building by agreement. It may be said: it is not necessary because tayammum is like ablution, evidenced by the permissibility of a person with ablution following a mutayammim, supported by what Qadikhan mentioned in the chapter on wiping over the socks from his Fatawa: that if a mutayammim is preceded by an event during his prayer, then leaves, then finds water, he performs ablution and builds. The difference between him and the mutayammim who finds water during his prayer, where he starts over, is that tayammum is nullified by the attribute of attribution to the occurrence of the event upon reaching water, because he becomes one with an event by the prior event, for reaching is not an event, and in this prayer tayammum is not nullified upon reaching water by the attribute of attribution because its nullification by the event occurring after tayammum. And it can be said: tayammum is nullified upon seeing water by the prior event, even if there is a occurring event, because what we mentioned from Muhammad that successive causes, like urination then nosebleed then vomiting, necessitate successive events for which one ablution suffices. And later, Allah willing, in the chapter of event in prayer, something will come that contradicts what Qadikhan mentioned. So it is established that building with tayammum is agreed upon. The fear of building is evident. What he estimated in al-Nahr with his saying 'even if he builds building' indicates that it is an absolute object for an omitted verb, and it can be a state, i.e., even if he prays with it building upon what he prayed with ablution before the occurrence of the event, and it can be an object for the sake of it on the view that it is not required that it be a mental action, i.e., even if his tayammum is for the sake of building. His saying: 'not until a substitute' we mentioned that it is made up if delayed by excuse, and its import is that if the imam attends without because it is a crowded day. And if he began with ablution then an event preceded him and he does not fear the zenith and does not hope to catch the imam before he finishes, then according to Abu Hanifa he performs tayammum and builds, and they said he performs ablution and not tayammum. Then the masters disagreed: some said it is a difference of time and era; in his time the cemetery of Kufa was far, and if he went for ablution the sun would pass, so the fear of missing was present, while in their time the cemetery of Baghdad was near, so they ruled according to their time. For this reason Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi said: in our lands, tayammum is not permissible for Eid initially or as a building because water surrounds the Eid prayer place, so ablution and building are possible without fear of missing, but if fear of missing is present, tayammum is permissible. And some made it a proof-based difference. Then they disagreed: some made it initial; they considered that the latecomer prays after the imam finishes, so there is no loss, while Abu Hanifa considered that fear remains, and an intervening factor occurs that invalidates his prayer, like returning a greeting or a congratulation. And some made it based on the issue that invalidating the Eid prayer requires no makeup according to him, so it is missed without substitute, while according to them makeup is required, so it is missed with substitute. Abu Bakr al-Iskaff went to this, but al-Qadi al-Ispijabi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: the correct is that makeup of Eid prayer by invalidation is not obligatory according to all. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: it can be said that tayammum in the city is permissible for the eclipse prayer and the regular sunnan prayers, except for the sunnah of Fajr, if one fears missing it if he performs ablution, because it is missed without substitute, for it is not made up, as in Eid, especially on the view that Eid prayer is sunnah, as chosen by al-Sarakhsi and others. As for the sunnah of Fajr, if he fears missing it with the fard prayer, he does not perform tayammum; if he fears missing it alone, then according to the qiyas of Muhammad's view, no, and according to their qiyas, he performs tayammum. For according to Muhammad, if he misses it by busying himself with the fard prayer with the congregation when fearing loss of the congregation, he makes it up after sunrise, while according to them, he does not make it up at all.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of tayammum for the Eid prayer. The author begins by establishing a qiyas: since the stronger prayer (Eid? actually janazah is dismissed) can be performed with weaker purification, the weaker prayer (Eid) can also be performed with weaker purification, even more so. The matn states that tayammum is allowed for Eid prayer even if one is building upon a previous prayer with ablution. The commentary then explains various scenarios: if one is an imam, according to the apparent narration, tayammum suffices if he fears the sun's passing of the zenith; otherwise not. For a follower who can catch part of the prayer with the imam after ablution, tayammum is not allowed. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises: when one begins with ablution then an event occurs without fear of sun's passing and no hope of catching the imam before finishing, Abu Hanifa permits tayammum and building, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say to perform ablution and not tayammum. The masters explain this difference as either due to changing circumstances (time and place) or as a principled disagreement. Some attribute the difference to whether a missed Eid prayer requires makeup: Abu Hanifa holds it is missed without substitute (no makeup), so fear of loss is greater; the Sahibayn hold it is missed with substitute (makeup required), so fear is lesser. However, al-Qadi al-Ispijabi clarifies that makeup is not required by consensus. The passage also discusses tayammum for other prayers like eclipse and sunnan, with special note on the sunnah of Fajr. Throughout, the commentary uses qiyas and istihsan to reconcile the positions.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
عيد (Eid): The two festive prayers (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha).
بناء (bina' (building)): Continuing the prayer after an interruption, building upon the previous part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he fears the sun's passing the zenith.
B) When he has no water at all.
C) When he is a follower.
D) When he arrives late.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for Eid prayer is permitted only when missing the prayer is feared and no substitute (makeup) is possible; the ruling is contextual, and later Hanafi scholars adjusted it based on water availability.

Tayammum Not Allowed for Fear of Missing Jumu'ah or Fard Prayer
Ruling on tayammum for fear of missing Jumu'ah and fard prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tayammum when fearing missing Jumu'ah or a fard prayer and explain the reason based on substitution with Zuhr.

Core Idea
Tayammum is not permitted for fear of missing Jumu'ah because it is replaced by Zuhr; the loss is not permanent.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding tayammum. While tayammum is normally a substitute for water when unavailable, fear of missing Jumu'ah or a fard prayer does not justify it. We will explore the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Zufr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is tayammum, and the ruling is that it is invalid (not permissible) for fear of missing Jumu'ah or fard prayer.
The text says 'لا يصح التيمم لخوف فوت الجمعة والوقت'.
2
Understand the reason for Jumu'ah
Note the key phrase 'لأنها تفوت إلى خلف وهو الظهر' – Jumu'ah is missed to a successor (Zuhr), so there is no permanent loss.
This is the core dalil aqli (qiyas).
3
Note the scope of tayammum
Recall that tayammum is only allowed when water is unavailable actually or legally (shar'iyyan). Fear of time loss is not a valid excuse.
The text emphasizes 'عند عدم القدرة على الماء حقيقة أو حكماً'.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufr (a Hanafi scholar) allowed tayammum for fear of missing Jumu'ah. Understand the basis of his view.
The text says 'وفيه خلاف زفر'.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Consider cases of missing sunnah alone vs. fard, and how the school's ruling applies.
The latter part of the passage discusses 'خوف فوتها وحدها'.

It is only permissible for them when unable to use water actually or legally. There is disagreement with Zufr as we mentioned. It was objected that this only applies on the view of Zufr; on the apparent chosen school, that ablution before zenith and he fears if he performs ablution the sun will pass, she is delayed, as investigated by some virtuous men. But it may be said: because it was prayed with a large gathering, if delayed for this excuse, perhaps it leads to its complete loss, unlike if delayed for an excuse like fitna or non-confirmation of moon sighting until after zenith, for then people prepare for it on the second day. It can also be imagined when he missed it with the fard and wants to make them up, and he fears the sun's passing if he prays the sunnah with ablution, so he performs tayammum and prays it, then performs ablution and prays the fard after. Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on tayammum for fear of missing Jumu'ah prayer or a fard prayer. The matn states that tayammum is not valid for these, and the commentary explains why: for Jumu'ah, it can be substituted with Zuhr prayer, so there is no permanent loss. For a fard prayer, tayammum is only allowed when one is genuinely unable to use water, not for fear of missing time. There is a reference to Zufr's differing opinion. The commentary then discusses a scenario from al-Hidayah about delaying prayer due to fear of sun's passing, and notes that this is not considered a valid excuse for tayammum because Jumu'ah can be delayed. The latter part of the passage discusses the case of 'fearing missing it alone' (sunnah prayer) and provides examples: if one is promised water and fears missing the sunnah prayer with the fard, or if one missed both and wants to make them up while fearing time. The text ends mid-sentence at 'the issue'.

وقت (waqt (time)): The time of a prescribed prayer (maktubah).

Tayammum for Eid Prayer After Hadath During Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tayammum for Eid prayer after hadath, and explain the factors that influenced their rulings.

Core Idea
The permissibility of tayammum depends on whether the prayer is lost without substitute and on practical access to water.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: a person who begins wudu for the Eid prayer but experiences hadath before completion. If repeating wudu would cause him to miss the Eid prayer, can he perform tayammum and join the prayer? Abu Hanifa permits it; the Sahibayn require wudu. We will explore the reasoning behind both views and how later scholars reconciled them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the exact situation: someone starts wudu for Eid prayer, then hadath occurs. He fears missing the prayer if he repeats wudu. Does he do tayammum or wudu?
The prayer time is limited, and the imam may finish before he can join.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa says tayammum and 'build' (continue) the prayer; the Sahibayn say wudu and no tayammum.
3
Analyze the first explanation: geographical context
Some scholars attributed the difference to the distance of the burial ground. In Abu Hanifa's Kufa, the cemetery was far, so going for wudu would cause loss of the sun time. In their Baghdad, it was close.
This suggests the ruling may be context-dependent.
4
Analyze the second explanation: risk of interruption
Abu Hanifa feared that even if he joins late, accidental responses (salam, congratulations) could spoil the prayer. The Sahibayn considered that the latecomer prays after the imam, so no loss.
5
Analyze the third explanation: replaceability of the prayer
Abu Hanifa held that the Eid prayer, if spoilt, has no qada (make-up). Therefore it is lost without substitute (la ila badal). The Sahibayn required qada, so it is replaceable.
This principle extends to other prayers like eclipse and sunnah prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شرع بالوضوء ثم سبقه الحدث ولم يخف زوال الشمس ولا يرجو إدراك الإمام قبل فراغه، فعند أبي حنيفة يتيمم ويبني وقالا يتوضأ ولا يتيمم ثم اختلف المشايخ فمنهم من قال إنه اختلاف عصر وزمان فكان في زمانه جبانة الكوفة بعيدة ولو انصرف للوضوء زالت الشمس فخوف الفوت قائم وفي زمنهما جبانة بغداد قريبة فأفتيا على وفق زمنهما، ولهذا كان شمس الأئمة الحلواني والسرخسي يقولان : في ديارنا لا يجوز التيمم للعيد ابتداء ولا بناء لأن الماء محيط بمصلى العيد فيمكن التوضؤ والبناء بلا خوف الفوت حتى لو خيف الفوت يجوز التيمم، ومنهم من جعله برهانياً . ثم اختلفوا فمنهم من جعله ابتدائياً فهما نظرا إلى أن اللاحق يصلي بعد فراغ الإمام فلا فوت وأبو حنيفة نظر إلى أن الخوف باق فيعتريه عارض يفسد عليه صلاته من ردّ سلام أو تهنئة ومنهم من جعله مبنياً على مسألة أن أفسد صلاة العيد لا قضاء عليه عنده فتفوت لا إلى بدل وعندهما عليه القضاء فتفوت إلى بدل وإليه ذهب أبو بكر الإسكاف، لكن قال القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي: الأصح أنه لا يجب قضاء صلاة العيد بالإفساد عند الكل. وفي شرح منية المصلي : لقائل أن يقول بجواز التيمم في المصر لصلاة الكسوف والسنن الرواتب ما عدا سنة الفجر إذا خاف فوتها لو توضأ فإنها تفوت لا إلى بدل فإنها لا تقضى كما في العيد، ولا سيما على القول بأن صلاة العيد سنة كما اختاره السرخسي وغيره. وأما سنة الفجر فإن خاف فوتها مع الفريضة لا يتيمم، وإن خاف فوتها وحدها فعلى قياس قول محمد لا وعلى قياس قولهما يتيمم فإن عند محمد إذا فاتته باشتغاله بالفريضة مع الجماعة عند خوف فوت الجماعة يقضيها بعد ارتفاع الشمس وعندهما لا يقضيها أصلاً.
If one started wudu then hadath preceded him, and he does not fear sunset nor hopes to catch the imam before he finishes, then according to Abu Hanifa he performs tayammum and builds (upon his prayer), while the two say he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum. Then the mashayikh differed: some said it is a difference of era and time, for in his time the cemetery of Kufa was far, and if he went for wudu the sun would have set, so fear of loss remained; in their time the cemetery of Baghdad was near, so they gave fatwa according to their time. For this reason Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi said: In our lands, tayammum is not allowed for Eid initially nor as building, because water surrounds the musalla of Eid, so wudu and building are possible without fear of loss; but if fear of loss exists, tayammum is allowed. Some made it argumentative. Then they differed: some made it initial; the two considered that the latecomer prays after the imam finishes, so no loss; Abu Hanifa considered that fear remains, and an accident could spoil his prayer, like responding to salam or congratulation. Some made it based on the issue that if one spoils the Eid prayer, there is no qada according to him, so it is lost without substitute; according to the two, qada is required, so it is lost with substitute. Abu Bakr al-Isfaf went to that. But al-Qadi al-Asbijabi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: The correct view is that qada of Eid prayer is not required for spoiling according to all. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: One could say that tayammum is allowed in the city for eclipse prayer and the regular sunnahs except the sunnah of Fajr if he fears missing it if he does wudu, for it is lost without substitute, as it is not made up like Eid, especially according to the view that Eid is sunnah as chosen by al-Sarakhsi and others. As for the sunnah of Fajr, if he fears missing it with the obligatory prayer, he does not do tayammum; if he fears missing it alone, then according to the analogy of Muhammad's view, no; according to the analogy of their view, he does tayammum, because according to Muhammad, if he misses it due to engagement with the obligatory prayer in congregation when fearing loss of congregation, he makes it up after sunrise; according to the two, he does not make it up at all.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a person who, after starting wudu for the Eid prayer, experiences a hadath (invalidator) and fears that if he repeats wudu he will miss the Eid prayer. Abu Hanifa rules that he may perform tayammum and then join the prayer (described as 'building' upon his previous intention), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) insist on wudu and forbid tayammum. The commentators offer various explanations for the difference. Some attribute it to geographical context: in Abu Hanifa's time, the Kufa cemetery was distant, so going for wudu would cause loss of the prayer; in the Sahibayn's time, the Baghdad cemetery was close, so no loss was feared. Others treat it as a principled disagreement: the Sahibayn consider that a latecomer can pray after the imam finishes, so no loss occurs; Abu Hanifa fears that during the congregation the person might encounter interruptions (like responding to greeting or congratulation) that spoil his prayer. A third interpretation links the dispute to the question of qada (make-up): according to Abu Hanifa, if one spoils the Eid prayer, there is no qada, so the prayer is lost without substitute; according to the two, qada is required, so the loss is not absolute. The passage then extends the discussion to other prayers: some allow tayammum for eclipse prayer and regular sunnahs except the Fajr sunnah, because the Fajr sunnah is not made up if missed. For the Fajr sunnah, if one fears missing it along with the obligatory prayer, tayammum is not allowed; but if only the sunnah is feared lost, then according to Muhammad's view, tayammum is not allowed because he can make it up later; according to the Sahibayn, it is allowed because they hold it is not made up at all.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): An event that invalidates wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, etc.).
بنى (bana): To build upon his prayer, meaning to continue with the prayer after performing tayammum without restarting from the beginning.
فوت (fawt): Loss of the prayer, meaning missing the entire time of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later scholars (al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi), when is tayammum allowed for Eid prayer?
A) Always, regardless of water availability.
B) Only when water is not available at all.
C) When there is genuine fear of missing the prayer even though water is available.
D) Never, because the Eid prayer has qada.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on tayammum for Eid prayer after hadath depends on whether the prayer is lost without substitute and on the practical availability of water, with later Hanafi scholars synthesizing the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Tayammum Not Allowed for Fear of Missing Friday or Time
Explaining why tayammum is not allowed for fear of missing Friday or time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for fear of missing Friday or prayer time, explain the substitute principle, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Tayammum is invalid when fear of loss involves prayers with substitutes.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: tayammum is not permitted solely to avoid missing Friday prayer or the prayer time. The core rationale is that these prayers have substitutes—Zuhr replaces Friday, and qada replaces the timely prayer—so the loss is not irreparable. The passage also addresses an intra-madhhab objection from Zufar and outlines exceptional cases where fear of losing the entire time may allow tayammum. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to apply the principle of substitution (khalaf) in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum due to fear of missing Friday prayer or the prayer time. The ruling is that such tayammum is not valid (la yasihh). Determine the hukm level: it is haram to use tayammum in these cases because water is accessible and the loss is compensable.
Invalidity here implies prohibition, as using an invalid purification method for prayer renders the prayer invalid.
2
Trace the reasoning: the substitute principle
The author argues that Friday prayer, if missed, is replaced by Zuhr, and the prayer time is replaced by qada. Thus, the loss is to a substitute (khalaf), not absolute. Tayammum is only justified when loss is absolute (no substitute, as in funeral or Eid prayer).
This is a qiyas-type reasoning: comparing to cases where tayammum is allowed (funeral/Eid) based on presence or absence of a substitute.
3
Address the objection based on Zufar's view
An objection is raised: according to the chosen Hanafi view, Friday is the substitute (khalaf) and Zuhr is the original (asl), so how can we say Friday is lost to a substitute? The response clarifies that in practice, when Friday is missed, one prays Zuhr, so Zuhr acts as a substitute in form (surah) though it is the original in meaning (ma'nan). This harmonizes the terminology.
The debate is within the Hanafi school; Zufar held the opposite view, allowing tayammum for fear of losing time.
4
Differentiate between loss of virtue and loss of essence
The author distinguishes fadilat al-waqt (virtue of time) from the act itself. The virtue of time is subsidiary, not intended for itself, so its loss does not justify tayammum. In contrast, funeral and Eid prayers are original acts; their loss is absolute, hence tayammum is allowed.
This distinction answers a potential objection: why is tayammum allowed for traveler or fearful rider? Those are based on textual concession (nas), not on fear of loss, and to prevent compounding of missed prayers.
5
Note the exceptions and practical applications
Exceptions exist when fear of losing the entire time is due to genuine obstacles: darkness, bugs, extreme heat/rain. In such cases, some narrations allow tayammum. Conversely, if one has a promise of water, he must wait even if time expires, because he is considered able to obtain water apparently.
These exceptions are based on the concept of 'ajz (inability), not mere fear of losing time. They are transmitted from later mashayikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (لا) لفوت جمعة ووقت أي لا يصح التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجمعة وصلاة مكتوبة وإنما يجوز التيمم لهما عند عدم القدرة على الماء حقيقة أو حكماً وفيه خلاف زفر كما قدمناه . أما عدم جوازه لخوف فوت الجمعة فلأنها تفوت إلى خلف وهو الظهر. كذا في الهداية. وأورد أن هذا لا يتأتى إلا على مذهب زفر، أما على ظاهر المذهب المختار من أن الجمعة خلف والظهر أصل فلا، ودفع بأنه متصور بصورة الخلف لأن الجمعة إذا فاتت يصلي الظهر فكان الظهر خلفاً صورة أصلاً معنى. وقد جمع بينهما في النافع فقال : لأنها تفوت إلى ما يقوم مقامها وهو الأصل. وأما عدم جوازه لخوف فوت الوقت فلأن الفوات إلى خلف القضاء. فإن قيل : فضيلة الجمعة والوقت تفوت لا إلى خلف ولهذا جاز للمسافر التيمم وجازت الصلاة للراكب الخائف مع ترك بعض الشروط والأركان وكل هذا الفضيلة الوقت قلنا : فضيلة الوقت والأداء وصف للمؤدي تابع له غير مقصود لذاته بخلاف صلاة الجنازة والعيد فإنها أصل فيكون فواتها فوات أصل مقصود، وجوازها للمسافر بالنص لا لخوف الفوت بل لأجل أن لا تتضاعف عليه الفوائت ويحرج في القضاء، وكذا صلاة الخوف للخوف دون خوف الفوت. هذا وقد قدمنا عن القنية أن التيمم لخوف فوت الوقت رواية عن مشايخنا وفرع عليها في باب التيمم أنه لو كان في سطح ليلاً وفي بيته ماء لكنه يخاف في الظلمة إن دخل البيت يتيمم إن خاف فوت الوقت، وكذا يتيمم في كلة لخوف البق أو مطر حر شديد إن خاف فوت الوقت، وعلى اعتبار العجز لا خوف الوقت فرع محمد رحمه الله ما لو وعده صاحبه أن يعطيه الإناء أنه ينتظر وإن خرج الوقت لأن الظاهر هو الوفاء بالعهد فكان قادراً على استعمال الماء ظاهراً. وكذا إذا وعد الكاسي العاري أن يعطيه الثوب إذا فرغ من صلاته لم تجزه الصلاة عرياناً لما قلنا. كذا في البدائع.
His statement (no) for fear of missing Friday and time, meaning tayammum is not valid due to fear of missing Friday prayer and an obligatory prayer. Rather, tayammum is allowed for them only when one is unable to use water, either actually or legally. There is a dispute with Zufar as we have mentioned. As for the non-permissibility due to fear of missing Friday, it is because it is lost to a substitute, which is Zuhr. Thus in al-Hidayah. It was objected that this only applies according to Zufar's madhhab, but according to the apparent chosen madhhab that Friday is the substitute and Zuhr is the original, this does not hold. And it was refuted that it is conceived in the form of a substitute because when Friday is missed, one prays Zuhr, so Zuhr is a substitute in form and an original in meaning. Al-Nafi' combined them: because it is lost to something that stands in its place, which is the original. As for the non-permissibility due to fear of missing time, it is because the loss is to a substitute, which is qada. If it is said: the virtue of Friday and the virtue of time are lost without substitute, and for this reason tayammum is allowed for the traveler, and prayer is allowed for the fearful rider while abandoning some conditions and pillars, and all this is the virtue of time. We say: the virtue of time and performance is a quality of the performer, subsidiary to him, not intended for itself, unlike the funeral and Eid prayers, for they are original, so their loss is the loss of an original intended. The permissibility for the traveler is by text, not due to fear of loss, but rather so that lapsed prayers do not multiply upon him and cause hardship in making them up. Similarly, the prayer of fear is due to fear, not fear of loss. And we have previously transmitted from al-Qunyah that tayammum for fear of losing time is a narration from our mashayikh, and they branched from it in the chapter of tayammum: if someone is on a roof at night and has water in his house, but he fears in the darkness that if he enters the house he will lose the time, he does tayammum if he fears losing the time. Similarly, he does tayammum in a mosquito net due to fear of bugs or extreme hot rain if he fears losing the time. And based on consideration of inability, not fear of time, Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) branched: if someone's companion promised to give him the vessel, he waits even if the time leaves, because the apparent is fulfillment of the promise, so he is considered able to use water apparently. Similarly, if one who is naked promised a dresser to give him a garment after he finishes his prayer, his prayer without clothes is not valid for what we said. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage explains the general ruling that tayammum is not permitted solely due to fear of missing Friday prayer or the prayer time. The reasoning is that these prayers have substitutes: Friday prayer is replaced by Zuhr prayer if missed, and the time of a prayer is replaced by the qada (make-up) of that prayer. Thus the loss is not absolute; there is a substitute. The text addresses an objection that according to the chosen madhhab, Friday is the substitute and Zuhr is the original, but the response clarifies that in practice, if Friday is missed, one prays Zuhr, so Zuhr acts as a substitute in form though it is the original in meaning. The passage then distinguishes between two types of loss: loss of the 'virtue' (fadilah) of time vs. loss of the prayer itself. The virtue of time is subsidiary and not intended in itself, unlike funeral and Eid prayers which are original acts, hence their loss warrants tayammum. The allowance for travelers to do tayammum is based on scriptural text, not on fear of missing time, but to avoid compounding of missed prayers. Finally, exceptions are noted: if one fears missing the entire prayer time due to obstacles like darkness, bugs, or severe weather, some narrations allow tayammum. However, if one has a promise of water, he must wait even if the time expires, because he is considered able to obtain water.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that replaces the original; here, Zuhr replaces Friday, and qada replaces timely prayer.
فوت (fawt): Loss of the opportunity to perform a prayer in its time.
فضيلة الوقت (fadilat al-waqt): The merit or virtue of performing the prayer at its optimal time (e.g., early time).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tayammum not allowed when one fears missing the Friday prayer?
A) Because Friday prayer is obligatory and cannot be replaced.
B) Because Friday prayer is replaced by Zuhr prayer.
C) Because tayammum is only for travelers.
D) Because water must be available.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is not permitted when fear of loss involves a prayer that has a substitute; the substitute principle is central to Hanafi rulings on tayammum.

No Repetition for Forgetting Water in the Saddlebag (Rahl)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum with forgotten water in rahl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum after forgetting water in the rahl, distinguish Abu Yusuf's position, and apply the condition of what is normally forgotten.

Core Idea
Forgetting water in a place where it is not normally found excuses tayammum; no repetition required.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether forgetting water in one's rahl (saddlebag or dwelling) requires repeating a prayer performed with tayammum. The key distinction is whether the water was in a location where forgetting it is typical. We will explore the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the act is performing tayammum and praying while genuinely forgetting that water is available in one's rahl. The dispute is over whether the prayer must be repeated (i'adah) after remembering the water.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi: between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that no repetition is required, provided the water was in a place where it is normally forgotten (e.g., the back of a saddlebag).
The key condition is 'mimma yunsa 'ādatan' (something normally forgotten).
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing position
Abu Yusuf requires repetition because the rahl is a typical place for water, so the person should have searched for it. Forgetfulness does not excuse him as it contradicts his knowledge.
Abu Yusuf considers the rahl as a 'ma'din al-mā' (source of water) by custom.
4
Identify the key condition and exceptions
The ruling is restricted to water being 'fī rahl' (in the saddlebag) and being of the type normally forgotten. If the water was on the person's back, head, or neck, all agree that repetition is required.
Additionally, doubt (zann) or uncertainty (shakk) does not permit tayammum by consensus.
5
Apply the condition to examples
If water is in the back of the rahl while driving (easily forgotten), no repetition. If water is hung around the neck (not normally forgotten), repetition is required by agreement.
This illustrates the principle: forgetfulness is excused only when consistent with normal patterns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولم يعد أن صلى به ونسي الماء في رحله أي ولم يعد إن صلى بالتيمم ناسياً الماء في رحله وهو مما ينسى عادة وكان موضوعاً بعلمه وهو للبعير كالسراج للدابة. ويقال لمنزل الإنسان ومأواه رحل أيضاً وهو المراد بقولهم نسي الماء في رحله. كذا في المغرب. لكن قد يقال : قولهم لو كان الماء في مؤخرة الرحل يفيد أن المراد بالرحل الأول وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : تلزمه الإعادة قيد بالنسيان لأن في الظن لا يجوز التيمم إجماعاً، ويعيد الصلاة لأن الرحل معدن الماء عادة فيفترض عليه الطلب كما يفرض عليه الطلب في العمرانات لأن العلم لا يبطل بالظن بخلاف النسيان لأنه أضداد من العلم وظنه بخلاف العادة لا يعتبر. وقيد بقوله في رحله لأنه لو كان على ظهره فنسيه ثم تيمم يعيد اتفاقاً. وكذا إذا كان على رأسه أو معلقاً في عنقه . وقيدنا بكونه مما ينسى عادة لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك كما إذا نسي الماء المعلق في مؤخر رحله وهو يسوق دابته فإنه يعيد اتفاقاً. وكذا إذاالزوال، ولكن الصورة الأولى هنا أنسب قوله : ( لكن قد يقال قولهم لو كان الماء الخ) قال في النهر : الظاهر أن المراد به ما يوضع فيه الماء عادة وإلى ذلك أشار المصنف. وهذا لأن رحله مفرد يعم كل رحل، سواء كان منزلاً أو رحل بعير. قوله : (لأن في الظنّ لا يجوز التيمم إجماعاً) أقول: وكذا في الشك كما في السراج خلافاً لما في النهر من عزوه إليه الجواز. وعبارة السراج مضاف
His statement (and he does not repeat) that he prayed by it and forgot water in his rahil, meaning he does not repeat if he prayed with tayammum while forgetting water in his rahil, and it is something that is normally forgotten, and it was placed with his knowledge, and it is for the camel like a lamp for the animal. The word rahil is also said for a person's home and dwelling, and that is what is meant by their saying 'he forgot water in his rahil'. Thus in al-Mughrib. But it may be said: their statement 'if the water was in the back of the rahil' indicates that the first rahil is meant, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: repetition is required of him. It is restricted by forgetfulness because in case of doubt, tayammum is not permissible by consensus, and he repeats the prayer because the rahil is usually a place where water is found, so he is obliged to search as he is obliged to search in inhabited areas, because knowledge is not invalidated by doubt, unlike forgetfulness because it is opposite of knowledge, and his doubt contrary to habit is not considered. It is restricted by his statement 'in his rahil' because if it was on his back, then he forgot it and did tayammum, he repeats by agreement. Similarly if it was on his head or hung around his neck. And we restricted it to what is normally forgotten, because if it were not so, as when he forgets the water hanging at the back of his rahil while driving his animal, then he repeats by agreement. Similarly if... but the first picture here is more appropriate. His statement (but it may be said: their statement 'if the water...') He said in al-Nahr: the apparent meaning is what is usually placed in water, and to that the author pointed. And this is because his rahil, singular, includes every rahil, whether a dwelling or a camel's saddle. His statement (because in case of doubt, tayammum is not permissible by consensus) I say: and similarly in case of uncertainty, as in al-Siraj, contrary to what is in al-Nahr attributing permissibility to it. And the expression in al-Siraj is 'mudaf' (appended).
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person who forgets that he has water in his rahil (saddlebag or dwelling), performs tayammum, and prays. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he does not need to repeat the prayer, because the forgetfulness is genuine and the water was not in a place where one would normally expect to find it (like on his person). Abu Yusuf, however, insists that he must repeat because the rahil is a typical place for water, so he should have looked; forgetfulness does not excuse him as it is contrary to his habit. The text specifies conditions: the water must be in his rahil (not on his body), and it must be the kind of thing that is normally forgotten. If the water was on his back, head, or neck, and he forgot it, then all agree he must repeat. The passage ends with a citation from al-Nahr clarifying that 'rahil' includes both dwelling and saddle, and a note that in case of doubt (zann) or uncertainty (shakk), tayammum is not permissible by consensus, though some attributions differ.

Key Terms
رحل (rahl): Saddlebag (for a camel) or a person's home/dwelling; the place where one would store water.
ناسيا (nasīyan): Forgetting; here it refers to genuinely forgetting the presence of water.
إعادة (i‘ādah): Repetition of the prayer; here, whether the prayer performed with tayammum must be repeated after remembering the water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a person forgets water in his rahil (saddlebag) and performs tayammum, what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) He does not repeat the prayer.
C) He must perform wudu and repeat.
D) It depends on whether he was traveling.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, forgetting water in a place where it is not normally forgotten excuses tayammum; no repetition is required.
