Tayammum Due to Fear of Missing Prayer Time
Inter-madhhab dispute on tayammum due to fear of missing time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not permit tayammum for fear of missing prayer time and contrast it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires actual inability to use water; fear of missing time is not a valid excuse.

This lesson explores a classic inter-madhhab dispute: may one perform tayammum simply out of fear that using water will cause missing the prayer time? The Hanafi school generally says no, while the Shafi'i school says yes. We will trace the arguments, including analogies to Friday prayer, the role of qada, and the nature of time's virtue.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: tayammum is not permitted for fear of missing time; actual inability to use water is required.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school (Imam al-Shafi'i) holds that tayammum is allowed because the virtue of the time is lost without compensation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that just as a traveler may perform tayammum even if water is available, so too one may perform tayammum to preserve the time.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between the virtue of time (subsidiary) and the act itself (original). The traveler's permission is based on revealed text, not fear of losing time, but to prevent accumulation of missed prayers.
Also note the exception from al-Qunyah for specific hardships like darkness or insects.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'is allow tayammum for fear of missing time; Hanafis generally forbid it except in cases of actual inability or the narrated exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم وهو الجمعة خلف والظهر أصل فلا، ودفع بأنه متصور بصورة الخلف لأن الجمعة إذا فاتت يصلي الظهر فكان الظهر خلفاً صورة أصلاً معنى. وقد جمع بينهما في النافع فقال : لأنها تفوت إلى ما يقوم مقامها وهو الأصل. وأما عدم جوازه لخوف فوت الوقت فلأن الفوات إلى خلف القضاء. فإن قيل : فضيلة الجمعة والوقت تفوت لا إلى خلف ولهذا جاز للمسافر التيمم وجازت الصلاة للراكب الخائف مع ترك بعض الشروط والأركان وكل هذا الفضيلة الوقت قلنا : فضيلة الوقت والأداء وصف للمؤدي تابع له غير مقصود لذاته بخلاف صلاة الجنازة والعيد فإنها أصل فيكون فواتها فوات أصل مقصود، وجوازها للمسافر بالنص لا لخوف الفوت بل لأجل أن لا تتضاعف عليه الفوائت ويحرج في القضاء، وكذا صلاة الخوف للخوف دون خوف الفوت. هذا وقد قدمنا عن القنية أن التيمم لخوف فوت الوقت رواية عن مشايخنا وفرع عليها في باب التيمم أنه لو كان في سطح ليلاً وفي بيته ماء لكنه يخاف في الظلمة إن دخل البيت يتيمم إن خاف فوت الوقت، وكذا يتيمم في كلة لخوف البق أو مطر حر شديد إن خاف فوت الوقت، وعلى اعتبار العجز لا خوف الوقت فرع محمد رحمه الله ما لو وعده صاحبه أن يعطيه الإناء أنه ينتظر وإن خرج الوقت لأن الظاهر هو الوفاء بالعهد فكان قادراً على استعمال الماء ظاهراً. وكذا إذا وعد الكاسي العاري أن يعطيه الثوب إذا فرغ من صلاته لم تجزه الصلاة عرياناً لما قلنا. كذا في البدائع.
The book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. And it is: Friday prayer is a substitute and noon prayer is the original, so [the analogy] is invalid. And it is rebutted by saying that it is conceived in the form of a substitute because when Friday prayer is missed, one prays noon prayer, so noon prayer is a substitute in form and original in meaning. And it is combined in al-Nafi' such that he said: because it [Friday prayer] passes to what stands in its place, which is the original. As for the impermissibility of tayammum due to fear of missing the time, it is because the missing goes to a substitute, which is making up. If it is said: The virtue of Friday prayer and the time are lost without a substitute, and therefore it is permissible for the traveler to perform tayammum, and it is permissible for the rider in fear to pray while leaving some conditions and pillars, and all of this is for the virtue of the time. We say: The virtue of the time and performance is a description of the performer, subsidiary to him, not intended for itself, unlike the funeral prayer and Eid prayer, for they are original, so missing them is missing an intended original. And its permissibility for the traveler is by textual proof, not for fear of losing time, but so that missed prayers do not multiply upon him and he would be in hardship in making them up. Similarly, the prayer of fear is due to fear, not fear of losing time. This and we have previously cited from al-Qunyah that tayammum for fear of losing time is a narration from our mashayikh, and he branches upon it in the chapter of tayammum that if one is on a rooftop at night and there is water in his house but he fears in the darkness if he enters the house, he performs tayammum if he fears losing the time. Similarly, he performs tayammum in a mosquito net due to fear of mosquitoes or severe heavy rain if he fears losing the time. And on the basis of inability, not fear of time, Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) derived the case of when his companion promises to give him the vessel that he waits even if the time exits, because the apparent is fulfillment of the promise, so he is apparently able to use water. Similarly, if the one who clothes the naked person promises to give him the garment after he finishes his prayer, it is not permissible for him to pray naked for what we said. Thus in al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of tayammum due to fear of missing the prayer time. The author begins by discussing a previous objection regarding Friday and noon prayers: some argued that since Friday is a substitute for noon, and noon is the original, tayammum due to fear of missing Friday's time would be analogous to tayammum due to inability to use water. The author rebuts this by showing that the analogy fails: Friday prayer's time is not an independent objective; missing it merely shifts to noon. Tayammum for fear of missing time is generally impermissible because the missed time is recovered through qada (making up). The opponent then raises a counter-argument: the virtue (fadila) of Friday and the time itself are lost without compensation, just as a traveler may perform tayammum even if water is available, or a fearful rider may pray with incomplete conditions. The author's response distinguishes between the virtue of the time, which is a subsidiary quality of the performer, and the acts themselves (like funeral and Eid prayers), which are original objectives. Tayammum for travelers is permitted by revealed text (nas), not due to fear of losing time, but to prevent accumulation of missed prayers. Similarly, the prayer of fear (salat al-khawf) is permitted due to actual fear, not fear of losing time. The passage then cites a narration from al-Qunyah that some Hanafi mashayikh allowed tayammum due to fear of losing time in specific circumstances like darkness, mosquitoes, or heavy rain—but this is a mere riwaya, not the relied-upon position. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani further derived a case emphasizing inability: if a companion promises to give water, one must wait even if time exits, because the promise creates apparent ability. Thus, tayammum for fear of missing time is generally not permitted; inability to use water is the operative factor.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or replacement; here, Friday prayer is a substitute for noon prayer when noon is the original.
فضل الوقت (fadl al-waqt): The virtue or merit of performing prayer in its prescribed time.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, is tayammum valid if one fears missing the prayer time due to using water?
A) Yes, because preserving the time is a primary objective.
B) No, because the time is recoverable through qada and the virtue is subsidiary.
C) Yes, if the fear is extreme like darkness or insects.
D) No, only if water is truly unavailable.

Key Takeaway
Fear of missing prayer time does not permit tayammum in the Hanafi school; only actual inability to use water is a valid excuse.

Forgetting Water in the Saddlebag: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with conditions and subcases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when water is forgotten in the saddlebag, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and identify the conditions that determine whether repetition is required.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness of water in a normal place excuses tayammum; suspicion does not.

Imagine a traveler on a long journey, performing tayammum only to later find water in his saddlebag—a place where water is normally kept. Did his prayer count? Within the Hanafi school, there is a disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes, while Abu Yusuf says the prayer must be repeated. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the precise conditions that govern the ruling, including where the water was stored and whether the forgetfulness was usual or unusual.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling and the dispute
Identify that the text from Kanz al-Daqaiq states no repetition is required when water is forgotten in the rahil. Then note that Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring repetition.
The base text is being commented on; the dispute is intra-Hanafi.
2
Understand the key distinction: forgetfulness vs. suspicion
Note that the ruling is restricted to forgetfulness (nisyan), not suspicion (zann). By consensus, if one merely suspects water is gone, tayammum is invalid and prayer must be repeated. Forgetfulness excused because it negates knowledge, but suspicion does not.
The passage explicitly says in case of suspicion, tayammum is not allowed by consensus.
3
Analyze the two opposing proofs
Abu Yusuf argues that the rahil is a typical place for water, so one should seek it just as in inhabited areas (amarat). The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that without knowledge, one is incapable of using water, and capability is a prerequisite for obligation. Since forgetfulness removes knowledge, tayammum is valid.
The two imams' reasoning is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy): loss of knowledge is like loss of any other instrument.
4
Apply the conditions: location and normalcy of forgetfulness
The ruling only applies if water is in a place where it is normally kept (e.g., the saddlebag) and the forgetfulness is typical. If water was on his back, head, or hung around his neck, repetition is required by consensus because these are not typical storage places. Also, if the water was placed by someone else without his knowledge, no repetition by consensus.
Subcases differentiate between riding, driving, and leading the animal, and front vs. back of the saddle.
5
Consider the extended debate: garment in rahil
The passage analogizes to a person praying naked while a pure garment is in his rahil without knowledge. Some, including al-Karkhi, say this is also disputed, not by consensus as others claim. This shows the rahil principle is not absolute.
This part is contested; the author of Fath al-Qadir questions the consensus claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو كائناً قوله (ولم يعد أن صلى به ونسي الماء في رحله أي ولم يعد إن صلى بالتيمم ناسياً الماء في رحله وهو مما ينسى عادة وكان موضوعاً بعلمه وهو للبعير كالسراج للدابة. ويقال لمنزل الإنسان ومأواه رحل أيضاً وهو المراد بقولهم نسي الماء في رحله. كذا في المغرب. لكن قد يقال : قولهم لو كان الماء في مؤخرة الرحل يفيد أن المراد بالرحل الأول وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : تلزمه الإعادة قيد بالنسيان لأن في الظن لا يجوز التيمم إجماعاً، ويعيد الصلاة لأن الرحل معدن الماء عادة فيفترض عليه الطلب كما يفرض عليه الطلب في العمرانات لأن العلم لا يبطل بالظن بخلاف النسيان لأنه أضداد من العلم وظنه بخلاف العادة لا يعتبر. وقيد بقوله في رحله لأنه لو كان على ظهره فنسيه ثم تيمم يعيد اتفاقاً. وكذا إذا كان على رأسه أو معلقاً في عنقه . وقيدنا بكونه مما ينسى عادة لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك كما إذا نسي الماء المعلق في مؤخر رحله وهو يسوق دابته فإنه يعيد اتفاقاً. وكذا إذا كان راكباً والماء في مقدم الرحل أو بين يديه راكباً بخلاف ما إذا كان سائقاً وهو في المقدم أو راكباً . وهو في المؤخر فإنه على الاختلاف، وكذا إذا كان القدير، وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن دعوى الإجماع سهو ليست بصحيحة. ونقل عن فخر الإسلام في شرح الجامع الصغير أنها على الاختلاف والحق ما في البدائع أنه لا رواية لهذا نصاً. وقال بعض المشايخ : أن لفظ الرواية في الجامع الصغير تدل على أنه يجوز بالإجماع فإنه قال في الرجل يكون في رحله ماء فنسي والنسيان يستدعي تقدم العلم ثم مع ذلك جعل عذراً عندهما فبقي موضع لا علم أصلاً ينبغي أن يجعل عذراً عند الكل، ولفظ الرواية في كتاب الصلاة يدل على أنه على الاختلاف فإنه قال : مسافر تيمم ومعه ماء في رحله وهو لا يعلم به وهذا يتناول حالة النسيان وغيرها لأبي يوسف وجهان: أحدهما أنه نسي ما لا ينسى عادة لأن أعز الأشياء في السفر لكونه سبباً لصيانة نفسه عن الهلاك فكان القلب متعلقاً فالتحق النسيان فيه بالعدم والثاني أن الرحل موضع الماء غالباً لحاجة المسافر إليه فكان الطلب واجباً كما في العمران ولهما أنه عجز عن استعمال الماء فلا يلزمه الاستعمال، وهذا لأنه لا قدرة بدون العلم لأن القادر على الفعل هو الذي لو أراد تحصيله يتأتى له ذلك ولا تكليف بدون القدرة، ولو فقدت قدرته بفقد سائر الآلات جاز تيممه، فإذا فقد العلم وهو أقوى الآلات أولى. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن هذا لا يفيد بعد ما قرر لأبي يوسف لثبوت العلم نظراً إلى الدليل اتفاقاً كما قال الكل في المسائل الملحق بها. وإنما المفيد ليس إلا منع وجود العلة أي لا نسلم أن الرحل دليل الماء الذي ثبوته يمنع التيمم أعني ماء الاستعمال بل الشرب مفقود في حق غير الشرب .اهـ. ولو صلى عرياناً وفي رحله ثوب طاهر لم يعلم به ثم علم قال بعضهم تلزمه الإعادة بالإجماع، وذكر الكرخي أنه على الاختلاف وهو الأصح. كذا هكذا قيد بالنسيان احترازاً عما إذا شك أو ظن أن ماءه قد فني فصلى ثم وجده فإنه يعيد إجماعاً اهـ فتنبه. قوله : (لكن يرد عليه لو صلى الخ) أقول : فيه نظر ظاهر لأنه إذا كانت هذه المسألة كمسألة الصلاة عارياً في لزوم الإعادة بالإجماع فوجهها ظاهر لأن الثوب في رحله والرحل معد للثوب على أنه لا يناسبه ما بعده مع أن ذلك في فتح القدير ونص ما فيه لكنه يشكل بمسألة الصلاة النجاسة فإنه قد اعتبر الرحل فيها دليل ماء الاستعمال ،اهـ وهذا لا غبار عليه ولعل لفظة «الطاهر» في عبارة المؤلف من تحريف النساخ والأصل المطهر أو أراد بالطاهر الماء الطاهر تأمل قوله : (لا يجوز فقد شرطه) قال الرملي :أقول : بل شرطه موجود لا مفقود لأن النسيان جعله في حكم مع المعدوم فانثلج الخاطر. قوله : (ولقائل أن يقول الخ) حاصله أن في كلامه تدافعاً لأن فقد شرط الخلف
Or being such. His statement: 'And he does not repeat if he prayed with it and forgot water in his saddlebag,' meaning he does not repeat if he prayed with tayammum having forgotten water in his saddlebag, and it is something normally forgotten, and it was placed with his knowledge. And it [rahil] for the camel is like a lamp for the animal. And the place of a person's dwelling and abode is also called rahil, and that is what is meant by their statement 'he forgot water in his rahil.' Thus in al-Mughrib. But it may be said: Their statement 'if the water was in the back of the saddle' indicates that what is meant is the first rahil, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said: Repetition is required of him. It is restricted by forgetfulness because in case of suspicion, tayammum is not permissible by consensus, and he repeats the prayer because the rahil is normally a place for water, so seeking is obligatory on him, just as seeking is obligatory in inhabited areas, because knowledge is not nullified by suspicion, unlike forgetfulness because it is opposite of knowledge, and his suspicion contrary to habit is not considered. It is restricted by his statement 'in his rahil' because if it was on his back and he forgot it then performed tayammum, he repeats by agreement. Similarly, if it was on his head or hung around his neck. And we restricted it to being something normally forgotten because if it were not so, like if he forgot water hung at the back of his saddle while driving his animal, then he repeats by agreement. Similarly, if he was riding and the water is at the front of the saddle or in front of him while riding, contrary to if he was driving and it is at the front, or riding and it is at the back, then it is subject to disagreement. Similarly, if he was leading in any case. And we restricted it to being placed with his knowledge because if someone else placed it, even his slave or hireling without his order, he does not repeat by agreement because one is not addressed by the action of another. Thus in al-Nihayah, and a group of commentators followed him, and al-Fath al-Qadir referred to it. But it was refuted in Ghayat al-Bayan that the claim of consensus is a mistake and not correct. And it is narrated from Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that it is subject to disagreement, and the truth is as in al-Bada'i' that there is no explicit narration for this. And some mashayikh said: The wording of the narration in al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that it is permissible by consensus, for he said concerning a man who has water in his rahil and forgets—forgetfulness requires prior knowledge—yet despite that, it is made an excuse according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. So a case where there is no knowledge at all should be made an excuse according to all. And the wording of the narration in the Book of Prayer indicates that it is subject to disagreement, for he said: A traveler performed tayammum while having water in his rahil and he did not know about it. This covers the case of forgetfulness and others. For Abu Yusuf there are two positions: one, that he forgot what is not normally forgotten because the most precious things in travel, being the means of preserving oneself from destruction, the heart is attached, so forgetfulness therein is deemed non-existence; the second, that the rahil is typically a place for water due to the traveler's need, so seeking was obligatory as in inhabited areas. For the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], he is unable to use water, so use is not required. This is because there is no capability without knowledge, for the one capable of an act is he who, if he intends to achieve it, can do so, and there is no obligation without capability. And if his capability is lost due to loss of other instruments, his tayammum is allowed. So if knowledge is lost, which is the strongest of instruments, it is more appropriate. But it was refuted in al-Fath al-Qadir that this does not benefit after what was established for Abu Yusuf, because knowledge is proven by evidence by agreement, as everyone said in the analogous cases. The only beneficial thing is the denial of the existence of the cause, i.e., we do not concede that the rahil is evidence of water whose existence prevents tayammum—I mean water for use, not for drinking, for drinking is absent in the case of non-drinking. End. And if one prayed naked while having a pure garment in his rahil without knowing, then later knew; some said repetition is required by consensus, and al-Karkhi mentioned that it is subject to disagreement, and that is more correct. Thus. This is how it is restricted by forgetfulness, to avoid the case where one doubts or suspects that his water has run out, then prays, then finds it: he repeats by consensus, so pay attention. His statement: 'But it may be objected that if he prayed...' I say: There is apparent consideration in it because if this issue is like the issue of praying naked in requiring repetition by consensus, its reasoning is apparent because the garment is in his rahil, and the rahil is prepared for the garment. But it is not consistent with what follows, although that is in al-Fath al-Qadir and its text. However, it is problematic with the issue of prayer with impurity, for the rahil is considered evidence of water for use there. So there is no problem with this, and perhaps the word 'al-tahir' in the author's expression is a scribal corruption, and the original is 'al-mutahhir', or he meant by 'al-tahir' pure water. Consider. His statement: 'It is not permissible, its condition is lost.' al-Ramli said: I say: Rather its condition is present, not lost, because forgetfulness puts it in the ruling of non-existent, so the mind is set at ease. His statement: 'And one may say...' The summary is that in his speech there is contradiction because the loss of the condition of the substitute...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This extensive passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on a person who performs tayammum having forgotten water that is in his saddlebag (rahil). The base text from Kanz al-Daqaiq states that he does not repeat the prayer. The commentator explains that this applies when the water was placed with his knowledge and is something normally forgotten. The rahil is like a camel's saddle; it can also mean a dwelling. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that no repetition is required, while Abu Yusuf requires it. The key distinction is forgetfulness versus suspicion: if one merely suspects the water is gone, all agree he must repeat, because suspicion does not override the presumption that water is present. Abu Yusuf argues that the rahil is a typical place for water, so one is obligated to seek it just as in inhabited areas. The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) base their view on the fact that without knowledge, one is incapable of using water, and capability is a prerequisite for obligation. They argue that loss of knowledge is like loss of any other means, and tayammum should be allowed. The passage then discusses conditions: if the water was on his back, head, or hung around his neck, and he forgot, he must repeat by consensus because such places are not typical storage. Additionally, if the water was not placed by him, but by a slave or hireling without his order, he does not repeat by consensus. Various subcases are considered based on whether the person is riding, driving, or leading the animal, and whether the water is in the front or back of the saddle—these affect whether the forgetfulness is considered normal. The discussion extends to the case of praying naked with a forgotten garment in the rahil: some say consensus on repetition, but al-Karkhi says it's disputed. Later, the author addresses objections about the condition of the substitute (khalaf) and clarifies that forgetfulness effectively makes the water non-existent for ruling purposes.

Key Terms
رحل (rahil): Saddlebag of a camel, also used for a person's dwelling. Here, it specifically refers to the saddlebag where water is typically stored.
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetfulness; a state opposite to knowledge that excuses the person from the obligation to use water if typical.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the ruling if a person forgets water that was hung on his back and performs tayammum?
A) He does not repeat, because forgetfulness is an excuse.
B) He must repeat, because the back is not a normal water storage place.
C) He must repeat only if he was riding.
D) The ruling depends on whether he was driving or riding.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness of water in a normally kept place excuses tayammum (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but suspicion or unusual forgetfulness requires repetition.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
Forgetting Water While Performing Tayammum: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum with forgotten water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on tayammum when water is forgotten in the saddlebag and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between the views.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness of water in the saddlebag: does it excuse tayammum or not? The Hanafi school disagrees.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when a traveler performs tayammum while water is actually in his saddlebag but he forgets or does not know about it, is his tayammum valid and must he repeat the prayer? The answer depends on the precise location of the water, whether he placed it himself, and the strength of the evidence. We will examine the arguments of Abu Yusuf (two aspects) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and see how later Hanafi authorities weighed them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the contested ruling
Read the opening lines: the traveler is riding, water is in front of the saddle; the text distinguishes cases where water is placed with or without the traveler's knowledge. The disputed ruling is whether tayammum and subsequent prayer are valid without repetition.
Note: if water was placed by another without the traveler's command, there is consensus that no repetition is required.
2
State Abu Yusuf's two aspects (wajhan)
The text reports for Abu Yusuf two opposing views: (1) the traveler forgot something not normally forgotten — water is crucial for survival, so forgetfulness is treated as non-existence, thus tayammum is invalid and repetition is required. (2) The saddlebag is the usual place for water, so searching is obligatory as in inhabited areas, again requiring repetition.
These aspects show the internal tension in Abu Yusuf's own reasoning.
3
State the Sahibayn's argument (lahuma)
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad together) argue that inability to use water due to lack of knowledge negates obligation: 'no obligation without ability' (la taklifa bila qudra). Knowledge is the strongest instrument for ability; if lost, tayammum is valid.
This is a straightforward application of the usul principle that obligation is contingent on capacity.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the Sahibayn, the traveler does not repeat his prayer. According to Abu Yusuf's first aspect, he must repeat. This difference matters in daily practice for travelers and for fatwa.
The text later lists many cases where forgetfulness is NOT excused, implying that this case is different.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The passage does not give a definitive tarjih but leans toward the Sahibayn's view by criticizing Abu Yusuf's second aspect (the saddlebag indicates drinking water, not ablution water). Later Hanafi authorities like the author of al-Hidayah and al-Fath al-Qadir treat the matter as disputed, but the operative fatwa in many later texts favors the Sahibayn.
The dispute remains unresolved in classical sources; the mufti must weigh the evidence.

لأن فوات الأصل إلى خلف لا يجوز الخلف مع فقد شرطه، بل إذا فقد شرطه مع فوات الأصل يصير فاقداً للطهورين فيلزمه حكمه وهو التأخير عنده والتشبه عندهما بالمصلين. كذا في فتح القدير. ولقائل أن يقول : قوله لأن أثناء الكتاب إن شاء الله تعالى .

Similarly when he is leading absolutely. We restricted it to being placed with his knowledge because if someone else placed it, even his slave or hireling without his command, he does not repeat by consensus, because a person is not addressed by the action of another. Thus in al-Nihayah, and a group of commentators followed him, and al-Fath al-Qadir referred to it. But Ghayat al-Bayan objected that the claim of consensus is an error and not correct. It is narrated from Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that it is subject to disagreement, and the truth is what is in al-Bada'i' that there is no transmission for this as a text. Some mashayikh said: The wording of the riwaya in al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that it is permissible by consensus, for he said concerning a man who has water in his saddlebag and forgets – and forgetfulness presupposes prior knowledge – yet despite that he made it an excuse in his view, so a place where there is absolutely no knowledge should be made an excuse for everyone. And the wording of the riwaya in Kitab al-Salah indicates that it is subject to disagreement, for he said: A traveler performs tayammum while he has water in his saddlebag and does not know about it, and this includes the state of forgetfulness and others. For Abu Yusuf there are two aspects: one is that he forgot something not normally forgotten because the most precious things in travel due to being a means of saving oneself from destruction, so the heart is attached, so forgetfulness is attached to non-existence; the second is that the saddlebag is the usual place for water due to the traveler's need for it, so searching is obligatory as in inhabited areas. And for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that he is unable to use water, so he is not obligated to use it. This is because there is no ability without knowledge, for the capable person is one who, if he wants to accomplish an action, it is possible for him, and there is no obligation without ability. And if his ability is lost due to loss of other instruments, his tayammum is permissible; if he loses knowledge, which is the strongest instrument, it is more appropriate. Al-Fath al-Qadir objected that this does not benefit after what was established for Abu Yusuf due to the establishment of knowledge by way of evidence universally, as everyone said in the related cases. Rather, the only benefit is the denial of the existence of the 'illa, i.e., we do not accept that the saddlebag is an indicator of water whose existence prevents tayammum – I mean water for ablution – but rather for drinking it is not present for other than drinking. And if he prayed naked while having a clean garment in his saddlebag without knowing, then he came to know, some said he must repeat by consensus, and al-Karkhi mentioned that it is subject to disagreement, which is more correct. Similarly, water from him? Thus it is restricted by forgetfulness to exclude the case where he doubts or thinks his water has run out, then prays, then finds it, for he repeats by consensus, so be aware. His statement: (But it is objected that if he prayed...) I say: It is apparently questionable because if this case is like the case of praying naked in the obligation to repeat by consensus, its face is clear because the garment is in his saddlebag and the saddlebag is prepared for the garment, but it does not suit what follows, although that is in al-Fath al-Qadir and its text. But it is problematic with the case of praying with a najis garment forgetting the tahir, for it is like the case of praying naked, although the saddlebag is not prepared for water for ablution but rather for water for drinking as we explained. And what occurred in Sharh al-Kanz and others of the difference between them and the case of forgetting water for ablution and performing tayammum, that the obligation of covering and removal of impurity is lost without a substitute, unlike ablution, does not satisfy the mind upon reflection because loss of the original to a substitute is not permissible when the condition of the substitute is lost. Rather, if its condition is lost along with the loss of the original, he becomes one who lacks both purifiers, so his ruling applies, which is delay according to him and imitating the praying according to the two. Thus in al-Fath al-Qadir. And it may be said: His statement 'because loss of the original...' is correct; but his statement 'rather if its condition is lost...' is not apparent because the condition for the permissibility of the substitute is inability to perform the original, and this condition is lost due to ability to perform the original, so how does loss of the condition of the substitute combine with loss of the original? Rather, the loss of the condition of the substitute necessitates the existence of the original because its condition is the loss of the original, so it is lost by its existence. And there is no difference in the book between remembering it during the time or after. If he passes by water while he is in tayammum but forgets that he is in tayammum, his tayammum is invalidated. If he pitches a tent over the mouth of a well covering its top and does not know about it, then performs tayammum and prays, then learns about the water, he is commanded to repeat. And they agreed that forgetfulness is not excused in cases such as: when a person in hadath forgets washing some of his limbs; when he prays sitting imagining inability to stand while able; when a judge rules by analogy forgetting the text; when he forgets the slave in kaffarah and fasts; when he performs wudu with impure water forgetfully; when he does something invalidating prayer forgetfully; when he does something prohibited in ihram forgetfully; and many cases that will be known during the book, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the Hanafi intra-school dispute regarding tayammum performed by a traveler who has water in his saddlebag but forgets or is unaware of it. The author examines various scenarios: the rider has water in front of him, behind him, or is leading the animal; the water is placed with or without his knowledge. The initial ruling differentiates between the saddlebag's position: if water is in front and known, there is disagreement. If placed without knowledge, there is consensus that no repetition is required because one is not held accountable for another's action. However, some scholars like Fakhr al-Islam report that even this is disputed. The core of the dispute is whether ignorance of the water's presence excuses tayammum. Abu Yusuf presents two arguments: first, forgetfulness of water in travel is unlikely due to its importance, so it is treated as non-existent; second, the saddlebag is the normal place for water, so searching is obligatory. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that inability to use water due to lack of knowledge negates obligation, as ability requires knowledge. The author then compares with the case of praying naked while having a clean garment in the saddlebag; some say consensus requires repetition, but al-Karkhi says it is disputed. The discussion continues to refine the conditions for the substitute (tayammum) versus the original (wudu), emphasizing that loss of the original's condition (knowledge of water) leads to complete lack of both purifiers. The passage concludes by listing various cases where forgetfulness is not excused, such as forgetting to wash limbs in wudu, praying while able to stand, etc., illustrating that the rule is context-dependent. Throughout, the author engages with earlier commentaries like al-Nihayah, Fath al-Qadir, and Ghayat al-Bayan, showing the maturation of the Hanafi discourse.

Key Terms
رَحْل (rahl): The saddlebag or luggage of a traveler, often where water is kept.
نِسْيَان (nisyān): Forgetfulness; in this context, the failure to recall the presence of water in one's saddlebag.
تَيَمُّم (tayammum): Dry ablution as a substitute for wudu when water is not available or cannot be used.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the Sahibayn's argument that a traveler who forgets water in his saddlebag does not need to repeat his prayer?
A) The saddlebag is not the usual place for water.
B) Ability to use water requires knowledge, and without knowledge there is no obligation.
C) Forgetfulness is always excused in travel.
D) The water was placed by someone else.

Key Takeaway
When water is forgotten in the saddlebag, the Hanafi school is divided: the Sahibayn excuse tayammum due to lack of knowledge, while a view from Abu Yusuf requires repetition based on the customary importance of water.

Searching for Water Before Tayammum: The Obligation and Distance
Ruling on talab al-ma' for a traveler before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation to search for water before tayammum and identify the distance required.

Core Idea
If a traveler hopes water is nearby, he must search a bowshot; otherwise, no search is required.

Before performing tayammum, a traveler must confirm that water is not available. The Hanafi school specifies that if the traveler has a reasonable hope (zann) that water is nearby (within less than a mile), he must search up to the distance of a bowshot (ghalwah). If he does not hope, no search is needed. This lesson explains the ruling, the conditions, and the proof from the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is searching for water (talab al-ma'). The ruling is wajib (obligatory) when the traveler hopes water is near; otherwise it is not wajib.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Determine the condition of hope
The obligation is conditioned on 'zann al-qurb' – a reasonable expectation that water is within less than a mile.
The limit of 'near' is defined as less than a mile; a mile or more is considered far.
3
Identify the required distance of search
The search must cover a bowshot (ghalwah), approximately 300-400 cubits, based on the practice reported by Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some say 300 cubits, some 400, some the distance of hearing a voice.
4
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is the narration of Abu Yusuf asking Abu Hanifa, establishing the ghalwah measure. The command to 'search' implies obligation when hope exists.
The dalil is ahad and zanni, but relied upon in the school.
5
Note the exception for inhabited areas
In towns ('umran), searching is obligatory by consensus, regardless of hope.
The rule is specific to travelers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة . قوله ( ويطلبه غلوة إن ظن قربه وإلا (لا) أي يجب على المسافر طلب الماء قدر غلوة إن ظن قربه، وإن لم يظن قربه لا يجب عليه وحد القرب ما دون الميل قيدنا به لأن الميل وما فوقه بعيد لا يوجب الطلب، وقيدنا بالمسافر لأن طلب الماء في العمران واجب اتفاقاً مطلقاً، وكذا لو كان بقرب منها وقد اختلفوا في مقدار الطلب فاختار المصنف هنا قدر في التبيين، أو ثلثمائة ذراع كما في الذخيرة، والمغرب إلى أربعمائة، واختار في لمستصفى أنه يطلب مقدار ما يسمع صوت أصحابه الموافق لما قال أبو يوسف : سألت أبا حنيفة عن المسافر لا يجد الماء أيطلب عن يمين الطريق غلوة وهي مقدار رمية كما سهم ويسمع صوته وهو التيمم هو القدرة ومعها لا يفوت الأصل. وفي النهر أقول : لا خفاء أن من شرائط التيمم طهارة المتيمم عليه فإذا فقد هذا فوات الأصل وهو القدرة على الماء صار فاقد الطهورين. وهذا وإن كان عدولاً . عن الظاهر إلا أنه يرتكب تصحيحاً لكلام هذا الإمام .
Issue. His statement: 'And he searches for it a bowshot if he thinks it is near, otherwise no.' Meaning: The traveler is obligated to search for water to the extent of a bowshot if he thinks it is near. If he does not think it is near, it is not obligatory. The limit of nearness is less than a mile; we restricted it thus because a mile or more is far and does not obligate search. We restricted it to the traveler because searching for water in inhabited areas is absolutely obligatory by consensus, similarly if he is near them. And they differed on the amount of search. The author chose here a qadr in al-Tabyeen, or three hundred cubits as in al-Dhakhirah, and in al-Mustasfa it is chosen that he searches the distance of hearing the voice of his companions, which agrees with what Abu Yusuf said: I asked Abu Hanifa about a traveler who does not find water: should he search to the right of the road a bowshot, which is the distance of an arrow shot? And he hears his voice, and tayammum is the ability, and with it the original is not lost. In al-Nahr, I say: It is clear that among the conditions of tayammum is the purification of the one performing tayammum. So if this is lost, the loss of the original, which is the ability to use water, he becomes one lacking both purifiers. And this, even if it is a departure from the apparent, is undertaken to correct the words of this imam.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage introduces the obligation of a traveler to search for water before performing tayammum. The key ruling: if the traveler hopes (ظن) that water is nearby (within less than a mile), he must search up to a bowshot (غلوة), which is approximately the distance an arrow travels (about 300-400 cubits). If he does not think it is near, no search is required. This obligation applies only to travelers; in towns or settlements, searching for water is obligatory by consensus. The author notes different opinions on the exact distance: some say three hundred cubits, others four hundred, and some say to the distance one can hear the voices of companions. This is based on what Abu Yusuf reported from Abu Hanifa. The passage then shifts to a subtle point: tayammum itself is a kind of ability (قدرة), and with this ability, the original (wudu) is not lost. However, one condition for tayammum is that the person performing it must be in a state of purification (i.e., the tayammum must be valid). If this condition is lost, then the person lacks both water and valid tayammum, becoming one who has neither purifier (فاقد الطهورين). The author comments that this interpretation, though departing from the apparent meaning, is necessary to reconcile the words of the imam (likely Abu Hanifa). Overall, this section establishes the fiqh of talab al-ma' as a prerequisite for tayammum.

Key Terms
غَلْوَة (ghalwah): A bowshot; a distance approximately 300-400 cubits, used as the limit of search for water.
عُمْرَان (ʿumrān): Inhabited areas, towns or settlements where water is expected to be available.
طَلَب الْمَاء (ṭalab al-māʾ): Searching for water as a prerequisite for tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to search for water before tayammum is conditional on the traveler's hope of finding water nearby, and the required distance is a bowshot.

Forgetting Water and Performing Tayammum: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forgetfulness and tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that forgetfulness does not excuse tayammum when water is available, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the subsequent obligation.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not create a legal excuse: if water was present, tayammum is invalid and prayer must be repeated.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a traveler forgets water in his saddlebag and performs tayammum? The core is whether forgetfulness (nisyan) can validate a substitute when the original is available. The Hanafi school agrees that forgetfulness does not excuse the obligation to use water, but they differ on what the person should do upon realization. We will trace the reasoning, critique a proposed distinction, and see how the ruling applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Problem and Common Ground
Identify the scenario: a person forgets water in his saddlebag, performs tayammum, and prays. Note that all Hanafi authorities agree forgetfulness does not make the tayammum valid; the prayer must be repeated.
2
Compare the Two Positions Within the School
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view (delay prayer until water is found) with the Sahibayn's view (imitate the congregation by performing tayammum and praying). Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
3
Analyze the Proof for Non‑Excuse
The key dalil: the condition for the substitute (tayammum) is the absence of the original (water). Forgetfulness does not change the fact that water was present; thus the condition is missing, rendering tayammum invalid. The passage rejects a distinction based on the saddlebag's purpose.
4
Evaluate the Tarjih (Relied‑Upon Position)
The text concludes with 'he is commanded to repeat' (أمر بالإعادة), indicating the operative ruling is that the prayer must be repeated. Note also the list of analogous cases where forgetfulness is not excused.
The mufta bihi position is repetition, though Abu Hanifa's delay and Sahibayn's imitation differ on the immediate action.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم لا لفوت جمعة ووقت ولم يعد أن صلى به ونسي الماء في رحله ويطلبه غلوة إن ظن في البدائع . فإن كان على الاختلاف فظاهر، وإن كان بالإجماع فالفرق على قولهما أن الرحل معد للثوب لا لماء الوضوء لكن يرد عليه لو صلى مع ثوب نجس ناسياً الطاهر فإنها كمسألة الصلاة عارياً مع أن الرحل ليس معداً لماء الاستعمال بل لماء الشرب كما بينا. وما وقع في شرح الكنز وغيره من الفرق بينهما وبين ما لو نسي ماء الوضوء فتيمم بأن فرض الستر وإزالة النجاسة فات لا إلى خلف بخلاف الوضوء، لا يثلج الخاطر عند التأمل لأن فوات الأصل إلى خلف لا يجوز الخلف مع فقد شرطه، بل إذا فقد شرطه مع فوات الأصل يصير فاقداً للطهورين فيلزمه حكمه وهو التأخير عنده والتشبه عندهما بالمصلين. كذا في فتح القدير. ولقائل أن يقول : قوله لأن فوات الأصل إلى آخره صحيح، وأما قوله «بل إذا فقد شرطه إلى آخره فليس بظاهر لأن شرط جواز الخلف عدم القدرة على الأصل وفقد هذا الشرط بالقدرة على الأصل فكيف يجتمع فقد شرط الخلف مع فوات الأصل؟ بل يلزم من فقد شرط الخلف وجود الأصل لأن شرطه فوات الأصل ففقده بوجوده، ولا فرق في الكتاب بين أن يذكره في الوقت أو بعده ولو مر بالماء وهو متيمم لكنه نسي أنه تيمم ينتقض تيممه، ولو ضرب الفسطاط على رأس البئر قد غطى رأسها ولم يعلم بذلك فتيمم وصلى ثم علم بالماء أمر بالإعادة واتفقوا على أن النسيان غير معفو في مسائل منها : ما لو نسي المحدث غسل بعض أعضائه، ومنها لو صلى قاعداً متوهماً عجزه عن القيام وكان قادراً، ومنها أن الحاكم إذا حكم بالقياس ناسياً النص ومنها لو نسي الرقبة في الكفارة فصام، ومنها لو توضأ بماء نجس ناسياً ومنها لو فعل ما ينافي الصلاة ناسياً، ومنها لو فعل محظور الأحرام ناسياً، ومنها مسائل كثيرة تعرف في أثناء الكتاب إن شاء الله تعالى .
The book of purification - chapter of tayammum. Not due to missing Jumu'ah or time, and he did not repeat after praying with it, and he forgot water in his saddlebag, and he seeks it for one bow-shot if he thinks [water is near]. In al-Bada'i. If it is based on ikhtilaf, it is apparent; if it is by consensus, the distinction according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the saddlebag is prepared for clothing, not for ablution water. But it is objected that if he prayed with a najis garment while forgetting the pure one, it is like the case of praying naked, even though the saddlebag is not prepared for used water but for drinking water as we explained. Whatever occurs in Sharh al-Kanz and others of the distinction between these two and the case of forgetting ablution water and performing tayammum—that the obligation of covering and removing impurity is lost without substitute, unlike ablution—does not satisfy the heart upon reflection because losing the original for substitute is not valid when the condition of the substitute is missing. But when its condition is missing along with the loss of the original, he becomes one who lacks both purifiers (tahurayn), so its ruling applies: which is delay according to him (Abu Hanifa) and imitating the praying people according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Quoted from Fath al-Qadir. Someone may say: His statement 'because losing the original...' is correct. As for his statement 'but when its condition is missing...', it is not apparent because the condition for the validity of the substitute is the inability to use the original, and the loss of this condition is due to ability to use the original. So how does the loss of the condition of the substitute coincide with the loss of the original? Rather, the loss of the condition of the substitute implies the existence of the original because its condition is the loss of the original, so its loss occurs through its existence. And there is no difference in the book between whether he remembers it during the time or after. Even if he passes by water while he is in tayammum but he forgot that he made tayammum, his tayammum is nullified. If he pitched a tent over the mouth of a well, covering its top, and he did not know that, so he performed tayammum and prayed, then he learned of the water, he is commanded to repeat. And they are agreed that forgetfulness is not excused in matters including: when a person in a state of hadath forgets to wash some of his limbs; when one prays sitting thinking he is unable to stand while he is able; when the judge rules by analogy forgetting the text; when one forgets the slave in the expiation and fasts; when one performs wudu with najis water forgetfully; when one does something that invalidates prayer forgetfully; when one does a prohibition of ihram forgetfully; and many other matters that will be known during the book, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author discusses the ruling when a traveler forgets that he has water in his saddlebag and performs tayammum. The core issue is whether forgetfulness excuses the obligation to repeat the prayer. According to the Hanafi school, forgetfulness does not excuse; if one had access to water but forgot it and performed tayammum, his tayammum is invalid and he must repeat the prayer if he remembers within the time. The passage first notes that if the failure to find water is due to an oversight (ikhtilaf), the ruling is as stated. If there is consensus (ijma'), the distinction made by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that the saddlebag is meant for clothing, not for water for wudu, so forgetting water is different from forgetting a pure garment. However, the author rejects an alternative distinction found in some commentaries that tayammum for missing water is like covering the 'awrah or removing najasah which have no substitute. He argues that this is flawed because the condition for the substitute (tayammum) is the absence of water; if the original (water) is present, even if forgotten, the condition for the substitute is missing, so the substitute is invalid. Therefore, the person becomes one who lacks both water and valid tayammum (faqid al-tahurayn). According to Abu Hanifa, such a person must delay prayer until he can find water; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, he should imitate the praying people (perform tayammum and pray with the congregation). The passage also discusses cases where forgetfulness is not excused, such as forgetting to wash a limb in wudu, praying while seated despite ability, a judge ruling by analogy ignoring a text, etc. It concludes that there is no difference between remembering within the time or after.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness; here it refers to unintentionally forgetting that one has water available.
الطهورين (al-tahurayn): The two purifiers: water and earth (for tayammum). When both are unavailable or invalid, one is faqid al-tahurayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) His tayammum is valid and prayer is acceptable.
B) His tayammum is invalid and he must repeat the prayer if he remembers.
C) He may continue with tayammum if he is a traveler.
D) He must delay prayer until he finds water again.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness does not change the objective condition for tayammum; if water was present, the tayammum is invalid and the prayer must be repeated.

Seeking Water for Tayammum: Obligation, Method, and Disputes
Explains the ruling on seeking water before tayammum, the method, and the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking water before tayammum, describe the method, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using Quranic examples.

Core Idea
Seeking water is not a condition of tayammum itself; it is a means to verify absence, and the obligation depends on probability.

Before performing tayammum, a traveler may need to look for water. But is this always required? The Hanafi school draws a careful line: seeking is obligatory only when there is a real chance of finding water. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq walks through the rulings, the method, and the Shafi'i disagreement, with a detailed Quranic argument that 'finding' does not presuppose prior seeking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is seeking water (talab) before tayammum. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory) under certain conditions, not fard. Note that the evidence for obligation is zanni.
Wajib vs fard: missing a wajib requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
2
Understand the method of seeking
The seeker must look in four directions (right, left, front, back) up to a distance of one ghaluwah (approx. 400 cubits). Walking is not necessarily required if looking suffices. If a nearby hill exists, he must climb it if no harm. He may send someone else or rely on information from a reliable person.
The text from al-Haqa'iq suggests looking is enough, but later commentators clarify that walking is implied to cover the distance.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from Quranic usage
The Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i claim that 'finding' (wujud) requires prior seeking. They cite multiple Quranic verses where 'wujud' occurs without prior search, e.g., 'We found what our Lord promised us true' (al-A'raf 44), 'He found you lost and guided' (al-Duha 7). Therefore, adding the condition of seeking is an impermissible addition to the text.
This is a classic Hanafi dalil naqli argument showing that the Shafi'i inference is not supported by linguistic usage.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that seeking is obligatory in all cases because the verse 'if you do not find water' implies that absence must be established through seeking. The Hanafi response: the textual evidence does not support this; however, in populated areas ('umranat), external indicators (buildings) suggest water, so absence is not established externally without seeking.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in a desert with certain absence, Hanafi allows tayammum without seeking; Shafi'i still requires seeking (but practically impossible).
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider three scenarios: 1) Desert with no sign of water → no seeking required. 2) Populated area → seeking wajib because buildings indicate water. 3) Strong probability of water nearby → seeking wajib. Mere hope (tama') → mustahabb (recommended) only. Also, if a companion has water, one must ask unless certain of refusal.
The passage details the sequence: if thought he would give but didn't, or if uncertain, the ruling varies.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
أو عن يساره؟ قال : إن طمع فيه فليفعل ولا يبعد فيضر بأصحابه إن انتظروه وبنفسه إن انقطع عنهم. ويوافقه ما صححه في البدائع فقال : والأصح أنه يطلب قدر ما لا يضر بنفسه ورفقته بالأنتظار فكان المعتمد. وعلى اعتبار الغلوة فالطلب أن ينظر يمينه وشماله وأمامه هو ووراءه غلوة. كذا في الحقائق وظاهره أنه لا يلزمه المشي بل يكفيه النظر في هذه الجهات وهو في مكانه. وهذا إذا كان حواليه لا يستتر عنه فإن كان بقربه جبل صغير ونحوه صعده ونظر حواليه إن لم يخف ضرراً على نفسه أو ماله الذي معه أو المخلف في رحله، فإن خاف لم يلزمه الصعود والمشي. كذا في التوشيح . ولو بعث من يطلب له كفاه عن الطلب بنفسه، وكذا لو أخبره من غير أن يرسله كذا في منية المصلي. ولو تيمم من غير طلب وكان الطلب واجباً وصلى ثم طلبه فلم يجده وجبت عليه الإعادة عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. كذا السراج الوهاج. وفي المستصفى وفي إيراد هذه المسألة عقيب المسألة المتقدمة لطيفة فإن الاختلاف في تلك المسألة بناء على اشتراط الطلب وعدمه .اهـ. وعند الشافعي يجب الطلب مطلقاً لقوله تعالى فلم تجدوا ماء لأن الوجود يقتضي سابقة الطلب وهي دعوى لا دليل عليها لقوله تعالى أن قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقا فهل وجدتم ما وعد ربكم حقا قالوا نعم [الأعراف: ٤٤] ولا طلب. وقوله تعالى ووجدك ضالاً فهدى [الضحى : ٧] وقوله فمن لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين ﴾ [النساء : ۹۲] وقوله ووجدوا ما عملوا حاضر [الكهف : ٤٩] ولم يطلبوا خطاياهم. وقوله تعالى وما وجدنا لأكثرهم ما عهد وإن وجدنا أكثرهم لفاسقين﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۰۲] وقوله فوجدا فيها جداراً يريد أن ينقض [الكهف: ۷۷] ولقوله عليه السلام من وجد لقطة فليعرفها ) (۱) ولا طلب من الواجد، ولقوله «من وجد زاداً وراحلة ويقال فلان وجد ماله وإن لم يطلبه ووجد مرضاً في نفسه ولم يطلبه، فقد ثبت أن الوجود يتحقق من غير طلب والله تعالى جعل شرط الجواز عدم الوجود من غير طلب فمن زاد شرط الطلب فقد زاد على النص وهو لا يجوز بخلاف العمرانات لأن العدم وإن ثبت حقيقة لم يثبت ظاهراً لأن كون الماء في العمرانات دليل ظاهر على وجود
قوله : (أي يجب على المسافر طلب الماء) يعني يفترض كما في الشرنبلالية مستدلاً بقول
قاضيخان يشترط . قوله : وظاهره أنه لا يلزمه المشي قال في النهر أقول: معنى ما في الحقائق أنه يقسم المشي مقدار الغلوة على هذه الجهات فيمشي على أنها أربعمائة ذراع من كل جانب مائة ذراع إذ الطلب لا يتم بمجرد النظر ويدل على ذلك ما مر عن الإمام وما في منية المصلي : لو بعث من يطلب له كفاه عن الطلب بنفسه، وكذا لو أخبره مكلف عدل من غير إرسال إذ على ما فهمه لا يحتاج إلى البعث أصلاً .اهـ. واعلم أن ما نقله هنا عن الحقائق هو مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله وذلك (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الزكاة باب ٦٦.

قربه وإلا لا ويطلبه من رفيقه فإن منعه تيمم وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله وله ثمنه لا
الماء لأن قيام العمارة بالماء فكان العدم ثابتاً من وجه دون وجه وشرط الجواز العدم المطلق ولا يثبت ذلك في العمرانات إلا بعد الطلب، وبخلاف ما إذا غلب على ظنه قربه لأن غلبة الظنّ تعمل عمل اليقين في حق وجوب العمل وإن لم تعمل في حق الاعتقاد كما في التحري في القبلة، وكما في دفع الزكاة لمن غلب على ظنه فقره، وكما إذا غلب على ظنه نجاسة الماء أو طهارته، وأما إذا لم يغلب على ظنه قربه فلا يجب بل يستحب إذا كان على طمع من وجود الماء. كذا في البدائع. وظاهره أنه إذا لم يطمع لا يستحب له الطلب، وعلل له في المبسوط بأنه لا فائدة فيه إذا لم يكن على رجاء منه. وبما تقرر علم أن المراد بالظن غالبه، والفرق بينهما على ما حققه اللامشي في أصوله أن أحد الطرفين إذا قوي وترجح على الآخر ولم يأخذ القلب ما ترجح به ولم يطرح الآخر فهو الظنّ، وإذا عقد القلب على أحدهما وترك الآخر فهو أكبر الظن وغالب الرأي .اهـ. وغلبة الظنّ هنا إما بأن وجد أمارة ظاهرة أو أخبره مخبر . كذا أطلقه في التوشيح وقيده في البدائع بالعدل.
قوله (ويطلبه من رفيقه فإن منعه تيمم أي يطلب الماء من رفيقه . أطلقه هنا وفصل في الوافي فقال : مع رفيقه ماء فظنّ أنه إن سأله أعطاه لم يجز التيمم، وإن كان عنده أنه لا يعطيه يتيمم، وإن شك في الإعطاء وتيمم وصلى فسأله فأعطاه يعيد. وعلل له في الكافي بأنه ظهر أنه كان قادراً وإن منعه قبل شروعه وأعطاه بعد فراغه لم يعد لأنه لم يتبين أن القدرة كانت ثابته اهـ. اعلم أن ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا الثلاثة وجوب السؤال من الرفيق كما يفيده ما في المبسوط قال : وإذا كان مع رفيقه ماء فعليه أن يسأله إلا على قول الحسن بن زياد فإنه كان يقول : السؤال ذل وفيه بعض الحرج وما شرع التيمم إلا لدفع الحرج ولكنا نقول : لأنه قال في الشافي عند قول النسفي ولا لفرضين وقبل الوقت ولا بغير طلب وفوت» ما نصه : المسألة الثالثة : لا يجوز لعادم الماء أن يتيمم إلا بعد الطلب عند توهم وجود الماء حواليه، ولا الطلب إلا بعد دخول الوقت والطلب أن ينظر يمينه وشماله وأمامه ووراءه غلوة، وعندنا الطلب وعند تحقق عدم الماء حواليه يتيمم من غير طلب إجماعاً اهـ كلامه. وكان المؤلف حمل كلامه على أن ذلك التفسير للطلب ليس خاصاً بقول الشافعي هذا وفي شرح المنية الصغير : فيطلب يميناً ويساراً قدر غلوة من كل جانب وهي ثلثمائة خطوة إلى أربعمائة وقيل قدر رمية سهم اهـ. وظاهره أن الطلب غلوة من جانبي اليمين واليسار ولذا قال في الشرح الكبير : ولا يلزمه أن يطلبه مقدار ميل من كل جانب للزوم الضرر .اهـ. ويؤيده ما مر من سؤال أبي يوسف لأبي حنيفة وجوابه له وكذا نقل بعضهم عن البرجندي وخزانة المفتين أنه يجب في جانب اليمين واليسار، وكذا في الشرنبلالية عن قاضيخان لكن فيها عن البرهان إن قدر الطلب بغلوة من
جانب ظنه اهـ .

Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the obligation of seeking water for tayammum. It begins by stating that a traveler must seek water, and if he has hope of finding it, he should do so without causing harm to himself or his companions. The relied-upon position is that he seeks water to the extent that does not harm himself or his party by waiting. The method of seeking is to look to his right, left, front, and back the distance of a ghaluwah (approximately 400 cubits). According to al-Haqa'iq, it appears that walking is not required; merely looking in these directions while stationary suffices. If there is a hill nearby, he should climb it and look around if no harm comes to him, his property, or his belongings. If harm is feared, he is not obliged to climb or walk. Sending someone else to seek water is sufficient, as is being informed by a reliable person without sending. If someone performs tayammum without seeking, though seeking was obligatory, and then later seeks but finds no water, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad he must repeat his prayer; Abu Yusuf disagrees. The Shafi'i school holds that seeking is absolutely obligatory, based on the verse 'if you do not find water' claiming that existence presupposes prior seeking. The Hanafi response uses numerous Quranic examples where 'finding' occurs without seeking, proving that existence can be realized without prior search. Therefore, adding a condition of seeking is an addition to the text, which is impermissible. However, in populated areas ('umranat), the absence of water is not established externally because buildings indicate the presence of water, so seeking is required there. If one has strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) that water is near, seeking becomes obligatory; otherwise it is recommended if there is hope. The passage then discusses seeking from a companion: it is obligatory to ask, except according to Hasan ibn Ziyad who considered asking as demeaning. If one thinks the companion will give water, tayammum is invalid without asking; if he thinks he will not give, he may do tayammum; if uncertain, he asks and if given, he repeats. The distance for seeking is generally a ghaluwah in each direction, with variations reported.

Key Terms
طلب (talab): The act of seeking water before tayammum; it can be by looking, walking, or sending someone, within a specific distance (ghaluwah).
غلوة (ghaluwah): A distance measure, roughly 400 cubits (about 200 meters), used to define the radius within which one must seek water.
ظن (zann): A belief that one side is stronger than the other without fully committing the heart; here used to determine when seeking becomes obligatory (ghalabat al-zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is seeking water for tayammum obligatory?
A) Always, in every situation.
B) Only when there is strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) that water is nearby.
C) Only when one is in a populated area ('umran).
D) Never; tayammum can be done immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires seeking water before tayammum only when there is evidence of its possible presence; otherwise, tayammum is valid without prior search.

Taharah — Purification

Seeking Water from a Companion for Tayammum: Conditions and Obligation
Commentary on ruling of seeking water from companion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which seeking water from a travel companion becomes obligatory (wajib) before performing tayammum, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Seeking water from a companion is wajib only when water is scarce and you predominantly believe he will give it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical issue for the traveller without water: must he ask his companion for water before resorting to tayammum? The answer is not simple, involving a well-known disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two chief students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Through careful analysis, later Hanafi authorities reconciled these views by distinguishing between situations where asking is humiliating and where it is not, ultimately tying the obligation to the predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) of being given water, especially in water-scarce areas. Understanding this ruling equips you to apply the correct fiqh in travel scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core fiqh question
What is the ruling on seeking water from a travel companion before performing tayammum? Is it obligatory, recommended, or neither? The passage examines this through multiple narrations and opinions within the Hanafi school.
2
Trace the ikhtilaf among the three imams
Abu Hanifa (in Zahir al-Riwayah) does not obligate seeking; his students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, obligate it. The author then introduces a third narration from Hasan b. Ziyad that also does not obligate. Identify who holds which view.
Note the pronoun map: 'lahu' refers to Abu Hanifa, 'lahuma' to the Sahibayn.
3
Understand the role of predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann)
The passage explains that the obligation hinges on whether one predominantly believes the companion will give water. If yes, tayammum is invalid without seeking. If no, tayammum is permissible. Also, the distinction between zann (conjecture) and ghalib al-zann (predominant opinion) is clarified.
Ghalib al-zann is a stronger level of certainty that compels action.
4
Reconcile the differing narrations
The author reconciles Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions: Abu Hanifa's view (non-obligation) applies when one thinks he will be refused or where water is abundant and asking is humiliating. The Sahibayn's view (obligation) applies when water is scarce and the companion is likely to give. This is the mufta bihi position of later scholars like Abu Nasr al-Saffar.
The reconciliation preserves the principles of both avoiding humiliation and ensuring water is sought when easily available.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Based on the mufta bihi, determine the ruling for different cases: water scarce and thinks he will be given (wajib to ask); water abundant and thinks he will be refused (not wajib); doubt (not wajib, but recommended if hope exists). Also note the manner of seeking (looking around for a bowshot) and the exception for a companion's bucket.
The hadith of the Prophet asking for needs is cited but distinguished due to his special status.

الذهاب لا تدل على الإعطاء قبله. اهـ. وقد المتعلقة بها عن الزيادات، وفي التوشيح وأجمعوا أنه إذا قال أبحت لك مالي به فإنه لا يجب عليه الحج وأجمعوا أن في الماء إذا وعده صاحبه أن يعطيه لا يتيمم وينتظر وإن خرج الوقت والفرق بينهما أن القدرة في الأول لا تكون إلا بالملك، وفي الثاني قدمنا الفروع لتحج الشك والظاهر حمل عباراتهم على هذا توفيقاً بينها فتأمل قوله : فاندفع بهذا ما وقع في الهداية الخ) قد يوفق بين ما في المبسوط وما في الهداية بأن الحسن رواه عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله في غير ظاهر الرواية وأخذ هو به فاعتمد في المبسوط ظاهر الرواية، واعتمد صاحب الهداية رواية الحسن لكونها أنسب بمذهب أبي حنيفة رحمه الله في عدم اعتبار القدرة بالغير وفي اعتبار العجز للحال والله سبحانه أعلم. كذا في شرح المنية للعلامة البرهان إبراهيم الحلبي. وذكر قبله أن الوجه هو التفصيل كما قال أنه أبو نصر الصفار : إنه إنما يجب السؤال في غير موضع عزة الماء فإنه حينئذ بتحقق ما قالا من مبذول عادة في كل موضع ظاهر المنع على ما يشهد به كل من عانى في الاسفار، فينبغي أن يجب الطلب ولا تصح الصلاة بدونه فيما إذا ظن الإعطاء لظهور دليلهما دون ما إذا ظن عدمه لكونه في موضع عزة الماء، أما إذا شك في موضع عزة الماء أو ظن المنع في غيره فالاحتياط في قولهما والتوسعة في قوله لأن في السؤال ذلاً، وقول من قال لا ذل في سؤال ما يحتاج إليه ممنوع واستدلاله بأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سأل بعض حوائجه من غيره مستدرك لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان أولى بالمؤمنين من أنفسهم فلا يقاس غيره عليه لأنه إذا سال افترض على المسؤول البذل ولا كذلك غيره
Chapter of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum: [If water is] near, otherwise no, and he seeks it from his companion, and if he prevents him, he performs tayammum. And if he does not give it except at its equivalent price, and he has the price, he does not take the water because the maintenance of buildings is with water, so the non-existence is established from one aspect and not from another, and the condition for permissibility is absolute non-existence, and that is not established in inhabited areas except after seeking. Contrary to when his predominant opinion is that it is near, because predominant opinion acts like certainty regarding the obligation to act, even though it does not act in matters of belief, as in facing the qibla, and as in giving zakat to one whom he predominantly believes to be poor, and as when he predominantly believes water to be impure or pure. But when his predominant opinion is not that it is near, it is not obligatory but recommended if he has hope of finding water. Thus in al-Bada'i'. Its apparent meaning is that if he has no hope, seeking is not recommended, and al-Mabsut explains that there is no benefit if there is no hope. From what has been established, it is known that what is meant by 'zann' is the predominant one, and the difference between them, as al-Lamishi verified in his Usul, is that when one side strengthens and outweighs the other, and the heart does not accept that outweighing nor reject the other, it is 'zann'. When the heart settles on one and leaves the other, it is 'akbar al-zann' and 'ghalib al-ra'y'. End. And predominant opinion here either by finding a clear sign or by an informer. Thus al-Tawshih stated it absolutely, and al-Bada'i' restricted it to the just. His statement: 'and he seeks it from his companion, and if he prevents him, he performs tayammum' means he seeks water from his companion. He stated it absolutely here and detailed in al-Wafi: If his companion has water and he thinks that if he asks he will give him, tayammum is not permissible; if he is certain he will not give him, he performs tayammum; if he doubts about giving and performs tayammum and prays, then asks and he gives, he repeats. Al-Kafi gives the reason: because it became apparent that he was able. If he prevented him before starting and gave after finishing, he does not repeat because it was not shown that ability existed. End. Know that the apparent transmission from our three imams is the obligation of asking the companion, as indicated in al-Mabsut: If his companion has water, he must ask him, except according to the saying of Hasan b. Ziyad, who said: Asking is humiliation and involves hardship, and tayammum was only legislated to remove hardship. But we say: because he said in al-Shafi at the statement of al-Nasafi: 'and not for two obligatory prayers nor before the time nor without seeking and loss' verbatim: The third issue: It is not permissible for one who lacks water to perform tayammum except after seeking when he suspects water around him, and seeking is only after entering the time, and the seeking is that he looks to his right, left, front, and back for a bowshot. According to us, seeking is required. And when there is certainty that there is no water around him, he performs tayammum without seeking, by consensus. End of his speech. The author took his speech to mean that this interpretation of seeking is not specific to al-Shafi'i's statement. In Sharh al-Munyah al-Saghir: He seeks right and left for a bowshot from each side, which is three hundred to four hundred steps, and it is said a bowshot. End. Its apparent meaning is that seeking is a bowshot from the right and left sides. Hence in al-Sharh al-Kabir: He is not required to seek for a mile from each side because of hardship. End. It is supported by what came of Abu Yusuf's question to Abu Hanifa and his answer to him. Similarly, some transmitted from al-Birjandi and Khizanat al-Muftin that it is obligatory on the right and left sides, and similarly in al-Sharnabaliyya from Qadikhan, but in it from al-Burhan is that the seeking is limited to a bowshot from the side he suspects. End. [PAGE_283] Chapter of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum 283: Water for purification is normally available among people, and there is no humiliation in asking for what one needs, for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) asked some of his needs from others. End. By this is repudiated what occurred in al-Hidaya and Sharh al-Aqta' concerning the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions: according to him, seeking is not obligatory; according to them, it is obligatory. And repudiated is what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the saying of Hasan is good. In al-Dhakhira, quoting al-Jassas, there is no difference between Abu Hanifa and his two companions: he meant when he predominantly believes he will prevent him, and they meant when the predominant opinion is that he will not prevent. In al-Mujtaba: the predominant is that there is no suspicion of water, so if there is a place where suspicion arises, seeking from him is not obligatory. End. If his companion has a bucket, he is not obligated to ask him. If he asks and he says, 'Wait until I draw water,' then according to Abu Hanifa it is recommended to wait for as long as the time does not go out; if he fears that, he performs tayammum; according to them, he waits even if he fears the time going out. The reason for their view is that when the promise exists, he becomes able by virtue of it because the default is that he will fulfill. On this same disagreement is the naked person if his companion promised him a garment. Thus in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Tawshih: If his companion has a bucket and he does not have water, he may perform tayammum before asking him about it. In al-Mujtaba: He saw water in someone else's hand during his prayer, then it went away before completion, so he asked him, and the other said, 'If you had asked me sooner, I would have given you.' There is no repetition upon him. If the promise was before starting, he repeats because it occurred in the start. The more correct view is that he does not repeat because the promise after loss does not indicate giving before it. End. And the related branches from al-Ziyadat. In al-Tawshih: They agreed that if he says, 'I have made permissible for you my wealth,' he is not obligated to perform Hajj. And they agreed that regarding water, if the owner promises to give it, he does not perform tayammum and waits even if the time exits. The difference is that ability in the first case is only through ownership, while in the second we have presented the branches to reject doubt. The apparent meaning is to reconcile their statements to achieve harmony, so reflect. His statement: 'By this is repudiated what occurred in al-Hidaya' etc. The reconciliation between what is in al-Mabsut and what is in al-Hidaya could be that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, and he took it, so al-Mabsut relied on the Zahir al-Riwayah, while the author of al-Hidaya relied on the narration of al-Hasan because it is more consistent with the school of Abu Hanifa in not considering ability through another and in considering current inability. And Allah Most High knows best. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah by the Allama al-Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi. He mentioned before that the correct approach is the detail as stated by Abu Nasr al-Saffar: Seeking is obligatory only where water is not scarce, because then what they said is verified: water is normally available in every place where prevention is apparent, as anyone who has experienced travel testifies. Accordingly, seeking must be obligatory and prayer without it is invalid when he thinks he will be given, due to the manifest evidence of their view, but not when he thinks he will not be given because the place is scarce in water. As for when he doubts in a water-scarce place or thinks prevention elsewhere, precaution is according to their view, and leniency according to his view because asking involves humiliation. The statement of those who say there is no humiliation in asking for what is needed is rejected, and his argument that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked some of his needs from others is invalid because he was more entitled to the believers than their own selves, so no one else can be analogized to him because when he asks, the person asked is obligated to give, but not so for others.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of seeking water from a companion for tayammum. The author explains the conditions under which one must ask a companion for water. The key distinction is whether the person has a predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) that the companion will give water. If he predominantly believes the water is near and he will be given, tayammum is not permissible; he must ask. If he predominantly believes he will not be given, he may perform tayammum without asking. If he is unsure (shakk) or has hope (tama') without predominant opinion, seeking is recommended but not obligatory. The author then discusses the nature of predominant opinion, distinguishing between zann (mere conjecture) and ghalib al-zann (strong predominant opinion). The text also clarifies that seeking water must be done in a specific manner: looking right, left, front, and back for about a bowshot (ghalwa), which is roughly 300-400 steps. However, seeking is not required in areas where water is normally available and asking is not considered humiliating, citing the Prophet's example. The author then addresses an apparent disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). He reconciles the different narrations: In Zahir al-Riwayah, Abu Hanifa does not obligate seeking, while in a narration by Hasan b. Ziyad, he does obligate it. The author of al-Hidayah preferred the latter because it aligns with Abu Hanifa's principle of not considering ability through another. The commentary ends with a detailed analysis from Abu Nasr al-Saffar: seeking is obligatory only where water is scarce and the person thinks he will be given; otherwise, given the humiliation, Abu Hanifa's view of leniency is preferred. The overall ruling is that the mufta bihi (relied-upon fatwa) is that seeking water from a companion is not obligatory unless there is a strong indication of being given, and even then, only if water is scarce. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet asking for his needs, but this is not analogized to others due to his special status.

Key Terms
طلب (talab): The act of seeking water from a companion, which involves looking left, right, front, and back for a bowshot.
غلوة (ghalwah): A bowshot, approximately 300-400 steps, used as the distance one must look for water.
رفيق (rafiq): A travel companion with whom one has a social relationship, and from whom one may seek water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled mufta bihi position in this passage, when is it obligatory to seek water from a companion before performing tayammum?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances
B) Only when the companion has a bucket
C) When water is scarce and one predominantly believes the companion will give
D) Only when one has no hope of finding water elsewhere

Key Takeaway
Seeking water from a companion before tayammum is wajib only when water is scarce and you have a strong belief that he will give it; otherwise, tayammum is valid without asking.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
