Seeking Water Before Tayammum: Resolving the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Resolving an intra-Hanafi dispute on talab al-ma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the detailed Hanafi position on seeking water before tayammum and apply the mufta bihi rule based on probability of obtaining water.

Core Idea
Seeking water is obligatory only when you strongly expect to receive it; otherwise, it is not.

A famous intra-Hanafi difference exists between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding whether one must actively seek water before resorting to tayammum. The apparent conflict is resolved by considering the context: if one expects to be given water, seeking becomes obligatory; if one expects refusal, it is not. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the nuanced reconciliation offered by later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Abu Hanifa says seeking is not obligatory (mustahab), while the Sahibayn say it is obligatory (wajib). Locate the key phrase in the passage that states this difference.
The phrase 'فعنده لا يلزمه الطلب، وعندهما يلزمه' summarizes the conflict.
2
Examine the basis of each view
Abu Hanifa relies on the general availability of water and the Prophet's example of asking without humiliation. The Sahibayn argue that a promise creates capability and seeking is a necessary means to an obligation.
The passage mentions the hadith of the Prophet asking for needs as a proof for Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Al-Jassas and later authors like Abu Nasr al-Saffar eliminate the disagreement by conditioning the obligation on ghalabat al-zann (strong assumption). If one strongly expects refusal, the obligation drops; if one strongly expects to receive, it stands.
The passage says 'مراده فيما إذا غلب على ظنه منعه إياه ومرادهما عند غلبة الظن بعدم المنع'.
4
Apply the detailed rule to scenarios
Consider cases: companion with a bucket, promise to give water, seeing water in someone's hand during prayer. The ruling depends on whether a promise creates de facto capability and whether time permits waiting.
The passage discusses the waiting period and the effect of a promise.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The preferred position, endorsed by al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Raiq, is the detailed view: seeking is obligatory when one expects to be given water; otherwise, it is not. This reconciles all narrations.
The passage ends with the reconciliation between al-Mabsut and al-Hidayah and the preference for the detail by Abu Nasr al-Saffar.

كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
ماء الطهارة مبذول عادة بين الناس وليس في سؤال ما يحتاج إليه مذلة فقد سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعض حوائجه من غيره .اهـ. فاندفع بهذا ما وقع في الهداية وشرح الأقطع الخلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه ؛ فعنده لا يلزمه الطلب، وعندهما يلزمه. واندفع ما في من غاية البيان من أن قول الحسن حسن. وفي الذخيرة نقلاً عن الجصاص أنه لا خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه فمراده فيما إذا غلب على ظنه منعه إياه ومرادهما عند غلبة الظن بعدم المنع. وفي المجتبى : الغالب عدم الظنة بالماء حتى لو كان في موضع تجري الظنة عليه لا يجب الطلب منه اهـ. ولو كان مع رفيقه دلو لم يجب أن يسأله ولو سألة فقال انتظر حتى أستقي فالمستحب عند أبي حنيفة أن ينتظر بقدر ما لا يفوت الوقت فإن خاف ذلك تيمم، وعندهما ينتظر. وإن خاف فوت الوقت وجه قولهما أن الوعد إذا وجد صار قادراً باعتباره لأن الظاهر أنه يفي به، وعلى هذا الخلاف العاري إذا وعد له رفيقه الثوب كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي فتح القدير والتوشيح: لو كان رفيقه دلو وليس معه له أن يتيمم قبل أن يسأله عنه. وفي المجتبى : رأى في صلاته ماء في يد غيره ثم ذهب منه قبل الفراغ فسأله فقال لو سألتني صحة لأعطيتك، فلا إعادة عليه وإن كانت العدة قبل الشروع يعيد لوقوع ا في الشروع، والأصح أنه لا يعيد لأن العدة بعد الذهاب لا تدل على الإعطاء قبله. اهـ. وقد المتعلقة بها عن الزيادات، وفي التوشيح وأجمعوا أنه إذا قال أبحت لك مالي به فإنه لا يجب عليه الحج وأجمعوا أن في الماء إذا وعده صاحبه أن يعطيه لا يتيمم وينتظر وإن خرج الوقت والفرق بينهما أن القدرة في الأول لا تكون إلا بالملك، وفي الثاني

Book of Purification - Chapter of Tayammum. Water for purification is usually available among people, and there is no humiliation in asking for what is needed, for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) asked some of his needs from others. End. So by this, what occurred in al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Aqta' regarding the difference between Abu Hanifa and his two companions is repelled. According to him, seeking is not obligatory; according to them, it is obligatory. And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the statement of al-Hasan is good is repelled. In al-Dhakhira, quoting from al-Jassas, there is no difference between Abu Hanifa and his two companions. His meaning is when he strongly assumes that he will be prevented, and their meaning is when he strongly assumes that he will not be prevented. In al-Mujtaba: the predominant assumption is that there is no suspicion of water, so even if he is in a place where suspicion arises, seeking is not obligatory. End. If his companion has a bucket, he does not have to ask him. If he asks him and he says, 'Wait until I draw water,' then according to Abu Hanifa it is recommended to wait as long as the time does not pass; if he fears that, he does tayammum. According to them, he waits. If he fears the time will pass, the basis of their statement is that when a promise is made, he becomes capable by virtue of it, because the apparent is that he will fulfill it. Similarly, the difference applies to a naked person if his companion promises him clothing. As in Mi'raj al-Diraya. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Tawshih: if his companion has a bucket and he has no water, he may do tayammum before asking him. In al-Mujtaba: he saw water in another's hands during his prayer, then it was removed before completion. He asked him and he said, 'If you had asked me earlier, I would have given you.' There is no repetition on him. But if the promise was before commencing, he repeats because it occurred during commencement. The most correct is that he does not repeat because the promise after the removal does not indicate giving before. End. The related issues from al-Ziyadat. In al-Tawshih, they agreed that if he says, 'I have permitted you my wealth for it,' then hajj is not obligatory on him. And they agreed that regarding water, if the owner promises to give it, he does not do tayammum and waits even if the time leaves. The difference between them is that capability in the first is only through ownership, and in the second... We have presented the branches to block doubt. The apparent is to carry their statements on this to reconcile them, so reflect. His statement: 'So by this, what occurred in al-Hidayah...' It may be reconciled between what is in al-Mabsut and what is in al-Hidayah by saying that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, and he adopted it. So he relied in al-Mabsut on Zahir al-Riwayah, and the author of al-Hidayah relied on al-Hasan's narration because it is more suitable to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa in not considering capability through others and considering incapacity at the moment. And Allah knows best. As in Sharh al-Munyah by al-Allama Burhan al-Din al-Halabi. He mentioned before that the correct is the detail as stated by Abu Nasr al-Saffar: seeking is obligatory only in a place where water is not scarce, because then the probability of refusal is realized. Water is usually available in every place that is not clearly prevented, as attested by anyone who has traveled. So seeking should be obligatory and prayer is not valid without it when one expects to be given, due to the strength of their evidence, but not when one expects refusal due to being in a place of water scarcity. If one is in doubt about water scarcity or expects refusal in other than a scarce place, then caution lies with their view (Sahibayn) and leniency with his view (Abu Hanifa), because asking involves humiliation. The statement of those who say there is no humiliation in asking for what is needed is rejected, and their proof that the Prophet asked some of his needs from others is problematic because the Prophet had a higher status over the believers, so others cannot be analogized to him. If he asks, the one asked is obliged to give, which is not the case for others.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq resolves a famous intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation to seek water before performing tayammum. The author begins by noting that water is generally available, so asking for it involves no humiliation, citing the Prophet's practice of asking others for needs. This repels the disagreement recorded in al-Hidayah and its gloss, where Abu Hanifa (ra) held that seeking is not obligatory while his two companions (Sahibayn) held it is obligatory. The key factor is the strength of expectation (ghalabat al-zann). If one strongly suspects he will be refused, there is no obligation to ask; if he strongly expects to be given, asking is required. The text cites various authorities: al-Jassas eliminates the disagreement by contextualizing it, al-Mujtaba confirms the general rule. It then discusses specific scenarios: if a companion has a bucket but promises to give water later, Abu Hanifa recommends waiting if time permits, while the Sahibayn require waiting even if time expires, based on the principle that a promise creates de facto capability. The passage concludes with a reconciliation between al-Mabsut and al-Hidayah, noting that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration (nawadir) was preferred by the author of al-Hidayah over the Zahir al-Riwayah. The later detail by Abu Nasr al-Saffar is endorsed: in areas of water scarcity, seeking is required only if one expects to be given.

Key Terms
طلب (talab): Actively seeking water from others before resorting to tayammum
عزة الماء (‘izzat al-ma’): Water scarcity; condition where water is not readily available
ظنة (zann): Strong assumption or suspicion regarding the likelihood of obtaining water
وعد (wa‘d): Promise to give water; creates a de facto capability according to Sahibayn

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the detailed view preferred in the text, when is it obligatory to ask for water before tayammum?
A) Always, even if you expect refusal.
B) Only when you strongly expect to receive water.
C) Never, because asking is humiliating.
D) Only when water is scarce.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to seek water before tayammum is conditional on the strength of expectation of receiving it, reconciling the apparent conflict between Abu Hanifa and his companions.

Tayammum When Water is Available for Purchase
Stating the conditions under which tayammum is permissible when water can be bought.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for tayammum when water is purchasable and apply the Hanafi qiyas on capability to determine when tayammum is invalid.

Core Idea
Capability on the substitute equals capability on the original; extortionate price triggers harm.

This lesson examines the conditions under which a person may perform tayammum when water is available for purchase. The Hanafi school establishes a clear principle: if you can buy water at a fair price, you must do so; tayammum is not valid. But what counts as 'fair'? The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq breaks this down into three scenarios based on the price level and introduces a key qiyas to expiation, helping you understand the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three price scenarios
The passage lists three possible prices: (1) thaman mithl (market value), (2) slight overcharge (ghaban yaseer), and (3) gross overcharge (ghaban fahish). Your task is to recall these and their rulings.
Memorize the three categories; they are the backbone of the ruling.
2
Apply the principle of capability
Understand that capability (qudra) to obtain the substitute (water via purchase) is treated as capability to obtain the original. Trace how this is derived from the analogy to buying a slave for expiation.
The qiyas is central: just as one who can buy a slave must do so (and cannot fast), one who can buy water must do so (and cannot do tayammum).
3
Define 'gross overcharge' (ghaban fahish)
The text gives multiple definitions; note that the preferred view (mufta bihi) is double the market value in that location, as in al-Nawadir.
This definition determines when harm (darar) exists and tayammum becomes permissible.
4
Derive the ruling for each scenario
For market value and slight overcharge: tayammum is invalid. For gross overcharge: tayammum is valid due to financial harm. Confirm this using the qiyas and the principle of darar.
The ruling hinges on the presence or absence of darar.
5
Examine the parallel case of a najis garment
The text draws an analogy: if one has a garment with najasah but no water, he prays in it without cutting the impurity. This illustrates how harm (inability to cut) drops the obligation.
Both cases show that hardship or loss can lift an otherwise obligatory duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله وله ثمنه لا يتيمم وإلا تيمم) وهذه المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه : إما أن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع الذي يعز فيه الماء أو بالغبن اليسير أو بالغبن الفاحش ; ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم لتحقق القدرة فإن القدرة على البدل قدرة على الماء كالقدرة على ثمن الرقبة في الكفارة تمنع الصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث يجوز له التيمم لوجود الضرر فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه والضرر في النفس مسقط في المال. كذا في العناية ونظيره الثوب النجس إذا لم يكن عنده ماء فإنه يصلي فيه ولا يلزمه قطع الثوب من موضع النجاسة والمراد بالثمن الفاضل عن حاجته على ما قدمناه . واختلفوا في تفسير الغبن الفاحش ; ففي النوادر هو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وفي رواية الحسن إذا قدر أن يشتري ما يساوي درهماً بدرهم ونصف لا يتيمم، وقيل ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقوّمين وقيل ما لا يتغابن في مثله لأن الضرر مسقط. واقتصر في البدائع والنهاية على ما في النوادر فكان هو الأول.
His statement: 'If he does not give it except for a price equivalent to its value and he has its price, he does not do tayammum; otherwise he does tayammum.' This issue has three aspects: either he gives it at its equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or with a slight overcharge, or with a gross overcharge. In the first and second aspects, tayammum does not suffice because capability is established, for capability on the substitute is capability on the water, like capability on the price of a slave in expiation prevents fasting. In the third aspect, tayammum is permissible due to harm, for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his self, and harm to the self is a ground for dropping obligation in matters of wealth. As in al-Inaya. Its analogy is a garment with najasah if he has no water: he prays in it and is not required to cut the garment at the place of najasah. What is meant by 'price' is the surplus above his need, as we have mentioned. They differed on the interpretation of gross overcharge (ghaban fahish). In al-Nawadir, it is double the value in that place. In the narration of al-Hasan, if he can buy what is worth a dirham for one and a half dirhams, he does not do tayammum. Some say it is what cannot be assessed by valuers. Some say it is what is not normally subject to overcharging in its like, because harm drops the obligation. Al-Bada'i' and al-Nihaya confined it to what is in al-Nawadir, so that is the first view.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on tayammum when water is available for purchase. The key principle is that if a person has the means to buy water at a fair price, he is considered capable of using it, and tayammum is invalid. The analogy is made to expiation: just as one who has the price of a slave can fast only if unable to buy, here one who can buy water at market price must do so. The ruling is categorized into three scenarios: (1) water sold at market value, (2) at a slight overcharge (yaseer), and (3) at a gross overcharge (fahish). In the first two, tayammum is not allowed because the person is capable of obtaining water without significant loss. In the third, tayammum is allowed because paying an extortionate price constitutes harm (darar) to one's wealth, and harm is grounds for leniency. The text then discusses the definition of ghban fahish, citing various opinions: in al-Nawadir it is double the value in that location; in another narration, it is paying one and a half times; some say it is any price that experts would not approve; others say it is any amount not normally overlooked in trade. The preferred view in al-Bada'i' and al-Nihaya is that of al-Nawadir (double the value). The passage also mentions the analogous case of a garment with najasah: if no water is available, one prays in it without cutting out the impurity.

Key Terms
ثمن مثل (thaman mithl): Market price or equivalent value of water in that location
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): Gross overcharge; defined in al-Nawadir as double the market price
ضرر (darar): Harm; here refers to financial harm from paying an extortionate price for water

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if water is available at double its market price, is tayammum permissible?
A) Yes, because double is considered ghban fahish.
B) No, only if it is more than double.
C) Yes, any overcharge makes tayammum permissible.
D) No, because one must still buy it.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is invalid when water is purchasable at market price or slight overcharge; only a gross overcharge (double) justifies tayammum due to financial harm.

Ruling on Tayammum for Predominant Wounds
Stating the rule for wounded person's purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a wounded person when most wudu limbs are wounded, and distinguish it from the case of a minority of wounds.

Core Idea
If most wudu limbs are wounded, tayammum replaces ablution; otherwise wash healthy parts and wipe wounds.

The wound ruling is a concession for the injured. When wounds cover the majority of the limbs used in wudu, washing becomes impractical or harmful. The Hanafi school sets a clear threshold: majority determines the mode of purification. This lesson unpacks the simple rule from al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a person with wounds on most wudu limbs: he must perform tayammum instead of wudu. Opposite case: wash.
The ruling is explicit and simple.
2
Define 'aktharuhu majruhan'
This means the majority of the limbs of wudu (face, hands, arms, feet) are wounded – more than half of them.
The count is by limbs, not by area of skin.
3
Apply the rule to scenarios
If most limbs are wounded → tayammum. If few limbs are wounded → wash healthy limbs and wipe over wounds.
This is the direct application of the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو أكثره مجروحاً تيمم وبعكسه يغسل) أي لو كان أكثر أعضاء الوضوء منه جراحاً يتيمم وبعكسه يغسل .
His statement: 'If most of him is wounded, he does tayammum; and conversely, he washes.' That is, if most of his wudu limbs are wounds, he does tayammum; and conversely, (if most are not wounded) he washes.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This brief passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq states a clear ruling: a person who has wounds covering most of the limbs of wudu (hands, face, arms, feet) should perform tayammum instead of washing. The criterion is the majority: if more than half of the wudu limbs are wounded, tayammum is performed; if fewer than half are wounded, the healthy parts are washed and the wounded are wiped (masah), or if wiping is harmful, just wash what you can. The text does not discuss the details of wiping over wounds, but simply gives the rule for the predominant case.

Key Terms
أكثرها مجروحاً (aktharuhu majruhan): The majority of the limbs of wudu being covered with wounds

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if most of his wudu limbs are wounded?
A) Wash the healthy parts and wipe the wounds.
B) Perform tayammum.
C) Pray without wudu or tayammum.
D) Wash all limbs anyway.

Key Takeaway
When most wudu limbs are wounded, tayammum replaces wudu; otherwise, wash and wipe.

When Must You Buy Water? Understanding the Tayammum Ruling on Purchasable Water
Commentary on when tayammum is allowed if water can be bought at a price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for purchasing water and apply the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when water is available at fair market price, slight overcharge, and gross overcharge.

Core Idea
Ability to buy water at fair price prevents tayammum; gross overcharge permits it — wealth is protected like life.

This lesson unpacks a key ruling in Taharah: when can a person perform tayammum if water is for sale? The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains three possibilities and the reasoning behind each, including a detailed analogy with atonement and a discussion of what constitutes 'gross overcharge'. By understanding this, you will see how Hanafi jurists balance religious duties with financial harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases: (1) water at fair market value, (2) slight overcharge, (3) gross overcharge. Note the ruling for each: tayammum invalid for (1) and (2), valid for (3).
The matn condenses these into 'if he is not given it except at a price equivalent to it and he has the price, he does not perform tayammum; otherwise, he performs tayammum.'
2
Extract the foundational analogy
Understand the qiyas: ability to buy water is like ability to buy a slave for atonement. Having the price means one is considered able to use water, just as having the price of a slave prevents fasting in atonement.
The commentator says, 'For ability on the substitute is ability on water, like ability on the price of a slave in atonement prevents fasting.'
3
Examine the harm principle
When the price is grossly overcharged, financial harm outweighs the duty to buy. The commentator compares this to an impure garment: if no water, one prays in it but is not obliged to cut out the impurity.
The inviolability of a Muslim's wealth is like the inviolability of his self; harm to the self renders obligation null in wealth.
4
Analyze the dispute on ghaban fahish
Identify the different definitions: double value (al-Nawadir), 1.5 dirhams for a dirham's worth (Riwayat al-Hasan), what is not subject to valuation, and what is not tolerated. Note that the preferred view (mufta bihi) is double value.
Al-Bada'i‘ and al-Nihayah restrict to the Nawadir definition, making it the relied-upon position.
5
Apply the ruling to a parallel case (buying a garment)
Compare with the case of a naked person who can buy a garment. Isma'il al-Imam said it is not obligatory to buy the garment for prayer, while others said it is obligatory by analogy to water. Note the author's leaning toward non-obligation.
The commentator notes that the appropriate version of the text is 'it is not obligatory' for the garment case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله وله ثمنه لا يتيمم وإلا تيمم) وهذه المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه : إما أن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع الذي يعز فيه الماء أو بالغبن اليسير أو بالغبن الفاحش ؛ ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم لتحقق القدرة فإن القدرة على البدل قدرة على الماء كالقدرة على ثمن الرقبة في الكفارة تمنع الصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث يجوز له التيمم لوجود الضرر فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه والضرر في النفس مسقط في المال. كذا في العناية ونظيره الثوب النجس إذا لم يكن عنده ماء فإنه يصلي فيه ولا يلزمه قطع الثوب من موضع النجاسة والمراد بالثمن الفاضل عن حاجته على ما قدمناه . واختلفوا في تفسير الغبن الفاحش ؛ ففي النوادر هو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وفي رواية الحسن إذا قدر أن يشتري ما يساوي درهماً بدرهم ونصف لا يتيمم، وقيل ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقوّمين وقيل ما لا يتغابن في مثله لأن الضرر مسقط. واقتصر في البدائع والنهاية على ما في النوادر فكان هو الأول، وقد قدمنا أنه إذا كان له مال غائب وأمكنه الشراء بثمن مؤجل وجب عليه الشراء بخلاف ما إذا وجد من يقرضه فإنه لا يجب عليه لأن الأجل لازم ولا مطالبة قبل حلوله بخلاف القرض قيد بالماء لأن العاري إذا قدر على شراء الثوب يوجد في بعض النسخ بياض بعد قوله الثوب» وفي بعضها لفظة «لا يجب» وفي بعضها لا يصلي عرياناً وهاتان النسختان مختلفتان حكماً لأن معنى الثانية منهما يجب. وفي المسألة قولان حكاهما في السراج فقال : ولو ملك ثمن الثوب هل يكلف شراءه قال إسمعيل الإمام : لا ولو ملك ثمن الماء يكلف شراءه. وقال عبد الله بن الفضل وأبو علي النسفي : يجب أن يكونا سواء ويكلف شراء الثوب كما يكلف شراء الماء .اهـ. والمتبادر من قول المؤلف قيد بالماء الخ المشي على القول الأول فالأنسب نسخة لا يجب وسنذكر المسألة أيضاً في شروط الصلاة والنسخ هناك مختلفة أيضاً، ففي بعضها الترديد وفي بعضها الجزم بعدم الوجوب، وكان صاحب النهر لم ير عبارة السراج فقال في شروط الصلاة ولو قدر عليه بثمن مثله لم يذكروه وينبغي أن يلزمه قياساً على شراء الماء اهـ . وما بحثه مخالف لما يفيده كلام أخيه
His statement: 'If he is not given it except at a price equivalent to it and he has the price, he does not perform tayammum; otherwise, he performs tayammum.' This issue has three aspects: Either he is given it at its equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or at a slight overcharge, or at a gross overcharge. In the first and second aspects, tayammum is not valid because ability is established, for ability on the substitute is ability on water, like ability on the price of a slave in atonement prevents fasting. In the third aspect, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm, for the inviolability of a Muslim's wealth is like the inviolability of his self, and harm to the self renders [obligation] null in wealth. Thus in al-`Inayah. Its parallel is the impure garment: if he has no water, he prays in it and is not obliged to cut the garment from the place of impurity. What is meant by 'price' is the surplus beyond his need as we stated. They differed in interpreting gross overcharge: in al-Nawadir it is double the value in that place; in a narration from al-Hasan: if he can buy what is worth a dirham for one and a half dirhams, he does not perform tayammum; it is said: what is not subject to the valuation of valuers; it is said: what there is no toleration of like it, because harm renders [obligation] null. In al-Bada'i` and al-Nihayah they restricted to what is in al-Nawadir, so it is the first. We have mentioned that if he has remote wealth and can purchase on deferred payment, purchase is obligatory for him, unlike if he finds someone who will lend him, for then it is not obligatory because the term is binding and no claim before its maturity, unlike the loan. He restricted it to water because if a naked person can afford to buy a garment... There is a blank in some copies after his word 'garment'; and in some copies the phrase 'it is not obligatory'; and in some copies 'he does not pray naked'. These two copies differ in ruling, for the meaning of the second is that it is obligatory. On this issue there are two opinions, narrated in al-Siraj: 'If he owns the price of a garment, is he obliged to buy it?' Isma`il al-Imam said: No; but if he owns the price of water, he is obliged to buy it. `Abdullah ibn al-Fadl and Abu `Ali al-Nasafi said: The two should be equal, and he is obliged to buy the garment as he is obliged to buy water. End. What is apparent from the author's statement 'restricted to water' etc. is following the first opinion, so the appropriate version is 'it is not obligatory'. We will also mention this issue in the conditions of prayer, and the versions there differ as well: in some there is hesitation, in some there is certainty of non-obligation. And the author of al-Nahr did not see the statement of al-Siraj, so he said in the conditions of prayer: 'If he can afford it at a similar price, they did not mention it, and it should be obligatory by analogy on the purchase of water.' End. And his research opposes what the statement of his brother indicates.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa’iq regarding tayammum when water is available for purchase. The matn states that if a person can obtain water only at a price he can afford, he must buy it; otherwise, tayammum is allowed. The commentator explains three scenarios: (1) water at fair market price (thaman mithl) or slight overcharge (ghaban yasir) — tayammum invalid because he is considered able to use water; (2) gross overcharge (ghaban fahish) — tayammum valid due to financial harm. The reasoning is that ability on the substitute is like ability on the original, analogous to having the price of a slave for atonement which prevents fasting. The harm of excessive loss overrides the duty to buy, since preserving one’s wealth is akin to preserving one’s life. The passage then records differing interpretations of what constitutes ‘gross overcharge’: the preferred view (from al-Nawadir, adopted in al-Bada’i‘ and al-Nihayah) is double the market price. There is also discussion about buying a garment for covering nakedness during prayer, where scholars differed on whether one must buy a garment if able. The commentator leans toward not obligating purchase of a garment, following Isma‘il al-Imam, but notes that the later scholar al-Nahr disagreed, arguing qiyas with water. The passage ends with a note that this issue will be revisited in the chapter on conditions of prayer.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): Gross overcharge; a price significantly above market value that causes substantial financial harm, defined as double the market value in this passage.
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): Fair market price; the standard price at which the commodity is normally sold in that location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person can buy water at a price that is double the market value, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon position in this passage?
A) He must purchase the water and tayammum is invalid.
B) He may perform tayammum because this is a gross overcharge.
C) He must borrow money to buy the water at any cost.
D) He should ask a neighbor for water without payment.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of tayammum when water is purchasable depends on whether the price is fair or grossly overcharged; the relied-upon threshold is double the market value.
